%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Little-group mismatch implies vanishing constant mixing}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We want to close the first remaining microscopic Dirac-condition,
\[
V(0)=0,
\]
for the block decomposition
\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R.
\]
Here \(\mathcal H_D\) is the shell-relevant local Dirac block, and \(\mathcal H_R\) is the remote sector.

\paragraph{Assumption audit.}
We assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(H_*\) is the little group (more precisely: the residual symmetry group at the selected crossing \(p=0\));
\item \(H_*\) acts unitarily on \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}\);
\item the decomposition
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R
\]
is \(H_*\)-invariant;
\item the microscopic Hamiltonian is \(H_*\)-equivariant at \(p=0\).
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Step 1. Block-equivariance forces the constant mixing to be an intertwiner.}
Because the decomposition is \(H_*\)-invariant, the symmetry action has block form
\[
U(h)=
\begin{pmatrix}
U_D(h) & 0\\
0 & U_R(h)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad h\in H_*,
\]
where \(U_D\) and \(U_R\) are the restricted representations on \(\mathcal H_D\) and \(\mathcal H_R\).

At \(p=0\), write
\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(0) & V(0)\\
V(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Equivariance means
\[
U(h)\,H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)\,U(h)^{-1}=H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)
\qquad
\forall h\in H_*.
\]
Comparing the off-diagonal block gives
\[
U_D(h)\,V(0)\,U_R(h)^{-1}=V(0)
\qquad
\forall h\in H_*.
\]
Therefore
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]

\paragraph{Step 2. Abstract little-group mismatch theorem.}
If
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
then the only possible intertwiner is the zero map. Since \(V(0)\) is such an intertwiner, it follows that
\[
V(0)=0.
\]

Hence we obtain the exact theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
V(0)=0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Step 3. Irreducible decomposition form.}
Let \(\{W_\lambda\}_\lambda\) be a full set of inequivalent irreducible \(H_*\)-modules. Decompose
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \bigoplus_\lambda m_\lambda^{(D)} W_\lambda,
\qquad
\mathcal H_R \cong \bigoplus_\lambda m_\lambda^{(R)} W_\lambda.
\]
Then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)
\cong
\bigoplus_\lambda
\mathrm{Mat}_{m_\lambda^{(D)}\times m_\lambda^{(R)}}(\mathbb C).
\]
Therefore
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\]
if and only if
\[
m_\lambda^{(D)}m_\lambda^{(R)}=0
\qquad
\text{for all } \lambda.
\]
Equivalently, \(\mathcal H_D\) and \(\mathcal H_R\) share no common irreducible \(H_*\)-sector.

\paragraph{Step 4. Honest correction for TECT.}
In TECT, one must be careful not to overstate what ordinary cubic little-group representation theory can do.

For the selected BCC shell axis, the ordinary stabilizers are abelian
(\(C_{2v}\) for an oriented shell direction and \(D_{2h}\) for the opposite pair),
so ordinary complex irreducible representations are one-dimensional.
Therefore the actual local Dirac carrier is not forced by an ordinary 2D little-group irrep.

The correct shell-relevant local carrier is instead
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
where

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\) is the opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\),
\item \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\) is the shell-relevant enriched internal/transverse doublet.
\end{itemize}

Thus the physically correct microscopic zero-mixing criterion is not
``ordinary cubic irreducibility'',
but rather \emph{sectorwise mismatch in shell-relevant labels}.

\paragraph{Step 5. Sectorwise remote-label mismatch criterion.}
Let
\[
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a
\]
be an \(H_*\)-invariant sector decomposition of the remote space.
A remote sector \(K_a\) can mix with \(\mathcal H_D\) at \(p=0\) only if it matches \(\mathcal H_D\) in all shell-relevant labels.

A sufficient exclusion criterion is that each \(K_a\) differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one of the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item selected shell-pair label \(\pm G_*\),
\item transverse versus longitudinal/volumetric character,
\item existence of the enriched shell-relevant internal doublet,
\item residual grading / parity / chirality,
\item any additional conserved microscopic label.
\end{enumerate}

If every remote sector fails at least one of these matching conditions, then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
\qquad
\forall a,
\]
hence
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
and therefore
\[
V(0)=0.
\]

So the TECT-sharp form of the theorem is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}
\quad+\quad
\text{sectorwise remote-label mismatch}
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Step 6. First nontrivial order in momentum.}
Once \(V(0)=0\), the leading inter-sector mixing starts at higher order in \(p\).
If the momentum representation is \(R_p\), then the linear coefficient must lie in
\[
V_i \in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(R_p\otimes \mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Therefore:

\begin{itemize}
\item if
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(R_p\otimes \mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
then
\[
V(p)=O(|p|^2);
\]

\item otherwise, generically,
\[
V(p)=O(|p|).
\]
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Step 7. Schur-complement consequence.}
Assume in addition that the remote block is spectrally gapped:
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing.
\]
Then for \(|E|<\Delta/2\),
\[
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
\]
Hence the Schur-complement self-energy
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger
\]
satisfies
\[
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2
\]
whenever
\[
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|.
\]
Therefore the effective low-energy Hamiltonian becomes
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)-\Sigma(E,p)
=
H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\]

\paragraph{Conclusion.}
The first remaining Dirac-closure condition is therefore reduced to a finite microscopic audit:
prove that the remote sectors share no shell-relevant representation content with
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]
Once that is done, one gets
\[
V(0)=0
\]
exactly.

\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(0) & V(0)\\
V(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus\mathcal H_R.
\]

\[
U(h)\mathcal H_D\subset \mathcal H_D,
\qquad
U(h)\mathcal H_R\subset \mathcal H_R,
\qquad
U(h)H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)U(h)^{-1}=H_{\mathrm{full}}(0).
\]

Then
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

In the honest TECT form, the local Dirac carrier is not forced by an ordinary cubic 2D irrep.
Rather,
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
and the practical criterion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{each remote sector differs from } \mathcal H_D
\text{ in at least one shell-relevant label}
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

The shell-relevant labels are:
\[
\pm G_*,
\quad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\quad
\text{enriched internal doublet},
\quad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{extra conserved labels}.
\]

\subsection{Summary}

If, in addition,
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R)\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
then
\[
\Sigma(E,p)
=
V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
\]
so
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\]

Hence the first remaining full Dirac-closure condition is reduced to a finite microscopic
sectorwise label-audit problem.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Remote-gap positivity as an independent spectral input}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now close the statement
\[
\Delta>0
\]
in the sharp theorem-level form that is actually justified in the present TECT framework.

The correct statement is not that the Class II correction \emph{creates} a remote gap automatically.
Rather, the remote gap is an \emph{independent spectral property} of the remote sector, and the Class II correction is compatible with it and preserves it under a sufficiently small bounded perturbation.

\paragraph{Block decomposition.}
Write the full microscopic Hamiltonian near the selected shell crossing as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:full_block_gap_user}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{itemize}
\item \(H_D(p)\) is the isolated doubled shell Dirac block,
\item \(H_R(p)\) is the remote sector.
\end{itemize}

The remote-gap condition is
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing
\qquad
\text{for all sufficiently small }p.
\label{eq:remote_gap_condition_user}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection*{A. Why shell nondegeneracy does not prove the remote gap}

Let
\begin{equation}
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
B & -C & 0\\
C & B & 0\\
0 & 0 & A
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det M=A(B^2+C^2)\neq 0.
\label{eq:detM_shell_user}
\end{equation}
This shell determinant controls only the nondegeneracy of the projected local Dirac symbol.
It does \emph{not} determine the spectrum of the complementary operator \(H_R\).

Hence
\[
\det M\neq 0
\]
is not a proof of
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R)\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing.
\]
So the theorem-level route to \(\Delta>0\) must be spectral, not determinant-based.

\subsubsection*{B. Unperturbed remote gap}

Assume there exists an unperturbed microscopic realization
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}^{(0)}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D^{(0)}(p) & V^{(0)}(p)\\
V^{(0)}(p)^\dagger & H_R^{(0)}(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:H0_decomp_user}
\end{equation}
whose remote sector has a uniform positive gap:
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap(-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing
\qquad
\text{for all }|p|\le p_*,
\label{eq:unpert_gap_user}
\end{equation}
for some \(\Delta_0>0\).

This is the genuine microscopic spectral input.

\subsubsection*{C. Class II correction as a bounded perturbation}

Now perturb the theory by a self-adjoint Class II correction:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=H_{\mathrm{full}}^{(0)}(p)+\delta H(p),
\label{eq:full_plus_delta_user}
\end{equation}
and correspondingly
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=H_R^{(0)}(p)+\delta H_R(p).
\label{eq:HR_pert_user}
\end{equation}
Assume that
\begin{equation}
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|\le \varepsilon.
\label{eq:deltaHR_bound_user}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Remote-gap stability under bounded perturbation]
Assume \eqref{eq:unpert_gap_user} and \eqref{eq:deltaHR_bound_user}.
If
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon<\Delta_0,
\label{eq:eps_less_gap_user}
\end{equation}
then the perturbed remote sector still satisfies
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta:=\Delta_0-\varepsilon>0,
\label{eq:perturbed_gap_user}
\end{equation}
for all \(|p|\le p_*\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Fix \(p\) and let \(\lambda\in\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\).
By standard spectral stability for self-adjoint bounded perturbations,
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(\lambda,\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\bigr)
\le
\|\delta H_R(p)\|.
\label{eq:spectral_variation_user}
\end{equation}
Since the unperturbed spectrum avoids \((-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)\), every spectral point of \(H_R^{(0)}(p)\) has absolute value at least \(\Delta_0\).
Hence
\begin{equation}
|\lambda|
\ge
\Delta_0-\|\delta H_R(p)\|
\ge
\Delta_0-\varepsilon
=
\Delta.
\label{eq:abs_lambda_gap_user}
\end{equation}
Because \(\Delta>0\), the interval \((-\Delta,\Delta)\) contains no spectrum of \(H_R(p)\).
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Corollary.}
If one assumes the stronger bound
\begin{equation}
\|\delta H_R\|<\frac{\Delta_0}{2},
\label{eq:half_gap_bound_user}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\Delta\ge \Delta_0-\|\delta H_R\|>\frac{\Delta_0}{2}>0.
\label{eq:half_gap_positive_user}
\end{equation}
This is the exact theorem-level meaning of the statement
\[
\text{``Class II is gap-compatible.''}
\]

\subsubsection*{D. Resolvent bound}

Let
\begin{equation}
|E|<\frac{\Delta}{2}.
\label{eq:E_window_user}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E,\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\bigr)\ge \frac{\Delta}{2},
\label{eq:dist_to_spec_user}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
\label{eq:resolvent_bound_user}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection*{E. Schur-complement consequence}

Assume also
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|.
\label{eq:V_small_gap_user}
\end{equation}
Then the reduced low-energy operator is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)-\Sigma(E,p),
\qquad
\Sigma(E,p):=
V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger.
\label{eq:Heff_gap_user}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:resolvent_bound_user} and \eqref{eq:V_small_gap_user},
\begin{equation}
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\|V(p)\|^2\,\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2.
\label{eq:sigma_gap_bound_user}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\label{eq:Heff_preserved_user}
\end{equation}
So the gapped remote sector alters the isolated Dirac block only at subleading quadratic order.

\subsubsection*{F. Honest theorem-level status}

Hence the mathematically honest closure is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_0>0
\ \text{for the unperturbed remote sector}
\quad+\quad
\|\delta H_R\|<\Delta_0
\Longrightarrow
\Delta=\Delta_0-\|\delta H_R\|>0.
}
\label{eq:final_remote_gap_box_user}
\end{equation}

In particular, Class II does not by itself prove the existence of the remote gap, but it preserves that gap under sufficiently small bounded perturbations.

\subsection{Final Spectral Isolation Theorem}

We now combine the three theorem-level inputs:
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\Delta>0,
\qquad
\text{mass protection}.
\]

Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell-relevant doubled block has the nondegenerate Dirac form
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)=\Gamma_i(Mp)_i,
\qquad
\{\Gamma_i,\Gamma_j\}=2\delta_{ij},
\qquad
\det M\neq 0;
\label{eq:HD_local_final_user}
\end{equation}

\item little-group mismatch implies
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|;
\label{eq:V0_linear_user}
\end{equation}

\item the remote sector satisfies
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing;
\label{eq:gap_final_user}
\end{equation}

\item the residual symmetry forbids all constant Dirac masses.
\end{enumerate}

Then, for \(|E|<\Delta/2\),
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(Mp)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
\label{eq:Final_Spectral_Isolation_user}
\end{equation}
and therefore the full microscopic theory contains a stable spectrally isolated massless Dirac cone.

\begin{proof}
By the remote-gap condition,
\[
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
\]
By \eqref{eq:V0_linear_user}, the Schur-complement correction is quadratic:
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\]
Hence the full low-energy Hamiltonian differs from the local shell Dirac block only by quadratic terms.
The residual symmetry excludes all constant mass operators, so no \(O(1)\) gap can appear.
Therefore the leading linear Dirac cone survives and remains spectrally isolated.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Remote-gap positivity is an independent spectral input.}
}
\]

\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing.
\]

The shell determinant
\[
\det M=A(B^2+C^2)
\]
controls only local shell-Dirac nondegeneracy, not the remote spectrum.

Assume an unperturbed realization with
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap(-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_0>0,
\]
and a bounded Class II correction
\[
H_R(p)=H_R^{(0)}(p)+\delta H_R(p),
\qquad
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|\le \varepsilon.
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon<\Delta_0
\Longrightarrow
\Delta:=\Delta_0-\varepsilon>0
}
\]
and
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing.
\]

For \(|E|<\Delta/2\),
\[
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
\]

If also
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
then
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|\le \frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2,
\]
hence
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II does not automatically prove } \Delta>0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{but it preserves a pre-existing remote gap under sufficiently small bounded perturbations.}
}
\]

Combining
\[
\det M\neq 0,\qquad V(0)=0,\qquad \Delta>0,\qquad \text{mass protection},
\]
one obtains
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=\Gamma_i(Mp)_i+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
}
\]
so the full microscopic theory contains a stable spectrally isolated massless Dirac cone.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Mass protection for the doubled shell Dirac block}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We close the last remaining theorem-level ingredient of the local Dirac-stability program:
the classification of all symmetry-allowed constant Hermitian \(4\times4\) operators on the doubled shell block,
and the criterion under which all genuine Dirac masses are forbidden.

\paragraph{Setup.}
Assume opposite-valley pairing has already been established, so that the isolated shell-relevant doubled block is
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
h_+(p) & 0\\
0 & h_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p),
\label{eq:HD_pair_setup_user}
\end{equation}
and after a shell-adapted basis choice and invertible linear momentum redefinition,
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i\,\alpha_i,
\qquad
\alpha_i:=\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i.
\label{eq:HD_alpha_user}
\end{equation}
Here \(\sigma_i\) acts on the internal Weyl doublet and \(\tau_i\) acts on the valley pair \((+G_*,-G_*)\).

Thus
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

\subsubsection*{A. Classification of constant little-group-scalar operators}

Let \(K\) be a constant Hermitian operator on \(\mathcal H_D\).
Write it in \(2\times2\) valley-block form:
\begin{equation}
K=
\begin{pmatrix}
A & B\\
B^\dagger & D
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A,D,B\in M_2(\mathbb C).
\label{eq:K_block_form_user}
\end{equation}

Assume \(K\) preserves the little-group action at the crossing point \(p=0\),
and that the two valley blocks carry the same irreducible little-group representation \(\rho\).
Then Schur's lemma gives
\begin{equation}
A=a_+\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
D=a_-\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
B=b\,\mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:Schur_reduction_user}
\end{equation}
with \(a_\pm\in\mathbb R\), \(b\in\mathbb C\).
Therefore every constant little-group-scalar Hermitian operator has the form
\begin{equation}
K
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:K_scalar_classification_user}
\end{equation}

So the allowed constant scalar operator space is four-dimensional.

\subsubsection*{B. Exact classification of genuine constant Dirac masses}

A genuine constant Dirac mass is a Hermitian matrix \(M\) satisfying
\begin{equation}
\{M,\alpha_i\}=0,
\qquad i=1,2,3.
\label{eq:mass_def_user}
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[Exact constant mass space]
For
\[
\alpha_i=\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i,
\]
the constant Hermitian matrices anticommting with all \(\alpha_i\) are exactly
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
\label{eq:mass_space_user}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Take a general constant Hermitian matrix in block form
\[
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
A & B\\
B^\dagger & D
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Using
\[
\alpha_i=
\begin{pmatrix}
\sigma_i & 0\\
0 & -\sigma_i
\end{pmatrix},
\]
the condition \(\{M,\alpha_i\}=0\) becomes
\begin{equation}
\{A,\sigma_i\}=0,
\qquad
\{D,\sigma_i\}=0,
\qquad
B\sigma_i-\sigma_i B=0,
\qquad
B^\dagger\sigma_i-\sigma_i B^\dagger=0,
\label{eq:anticomm_eqs_user}
\end{equation}
for all \(i=1,2,3\).

Since the Pauli matrices generate \(M_2(\mathbb C)\), the anticommutation equations imply
\[
A=0,\qquad D=0,
\]
while the commutation equations imply
\[
B=b\,\mathbf 1_2
\]
for some \(b\in\mathbb C\).
Hence
\begin{equation}
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & b\,\mathbf 1_2\\
\bar b\,\mathbf 1_2 & 0
\end{pmatrix}
=
(\Re b)\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
(\Im b)\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:mass_form_user}
\end{equation}
This proves \eqref{eq:mass_space_user}.
\end{proof}

Therefore the only genuine constant masses are
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\qquad \tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

By contrast,
\[
\mathbf 1_4
\]
is only an overall energy shift, and
\[
\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
is a valley-energy splitting term, not a genuine Dirac mass.

\subsubsection*{C. Residual valley symmetry and mass protection}

Define the valley-charge generator
\begin{equation}
Q_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:Qv_user}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
[Q_V,H_D(p)]=0,
\label{eq:Qv_comm_user}
\end{equation}
so the doubled block carries a residual valley symmetry
\begin{equation}
U_\theta:=e^{\,i\theta Q_V/2}.
\label{eq:Uv_user}
\end{equation}

Now compute the transformation of the two mass generators:
\begin{equation}
U_\theta
(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
U_\theta^{-1}
=
\cos\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\sin\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\label{eq:taux_rot_user}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
U_\theta
(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
U_\theta^{-1}
=
-\sin\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\cos\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:tauy_rot_user}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
U_\theta
\bigl((\tau_x\pm i\tau_y)\otimes \mathbf 1_2\bigr)
U_\theta^{-1}
=
e^{\pm i\theta}
\bigl((\tau_x\pm i\tau_y)\otimes \mathbf 1_2\bigr).
\label{eq:charged_mass_user}
\end{equation}
Thus the genuine Dirac-mass operators carry nonzero valley charge.

\begin{theorem}[Mass protection from residual valley symmetry]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the doubled low-energy block has the kinetic form \eqref{eq:HD_alpha_user};
\item the constant operator under consideration preserves the little-group action at \(p=0\);
\item the residual valley symmetry generated by \(Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2\) is exact on the isolated doubled block.
\end{enumerate}
Then every symmetry-allowed constant Hermitian operator is of the form
\begin{equation}
K
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:K_allowed_user}
\end{equation}
and in particular the genuine mass coefficients vanish:
\begin{equation}
m_1=m_2=0.
\label{eq:masses_zero_user}
\end{equation}
Hence no constant Dirac mass is allowed.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:K_scalar_classification_user}, every constant little-group-scalar Hermitian operator has the form
\[
K=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Exact \(U(1)_V\) invariance requires
\[
U_\theta K U_\theta^{-1}=K
\qquad
\forall \theta.
\]
The terms \(\mathbf 1_4\) and \(\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2\) are invariant, whereas
\eqref{eq:taux_rot_user}--\eqref{eq:charged_mass_user} show that
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\qquad
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
transform nontrivially.
Therefore they are forbidden unless
\[
m_1=m_2=0.
\]
By \eqref{eq:mass_space_user}, these are precisely all genuine constant Dirac masses.
Hence no constant Dirac mass is allowed.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Weaker version.}
The full continuous \(U(1)_V\) is stronger than necessary.
The discrete remnant
\begin{equation}
S_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
S_V^2=\mathbf 1_4,
\label{eq:Zv_user}
\end{equation}
already suffices, since
\begin{equation}
S_V(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\qquad
S_V(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:Z2_forbid_user}
\end{equation}
So an exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) also forbids all genuine constant masses.

\subsubsection*{D. Basis-free finite algebraic criterion}

Let
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}
=
\{K\in \mathrm{Herm}(4): U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K\ \forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}\}
\label{eq:Ares_user}
\end{equation}
be the residual-symmetry allowed constant operator algebra.
Then the exact finite mass-protection criterion is
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\cap
\{K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4): \{K,\alpha_i\}=0\ \forall i\}
=
\{0\}.
\label{eq:finite_mass_criterion_user}
\end{equation}
If \eqref{eq:finite_mass_criterion_user} holds, then no symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass exists.

\subsubsection*{E. Honest TECT/Class II status}

The canonical minimal Class II correction is gradient-linear and renormalizes the derivative shell coefficients
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}},\quad B_{\mathrm{eff}},\quad C_{\mathrm{eff}},
\]
rather than inserting an independent constant \(4\times4\) Dirac mass by construction.
Therefore Class II is \emph{compatible} with mass protection.

However, this does not by itself prove that all symmetry-allowed constant masses are forbidden in the full corrected microscopic theory.
That still depends on the actual residual symmetry algebra \(A_{\mathrm{res}}\) of the enriched shell block.

Hence the mathematically honest final statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Mass protection is completely reduced to the finite classification problem }
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\cap
\{K:\{K,\alpha_i\}=0\}
=
\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:honest_mass_status_user}
\end{equation}
Moreover, if exact residual \(U(1)_V\) or \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) survives in the actual TECT realization, then this criterion is automatically satisfied.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\qquad
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i\,\alpha_i,
\qquad
\alpha_i=\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i.
}
\]

Every constant little-group-scalar Hermitian operator on the doubled block is
\[
K
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

The genuine constant Dirac masses are exactly
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
}
\]

Indeed,
\[
\{M,\alpha_i\}=0\ \forall i
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
M\in \mathcal M_D.
\]

Define the valley-charge generator
\[
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_\theta=e^{i\theta Q_V/2}.
\]
Then
\[
U_\theta
(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
U_\theta^{-1}
=
\cos\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\sin\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\]
\[
U_\theta
(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
U_\theta^{-1}
=
-\sin\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\cos\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\]
Hence the genuine mass operators carry nonzero valley charge.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If exact residual }U(1)_V\text{ survives, all constant Dirac masses are forbidden.}
}
\]

Even the weaker remnant
\[
S_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
already suffices, because
\[
S_V(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}=-(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\qquad
S_V(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}=-(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\]

Equivalently, the exact finite algebraic criterion is
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\cap
\{K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4):\{K,\alpha_i\}=0\ \forall i\}
=
\{0\}.
}
\]

Hence the honest final status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{mass protection is reduced completely to a finite }4\times4\text{ symmetry classification problem.}
}
\]

In the current TECT/Class II route:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II is compatible with mass protection,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{actual mass protection still requires verification that the true residual symmetry forbids }
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
}
\]

\section*{Dirac Emergence Closure Theorem in the Class II Route}

\subsection*{1. Local shell-relevant Dirac block}

In the current Class II route, the reduced local \(S^2\)-transport ansatz is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:ClassII_local_ansatz_final}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, writing
\[
p=(p_1,p_2,p_\parallel),
\]
the symbol can be expressed as
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=q_a(p)\sigma_a,
\qquad
q(p)=Mp,
\label{eq:qMp_final}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:M_ClassII_final}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:detM_ClassII_final}
\end{equation}
Therefore the local nondegeneracy condition is exactly
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:local_nondeg_final}
\end{equation}
In the coupling notation of the Class II seed,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa,
\label{eq:ClassII_coeffs_final}
\end{equation}
so \eqref{eq:local_nondeg_final} is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:ClassII_coupling_nondeg_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Doubled local Dirac block}

Assume that the opposite shell partner exists and that the matched opposite-valley reduction has already been carried out.
Then the isolated shell-relevant doubled block takes the \(4\times 4\) Dirac form
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)=\Gamma_i(Mp)_i,
\qquad
\{\Gamma_i,\Gamma_j\}=2\delta_{ij},
\label{eq:HD_final_theorem}
\end{equation}
with \(M\) given by \eqref{eq:M_ClassII_final}.
By \eqref{eq:detM_ClassII_final} and \eqref{eq:local_nondeg_final},
\begin{equation}
\det M\neq 0.
\label{eq:detM_not_zero_final}
\end{equation}
Thus \(H_D(p)\) is a nondegenerate local massless Dirac block.

\subsection*{3. Full microscopic block decomposition}

Let the full microscopic linearized Hamiltonian near the selected shell crossing be written as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Hfull_final_theorem}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{itemize}
\item \(H_D(p)\) is the shell-relevant doubled \(4\times4\) Dirac block,
\item \(H_R(p)\) is the remote sector,
\item \(V(p)\) is the inter-sector mixing.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{4. Three additional closure hypotheses}

Assume:

\paragraph{(H1) Little-group mismatch / zero constant mixing.}
The enriched shell block and the remote sector share no common residual representation sector at \(p=0\), so that
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|
\quad
\text{for sufficiently small }p.
\label{eq:Vzero_linear_final}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(H2) Positive remote spectral gap.}
There exists \(\Delta>0\) such that
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing
\qquad
\text{for sufficiently small }p.
\label{eq:remote_gap_final_theorem}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(H3) Mass protection.}
No symmetry-allowed constant Hermitian \(4\times4\) operator on the doubled block is a Dirac mass.
Equivalently, if \(G_{\mathrm{res}}\) is the residual low-energy symmetry group and
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}
=
\{K\in \mathrm{Herm}(4): U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K\ \forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}\},
\label{eq:Ares_final_theorem}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\cap
\{K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4): \{K,\Gamma_i\}=0\ \forall i\}
=
\{0\}.
\label{eq:mass_protection_final_theorem}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Resolvent bound}

Let \(|E|<\Delta/2\).
By \eqref{eq:remote_gap_final_theorem},
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
\label{eq:resolvent_bound_final_theorem}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Schur-complement reduction}

The exact low-energy effective Hamiltonian on the doubled block is the Feshbach--Schur operator
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)-\Sigma(E,p),
\label{eq:Heff_final_theorem}
\end{equation}
with self-energy
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(E,p)
=
V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger.
\label{eq:Sigma_final_theorem}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:Vzero_linear_final} and \eqref{eq:resolvent_bound_final_theorem},
\begin{equation}
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\|V(p)\|^2\,\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2.
\label{eq:Sigma_bound_final_theorem}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\label{eq:Heff_quadratic_final_theorem}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Exclusion of an induced constant mass}

By \eqref{eq:mass_protection_final_theorem}, no symmetry-allowed constant operator can anticommute with all three kinetic gamma matrices.
Therefore the Schur-complement correction cannot generate an \(O(1)\) Dirac mass term.
Thus the effective Hamiltonian remains massless at leading order:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(0,0)=0.
\label{eq:no_mass_generated_final_theorem}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{8. Final closure theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Dirac Emergence Closure Theorem, Class II form]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the local Class II nondegeneracy condition holds,
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\]
equivalently
\[
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0);
\]
\item the opposite-valley partner exists and yields the doubled local Dirac block \eqref{eq:HD_final_theorem};
\item the little-group mismatch hypothesis \eqref{eq:Vzero_linear_final} holds;
\item the remote spectral gap hypothesis \eqref{eq:remote_gap_final_theorem} holds;
\item the mass-protection hypothesis \eqref{eq:mass_protection_final_theorem} holds.
\end{enumerate}
Then, for sufficiently small \(p\) and \(|E|<\Delta/2\), the full TECT linearized theory contains a spectrally isolated four-dimensional low-energy sector whose effective Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{Dirac}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(Mp)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
\qquad
\{\Gamma_i,\Gamma_j\}=2\delta_{ij},
\qquad
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2)\neq 0.
\label{eq:Dirac_Closure_Theorem_ClassII}
\end{equation}
In particular, the full theory contains a stable, spectrally isolated, massless Dirac cone.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Item (1) implies \(\det M\neq 0\), so the local shell-relevant block is a nondegenerate massless Dirac symbol.
Item (2) upgrades this to the doubled \(4\times4\) Dirac block.
Item (3) removes constant inter-sector mixing and makes the first nontrivial mixing at least linear in \(p\).
Item (4) provides the uniform resolvent bound \eqref{eq:resolvent_bound_final_theorem}.
Hence the Schur-complement self-energy is quadratic in momentum, as in \eqref{eq:Sigma_bound_final_theorem}, and the effective Hamiltonian differs from the local Dirac block only by \(O(|p|^2/\Delta)\).
Item (5) excludes all symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass terms.
Therefore the leading linear Dirac cone survives, remains massless, and stays spectrally isolated from all remote states.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{9. Honest logical status}

What is now genuinely closed is the implication
\[
\text{local Class II shell Dirac nondegeneracy}
+
\text{opposite-valley doubling}
+
\text{zero constant mixing}
+
\text{positive remote gap}
+
\text{mass protection}
\Longrightarrow
\text{stable spectrally isolated massless Dirac cone}.
\]

What may still remain open in an actual microscopic realization is only the direct verification that these hypotheses are indeed satisfied by the final microscopic TECT/Class II linearization.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2)
}
\]

Hence the local shell nondegeneracy condition is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
}
\]
equivalently
\[
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Let the full microscopic Hamiltonian be
\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
H_D(p)=\Gamma_i(Mp)_i,
\qquad
\{\Gamma_i,\Gamma_j\}=2\delta_{ij}.
\]

Assume:
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta>0,
\]
and
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\cap
\{K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4):\{K,\Gamma_i\}=0\ \forall i\}
=

\]

Then for \(|E|<\Delta/2\),

\]
and the Schur-complement self-energy obeys

\Sigma(E,p)=V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|\le \frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2.

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{Dirac}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(Mp)_i
+

\qquad

}

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
\text{local Class II nondegeneracy}
+
\text{opposite-valley doubling}
+
V(0)=0
+
\Delta>0
+
\text{mass protection}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Longrightarrow
\text{stable spectrally isolated massless Dirac cone.}
}
\]

Honest final status:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the theorem-level implication is closed,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual microscopic TECT/Class II realization still requires finite verification of the input hypotheses.}
}

\section*{Master Verification Checklist for the Microscopic Class II Closure}

\subsection*{0. Fixed data and notation}

Choose and freeze the following data once and for all:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the selected shell vector
\[
G_* \in \mathbb R^3\setminus\{0\},
\qquad
\hat n:=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|};
\]

\item an orthonormal shell frame
\[
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\},
\qquad
e_\alpha\cdot \hat n=0,
\qquad
e_\alpha\cdot e_\beta=\delta_{\alpha\beta};
\]

\item the actual symmetry-allowed microscopic tensor space
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}} \subset \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{int}};
\]

\item the shell-relevant internal channels \(u^{(1)},u^{(2)}\);

\item the opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\);

\item the residual symmetry group \(H_*\) at the selected crossing.
\end{enumerate}

All later tests depend on this frozen choice. If these data are changed midstream, all previously computed witness statements must be recomputed.

\subsection*{1. Task I: shell witness nonvanishing}

\paragraph{Goal.}
Verify that the local shell-reduced Dirac block exists at all.

\paragraph{Exact finite criterion.}
For each transverse Dirac channel \(\alpha=1,2\), define
\[
T^{(\alpha)}_{ija}=e_{\alpha i}G_{*j}u^{(\alpha)}_a.
\]
Then the exact criterion is
\[
P_V T^{(1)}\neq 0,
\qquad
P_V T^{(2)}\neq 0,
\]
where \(P_V\) is the orthogonal projector onto the symmetry-allowed tensor space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).

Equivalently, it suffices to construct explicit seed tensors
\[
N^{(1)}_{\mathrm{seed}},N^{(2)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}
\]
such that
\[
\langle T^{(1)},N^{(1)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\rangle\neq 0,
\qquad
\langle T^{(2)},N^{(2)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\rangle\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Class II coefficient language.}
In the shell-adapted coefficient form, compute
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}},\qquad B_{\mathrm{eff}},\qquad C_{\mathrm{eff}},
\]
or equivalently
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta.
\]
Completion requires
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\neq 0,
\qquad
(B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}})\neq (0,0),
\]
equivalently
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\]
equivalently
\[
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

\paragraph{Deliverable.}
Produce either:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a projection calculation showing
\[
P_V T^{(1)}\neq 0,\qquad P_V T^{(2)}\neq 0,
\]
or
\item explicit admissible seed tensors producing nonzero overlaps.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Pass/fail meaning.}
If this task fails, no local shell Weyl/Dirac block exists in the actual microscopic tensor space, and the Class II route is not microscopically realized.

\subsection*{2. Task II: opposite-valley matching}

\paragraph{Goal.}
Upgrade two Weyl valleys into one local Dirac pair.

\paragraph{Exact criterion.}
At \(+G_*\) and \(-G_*\), compute the shell witness triples
\[
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+),
\qquad
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-).
\]
Completion requires
\[
W_\parallel^-\!=W_\parallel^+,\qquad
W_I^-\!=W_I^+,\qquad
W_J^-\!=W_J^+.
\]

\paragraph{Equivalent coefficient form.}
In coefficient language:
\[
A^-=A^+,\qquad B^-=B^+,\qquad C^-=C^+.
\]

\paragraph{Deliverable.}
Produce the explicit matched transformation law under the opposite-valley map and verify equality of the two triples.

\paragraph{Pass/fail meaning.}
If this task fails, one may still have local Weyl sectors, but not a genuine doubled local Dirac block.

\subsection*{3. Task III: zero constant mixing}

\paragraph{Goal.}
Prove
\[
V(0)=0.
\]

\paragraph{Exact criterion.}
Let
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R,
\]
where \(\mathcal H_D\) is the isolated doubled shell block and \(\mathcal H_R\) is the remote sector.
Decompose both under the residual symmetry \(H_*\).
Completion requires
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

\paragraph{Operational version.}
Decompose
\[
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a.
\]
For each remote sector \(K_a\), verify that it differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label:
\[
\pm G_*,
\quad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\quad
\text{enriched internal doublet},
\quad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{other conserved microscopic labels}.
\]
If every \(K_a\) fails at least one matching condition, then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
\quad\forall a,
\]
hence
\[
V(0)=0.
\]

\paragraph{Deliverable.}
A table of remote sectors \(K_a\) with a mismatch flag for each shell-relevant label.

\paragraph{Pass/fail meaning.}
If even one remote sector shares all shell-relevant labels with \(\mathcal H_D\), constant mixing is not excluded and the local Dirac node is not yet stable.

\subsection*{4. Task IV: remote spectral gap}

\paragraph{Goal.}
Prove the existence of
\[
\Delta>0
\]
such that
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing
\]
for all sufficiently small \(p\).

\paragraph{Important honesty condition.}
This is an independent spectral input.
It does \emph{not} follow from
\[
\det M\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Minimal finite test.}
Choose a first nontrivial truncated remote basis
\[
\mathcal B_R^{(N)}=\{\text{remote shell/Bloch basis states up to order }N\}.
\]
Construct the truncated remote matrix
\[
H_R^{(N)}(p).
\]
Define
\[
\Delta_N:=\inf_{|p|\le p_*}\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(N)}(p))\bigr).
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(\Delta_N\le 0\), the truncation does not support a remote gap;
\item if \(\Delta_N>0\), estimate the truncation error
\[
\|H_R-H_R^{(N)}\|\le \varepsilon_N.
\]
If
\[
\varepsilon_N<\Delta_N,
\]
then
\[
\Delta\ge \Delta_N-\varepsilon_N>0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Alternative perturbative route.}
If one already has an unperturbed gapped realization
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap(-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing,
\]
and the Class II correction obeys
\[
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|<\Delta_0,
\]
then
\[
\Delta\ge \Delta_0-\|\delta H_R\|>0.
\]

\paragraph{Deliverable.}
Either:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a finite Bloch/shell-truncated spectral computation with a rigorous lower bound, or
\item a perturbative gap-stability estimate from an already-gapped realization.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Pass/fail meaning.}
If this task fails, the low-energy block may mix resonantly with remote states and spectral isolation is not established.

\subsection*{5. Task V: mass protection}

\paragraph{Goal.}
Exclude all symmetry-allowed constant Dirac masses.

\paragraph{Exact mass space.}
For the doubled local Dirac block
\[
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i),
\]
the full constant Dirac-mass space is
\[
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
\]

\paragraph{Exact completion criterion.}
Let
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}
=
\{K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4):U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K\ \forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}\}
\]
be the residual-symmetry allowed constant algebra.
Completion requires
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\]

\paragraph{Sufficient mechanism.}
It is sufficient to prove exact residual valley symmetry
\[
U(1)_V
\quad\text{or already}\quad
\mathbb Z_2^V.
\]
Indeed, with
\[
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
the two mass generators transform nontrivially and are forbidden.

\paragraph{Deliverable.}
Either:
\begin{enumerate}
\item an explicit basis computation of \(A_{\mathrm{res}}\) and proof that it excludes
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\qquad \tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
or
\item a proof that exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) or \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) survives.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Pass/fail meaning.}
If this task fails, the doubled Dirac block is not protected against a constant symmetry-preserving mass.

\subsection*{6. Final assembly step}

Once Tasks I--V are passed, define
\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item Task I gives the local Weyl block;
\item Task II gives opposite-valley doubling into a local Dirac block;
\item Task III gives
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad \|V(p)\|\le c|p|;
\]
\item Task IV gives
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing;
\]
\item Task V forbids any constant Dirac mass.
\end{enumerate}
Hence the Schur-complement effective Hamiltonian satisfies
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(Mp)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
\qquad
\det M\neq 0,
\]
so the full microscopic Class II realization contains a stable spectrally isolated massless Dirac cone.

\subsection*{7. Optimal execution order}

The optimal practical order is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Task I } \to \text{ Task II } \to \text{ Task III } \to \text{ Task IV } \to \text{ Task V}.
}
\]

This order is optimal because Tasks I and II first establish that the local shell Dirac block actually exists, while Tasks III--V then certify its stability inside the full theory.

\subsection*{8. Honest final status}

What is already theorem-level closed is the implication
\[
\text{Tasks I--V completed}
\Longrightarrow
\text{stable spectrally isolated massless local Dirac cone}.
\]

What remains open microscopically is only whether the actual final TECT/Class II linearization passes each of Tasks I--V.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Master Verification Checklist for the actual microscopic Class II realization}
}
\]

\[
\textbf{Task I: shell witness nonvanishing}

P_VT^{(1)}\neq 0,\qquad P_VT^{(2)}\neq 0,

equivalently

g_c\neq 0,\qquad (g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)=(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+),
\]
equivalently

A^-=A^+,\qquad B^-=B^+,\qquad C^-=C^+.
\]

\Longrightarrow

\]

\[

\qquad (\Delta>0).

This must be checked independently by a finite Bloch/shell-truncated spectral calculation
or by perturbative stability from an already-gapped realization.

and completion requires

\[

\quad\text{or}\quad

so the full microscopic TECT/Class II realization contains a
