\section*{Task I: Actual execution form of the witness-nonvanishing test}

\subsection*{A. Exact finite-dimensional formulation}

Let
\[
W=\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the ambient finite-dimensional tensor space, and let
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset W
\]
be the actual symmetry-allowed microscopic tensor space surviving the linearization around the chosen TECT defect background.

Fix the shell data:
\[
G_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\hat n:=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}\ \text{orthonormal}.
\]

For each required reduced channel \(\alpha\), define the shell target covector
\[
T^{(\alpha)}_{ija}=e_{\alpha i}G_{*j}u^{(\alpha)}_a,
\]
and the corresponding linear witness functional
\[
L_\alpha(N):=\langle T^{(\alpha)},N\rangle.
\]

Then the exact criterion is
\[
L_\alpha|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\equiv 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0,
\]
where \(P_V:W\to V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\) is the orthogonal projector.

Hence Task I is completed once one proves
\[
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\]
for the longitudinal channel and for the transverse channel(s).

\subsection*{B. Basis-level operational test}

Choose any basis
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d
\]
of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\), where \(d=\dim V_{\mathrm{TECT}}<\infty\).
Write
\[
N=\sum_{A=1}^d x_A E_A.
\]
Then
\[
L_\alpha(N)=\sum_{A=1}^d x_A\,\ell_{\alpha A},
\qquad
\ell_{\alpha A}:=\langle T^{(\alpha)},E_A\rangle.
\]

Therefore:
\[
P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\ell_{\alpha A}=0\ \ \forall A,
\]
while
\[
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\exists A\ \text{such that}\ \ell_{\alpha A}\neq 0.
\]

So the actual computation is finite:
\[
\text{compute the overlap vector } \ell_\alpha=(\ell_{\alpha1},\dots,\ell_{\alpha d}).
\]
If it is not identically zero, the channel survives generically.

\subsection*{C. Seed criterion}

A stronger and faster sufficient test is:

if there exists a single admissible tensor
\[
N^{(\alpha)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}
\]
such that
\[
\langle T^{(\alpha)},N^{(\alpha)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\rangle\neq 0,
\]
then automatically
\[
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0.
\]

Thus Task I can be closed either by a full projector computation or by constructing one explicit allowed seed tensor per required channel.

\subsection*{D. Canonical Class II seed directions}

Inside the minimal Class II parametrization, the induced tensor is organized by
\[
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\]
together with the shell-adapted coefficients
\[
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
\[
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
\[
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\]

This immediately gives three canonical seed directions:

\paragraph{Longitudinal seed}
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad c_I=c_J=0.
\]
This produces
\[
g_c\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Even transverse seed}
\[
c_\parallel=0,\qquad c_I\neq 0,\qquad c_J=0.
\]
This produces
\[
g_E\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Odd transverse seed}
\[
c_\parallel=0,\qquad c_I=0,\qquad c_J\neq 0.
\]
This produces
\[
g_O\neq 0.
\]

Hence, inside the minimal Class II truncation,
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]

Therefore the witness problem is already reduced to the question whether these seed directions are actually present in the true symmetry-allowed tensor space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).

\subsection*{E. Immediate consequence for Task I}

Suppose the actual microscopic tensor space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\) contains:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one admissible longitudinal seed with \(c_\parallel\neq 0\),
\item one admissible transverse seed with \((c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0)\).
\end{enumerate}

Then
\[
g_c(N)\neq 0
\]
and
\[
(g_E(N),g_O(N))\neq (0,0)
\]
hold on an open dense full-measure subset of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).

Equivalently,
\[
\lambda_\parallel(N)\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha(N),\beta(N))\neq (0,0)
\]
generically on \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\), and the local \(S^2\) reduced symbol is nondegenerate.

\subsection*{F. Actual deliverable for the final microscopic model}

To close Task I in the actual final TECT realization, one must provide exactly one of the following:

\paragraph{Route 1: projector computation}
Construct a basis of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\) and compute
\[
\ell_{\parallel,A}=\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{I,A}=\langle T^{(I)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{J,A}=\langle T^{(J)},E_A\rangle.
\]
Then verify:
\[
(\ell_{\parallel,1},\dots,\ell_{\parallel,d})\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
(\ell_{I,1},\dots,\ell_{I,d},\ell_{J,1},\dots,\ell_{J,d})\not\equiv 0.
\]

\paragraph{Route 2: explicit seed construction}
Produce explicit admissible tensors
\[
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)},\qquad N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp)}
\]
in the final microscopic symmetry class such that
\[
\langle T^{(\parallel)},N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)}\rangle\neq 0,
\qquad
\det T_\perp\bigl(N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp)}\bigr)\neq 0.
\]

\subsection*{G. Honest final status}

Thus the mathematically honest conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Task I is completely closed inside the minimal Class II truncation.}
}
\]

What is still open is only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{whether the actual full TECT microscopic symmetry-allowed space }V_{\mathrm{TECT}}
\text{ really contains those Class II seed directions.}
}
\]

So the remaining work is not conceptual; it is an explicit finite tensor-space inclusion test.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Task I is a finite tensor-space test.}
}
\]

Let
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the actual symmetry-allowed microscopic tensor space.

For each required shell channel \(\alpha\), define
\[
T^{(\alpha)}_{ija}=e_{\alpha i}G_{*j}u^{(\alpha)}_a,
\qquad
L_\alpha(N)=\langle T^{(\alpha)},N\rangle.
\]

Then:
\[
\boxed{
L_\alpha|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\equiv 0
\Longleftrightarrow
P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0.
}
\]

Hence Task I is complete once
\[
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\]
is proved for the required channels.

A sufficient condition is the existence of one explicit admissible seed
\[
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\alpha)}\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}
\]
such that
\[
\langle T^{(\alpha)},N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\alpha)}\rangle\neq 0.
\]

Inside the minimal Class II parametrization,
\[
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
\[
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
and therefore
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]

So the canonical seed directions are:
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0 \Rightarrow g_c\neq 0,
\]
\[
c_I\neq 0 \Rightarrow g_E\neq 0,
\]
\[
c_J\neq 0 \Rightarrow g_O\neq 0.
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the minimal Class II truncation, the witness problem is already closed.}
}
\]

The only remaining Task I question is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the actual full TECT microscopic space }V_{\mathrm{TECT}}
\text{ really contain those Class II seed directions?}
}
\]

If yes, then generically
\[
g_c\neq 0,\qquad (g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0),
\]
hence the local \(S^2\) symbol is nondegenerate.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Task I in the explicit Class II basis \texorpdfstring{$\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}$}{B}}

\subsection*{1. Ambient tensor space and witness functionals}

Let
\[
W=\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{int}},
\qquad
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset W
\]
be the actual symmetry-allowed microscopic tensor space around the chosen TECT defect background.

Fix the shell frame
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}\ \text{orthonormal}.
\]

Define the shell witness covectors
\[
T^{(\parallel)}_{ijb}:=\hat n_i G_{*j}\,\delta^{b3},
\]
\[
T^{(I)}_{ijb}:=\hat n_i e_{1j}\,\delta^{b1}+\hat n_i e_{2j}\,\delta^{b2},
\]
\[
T^{(J)}_{ijb}:=-\hat n_i e_{2j}\,\delta^{b1}+\hat n_i e_{1j}\,\delta^{b2}.
\]
The corresponding linear functionals are
\[
L_\parallel(N)=\langle T^{(\parallel)},N\rangle,
\qquad
L_I(N)=\langle T^{(I)},N\rangle,
\qquad
L_J(N)=\langle T^{(J)},N\rangle.
\]

These are precisely the shell witness maps whose nonvanishing decides whether the longitudinal
and transverse reduced channels survive. The exact dichotomy is
\[
L_\alpha|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\equiv 0
\Longleftrightarrow
P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0,
\]
and if \(P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0\), then the channel is generically nonzero on an open dense full-measure subset of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).

\subsection*{2. Canonical Class II basis tensors}

Inside the minimal Class II ansatz, choose the three canonical shell-adapted basis tensors
\[
B_\parallel:\quad
(B_\parallel)^3_{ij}=\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
(B_\parallel)^1_{ij}=(B_\parallel)^2_{ij}=0,
\]
\[
B_I:\quad
(B_I)^1_{ij}=\hat n_i e_{1j},
\qquad
(B_I)^2_{ij}=\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
(B_I)^3_{ij}=0,
\]
\[
B_J:\quad
(B_J)^1_{ij}=-\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
(B_J)^2_{ij}=\hat n_i e_{1j},
\qquad
(B_J)^3_{ij}=0.
\]

Equivalently, an arbitrary tensor in the explicit seed subspace is
\[
N=c_\parallel B_\parallel + c_I B_I + c_J B_J.
\]

This is exactly the shell-relevant image of the minimal Class II seed parametrization
\[
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
\[
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}.
\]

\subsection*{3. Overlap matrix}

Define the \(3\times 3\) witness matrix
\[
\mathcal M_{\alpha A}:=\langle T^{(\alpha)},B_A\rangle,
\qquad
\alpha\in\{\parallel,I,J\},
\quad
A\in\{\parallel,I,J\}.
\]

With the canonical inner product on \(W\), and after normalizing the shell frame,
one gets the orthogonality pattern
\[
\langle T^{(\parallel)},B_I\rangle=0,
\qquad
\langle T^{(\parallel)},B_J\rangle=0,
\]
\[
\langle T^{(I)},B_\parallel\rangle=0,
\qquad
\langle T^{(J)},B_\parallel\rangle=0,
\]
\[
\langle T^{(I)},B_J\rangle=0,
\qquad
\langle T^{(J)},B_I\rangle=0,
\]
while
\[
\langle T^{(\parallel)},B_\parallel\rangle\neq 0,
\qquad
\langle T^{(I)},B_I\rangle\neq 0,
\qquad
\langle T^{(J)},B_J\rangle\neq 0.
\]

Hence in the canonical Class II basis,
\[
\mathcal M=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mu_\parallel & 0 & 0\\
0 & \mu_I & 0\\
0 & 0 & \mu_J
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\mu_\parallel\neq 0,\quad \mu_I\neq 0,\quad \mu_J\neq 0.
\]

Therefore for
\[
N=c_\parallel B_\parallel+c_I B_I+c_J B_J,
\]
the witnesses are exactly
\[
L_\parallel(N)=\mu_\parallel c_\parallel,
\qquad
L_I(N)=\mu_I c_I,
\qquad
L_J(N)=\mu_J c_J.
\]

So the reduced Class II coefficients satisfy
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]

\subsection*{4. Exact Task I completion criterion in this basis}

In this basis, Task I reduces to the explicit condition
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
\]

Equivalently,
\[
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

Equivalently, the reduced local \(S^2\) transport symbol
\[
A_1(p)=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\]
is nondegenerate if and only if
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]

\subsection*{5. Operational microscopic test}

Let
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d
\]
be a basis of the actual microscopic allowed space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).

To decide whether the explicit Class II seed subspace is really embedded in \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\), do the following:

\[
\text{(i) express each }B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\text{ in the basis }\{E_A\},
\]
or equivalently test whether
\[
B_\parallel,\ B_I,\ B_J\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}.
\]

If exact membership is unavailable, compute the projection coefficients
\[
\Pi_{A}^{(\parallel)}=\langle E_A,B_\parallel\rangle,
\qquad
\Pi_{A}^{(I)}=\langle E_A,B_I\rangle,
\qquad
\Pi_{A}^{(J)}=\langle E_A,B_J\rangle.
\]

Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(P_VB_\parallel\neq 0\), the longitudinal witness survives generically;
\item if \(P_VB_I\neq 0\) or \(P_VB_J\neq 0\), the transverse witness survives generically;
\item if both statements hold, then Task I is complete.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{6. Honest final status}

Thus the exact status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the explicit Class II seed space, Task I is completely closed.}
}
\]

What remains open is only the finite embedding question

\[
\boxed{
B_\parallel,\ B_I,\ B_J\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}} \ ? 
}
\]

or at least

\[
\boxed{
P_VB_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(P_VB_I,P_VB_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

This is the final actual microscopic form of Task I.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
B_\parallel:\ N^3_{ij}=\hat n_i\hat n_j,\qquad
B_I:\ (N^1_{ij},N^2_{ij})=(\hat n_i e_{1j},\hat n_i e_{2j}),\qquad
B_J:\ (N^1_{ij},N^2_{ij})=(-\hat n_i e_{2j},\hat n_i e_{1j})
}
\]

For
\[
N=c_\parallel B_\parallel+c_I B_I+c_J B_J,
\]
the witness matrix is diagonal in the canonical shell basis:
\[
\mathcal M_{\alpha A}=\langle T^{(\alpha)},B_A\rangle
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mu_\parallel & 0 & 0\\
0 & \mu_I & 0\\
0 & 0 & \mu_J
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\mu_\parallel,\mu_I,\mu_J\neq 0.
\]

Hence
\[
L_\parallel(N)=\mu_\parallel c_\parallel,
\qquad
L_I(N)=\mu_I c_I,
\qquad
L_J(N)=\mu_J c_J.
\]

Equivalently,
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]

Therefore Task I in this basis is exactly:
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the explicit Class II seed subspace, Task I is already closed.}
}
\]

The only remaining microscopic question is:
\[
\boxed{
B_\parallel,\ B_I,\ B_J \in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}
\ \text{ ?}
}
\]
or at least
\[
\boxed{
P_VB_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(P_VB_I,P_VB_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Task II: Opposite-valley matching table in the explicit Class II basis}

\subsection*{1. Positive and negative valley frames}

Fix the positive-valley shell point \(+G_*\) and the adapted orthonormal frame
\[
\hat n_+ := \frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_{1+},e_{2+},\hat n_+\}.
\]

For the opposite valley \(-G_*\), choose the matched opposite-valley frame
\begin{equation}
\hat n_-=-\hat n_+,
\qquad
e_{1-}=e_{1+},
\qquad
e_{2-}=-e_{2+},
\label{eq:matched_negative_frame_user}
\end{equation}
so that
\[
e_{1-}\times e_{2-}=\hat n_-.
\]

This is the canonical frame choice for comparing the two shell valleys.

\subsection*{2. Canonical basis tensors at the two valleys}

At the positive valley define
\begin{equation}
(B_\parallel^+)^3_{ij}=\hat n_{+i}\hat n_{+j},
\qquad
(B_\parallel^+)^1_{ij}=(B_\parallel^+)^2_{ij}=0,
\label{eq:Bpar_plus_user}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(B_I^+)^1_{ij}=\hat n_{+i}e_{1+\,j},
\qquad
(B_I^+)^2_{ij}=\hat n_{+i}e_{2+\,j},
\qquad
(B_I^+)^3_{ij}=0,
\label{eq:BI_plus_user}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(B_J^+)^1_{ij}=-\hat n_{+i}e_{2+\,j},
\qquad
(B_J^+)^2_{ij}=\hat n_{+i}e_{1+\,j},
\qquad
(B_J^+)^3_{ij}=0.
\label{eq:BJ_plus_user}
\end{equation}

At the negative valley define the analogous basis using the matched frame:
\begin{equation}
(B_\parallel^-)^3_{ij}=\hat n_{-i}\hat n_{-j},
\qquad
(B_\parallel^-)^1_{ij}=(B_\parallel^-)^2_{ij}=0,
\label{eq:Bpar_minus_user}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(B_I^-)^1_{ij}=\hat n_{-i}e_{1-\,j},
\qquad
(B_I^-)^2_{ij}=\hat n_{-i}e_{2-\,j},
\qquad
(B_I^-)^3_{ij}=0,
\label{eq:BI_minus_user}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(B_J^-)^1_{ij}=-\hat n_{-i}e_{2-\,j},
\qquad
(B_J^-)^2_{ij}=\hat n_{-i}e_{1-\,j},
\qquad
(B_J^-)^3_{ij}=0.
\label{eq:BJ_minus_user}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:matched_negative_frame_user}, one finds
\begin{equation}
B_\parallel^- = B_\parallel^+,
\label{eq:Bpar_match_user}
\end{equation}
because
\[
\hat n_- \hat n_- = (-\hat n_+)(-\hat n_+) = \hat n_+\hat n_+.
\]

For the transverse basis:
\begin{align}
(B_I^-)^1_{ij}
&=\hat n_{-i}e_{1-\,j}
=(-\hat n_{+i})e_{1+\,j}
=-(B_I^+)^1_{ij},
\\
(B_I^-)^2_{ij}
&=\hat n_{-i}e_{2-\,j}
=(-\hat n_{+i})(-e_{2+\,j})
=(B_I^+)^2_{ij},
\end{align}
and similarly
\begin{align}
(B_J^-)^1_{ij}
&=-\hat n_{-i}e_{2-\,j}
=-(-\hat n_{+i})(-e_{2+\,j})
=-(B_J^+)^1_{ij},
\\
(B_J^-)^2_{ij}
&=\hat n_{-i}e_{1-\,j}
=(-\hat n_{+i})e_{1+\,j}
=-(B_J^+)^2_{ij}.
\end{align}

So the raw component-level tensors do not match term-by-term naively.
What matters is the matched witness extraction in the valley-adapted frame.

\subsection*{3. Witness extraction formulas at each valley}

For any tensor \(N\) in the shell-relevant axial family,
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:axial_family_taskII_user}
\end{equation}
the witness functionals are
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}[N]
=
\hat n_i\hat n_j N^3_{ij},
\label{eq:Wpar_taskII_user}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W_I[N]
=
\frac12
\left(
e_{1j}\hat n_i N^1_{ij}
+
e_{2j}\hat n_i N^2_{ij}
\right),
\label{eq:WI_taskII_user}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W_J[N]
=
\frac12
\left(
e_{1j}\hat n_i N^2_{ij}
-
e_{2j}\hat n_i N^1_{ij}
\right).
\label{eq:WJ_taskII_user}
\end{equation}
These extract exactly
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}[N]=A,
\qquad
W_I[N]=B,
\qquad
W_J[N]=C.
\label{eq:witness_extract_exact_taskII_user}
\end{equation}

Therefore the opposite-valley matching problem reduces exactly to
\begin{equation}
A^-=A^+,
\qquad
B^-=B^+,
\qquad
C^-=C^+.
\label{eq:ABC_matching_taskII_user}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}^-=W_{\parallel}^+,
\qquad
W_I^-=W_I^+,
\qquad
W_J^-=W_J^+.
\label{eq:triple_matching_taskII_user}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Explicit matching table}

The practical Task II table is therefore:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{Valley} & W_{\parallel} & W_I & W_J\\
\hline
+G_* & A^+ & B^+ & C^+\\
-G_* & A^- & B^- & C^-\\
\hline
\text{Dirac matching condition} & A^-=A^+ & B^-=B^+ & C^-=C^+
\end{array}
\]

Equivalently, in the reduced Class II coefficient language,
\[
\lambda_\parallel^\pm=\kappa_*|G_*|A^\pm,
\qquad
\alpha^\pm=\kappa_*|G_*|B^\pm,
\qquad
\beta^\pm=\kappa_*|G_*|C^\pm,
\]
so the same table becomes
\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{Valley} & \lambda_\parallel & \alpha & \beta\\
\hline
+G_* & \lambda_\parallel^+ & \alpha^+ & \beta^+\\
-G_* & \lambda_\parallel^- & \alpha^- & \beta^-\\
\hline
\text{Dirac matching condition}
& \lambda_\parallel^-=\lambda_\parallel^+
& \alpha^-=\alpha^+
& \beta^-=\beta^+
\end{array}
\]

\subsection*{5. Consequence for the reduced Hamiltonians}

At the positive valley,
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel^+ p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha^+ (p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta^+ (-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:hplus_taskII_user}
\end{equation}

At the negative valley, in its own matched frame,
\begin{equation}
h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel^- p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha^- (p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta^- (-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:hminus_taskII_user}
\end{equation}

If the coefficient matching conditions hold,
\[
\lambda_\parallel^-=\lambda_\parallel^+,
\qquad
\alpha^-=\alpha^+,
\qquad
\beta^-=\beta^+,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)=-h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(-p).
\label{eq:pairing_taskII_user}
\end{equation}

Thus the doubled block
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
h_+(p) & 0\\
0 & h_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}
\label{eq:HD_taskII_user}
\end{equation}
takes the canonical opposite-valley Weyl-pair form, and is unitarily equivalent to a massless Dirac Hamiltonian.

\subsection*{6. Canonical Class II automatic matching}

In the canonical minimal Class II representative, the induced tensor corrections satisfy
\[
\delta A=-\mu c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\mu c_J.
\]
If the opposite-valley exchange acts evenly on the underlying Class II seed data, then the same coefficients appear at the negative valley:
\[
A^-=A^+,
\qquad
B^-=B^+,
\qquad
C^-=C^+.
\]
Hence
\[
W^-_{\parallel}=W^+_{\parallel},
\qquad
W^-_I=W^+_I,
\qquad
W^-_J=W^+_J,
\]
so Task II is automatically satisfied once the opposite shell pair exists and the canonical Class II data are even under the matched valley transformation.

\subsection*{7. Honest final status}

Therefore the mathematically honest conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Task II is completely reduced to a finite coefficient-matching table.}
}
\]

Moreover,

\[
\boxed{
\text{for the canonical minimal Class II representative, opposite-valley matching is automatic}
}
\]
provided:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\) exists, and
\item the Class II seed data are even under the matched opposite-valley transformation.
\end{enumerate}

What is still not proved from the full microscopic TECT equations is only whether those two hypotheses are indeed realized automatically in the actual final microscopic model.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\hat n_-=-\hat n_+,
\qquad
e_{1-}=e_{1+},
\qquad
e_{2-}=-e_{2+},
\qquad
e_{1-}\times e_{2-}=\hat n_-.
}
\]

For the shell-relevant axial family
\[
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
the witness extraction is exact:
\[
W_{\parallel}[N]=A,
\qquad
W_I[N]=B,
\qquad
W_J[N]=C.
\]

Therefore the opposite-valley matching problem is exactly

\[
\boxed{
(W^-_{\parallel},W^-_I,W^-_J)=(W^+_{\parallel},W^+_I,W^+_J)
}
\]
equivalently
\[
\boxed{
A^-=A^+,
\qquad
B^-=B^+,
\qquad
C^-=C^+.
}
\]

Equivalently, in reduced coefficient language,
\[
\lambda_\parallel^\pm=\kappa_*|G_*|A^\pm,
\qquad
\alpha^\pm=\kappa_*|G_*|B^\pm,
\qquad
\beta^\pm=\kappa_*|G_*|C^\pm,
\]
and Task II is

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^-=\lambda_\parallel^+,
\qquad
\alpha^-=\alpha^+,
\qquad
\beta^-=\beta^+.
}
\]

Then
\[
h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)= -\,h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(-p),
\]
so if both valleys are Weyl, the doubled block
\[
H_D(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
h_+(p) & 0\\
0 & h_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}
\]
is unitarily equivalent to a massless Dirac Hamiltonian.

For the canonical minimal Class II representative:
\[
\delta A=-\mu c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\mu c_J.
\]
Hence, if the opposite-valley exchange acts evenly on the seed data, then automatically
\[
A^-=A^+,\qquad B^-=B^+,\qquad C^-=C^+,
\]
so Task II is automatic.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Task II is therefore a finite coefficient-matching test, and it is already closed at the canonical Class II level.}
}
\]

What remains open microscopically is only:
\[
\boxed{
\text{whether the actual full TECT dynamics guarantees the existence of }\pm G_*
\text{ and the required exact opposite-valley symmetry.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Task III: Remote-sector mismatch table for proving \texorpdfstring{$V(0)=0$}{V(0)=0}}

\subsection*{1. Exact theorem-level statement}

Let the full microscopic Hilbert space decompose as
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R,
\qquad
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a,
\]
where
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
is the isolated shell-relevant doubled Dirac block and \(K_a\) are \(H_*\)-invariant remote sectors.

At the shell crossing \(p=0\),
\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(0) & V(0)\\
V(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
If \(H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)\) is \(H_*\)-equivariant and the splitting is \(H_*\)-invariant, then
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Therefore a sufficient exact criterion for zero constant mixing is
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]
Since
\[
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a,
\]
it is enough to verify
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
\qquad
\forall a.
\]

\subsection*{2. Honest form of the local carrier}

The ordinary cubic little groups
\[
\mathrm{Stab}(+\hat n)\cong C_{2v},
\qquad
\mathrm{Stab}(\{\pm \hat n\})\cong D_{2h}
\]
are abelian, so their ordinary complex irreducible representations are one-dimensional.
Hence the relevant local Dirac carrier should \emph{not} be described as an ordinary bare-cubic 2D irrep.

The correct shell-relevant local carrier is
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
where
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\) is the opposite-shell pair \(\pm G_*\),
\item \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\) is the enriched transverse/internal matching doublet.
\end{itemize}

Therefore the actual little-group mismatch test must be performed in terms of shell-relevant labels, not in terms of naive bare-cubic 2D irreps.

\subsection*{3. Shell-relevant label set}

For each remote sector \(K_a\), define the following label data:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Shell-pair label}:
does \(K_a\) belong to the selected opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\), or to a different shell orbit?

\item \textbf{Kinematic type}:
is \(K_a\) transverse/non-volumetric, or longitudinal/volumetric/mixed?

\item \textbf{Internal-doublet content}:
does \(K_a\) contain the same enriched transverse internal doublet \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\) as \(\mathcal H_D\)?

\item \textbf{Grading / parity / chirality}:
does \(K_a\) lie in the same grading/parity sector as the doubled shell block?

\item \textbf{Extra conserved microscopic labels}:
for example defect charge, worldvolume parity, exchange parity, or any further exact conserved label.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{4. Sectorwise mismatch criterion}

A remote sector \(K_a\) is excluded from constant mixing if it differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one of the above labels.
Formally:
\[
\text{if }K_a\text{ differs from }\mathcal H_D\text{ in at least one shell-relevant label, then }
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

Thus the operational zero-mixing theorem becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\forall a,\ \exists\ \text{at least one shell-relevant mismatch between }K_a\text{ and }\mathcal H_D
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

\subsection*{5. Remote-sector mismatch table}

The actual microscopic audit should be carried out using the following table:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c|c|c|c}
\text{sector }K_a
&
\pm G_*
&
\text{transverse?}
&
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\text{ present?}
&
\text{grading/parity/chirality}
&
\text{extra conserved label}
&
\text{verdict}
\\
\hline
K_1 & \text{same / different} & \text{yes / no} & \text{yes / no} & \text{same / different} & \text{same / different} & \text{exclude / dangerous}
\\
K_2 & \text{same / different} & \text{yes / no} & \text{yes / no} & \text{same / different} & \text{same / different} & \text{exclude / dangerous}
\\
\vdots & \vdots & \vdots & \vdots & \vdots & \vdots & \vdots
\end{array}
\]

The rule is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{``exclude'' if at least one column mismatches;}
\qquad
\text{``dangerous'' only if every column matches.}
}
\]

\subsection*{6. Standard exclusion subcases}

The following subcases are immediate:

\paragraph{Case A: different shell orbit}
If \(K_a\) is not supported on the selected opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\), then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

\paragraph{Case B: same shell but wrong kinematic type}
If \(K_a\) is longitudinal/volumetric while \(\mathcal H_D\) is transverse/non-volumetric, then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

\paragraph{Case C: same shell and transverse, but no matching internal doublet}
If \(K_a\) lacks the enriched internal matching doublet \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\), then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

\paragraph{Case D: wrong grading / parity / chirality}
If the grading or parity sector differs, then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

\paragraph{Case E: extra conserved label mismatch}
If any additional exact microscopic label differs, then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

\subsection*{7. Dangerous sectors}

A remote sector is genuinely dangerous only if it survives all five tests:

\[
\text{same shell pair } \pm G_*,
\quad
\text{same transverse character},
\quad
\text{same enriched internal doublet},
\quad
\text{same grading/parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{same extra conserved labels}.
\]

Only such a sector can contribute to
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)
\]
and hence possibly generate \(V(0)\neq 0\).

So the actual microscopic \(V(0)=0\) problem is sharply reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Find all dangerous sectors }K_a\text{ that match } \mathcal H_D \text{ in every shell-relevant label.}
}
\]

If none exist, then
\[
V(0)=0
\]
is proved.

\subsection*{8. Final practical checklist}

To complete Task III in the actual microscopic model, one must provide:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit decomposition
\[
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a;
\]

\item for each \(K_a\), the five shell-relevant labels;

\item the completed mismatch table;

\item a proof that every row has at least one mismatch.
\end{enumerate}

Once that is done,
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\]
follows immediately, and therefore
\[
V(0)=0.
\]

\subsection*{9. Honest final status}

Thus the theorem-level part is closed:
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
\]

What remains open microscopically is only:
\[
\boxed{
\text{identify the actual remote-sector content }K_a
\text{ and verify the shell-relevant mismatch row by row.}
}
\]

This is not a conceptual problem anymore.
It is a finite sector-classification audit.


\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(0) & V(0)\\
V(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
}
\]

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

The correct local Dirac carrier is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
}
\]
not a bare-cubic ordinary 2D irrep.

Decompose the remote space as
\[
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a.
\]

For each \(K_a\), check the five shell-relevant labels:

\[
\pm G_*,
\quad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\quad
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\text{ presence},
\quad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{extra conserved labels}.
\]

Then the operational criterion is:

\[
\boxed{
\forall a,\ K_a \text{ differs from } \mathcal H_D \text{ in at least one shell-relevant label}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
}
\]

and therefore

\[
\boxed{
\forall a,\ \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

The remote-sector mismatch table is:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c|c|c|c}
K_a
&
\pm G_*
&
\text{transverse?}
&
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\text{ present?}
&
\text{grading/parity/chirality}
&
\text{extra conserved label}
&
\text{verdict}
\\
\hline
K_1 & \cdots & \cdots & \cdots & \cdots & \cdots & \text{exclude / dangerous}
\\
K_2 & \cdots & \cdots & \cdots & \cdots & \cdots & \text{exclude / dangerous}
\\
\vdots & \vdots & \vdots & \vdots & \vdots & \vdots & \vdots
\end{array}
\]

Rule:
\[
\boxed{
\text{exclude if at least one mismatch exists;}
\qquad
\text{dangerous only if every label matches.}
}
\]

Thus Task III is no longer conceptual.
It is a finite sectorwise label-audit problem.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Task IV: Minimal truncated remote-gap lower-bound theorem}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

We now reduce the remote-gap problem to the first nontrivial finite truncation.
The objective is to replace the abstract condition
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing
\]
by an explicit finite-dimensional lower-bound inequality.

\subsection*{2. Minimal truncated Hilbert space}

Consider the shell-relevant minimal truncation
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\label{eq:Hfull_truncated_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\) is the local doubled Dirac carrier;
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}\) is the volumetric/longitudinal sector;
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}\) is the higher-shell sector not belonging to the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\);
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}\) is the same-shell but non-enriched sector;
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}\) contains modes with internal content not matching the selected shell doublet.
\end{itemize}

This is the smallest truncation in which all previously identified dangerous remote channels are explicitly present.

\subsection*{3. Block decomposition}

Write the truncated Hamiltonian as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V_{DR}(p)\\
V_{DR}(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Hfull_tr_block_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
with remote block
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p).
\label{eq:HR_split_TaskIV}
\end{equation}

By the Task III mismatch audit, we assume
\begin{equation}
V_{DR}(0)=0.
\label{eq:VDR0_zero_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
Hence the only remaining question is whether \(H_R(p)\) can approach zero spectrally.

\subsection*{4. Sector-center energies and remote-remote mixing norm}

Let the block-diagonal part \(D_R(p)\) have sector-center energies
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p).
\]
Define
\begin{equation}
\delta_0(p)
=
\min\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|
\},
\label{eq:delta0_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\eta_R(p):=\|R_R(p)\|.
\label{eq:etaR_TaskIV}
\end{equation}

Then for every \(\psi\in\mathcal H_R\),
\begin{equation}
\|H_R(p)\psi\|
=
\|(D_R(p)+R_R(p))\psi\|
\ge
\|D_R(p)\psi\|-\|R_R(p)\psi\|
\ge
(\delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p))\|\psi\|.
\label{eq:pointwise_bound_TaskIV}
\end{equation}

Therefore, if
\begin{equation}
\delta_0(p)>\eta_R(p),
\label{eq:pointwise_gap_condition_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta(p),\Delta(p))=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta(p)\ge \delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p)>0.
\label{eq:pointwise_gap_TaskIV}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Uniform gap on a neighborhood}

Fix
\[
N_\rho:=\{p:|p|\le \rho\}.
\]
Define
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\label{eq:uniform_quantities_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\label{eq:uniform_gap_condition_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho),
\label{eq:uniform_gap_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Delta_\rho:=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
\label{eq:Delta_rho_TaskIV}
\end{equation}

Thus the remote-gap problem in the minimal truncation is reduced to the explicit finite-dimensional inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:master_minimal_gap_condition_TaskIV}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Gershgorin alternative}

If \(H_R(p)\) is written in a finite basis with matrix elements \((H_R)_{ab}(p)\), define
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_a
\Bigl(
|(H_R)_{aa}(p)|
-
\sum_{b\neq a}|(H_R)_{ab}(p)|
\Bigr).
\label{eq:Gershgorin_gap_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0,
\label{eq:Gershgorin_positive_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
then \(H_R(p)\) has a uniform spectral gap on \(N_\rho\).

So there are two equivalent practical routes:
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0.
\]

\subsection*{7. Sectorwise lower bounds}

The next step is to estimate the individual diagonal sector gaps entering \(\delta_{0,\rho}\).

\paragraph{(a) Higher-shell sector.}
Assume radial shell separation
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
\inf_{Q\in\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}}
\bigl||Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr|
>0.
\label{eq:delta_shell_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
For a Brazovskii-type kernel
\begin{equation}
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2,
\label{eq:Brazovskii_kernel_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
a sufficient lower bound is
\begin{equation}
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2>|r_*|
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|>0.
\label{eq:high_shell_bound_TaskIV}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(b) Volumetric sector.}
If the locking mode has mass gap \(M_\sigma>0\), then
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma>0.
\label{eq:vol_bound_TaskIV}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(c) Wrong-internal sector.}
If the internal operator has spectral separation
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}
=
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
\operatorname{spec}(I|_{U_{\mathrm{wrong}}}),
\operatorname{spec}(I|_{U_D})
\bigr)>0,
\label{eq:mint_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}\ge m_{\mathrm{int}}>0.
\label{eq:wrong_int_bound_TaskIV}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(d) Same-shell non-enriched sector.}
This sector is model-specific.
Its contribution is encoded in the finite truncated diagonal energy
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p),
\]
so the required quantity is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|.
\label{eq:nonenr_bound_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
This is a finite eigenvalue computation in the chosen truncation.

\subsection*{8. Minimal explicit benchmark}

Combining the sectorwise bounds, define
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}
:=
\min\Bigl\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}
\Bigr\}.
\label{eq:delta0_bench_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
Then a sufficient explicit minimal-truncation gap criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:bench_gap_condition_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
Under this condition,
\begin{equation}
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}-\eta_{R,\rho}
>0.
\label{eq:bench_gap_positive_TaskIV}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{9. Honest correction of the route}

The shell determinant
\begin{equation}
\det M=A(B^2+C^2)
\label{eq:detM_not_gap_TaskIV}
\end{equation}
controls the nondegeneracy of the local Dirac symbol only.
It does \emph{not} prove
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R)\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing.
\]
Therefore any argument claiming
\[
\delta(\det M)>0
\Longrightarrow
\Delta>0
\]
must be discarded as non-rigorous.

The correct theorem-level route is exclusively spectral:
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0.
}
\]

\subsection*{10. Conclusion}

Thus Task IV is reduced to a finite minimal-truncation spectral audit:
\begin{enumerate}
\item compute or bound the four diagonal sector gaps;
\item bound the remote-remote mixing norm \(\eta_{R,\rho}\);
\item verify \(\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}\) or, equivalently, a Gershgorin lower bound.
\end{enumerate}

Once this is done,
\[
\Delta_\rho>0
\]
is proved on the neighborhood \(N_\rho\).

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
}
\]

\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V_{DR}(p)\\
V_{DR}(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p).
\]

Define
\[
\delta_0(p)
=
\min\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|
\},
\qquad
\eta_R(p)=\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

Then
\[
\|H_R(p)\psi\|
\ge
(\delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p))\|\psi\|.
\]

Hence, if
\[
\delta_0(p)>\eta_R(p),
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta(p),\Delta(p))=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta(p)\ge \delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p)>0.
\]

On
\[
N_\rho=\{p:|p|\le \rho\},
\]
define
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\]
If
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

A Gershgorin alternative is
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_a
\Bigl(
|(H_R)_{aa}(p)|-\sum_{b\neq a}|(H_R)_{ab}(p)|
\Bigr)>0.
\]

Sectorwise sufficient lower bounds are:

\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|>0,
\]
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma>0,
\]
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}\ge m_{\mathrm{int}}>0,
\]
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|.
\]

Therefore a sufficient explicit benchmark is
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}
:=
\min\Bigl\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}
\Bigr\},
\]
with condition
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]

This proves
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho>0
}
\]
in the minimal truncation.

Important honesty clause:
\[
\boxed{
\det M=A(B^2+C^2)
\text{ does not prove } \Delta>0.
}
\]
The correct route is purely spectral:
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0.
}
\]
