\section*{Task IV sectorwise benchmark table}

\subsection*{A. Master spectral condition}

On the minimal truncation
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\]
write
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\]
with
\[
\delta_0(p)
=
\min\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|
\},
\qquad
\eta_R(p)=\|R_R(p)\|.
\]
On a neighborhood
\[
N_\rho:=\{p:|p|\le \rho\},
\]
define
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}:=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\]
Then the uniform remote-gap criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho:=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

Equivalently, in a fixed basis one may use the Gershgorin bound
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_a
\Bigl(
|(H_R)_{aa}(p)|-\sum_{b\neq a}|(H_R)_{ab}(p)|
\Bigr)>0.
\]

\subsection*{B. Sectorwise benchmark table}

We now isolate the diagonal benchmark for each remote sector.

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c|c}
\text{sector}
&
\text{label mismatch source}
&
\text{benchmark quantity}
&
\text{sufficient lower bound}
&
\text{status}
\\
\hline
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
&
\text{volumetric / longitudinal}
&
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}
&
\inf_{|p|\le \rho} |\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|
\ \text{or}\ c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma
&
\text{model-dependent but structurally natural}
\\
\hline
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
&
\text{different shell orbit}
&
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)}
&
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|
&
\text{explicit if shell separation is known}
\\
\hline
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
&
\text{same shell, no enriched doublet}
&
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}
&
\inf_{|p|\le \rho} |\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|
&
\text{must be computed in truncation}
\\
\hline
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
&
\text{wrong internal irrep}
&
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}
&
m_{\mathrm{int}}
:=
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
\operatorname{spec}(I|_{U_{\mathrm{wrong}}}),
\operatorname{spec}(I|_{U_D})
\bigr)
&
\text{explicit if internal spectrum is known}
\end{array}
\]

\subsection*{C. Volumetric sector benchmark}

The volumetric sector is structurally separated from the local Dirac carrier because it is longitudinal/volumetric rather than transverse.
Its spectral lower bound should be measured by
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|.
\]
If the volumetric locking mode \(\sigma\) is heavy with gap \(M_\sigma>0\), then a natural sufficient benchmark is
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma>0
\]
for some model-dependent \(c_{\mathrm{vol}}>0\).

This is physically justified by the volumetric-locking mechanism: the heavy scalar \(\sigma\) stiffens the longitudinal sector while leaving the transverse modes light.

\subsection*{D. Higher-shell benchmark}

For the higher-shell sector, the natural diagonal separation comes from radial shell mismatch.
If
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
\inf_{Q\in\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}}
\bigl||Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr|>0,
\]
and the quadratic kernel is of Brazovskii type
\[
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2,
\]
then a sufficient lower bound is
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|.
\]
Hence a positive benchmark follows if
\[
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2>|r_*|.
\]

\subsection*{E. Wrong-internal benchmark}

For the wrong-internal sector, the natural diagonal separation comes from the internal operator itself.
Let
\[
U_D
\]
be the selected shell-relevant internal doublet space and
\[
U_{\mathrm{wrong}}
\]
the internal space carried by the wrong-internal sector.
Define the internal spectral distance
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}
:=
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
\operatorname{spec}(I|_{U_{\mathrm{wrong}}}),
\operatorname{spec}(I|_{U_D})
\bigr).
\]
Then
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
m_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
is a natural sufficient bound, provided the internal splitting remains stable on \(N_\rho\).

\subsection*{F. Same-shell non-enriched benchmark}

This is the only sector for which no universal symbolic lower bound is currently available.
The correct definition is simply
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|.
\]
So this quantity must be extracted by an actual finite truncated eigenvalue computation.

Honest status:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the non-enriched same-shell sector is the least automatic benchmark and must be computed explicitly.}
}
\]

\subsection*{G. Combined benchmark}

Define
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}
:=
\min\Bigl\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}
\Bigr\}.
\]
Then the sufficient explicit remote-gap criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]
Under this condition,
\[
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}-\eta_{R,\rho}
>0.
\]

\subsection*{H. Off-diagonal mixing budget}

The remaining quantity is
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]
This must be bounded from the remote-remote off-diagonal couplings:
\[
R_{\mathrm{vol,high}},
\quad
R_{\mathrm{vol,non\text{-}enr}},
\quad
R_{\mathrm{high,wrong\text{-}int}},
\quad \ldots
\]
A sufficient norm budget is any estimate of the form
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\neq b}\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|
\]
or, basiswise,
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\max_a \sum_{b\neq a}|(H_R)_{ab}(p)|.
\]
The latter is exactly the Gershgorin route.

\subsection*{I. Important honesty clause}

The quantity
\[
\det M=A(B^2+C^2)
\]
controls only the nondegeneracy of the local shell Dirac symbol.
It does not imply any lower bound on the remote spectrum.
Hence the route
\[
\delta(\det M)>0 \Longrightarrow \Delta>0
\]
must be rejected as non-rigorous.

The correct route is only:
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0.
}
\]

\subsection*{J. Final execution list}

To actually close Task IV, one must provide:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a bound or explicit value for \(\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}\);
\item a shell-separation estimate for \(\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)}\);
\item a truncated eigenvalue computation for \(\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}\);
\item an internal spectral-separation estimate for \(\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}\);
\item a bound on \(\eta_{R,\rho}\).
\end{enumerate}
Once these are in hand, the inequality
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\]
completes Task IV.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Task IV reduces to one finite inequality}
\qquad
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]

Define
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}
:=
\min\Bigl\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}
\Bigr\},
\]
with sectorwise benchmarks

\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|
\quad
\text{or a heavy-locking bound } \Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,
\]

\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|,
\qquad
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
\inf_{Q\in\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}}
\bigl||Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr|,
\]

\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,
\]

\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
m_{\mathrm{int}}
:=
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
\operatorname{spec}(I|_{U_{\mathrm{wrong}}}),
\operatorname{spec}(I|_{U_D})
\bigr).
\]

The off-diagonal remote-remote budget is
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

Equivalent Gershgorin route:
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_a
\Bigl(
|(H_R)_{aa}(p)|-\sum_{b\neq a}|(H_R)_{ab}(p)|
\Bigr)>0.
\]

Honest correction:
\[
\boxed{
\det M=A(B^2+C^2)
\text{ does not prove } \Delta>0.
}
\]

Therefore the actual execution list is:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)},
\quad
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)},
\quad
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)},
\quad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)},
\quad
\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]

Once these five quantities are bounded, Task IV is complete.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Explicit lower-bound lemmas for the first two remote-gap benchmarks}

\subsection*{A. Higher-shell lower-bound lemma}

\paragraph{Setup.}
Let the selected shell radius be
\[
q_*:=|G_*|.
\]
Let \(\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}\) denote the set of reciprocal modes belonging to shell orbits different from the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\).
Define the shell-separation parameter
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}
:=
\inf_{Q\in\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}}
\bigl||Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr|.
\label{eq:delta_shell_explicit_user}
\end{equation}

Assume the quadratic diagonal kernel on the remote sector is of Brazovskii type:
\begin{equation}
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2,
\qquad
K>0.
\label{eq:Brazovskii_high_user}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Lemma (higher-shell explicit bound).}
For every \(Q\in\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}\),
\begin{equation}
|\Lambda(Q)|
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|.
\label{eq:Lambda_high_bound_user}
\end{equation}
Hence the diagonal benchmark for the higher-shell sector satisfies
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|.
\label{eq:Delta_high_general_user}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\begin{equation}
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2>|r_*|,
\label{eq:Delta_high_positive_condition_user}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}>0.
\label{eq:Delta_high_positive_user}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Proof.}
By definition of \(\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}\),
\[
(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2\ge \delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2
\qquad
\forall Q\in\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}.
\]
Therefore
\[
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2
\]
satisfies
\[
\Lambda(Q)\ge -|r_*|+K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2.
\]
Hence
\[
|\Lambda(Q)|\ge K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|.
\]
Taking the infimum over the higher-shell sector yields \eqref{eq:Delta_high_general_user}.
\qed

\paragraph{BCC specialization.}
In the explicit BCC reciprocal arithmetic adopted in the current TECT shell normalization,
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=2.
\label{eq:BCC_delta_shell_user}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|
=
4K-|r_*|.
\label{eq:BCC_high_explicit_user}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in the unit-shell normalization one may write
\[
\widehat\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}\ge K-|r_*|.
\]

\subsection*{B. Wrong-internal lower-bound lemma}

\paragraph{Setup.}
Let the shell-point internal carrier be the minimal complex three-dimensional space
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{int}}=\mathbb C^3=\mathbb C\hat n\oplus \hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}.
\label{eq:Uint_C3_user}
\end{equation}
Assume effective transverse \(SO(2)\) acts on \(\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}\), so that the unperturbed internal operator \(I_0\) satisfies
\begin{equation}
I_0|_{\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}}=E_*\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
I_0\hat n=E_L\,\hat n.
\label{eq:I0_split_user}
\end{equation}
Then define
\begin{equation}
U_D:=\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C},
\qquad
U_{\mathrm{wrong}}:=\mathbb C\hat n.
\label{eq:UD_Uwrong_user}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Lemma (wrong-internal explicit bound).}
The unperturbed wrong-internal spectral distance is
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
\operatorname{spec}(I_0|_{U_{\mathrm{wrong}}}),
\operatorname{spec}(I_0|_{U_D})
\bigr)
=
|E_L-E_*|.
\label{eq:mint0_explicit_user}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
|E_L-E_*|.
\label{eq:Delta_wrongint_explicit_user}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\begin{equation}
E_L\neq E_*,
\label{eq:EL_not_Estar_user}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}>0.
\label{eq:Delta_wrongint_positive_user}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Proof.}
By \eqref{eq:I0_split_user},
\[
\operatorname{spec}(I_0|_{U_D})=\{E_*\},
\qquad
\operatorname{spec}(I_0|_{U_{\mathrm{wrong}}})=\{E_L\}.
\]
Therefore
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
\operatorname{dist}(\{E_L\},\{E_*\})
=
|E_L-E_*|.
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:mint0_explicit_user} and hence \eqref{eq:Delta_wrongint_explicit_user}.
\qed

\paragraph{Perturbative stability.}
Let
\begin{equation}
I=I_0+\delta I,
\qquad
Q=P_{U_{\mathrm{wrong}}}.
\label{eq:I_pert_user}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\|Q\,\delta I\,Q\|\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}},
\label{eq:eps_int_user}
\end{equation}
then the perturbed internal gap satisfies
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}
\ge
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}
=
|E_L-E_*|-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
\label{eq:mint_stable_user}
\end{equation}
Hence, if
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}<|E_L-E_*|,
\label{eq:eps_less_internal_gap_user}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}>0
\qquad\text{and hence}\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}>0.
\label{eq:wrongint_stable_positive_user}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{C. Combined two-sector benchmark}

Combining the two lemmas, the first two explicit remote-sector benchmarks are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}\ge K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|
}
\label{eq:boxed_high_user}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}\ge |E_L-E_*|
}
\label{eq:boxed_wrongint_user}
\end{equation}
(with the latter stable under bounded perturbations up to \(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}\)).

For the current BCC normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}\ge 4K-|r_*|,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}\ge |E_L-E_*|.
}
\label{eq:two_explicit_benchmarks_user}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{D. Honest status}

These two sectors are now the most explicit parts of the minimal remote-gap program.
What still remains model-specific is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the volumetric benchmark \(\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}\), which needs a heavy-locking input \(M_\sigma\);
\item the same-shell non-enriched benchmark \(\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}\), which requires an actual finite truncated eigenvalue computation;
\item the remote-remote mixing budget \(\eta_{R,\rho}\).
\end{enumerate}

Thus the first two remote-gap entries are reduced to explicit scalar inequalities, while the latter three still require direct microscopic input.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{First explicit remote-gap benchmarks}
}
\]

\[
\textbf{Higher-shell sector:}
\]
Let
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
\inf_{Q\in\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}}
\bigl||Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr|>0,
\]
and assume
\[
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2,
\qquad
K>0.
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|.
}
\]
For the current BCC reciprocal arithmetic,
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=2,
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}\ge 4K-|r_*|.
}
\]

\[
\textbf{Wrong-internal sector:}
\]
In the minimal shell-point carrier
\[
U_{\mathrm{int}}=\mathbb C^3=\mathbb C\hat n\oplus \hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C},
\]
assume
\[
I_0|_{\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}}=E_*\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
I_0\hat n=E_L\,\hat n.
\]
Then
\[
U_D=\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C},
\qquad
U_{\mathrm{wrong}}=\mathbb C\hat n,
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
|E_L-E_*|.
}
\]

Under bounded perturbation
\[
I=I_0+\delta I,
\qquad
\|Q\delta I Q\|\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
the gap is stable:
\[
\boxed{
m_{\mathrm{int}}
\ge
|E_L-E_*|-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
}
\]

Hence the first two explicit minimal-truncation benchmarks are
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}\ge 4K-|r_*|,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}\ge |E_L-E_*|.
}
\]

Honest status:
\[
\boxed{
\text{these two sectors are structurally the easiest parts of Task IV.}
}
\]
What still remains model-specific is
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)},
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)},
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Shell-point longitudinal--transverse splitting theorem}

\subsection*{1. Effective shell-point operator after integrating out the heavy volumetric mode}

After integrating out the heavy volumetric mode \(\sigma\), the effective quadratic operator on the displacement sector takes the split form
\begin{equation}
D^{\mathrm{eff}}_{ij}(k)
=
\left[
(\lambda+2\mu)k^2
+
\frac{g^2k^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2k^2}
\right]P^L_{ij}
+
\mu k^2 P^T_{ij},
\label{eq:Deff_split_user_final}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
P_L=\hat n\hat n^\dagger,
\qquad
P_T=\mathbf 1_3-P_L,
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
q_*:=|G_*|.
\label{eq:PLPT_user_final}
\end{equation}

Evaluating at the selected shell point \(k=G_*\), the shell-point operator becomes
\begin{equation}
H_0
=
E_L\,P_L
+
E_*\,P_T,
\label{eq:H0_PLPT_user_final}
\end{equation}
with transverse and longitudinal energies
\begin{equation}
E_*(G_*)=\mu q_*^2,
\label{eq:Estar_user_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
E_L(G_*)
=
(\lambda+2\mu)q_*^2
+
\frac{g^2 q_*^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}.
\label{eq:EL_user_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore the shell-point internal space splits canonically as
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{int}}
=
\mathbb C^3
=
\mathbb C\hat n
\oplus
\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C},
\label{eq:Uint_split_user_final}
\end{equation}
where the longitudinal line \(\mathbb C\hat n\) carries energy \(E_L\), while the transverse plane \(\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}\) carries the protected energy \(E_*\mathbf 1_2\).

\subsection*{2. Exact longitudinal--transverse splitting}

Subtracting \eqref{eq:Estar_user_final} from \eqref{eq:EL_user_final}, one obtains
\begin{equation}
E_L-E_*
=
q_*^2
\left[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right].
\label{eq:EL_minus_Estar_user_final}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
H_0
=
E_*\,\mathbf 1_3
+
(E_L-E_*)P_L.
\label{eq:H0_shifted_split_user_final}
\end{equation}

This makes the wrong-internal spectral distance completely explicit:
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
\operatorname{spec}(H_0|_{\mathbb C\hat n}),
\operatorname{spec}(H_0|_{\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}})
\bigr)
=
|E_L-E_*|.
\label{eq:mint0_user_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore the wrong-internal diagonal benchmark is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|.
}
\label{eq:Delta_wrongint_explicit_user_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{3. Strong sufficient positivity condition}

A stronger sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
>0.
\label{eq:strong_positive_condition_user_final}
\end{equation}
Under \eqref{eq:strong_positive_condition_user_final},
\begin{equation}
E_L>E_*,
\qquad
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}>0.
\label{eq:EL_greater_Estar_user_final}
\end{equation}

Thus the wrong-internal sector is spectrally separated from the shell-relevant transverse doublet.

\subsection*{4. Perturbative stability}

Let the shell-point operator be perturbed:
\begin{equation}
H=H_0+\delta H,
\qquad
Q=P_L.
\label{eq:Hpert_user_final}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\|Q\,\delta H\,Q\|\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}},
\label{eq:epsint_user_final}
\end{equation}
then the wrong-internal gap is stable:
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}
\ge
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
\label{eq:mint_stability_user_final}
\end{equation}
Hence, if
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}
<
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\label{eq:eps_condition_user_final}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}>0
\qquad\text{and thus}\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}>0.
\label{eq:wrongint_positive_stable_user_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Embedding into the Task IV benchmark}

The explicit diagonal benchmark of the remote sector may now be sharpened to
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:Delta_bench_explicit_user_final}
\end{equation}
Therefore the explicit spectral isolation criterion becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho>0.
}
\label{eq:master_explicit_gap_user_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Honest status}

At this stage, the wrong-internal entry is no longer abstract.
It has been reduced fully to the scalar shell-point splitting
\[
E_L-E_*
=
q_*^2
\left[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right].
\]
Thus among the diagonal remote-sector benchmarks, the wrong-internal sector is now one of the most explicit.

What still remains model-dependent are:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the precise heavy volumetric benchmark \(c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma\),
\item the non-enriched same-shell benchmark,
\item the off-diagonal remote mixing budget \(\eta_{R,\rho}\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
E_*(G_*)=\mu q_*^2,
\qquad
E_L(G_*)
=
(\lambda+2\mu)q_*^2
+
\frac{g^2 q_*^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
E_L-E_*
=
q_*^2
\left[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right].
}
\]

Hence the wrong-internal shell-point gap is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
|E_L-E_*|
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|.
}
\]

A stronger sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
>0
\Longrightarrow
E_L>E_*
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}>0.
}
\]

Under bounded perturbation
\[
H=H_0+\delta H,
\qquad
\|Q\,\delta H\,Q\|\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
the gap is stable:
\[
\boxed{
m_{\mathrm{int}}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
}
\]

Thus the explicit remote-sector benchmark can be sharpened to
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\]

If
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho>0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Heavy-volumetric benchmark theorem}

\subsection*{A. Correct object of the volumetric benchmark}

The volumetric remote benchmark must refer to the genuinely heavy volumetric field \(\sigma\) itself,
not to the longitudinal--transverse splitting inside the shell-point displacement carrier.

These are two different remote-gap entries:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the \textbf{heavy volumetric sector}, carried by the gapped scalar field \(\sigma\);
\item the \textbf{wrong-internal sector}, measured by the shell-point splitting
\[
E_L-E_*
=
q_*^2
\left[
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right].
\]
\end{enumerate}

Thus \(\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}\) and \(\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}\) must not be identified.

\subsection*{B. Starting quadratic longitudinal--volumetric sector}

The relevant quadratic sector is
\begin{equation}
L_{L,\sigma}^{(2)}
=
\frac12 \rho |\dot u_L|^2
-\frac12 (\lambda+2\mu)k^2|u_L|^2
+\frac12 |\dot \sigma|^2
-\frac12 (M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 k^2)|\sigma|^2
+g\,\sigma(-k)\,ik\,u_L(k)+\mathrm{c.c.}
\label{eq:LLsigma_start_vol_user}
\end{equation}
The coupling is longitudinal-only, because it depends on
\[
k_i u_i = k\,u_L.
\]
Hence the transverse sector is decoupled from \(\sigma\) at quadratic order.

The heavy operator of the pure volumetric field is
\begin{equation}
K_\sigma
=
M_\sigma^2-c_\sigma^2\nabla^2+\partial_t^2,
\label{eq:Ksigma_vol_user}
\end{equation}
whose Fourier symbol is
\begin{equation}
K_\sigma(\omega,k)=M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 k^2-\omega^2.
\label{eq:Ksigma_symbol_vol_user}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{C. Frequency-scale heavy volumetric gap}

The pure \(\sigma\)-dispersion is
\begin{equation}
\omega_\sigma(k)=\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 k^2}.
\label{eq:omega_sigma_user}
\end{equation}

Now localize near the selected shell point:
\[
k=G_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\le \rho,
\qquad
q_*:=|G_*|.
\]
Assume
\begin{equation}
0<\rho<q_*.
\label{eq:rho_small_user}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
|k|=|G_*+p|\ge q_*-\rho.
\label{eq:k_lower_user}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\omega_\sigma(k)
\ge
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2}.
\label{eq:omega_lower_user}
\end{equation}

This gives the explicit heavy-volumetric frequency benchmark:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0),\mathrm{freq}}
\ge
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2}.
}
\label{eq:Delta_vol_freq_user}
\end{equation}

In particular,
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0),\mathrm{freq}}
\ge
M_\sigma.
\label{eq:Delta_vol_ge_M_user}
\end{equation}

Hence the earlier symbolic notation
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma
\]
may be made completely explicit at the frequency level by taking
\begin{equation}
c_{\mathrm{vol}}=1.
\label{eq:cvol_one_user}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{D. Quadratic-Hessian-scale benchmark}

If one works not with frequency eigenvalues but with the static quadratic kernel / Hessian normalization,
then the natural volumetric benchmark is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0),\mathrm{quad}}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\left(M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2|G_*+p|^2\right).
\label{eq:Delta_vol_quad_def_user}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:k_lower_user},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0),\mathrm{quad}}
\ge
M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2.
}
\label{eq:Delta_vol_quad_user}
\end{equation}

Thus the previous shorthand \(c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma\) is not wrong, but it hides the choice of spectral normalization:

\begin{itemize}
\item in \textbf{frequency} units, the benchmark is \(\ge M_\sigma\);
\item in \textbf{quadratic-kernel} units, the benchmark is \(\ge M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2\).
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{E. Relation to the effective longitudinal stiffening}

Integrating out the heavy \(\sigma\) field yields the effective longitudinal block
\begin{equation}
D_{ij}^{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
\left[
(\lambda+2\mu)k^2
+
\frac{g^2k^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 k^2}
\right]P^L_{ij}
+
\mu k^2 P^T_{ij}.
\label{eq:Deff_vol_user}
\end{equation}
This shows two things:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the heavy volumetric mode shifts only the longitudinal block;
\item the transverse block remains unchanged at leading order.
\end{enumerate}

At the shell point \(k=G_*\), this yields
\begin{equation}
E_*(G_*)=\mu q_*^2,
\qquad
E_L(G_*)
=
(\lambda+2\mu)q_*^2
+
\frac{g^2 q_*^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}.
\label{eq:EL_Estar_repeat_user}
\end{equation}
Hence the wrong-internal benchmark is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
|E_L-E_*|
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|.
\label{eq:wrongint_repeat_user}
\end{equation}

This must be kept distinct from \(\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}\).

\subsection*{F. EFT suppression and infrared closure}

Because \(K_\sigma^{-1}\) admits the derivative expansion
\begin{equation}
K_\sigma^{-1}
=
\frac{1}{M_\sigma^2}
\left[
1+\frac{c_\sigma^2\nabla^2-\partial_t^2}{M_\sigma^2}
+O\!\left(\frac{\partial^4}{M_\sigma^4}\right)
\right],
\label{eq:Ksigma_inv_user}
\end{equation}
integrating out \(\sigma\) induces only local higher-dimension operators suppressed by powers of \(M_\sigma^{-2}\).

At tree level, heavy-\(\sigma\)-mediated transverse amplitudes satisfy
\begin{equation}
\mathcal A_{TT\to TT}^{(\sigma)}
=
O\!\left(\frac{p^{2m}}{M_\sigma^2}\right)
+
O\!\left(\frac{p^{2m+2}}{M_\sigma^4}\right),
\qquad
m\ge 1,
\label{eq:ATT_sigma_user}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\mathcal A_{TT\to TT}^{(\sigma)}\to 0
\qquad
\text{as } \omega,|p|\to 0.
\label{eq:ATT_sigma_zero_user}
\end{equation}

Thus the heavy-volumetric sector contributes to the remote benchmark by a genuine positive gap,
while its induced corrections to the low-energy transverse sector are infrared-irrelevant.

\subsection*{G. Refined benchmark replacement}

The earlier coarse benchmark
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma
\]
may now be refined to either of the following fully explicit forms:

\paragraph{Frequency version}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2}.
}
\label{eq:Delta_vol_final_freq_user}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Quadratic-kernel version}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2.
}
\label{eq:Delta_vol_final_quad_user}
\end{equation}

Therefore the master remote-gap benchmark may be rewritten more explicitly as
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{ref}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\Biggr\},
\label{eq:bench_refined_vol_user}
\end{equation}
in frequency normalization,
or with the second slot replaced by \eqref{eq:Delta_vol_final_quad_user} in quadratic-kernel normalization.

\subsection*{H. Honest status}

At this point:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the higher-shell benchmark is explicit;
\item the wrong-internal benchmark is explicit;
\item the heavy-volumetric benchmark is explicit;
\item what remains non-automatic is mainly the same-shell non-enriched benchmark and the off-diagonal remote mixing budget.
\end{enumerate}

So the volumetric slot is no longer a vague symbol.
It is reduced to the actual heavy \(\sigma\)-dispersion near the selected shell.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Heavy volumetric benchmark}
}
\]

The quadratic longitudinal--volumetric sector is
\[
L_{L,\sigma}^{(2)}
=
\frac12 \rho |\dot u_L|^2
-\frac12 (\lambda+2\mu)k^2|u_L|^2
+\frac12 |\dot \sigma|^2
-\frac12 (M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 k^2)|\sigma|^2
+g\,\sigma(-k)\,ik\,u_L(k)+\mathrm{c.c.}
\]

Hence the pure heavy-\(\sigma\) dispersion is
\[
\omega_\sigma(k)=\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 k^2}.
\]

For
\[
k=G_*+p,\qquad |p|\le \rho<q_*:=|G_*|,
\]
one has
\[
|k|\ge q_*-\rho.
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0),\mathrm{freq}}
\ge
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2}
\ge
M_\sigma.
}
\]

In quadratic-kernel normalization, equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0),\mathrm{quad}}
\ge
M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2.
}
\]

Thus the previous shorthand
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma
\]
is refined as follows:

\[
\boxed{
\text{in frequency units, } c_{\mathrm{vol}}=1;
\qquad
\text{in quadratic-kernel units, use } M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2.
}
\]

Important distinction:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}
\neq
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}.
}
\]
The latter is the shell-point longitudinal--transverse splitting:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|.
\]

Therefore the refined explicit benchmark is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{ref}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\]

If
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{ref}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho>0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Minimal finite matrix theorem for the same-shell non-enriched sector}

\subsection*{A. Honest logical status}

Within the minimal truncation,
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\]
the sector
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\]
is defined as the \emph{same-shell but non-enriched sector}. It carries the shell label \(\pm G_*\) and transverse character, but it does \emph{not} carry the enriched internal doublet that defines the local Dirac block \(\mathcal H_D\). Therefore it is excluded from constant mixing at \(p=0\) by shell-relevant label mismatch, but its spectral distance from zero is \emph{not} automatic. It must be checked by a finite truncated eigenvalue computation. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6} :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\subsection*{B. Bloch reduction and shell projection}

Let \(H_{\phi_0}\) be the microscopic linearization around the periodic BCC background.
By Floquet--Bloch decomposition,
\[
H_{\phi_0}
\simeq
\int_{BZ}^{\oplus}
H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\,dk.
\]
Near the selected reciprocal shell point, one writes
\[
k=G_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\le \rho.
\]
The correct finite-dimensional object is then the shell-projected Bloch matrix
\[
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*} H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(G_*+p)\Pi_{S_*},
\]
where \(S_*\) is a finite set of near-resonant reciprocal harmonics. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

This shell-projected space is then split into
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}
=
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{rest}}^{(N)},
\]
where
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_D^{(N)}\) is the enriched shell doublet sector producing the local Dirac block,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}\) is the complementary same-shell sector that does not carry the enriched doublet,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{rest}}^{(N)}\) collects all additional truncated states.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{C. Definition of the non-enriched projected matrix}

Let
\[
P_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
:
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}
\to
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
\]
be the orthogonal projector.
Define the finite same-shell non-enriched block by
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
:=
P_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
\,H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)\,
P_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}.
\label{eq:H_nonenr_N_def}
\end{equation}

Then the finite truncation benchmark is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}
\!\Bigl(
0,\operatorname{spec}\bigl(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)\bigr)
\Bigr).
\label{eq:Delta_nonenr_N_def}
\end{equation}

This is the exact finite matrix quantity that must be computed.

\subsection*{D. Minimal finite matrix theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Minimal same-shell non-enriched benchmark theorem]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\) is the Bloch fiber of the periodic microscopic linearization;
\item \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)\) is a finite shell-projected truncation on a neighborhood \(|p|\le \rho\);
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}\) splits as
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{rest}}^{(N)};
\]
\item the same-shell non-enriched sector indeed carries no enriched internal doublet, so it is distinct from \(\mathcal H_D^{(N)}\) at the label level.
\end{enumerate}
Then the diagonal benchmark entering the remote-gap inequality is precisely
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}
\ \leadsto\
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}
\!\Bigl(
0,\operatorname{spec}\bigl(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)\bigr)
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:minimal_nonenr_theorem}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}>0,
\label{eq:positive_finite_nonenr}
\end{equation}
then the truncated same-shell non-enriched sector is spectrally separated from zero on \(N_\rho\).
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
This theorem does \emph{not} yet prove the exact infinite-dimensional same-shell non-enriched gap.
What it proves is that the microscopic problem is reduced to an explicit finite matrix spectral audit.

\subsection*{E. Gershgorin / coercivity version}

Choose any orthonormal basis \(\{v_a\}_{a=1}^{m_N}\) of \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}\).
Write the matrix
\[
\bigl(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)\bigr)_{ab}.
\]
Define the Gershgorin lower bound
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(G,N)}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\min_a
\left(
\left|
\bigl(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)\bigr)_{aa}
\right|
-
\sum_{b\neq a}
\left|
\bigl(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)\bigr)_{ab}
\right|
\right).
\label{eq:gersh_nonenr}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(G,N)}>0,
\label{eq:gersh_positive_nonenr}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(G,N)}
>0.
\label{eq:gersh_implies_gap_nonenr}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, if one has a coercive decomposition
\[
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)=D_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)+R_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p),
\]
with
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\min_a
\left|
\bigl(D_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)\bigr)_{aa}
\right|,
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\|R_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)\|,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}>0.
\label{eq:coercive_nonenr}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{F. Truncation-to-exact upgrade}

Suppose the exact same-shell non-enriched operator is
\[
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p),
\]
and the truncation error obeys
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\left\|
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)
-
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
\right\|
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\label{eq:trunc_error_nonenr}
\end{equation}
Then the exact benchmark satisfies
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
>0.
\label{eq:upgrade_nonenr}
\end{equation}

Thus a positive finite-truncation eigenvalue gap plus a smaller truncation error is sufficient to close the exact same-shell non-enriched slot.

\subsection*{G. Embedding into the master remote-gap inequality}

The master diagonal benchmark can now be sharpened to
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:bench_fin_nonenr}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\label{eq:bench_fin_condition}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\Delta_\rho>0.
\label{eq:final_gap_nonenr_embedded}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{H. Honest final status}

Therefore:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the higher-shell slot is explicit;
\item the wrong-internal slot is explicit;
\item the heavy-volumetric slot is explicit;
\item the same-shell non-enriched slot is reduced exactly to a finite truncated matrix eigenvalue problem;
\item the remaining global ingredient is the remote-remote mixing norm budget \(\eta_{R,\rho}\).
\end{enumerate}

So the genuinely non-automatic part of Task IV has now been reduced to one finite matrix computation plus one norm bound.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Same-shell non-enriched slot is not automatic.}
}
\]

The minimal truncation contains
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\]
where
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
=
\text{same-shell but non-enriched sector}.
\]

Because it lacks the enriched internal doublet, it is excluded from constant mixing at \(p=0\):
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}\to D}(0)=0.
\]
But this does \emph{not} automatically imply a positive spectral gap.

Let
\[
H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}^{(N)}H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(G_*+p)\Pi_{S_*}^{(N)}
\]
be a finite shell-projected Bloch matrix, and let
\[
P_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
\]
project onto the same-shell complementary sector without the enriched doublet.
Define
\[
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
=
P_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)
P_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}.
\]

Then the correct finite benchmark is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}
\!\Bigl(
0,\operatorname{spec}\bigl(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)\bigr)
\Bigr).
}
\]

If
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}>0,
\]
then the truncated same-shell non-enriched sector is spectrally separated from zero.

If moreover
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\left\|
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)
-
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
\right\|
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
>0.
}
\]

So the master benchmark becomes
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\]

If
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\]
then
\[
\Delta_\rho>0.
\]

Hence the truly non-automatic same-shell part of Task IV is reduced to one finite matrix eigenvalue computation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Block-norm and Gershgorin budget theorem for the final remote-gap slot}

\subsection*{A. Starting point}

At the minimal truncation level, the remote block is written as
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\label{eq:HR_DR_RR_budget}
\end{equation}
where \(D_R(p)\) is the diagonal (or sector-center) benchmark part and \(R_R(p)\) is the residual remote--remote mixing.
The pointwise and uniform remote-gap criteria are already known:
\begin{equation}
\delta_0(p)>\eta_R(p):=\|R_R(p)\|
\Longrightarrow
\Delta(p)\ge \delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p)>0,
\label{eq:pointwise_budget_start}
\end{equation}
and on \(N_\rho=\{|p|\le \rho\}\),
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
\label{eq:uniform_budget_start}
\end{equation}

Thus the only remaining issue is to produce a usable upper bound on
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

\subsection*{B. Sectorwise block decomposition}

Let the minimal truncated remote space be
\[
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\]
Write
\begin{equation}
R_R(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & R_{\mathrm{vol,high}} & R_{\mathrm{vol,non}} & R_{\mathrm{vol,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{high,vol}} & 0 & R_{\mathrm{high,non}} & R_{\mathrm{high,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{non,vol}} & R_{\mathrm{non,high}} & 0 & R_{\mathrm{non,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{wrong,vol}} & R_{\mathrm{wrong,high}} & R_{\mathrm{wrong,non}} & 0
\end{pmatrix}(p),
\label{eq:RR_sector_matrix}
\end{equation}
where each block
\[
R_{ab}(p):\mathcal H_b\to \mathcal H_a
\]
is an off-diagonal remote--remote coupling.

Define the pairwise budgets
\begin{equation}
\eta_{ab,\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|.
\label{eq:eta_ab_def}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{C. Basic block-norm budget}

By the triangle inequality for operator norms, one has the sufficient estimate
\begin{equation}
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
\label{eq:basic_block_budget}
\end{equation}

Therefore a fully explicit sufficient criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:block_budget_master}
\end{equation}

This is crude but rigorous.

\subsection*{D. Row-sum / Gershgorin budget}

Choose any orthonormal basis of the remote space and write
\[
(H_R)_{mn}(p)
\]
for the matrix elements.
Define the row sums
\begin{equation}
R_m(p):=\sum_{n\neq m}|(H_R)_{mn}(p)|.
\label{eq:row_sums_budget}
\end{equation}
Then the Gershgorin lower bound is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\min_m
\Bigl(
|(H_R)_{mm}(p)|-R_m(p)
\Bigr).
\label{eq:Gersh_budget_final}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0,
\label{eq:Gersh_positive_final}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_{G,\rho},\Delta_{G,\rho})=\varnothing
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho).
\label{eq:Gersh_gap_final}
\end{equation}

This route is often sharper than \eqref{eq:basic_block_budget} when the remote matrix is sparse.

\subsection*{E. Full remote completion with tails}

For the full remote sector, let
\[
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p),
\]
where \(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) carries the global diagonal benchmark
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho},
\]
and \(R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) contains:
\begin{itemize}
\item all remote--remote off-diagonal mixing,
\item all couplings to tail sectors,
\item all bounded residual corrections to the diagonal benchmark.
\end{itemize}
Define
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\|.
\label{eq:eta_rem_def_final}
\end{equation}

Then the master explicit spectral inequality is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
>0.
}
\label{eq:master_explicit_spectral_ineq}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{F. Explicit power-counting / heavy-suppression budget}

By the previously established tail-coupling estimate theorem, one may bound
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}} K_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}} \frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge 1.
\label{eq:eta_rem_explicit_bound}
\end{equation}
Thus all remote mixing is at least \(O(\rho)\) near the crossing, and heavy-mediated sectors carry additional suppression by inverse powers of heavy masses.

Substituting \eqref{eq:eta_rem_explicit_bound} into \eqref{eq:master_explicit_spectral_ineq}, one obtains the fully explicit sufficient condition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}
>
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}} K_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}} \frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}.
}
\label{eq:final_explicit_budget_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{G. Final Task IV closure statement}

Combining the previously established diagonal benchmarks
\[
4K-|r_*|,
\qquad
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\qquad
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\]
define
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:Delta_bench_full_final}
\end{equation}

Then a sufficient final Task IV criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:TaskIV_final_closed_condition}
\end{equation}
Under \eqref{eq:TaskIV_final_closed_condition},
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho},\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho})
=
\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}>0.
\label{eq:TaskIV_final_gap}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{H. Honest final status}

At this point, Task IV is no longer conceptually open.
It has been reduced completely to:
\begin{enumerate}
\item four explicit diagonal benchmark entries;
\item one same-shell finite matrix eigenvalue audit;
\item one remote mixing norm budget.
\end{enumerate}

So the remaining issue is purely microscopic and quantitative:
evaluate the constants and verify the single inequality
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Final remote mixing budget}
}
\]

At the minimal truncation level,
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

The uniform remote-gap criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

Write the remote mixing in sector blocks:
\[
R_R(p)=\bigl(R_{ab}(p)\bigr)_{a\neq b},
\qquad
a,b\in\{\mathrm{vol},\mathrm{high},\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}\}.
\]
Define pairwise budgets
\[
\eta_{ab,\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|.
\]
Then a sufficient block-norm budget is
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}\le \sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
}
\]

A sharper Gershgorin version is:
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_m
\Bigl(
|(H_R)_{mm}(p)|-\sum_{n\neq m}|(H_R)_{mn}(p)|
\Bigr).
\]
If
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0,
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_{G,\rho},\Delta_{G,\rho})=\varnothing
\qquad (|p|\le \rho).
}
\]

For the full remote block,
\[
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p),
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\|.
\]
The master explicit spectral inequality is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}>0.
}
\]

Moreover,
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}} K_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}} \frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge 1.
}
\]

Therefore the fully explicit final Task IV criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

Here
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\]

If this one inequality holds, then Task IV is complete:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho>0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Task V: Residual-symmetry audit table for actual mass protection}

\subsection*{A. Exact theorem-level starting point}

For the doubled local Dirac block
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i),
\label{eq:HD_mass_audit}
\end{equation}
the full little-group-scalar constant Hermitian operator space is
\begin{equation}
K
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:K_mass_audit}
\end{equation}
The genuine constant Dirac-mass space is exactly
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
\label{eq:mass_space_audit}
\end{equation}
Thus the actual microscopic mass-protection problem is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\cap
\mathcal M_D
=
\{0\},
\label{eq:Ares_cap_M_zero}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}
=
\{K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4):U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K\ \forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}\}.
\label{eq:Ares_def_audit}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{B. Residual-symmetry audit table}

The practical classification table is:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{Residual structure}
&
\text{Action on }\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
&
\text{Does it forbid all constant masses?}
&
\text{Microscopic status}
\\
\hline
\text{little-group scalarity only}
&
\text{allows both}
&
\text{No}
&
\text{automatic theorem only}
\\
\hline
\text{opposite-valley matching only}
&
\text{fixes }h_-(p)=-h_+(-p),\ \text{but does not remove }\tau_x,\tau_y
&
\text{No}
&
\text{already closed structurally}
\\
\hline
\text{exact valley }U(1)_V
&
(\tau_x,\tau_y)\ \text{rotate as a charged doublet}
&
\text{Yes}
&
\text{sufficient if actually preserved}
\\
\hline
\text{exact valley }\mathbb Z_2^V
&
\tau_x,\tau_y\mapsto -\tau_x,-\tau_y
&
\text{Yes}
&
\text{weaker sufficient condition}
\\
\hline
\text{Class II gradient-linear structure}
&
\text{does not insert a constant mass directly}
&
\text{Compatible only}
&
\text{not by itself a proof}
\end{array}
\]

\subsection*{C. Why exact valley \(U(1)_V\) is sufficient}

Define the valley-charge generator
\begin{equation}
Q_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_\theta:=e^{\,i\theta Q_V/2}.
\label{eq:Qv_Utheta_audit}
\end{equation}
Since
\begin{equation}
[Q_V,H_D(p)]=0,
\label{eq:Qv_comm_audit}
\end{equation}
the doubled kinetic block is compatible with a residual valley symmetry.

Now
\begin{equation}
U_\theta(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
=
\cos\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\sin\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\label{eq:taux_rot_audit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
U_\theta(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
=
-\sin\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\cos\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:tauy_rot_audit}
\end{equation}
Therefore no nonzero element of
\[
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}
\]
is invariant under all \(\theta\), so
\begin{equation}
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\label{eq:AU1_cap_M_zero}
\end{equation}
Hence exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) is a sufficient protection mechanism.

\subsection*{D. Why exact valley \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) is already enough}

Let
\begin{equation}
S_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
S_V^2=\mathbf 1_4.
\label{eq:SV_def_audit}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
S_V(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\qquad
S_V(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:SV_flip_audit}
\end{equation}
Hence any \(S_V\)-invariant constant operator must have
\[
m_1=m_2=0.
\]
Therefore exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) already suffices.

\subsection*{E. What is \emph{not} sufficient}

\paragraph{(i) Little-group scalarity alone.}
Little-group scalarity only reduces the allowed constant algebra to
\[
\mathbf 1_4,\ \tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
It does not eliminate the two mass generators.

\paragraph{(ii) Opposite-valley pairing alone.}
The relation
\[
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p)
\]
guarantees Dirac doubling, but it does not by itself remove a constant intervalley operator
\[
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2+m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

\paragraph{(iii) Class II structural compatibility.}
The canonical minimal Class II correction renormalizes the derivative shell coefficients \(A,B,C\) and does not insert a constant mass operator directly.
Therefore it is mass-protection compatible.
But this is weaker than the theorem
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\]
Hence the actual symmetry exclusion still has to be checked independently.

\subsection*{F. Actual microscopic audit procedure}

To close Task V in the actual microscopic TECT/Class II realization, perform exactly the following finite audit:

\paragraph{Step 1. Identify the actual residual symmetry group.}
Determine the low-energy residual symmetry group \(G_{\mathrm{res}}\) acting on the isolated doubled shell block after all shell-enriched corrections are included.

\paragraph{Step 2. Construct the \(4\times4\) representation.}
Write the actual representation
\[
U(g)\in U(4),
\qquad g\in G_{\mathrm{res}},
\]
on
\[
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

\paragraph{Step 3. Solve the symmetry filter.}
Solve the linear equations
\begin{equation}
U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K
\qquad
\forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}
\label{eq:symmetry_filter_audit}
\end{equation}
for
\[
K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4),
\]
to obtain the allowed constant algebra \(A_{\mathrm{res}}\).

\paragraph{Step 4. Solve the mass filter.}
Inside \(A_{\mathrm{res}}\), solve
\begin{equation}
\{K,\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i\}=0,
\qquad
i=1,2,3.
\label{eq:mass_filter_audit}
\end{equation}
If the only solution is \(K=0\), then mass protection holds.

\paragraph{Equivalent shortcut.}
If one can prove directly that exact residual \(U(1)_V\) or exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) survives, then Step 4 is automatic.

\subsection*{G. Final theorem-level / microscopic separation}

Thus the exact logical separation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{theorem-level closure: }
U(1)_V\ \text{or}\ \mathbb Z_2^V
\Longrightarrow
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\]

But:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual microscopic open problem: does the full corrected TECT/Class II realization really preserve such a residual symmetry?}
}
\]

So Task V is no longer conceptual.
It is a finite residual-symmetry audit on the \(4\times4\) doubled shell block.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Task V reduces to one finite symmetry audit: }
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\]

For
\[
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i),
\]
the allowed little-group-scalar constant Hermitian operators are
\[
K
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

The genuine Dirac-mass space is exactly
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
}
\]

Residual-symmetry audit table:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{Residual structure} & \text{Effect on } \mathcal M_D & \text{Mass protection?}\\
\hline
\text{little-group scalarity only} & \text{allows } \tau_x,\tau_y & \text{No}\\
\text{opposite-valley matching only} & \text{does not eliminate } \tau_x,\tau_y & \text{No}\\
\text{exact }U(1)_V & (\tau_x,\tau_y)\text{ rotate nontrivially} & \text{Yes}\\
\text{exact }\mathbb Z_2^V & \tau_x,\tau_y\mapsto -\tau_x,-\tau_y & \text{Yes}\\
\text{Class II gradient-linear form} & \text{compatible only} & \text{Not sufficient}
\end{array}
\]

With
\[
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_\theta=e^{i\theta Q_V/2},
\]
one has
\[
U_\theta(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
=
\cos\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\sin\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\]
\[
U_\theta(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
=
-\sin\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\cos\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\]

Even the weaker remnant
\[
S_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
already suffices:
\[
S_V(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}=-(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\qquad
S_V(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}=-(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\]

Hence the actual microscopic procedure is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(1) identify }G_{\mathrm{res}},
\quad
\text{(2) construct }U(g),
\quad
\text{(3) solve }U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K,
\quad
\text{(4) test whether }\tau_x,\tau_y\text{ survive.}
}
\]

If they do not survive, then
\[
\boxed{
\text{mass protection holds.}
}
\]

Honest final status:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the mass-classification theorem is closed,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual residual symmetry algebra of the microscopic TECT/Class II realization still has to be verified.}
}
\]

\section*{Orthodox route selection: coercivity first, finite truncation second}

\subsection*{1. Why the coercivity route is the correct orthodox route}

The last abstract slot in the master remote-gap inequality is the extra-sector benchmark
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}.
\]
At this point there are two logically valid routes:

\paragraph{Route A: direct finite spectral computation}
Construct a finite shell/Bloch truncation
\[
H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(N)}(p)
\]
and compute
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(N)}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\Bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(N)}(p))\Bigr).
\]
Then control the truncation error
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(N)}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(N)}
\]
to upgrade to the exact benchmark.

\paragraph{Route B: analytic coercivity replacement}
Write the extra-sector operator as
\[
H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)=P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,D)+B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p),
\]
and prove:
\begin{enumerate}
\item uniform principal-symbol positivity:
\[
\langle u,s_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,\xi)u\rangle
\ge
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\langle\xi\rangle^m\|u\|^2;
\]
\item sectorwise Poincar\'e/Fourier exclusion:
\[
\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2\ge \Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\|\psi\|^2;
\]
\item lower-order control:
\[
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}[\psi]|
\le
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\|\psi\|^2.
\]
\end{enumerate}
Then the principal-symbol coercivity theorem gives
\[
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
\ge
\Bigl(
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Bigr)\|\psi\|^2.
\]
Hence, if
\[
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\]
the extra sector is uniformly coercive with
\[
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>0.
\]

After bounded extra-sector correction
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|\delta H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\|
<
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\]
one gets the exact replacement
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}>0.
\]

\subsection*{2. Why Route B is more orthodox}

Route B is better in the strict theorem-building sense because:

\begin{enumerate}
\item it produces an exact infinite-dimensional bound rather than a truncation-dependent numerical witness;
\item it isolates the true conceptual ingredients:
\[
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}},\quad
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},\quad
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}},\quad
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho};
\]
\item once established, it eliminates the need for a minimum-eigenvalue computation entirely.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the correct orthodox order is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{First attempt analytic coercivity closure.}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{Use a finite truncated minimum-eigenvalue computation only if coercivity cannot be instantiated.}
}
\]

\subsection*{3. Explicit BCC Bloch-coercive realization}

For the BCC shell geometry, the document already provides an explicit Fourier-exclusion constant
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}
=
1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2,
\]
valid whenever
\[
0<\rho<\sqrt3-\sqrt2.
\]
Under this condition,
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}>0.
\]

The explicit BCC coercivity bound then becomes
\[
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\ge
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,
\bigl(1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2\bigr)^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\]
Hence a sufficient fully analytic positivity condition is
\[
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,
\bigl(1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2\bigr)^2
>
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\]

This converts the extra-sector slot from an abstract unknown into an explicit analytic quantity.

\subsection*{4. Consequence for the master remote-gap inequality}

Once the extra-sector slot is replaced analytically, the master benchmark becomes
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})K\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2-\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Biggr\}.
\]
Then the full remote-gap condition is reduced to the single explicit inequality
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}}.
\]

At that point, the remote spectral gap is closed without any finite-matrix minimum-eigenvalue computation.

\subsection*{5. Final orthodox decision rule}

The correct strict decision rule is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If } \kappa_{\mathrm{extra}},\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}},\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\text{ can be extracted from the actual microscopic operator,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{then the coercivity route is the proper primary route.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{If one of these constants cannot yet be controlled,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{then the finite truncated minimum-eigenvalue computation becomes the correct fallback verifier.}
}
\]

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Orthodox route}=\text{analytic coercivity first}.
}
\]

The extra-sector slot
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\]
should first be replaced by the coercive bound
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\]
where
\[
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\]

If
\[
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}<c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}>0
}
\]
without any finite minimum-eigenvalue computation.

For the explicit BCC Bloch-exclusion route,
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}=1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2,
\qquad
0<\rho<\sqrt3-\sqrt2,
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\ge
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,
(1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2)^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\]

Thus the master fully analytic benchmark becomes
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})K\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2-\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Biggr\}.
\]

If
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}},
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}>0.
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use finite truncated minimum-eigenvalue computation only if the coercivity constants cannot yet be instantiated.}
}
\]
