\section*{Extra-sector principal symbol identification theorem}

\subsection*{A. Goal}

We now carry out the orthodox analytic route for the remaining extra-sector slot.
The purpose is to identify, in the actual BCC first-shell setting, the abstract constants
\[
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}},
\qquad
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\qquad
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}},
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\]
appearing in the principal-symbol coercivity theorem.

The key point is that the first two constants can already be identified explicitly,
while the last two remain model-dependent lower-order data.

\subsection*{B. Abstract coercivity theorem to be instantiated}

The extra-sector operator is written as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)
=
P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,D)+B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p),
\label{eq:Hextra_split_ident}
\end{equation}
with quadratic form
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
=
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{pr},p}[\psi]+\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}[\psi].
\label{eq:qextra_split_ident}
\end{equation}
If the principal symbol is uniformly positive with constant \(\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}>0\),
the sectorwise Fourier/Poincar\'e exclusion holds with constant \(\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}>0\),
and the lower-order part obeys
\begin{equation}
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}[\psi]|
\le
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\|\psi\|^2,
\qquad
0\le \alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}<1,
\label{eq:lower_order_bound_ident}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
\ge
\Bigl(
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Bigr)\|\psi\|^2.
\label{eq:principal_coercive_bound_ident}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\label{eq:cextra_abstract_ident}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{C. Principal symbol on the BCC extra sector}

In the present BCC shell setting, the extra sector is defined by excluding the selected soft shell carrier.
Therefore the principal operator is governed by the same Brazovskii-type quadratic principal kernel that controls shell-radius departure:
\begin{equation}
P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,D)\sim K\bigl(|Q+p|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2
\qquad
\text{on each excluded harmonic }Q.
\label{eq:Ppr_BCC_ident}
\end{equation}
Thus the principal symbol is positive with leading coefficient
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}=K.
}
\label{eq:kappa_ident_final}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the identification stated in the document.

\subsection*{D. BCC Bloch-exclusion constant}

Let the selected shell point be normalized so that
\begin{equation}
q_*^2=1.
\label{eq:qstar_norm_ident}
\end{equation}
Let \(k=G_*+p\), with \(|p|\le \rho\), and let the extra sector contain only excluded harmonics.
Then the BCC first-shell arithmetic gives the explicit lower bound
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}
=
1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2,
\label{eq:deltaBloch_ident}
\end{equation}
valid whenever
\begin{equation}
0<\rho<\sqrt3-\sqrt2.
\label{eq:rho_ident_condition}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}>0.
\label{eq:deltaBloch_positive_ident}
\end{equation}

Because the extra sector excludes the selected soft shell, its Fourier/Poincar\'e exclusion constant is exactly the square of the Bloch-exclusion distance:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2.
}
\label{eq:Lambda_ident_final}
\end{equation}

This is again the explicit identification stated in the document.

\subsection*{E. Resulting explicit coercivity constant}

Substituting
\[
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}=K,
\qquad
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}=\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
\]
into the abstract coercivity formula gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:cextra_identified_final}
\end{equation}
Hence the sufficient positivity condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
>
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:extra_gap_condition_identified}
\end{equation}
Using the explicit BCC formula,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,
\bigl(1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2\bigr)^2
>
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:explicit_BCC_gap_condition_identified}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{F. Master benchmark replacement}

Therefore the extra-sector slot in the master remote-gap inequality is no longer abstract:
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\leadsto
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\label{eq:extra_slot_replace_ident}
\end{equation}
So the fully analytic benchmark becomes
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})K\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:bench_Bloch_ident}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}},
\label{eq:bench_final_condition_ident}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}>0.
\label{eq:full_gap_ident}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{G. What remains actually open}

At this point, the principal-symbol identification itself is finished.
The only remaining microscopic work is to extract the lower-order relative-bound constants:
\begin{equation}
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}},
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\label{eq:remaining_constants_ident}
\end{equation}

Thus the honest status is:

\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\ \text{and}\ \Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\text{ are already explicitly identified in the BCC route;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{the remaining analytic gap problem is entirely concentrated in }
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}},\ \beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},\ \varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\]

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)
=
P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,D)+B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p)
}
\]

Abstract principal-symbol coercivity gives
\[
\boxed{
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\]

In the explicit BCC first-shell route, the principal part is identified with the Brazovskii shell-separation kernel, so
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}=K.
}
\]

The Bloch/Fourier exclusion constant is
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}
=
1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2,
\qquad
0<\rho<\sqrt3-\sqrt2,
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\]

A sufficient positivity condition is
\[
\boxed{
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,
\bigl(1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2\bigr)^2
>
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\]

So the extra-sector slot in the master remote-gap benchmark becomes
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\leadsto
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\]

Hence the principal-symbol identification problem is already closed.
What remains open is only the lower-order control:
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}},\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Extra-sector lower-order remainder bound theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
The principal-symbol part of the extra-sector coercivity problem has already been identified:
\[
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}=K,
\qquad
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}=\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2,
\qquad
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}=1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2.
\]
What remains is to control the lower-order remainder
\[
B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p)
\]
by a relative form bound with respect to the principal quadratic form.

\paragraph{Starting split.}
Write
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)
=
P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,D)+B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p),
\qquad
|p|\le \rho,
\label{eq:Hextra_split_lo_user}
\end{equation}
with quadratic form
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
=
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{pr},p}[\psi]
+
\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}[\psi].
\label{eq:qextra_split_lo_user}
\end{equation}

Assume the principal part satisfies the already-established BCC coercive lower bound
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{pr},p}[\psi]
\ge
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2\,\|\psi\|^2
\qquad
\text{on the extra sector}.
\label{eq:qpr_bloch_user}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Abstract relative-form hypothesis.}
Assume that the lower-order quadratic form obeys
\begin{equation}
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}[\psi]|
\le
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}\,K\,\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\,\|\psi\|^2,
\qquad
0\le \alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}<1,
\label{eq:blo_relative_user}
\end{equation}
uniformly for \(|p|\le \rho\).

Then, combining the principal coercivity theorem with the BCC identification
\[
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}=K,
\qquad
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}=\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2,
\]
one obtains
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
\ge
\Bigl(
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Bigr)\|\psi\|^2.
\label{eq:coercive_final_lo_user}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:cextra_lo_user}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Sufficient positivity condition.}
Therefore a sufficient analytic positivity condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,K\,
\bigl(1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2\bigr)^2
>
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:positive_lo_condition_user}
\end{equation}
If \eqref{eq:positive_lo_condition_user} holds, then
\begin{equation}
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}>0.
\label{eq:cextra_positive_lo_user}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Bounded correction stability.}
Now let
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)
=
H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p),
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|\delta H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\|.
\label{eq:Hextra_pert_lo_user}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}<c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\label{eq:eps_less_cextra_lo_user}
\end{equation}
then the extra-sector gap is stable and
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>0.
\label{eq:extra_gap_stable_lo_user}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Decomposition of the lower-order remainder.}
For practical microscopic auditing, it is useful to split
\begin{equation}
B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p)
=
\sum_{\ell=1}^L B_{\mathrm{lo}}^{(\ell)}(p),
\label{eq:Blo_sum_user}
\end{equation}
with corresponding quadratic forms
\[
\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}^{(\ell)}[\psi].
\]
Suppose each piece satisfies
\begin{equation}
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}^{(\ell)}[\psi]|
\le
\alpha_\ell\,K\,\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
\beta_{\ell,\rho}\,\|\psi\|^2.
\label{eq:piecewise_relative_user}
\end{equation}
Then summing gives
\begin{equation}
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}
=
\sum_{\ell=1}^L \alpha_\ell,
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\sum_{\ell=1}^L \beta_{\ell,\rho}.
\label{eq:alpha_beta_sum_user}
\end{equation}
Hence a sufficient condition is simply
\begin{equation}
\sum_{\ell=1}^L \alpha_\ell < 1,
\qquad
\sum_{\ell=1}^L \beta_{\ell,\rho}
<
K\bigl(1-\sum_{\ell=1}^L\alpha_\ell\bigr)\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2.
\label{eq:piecewise_sufficient_user}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Interpretation of the pieces.}
In the actual microscopic TECT operator, the lower-order pieces typically arise from:
\begin{enumerate}
\item bounded zeroth-order endomorphism terms;
\item first-order transport terms restricted to the extra sector;
\item finite shell-curvature corrections in the Bloch reduction;
\item bounded residual couplings induced by integrating out heavy sectors.
\end{enumerate}
The first and fourth usually contribute only to \(\beta_{\ell,\rho}\),
while the second and third may contribute to both \(\alpha_\ell\) and \(\beta_{\ell,\rho}\).

\paragraph{Final replacement in the master benchmark.}
Thus the extra-sector slot in the master remote-gap inequality becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\leadsto
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:extra_slot_final_replace_user}
\end{equation}
Therefore the fully analytic BCC benchmark becomes
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:bench_bloch_lo_user}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}},
\label{eq:master_lo_condition_user}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}>0.
\label{eq:full_gap_lo_user}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Honest status.}
At this stage, the remaining analytic work is concentrated entirely in
\[
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}},
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\]
The principal-symbol part is already closed.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)
=
P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,D)+B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p),
\qquad
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}
=
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{pr},p}
+
\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}.
}
\]

The principal-symbol part is already fixed:
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}=K,
\qquad
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2,
\qquad
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}=1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2.
}
\]

Assume the lower-order remainder satisfies
\[
\boxed{
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}[\psi]|
\le
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}\,K\,\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\,\|\psi\|^2,
\qquad
0\le \alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}<1.
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\]

A sufficient positivity condition is
\[
\boxed{
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,
(1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2)^2
>
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\]

If moreover
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|\delta H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\|
<
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>0.
}
\]

Equivalently, the extra-sector slot becomes
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\leadsto
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\]

Thus the principal-symbol part is closed, and the only remaining analytic constants are
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}},
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Lower-order remainder decomposition table}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now convert the abstract lower-order remainder
\[
B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p)
\]
into an operator-level decomposition adapted to the actual TECT/BCC microscopic architecture, so that the abstract relative-form bound
\[
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}[\psi]|
\le
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}\,K\,\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\,\|\psi\|^2
\]
is reduced to a finite table of piecewise bounds.

\paragraph{Structural input from the microscopic operator.}
The document already fixes the following operator-level ingredients:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact BCC linearized Hessian decomposes as
\[
D_{ij}(k)=D^{\mathrm{iso}}_{ij}(k)+\Delta D_{ij}(k),
\]
where \(\Delta D_{ij}(k)\) is the genuine cubic-anisotropic remainder;

\item the projector-Hessian static sector takes the form
\[
H_B^{\mathrm{stat}}
=
-\rho\partial_\xi^2-\rho\partial_y^2
+
W_B(\xi)
-
\rho\theta'(\xi)^2
\begin{pmatrix}
2&0\\0&1
\end{pmatrix}
+\cdots;
\]

\item restoring slow worldvolume dependence produces the first-order transport operator
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu};
\]

\item integrating out the heavy volumetric mode yields a local \(1/M_\sigma^2\) expansion with explicit remainder bounds.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the natural lower-order decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p)
=
B_{\mathrm{cub}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm{H}}(p).
}
\label{eq:Blo_decomposition_table}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection*{A. Cubic anisotropy remainder}

Define
\begin{equation}
B_{\mathrm{cub}}(p)
:=
\Delta D(p,D),
\label{eq:Bcub_def}
\end{equation}
where \(\Delta D\) is the exact cubic anisotropy remainder of the BCC linearized Hessian.

Its quadratic form is
\[
\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{cub},p}[\psi]
=
\langle \psi,\Delta D(p,D)\psi\rangle.
\]

\paragraph{Relative-form role.}
If the cubic anisotropy is relatively small with respect to the isotropic principal part,
then one seeks a bound
\begin{equation}
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{cub},p}[\psi]|
\le
\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}\,K\,\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}\,\|\psi\|^2.
\label{eq:Bcub_bound}
\end{equation}
In an RG-improved or infrared-isotropized regime, \(\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}\) should be small.
Thus \(B_{\mathrm{cub}}\) is the natural source of the relative principal-form coefficient \(\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}\).

\subsubsection*{B. Bounded potential / endomorphism sector}

Collect the bounded static endomorphism terms into
\begin{equation}
B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)
:=
W_B(\xi)
-
\rho\theta'(\xi)^2
\begin{pmatrix}
2&0\\0&1
\end{pmatrix}
+
B_{\mathrm{bd}}(p),
\label{eq:Bpot_def}
\end{equation}
where \(B_{\mathrm{bd}}(p)\) denotes any additional bounded zeroth-order shell/Bloch endomorphism terms on the extra sector.

Its form satisfies the purely bounded estimate
\begin{equation}
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{pot},p}[\psi]|
\le
\|B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)\|\,\|\psi\|^2.
\label{eq:Bpot_bound0}
\end{equation}
Hence one may take
\begin{equation}
\alpha_{\mathrm{pot}}=0,
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)\|.
\label{eq:Bpot_alphabeta}
\end{equation}

So \(B_{\mathrm{pot}}\) contributes only to the \(\beta\)-budget.

\subsubsection*{C. First-order transport remainder}

Restrict the worldvolume transport operator to the extra sector:
\begin{equation}
B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)
:=
-i\,P_{\mathrm{extra}}V^\mu(\xi)P_{\mathrm{extra}}\partial_{y^\mu}.
\label{eq:Btr_def}
\end{equation}
Its form is first-order in derivatives and therefore lower-order relative to the principal sector.

Using the standard \(\varepsilon\)-Sobolev estimate, for every \(\varepsilon>0\),
\begin{equation}
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{tr},p}[\psi]|
\le
\varepsilon\,K\,\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
C_{\mathrm{tr}}(\varepsilon,\rho)\,\|\psi\|^2.
\label{eq:Btr_eps_bound}
\end{equation}
Thus one may set
\begin{equation}
\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}=\varepsilon,
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}=C_{\mathrm{tr}}(\varepsilon,\rho).
\label{eq:Btr_alphabeta}
\end{equation}

Hence the transport remainder contributes to both \(\alpha\) and \(\beta\), but its \(\alpha\)-contribution can be made arbitrarily small at the expense of enlarging \(\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}\).

\subsubsection*{D. Heavy-induced local correction}

Let \(B_{\mathrm{H}}(p)\) denote the operator induced by integrating out the heavy volumetric mode after subtracting the leading principal longitudinal stiffening already accounted for elsewhere.
By the \(1/M_\sigma^2\) expansion with explicit remainder control,
\begin{equation}
B_{\mathrm{H}}(p)
=
\frac{1}{M_\sigma^2}\mathcal O_2(p,D)
+
\frac{1}{M_\sigma^4}\mathcal O_4(p,D)
+
R_{\mathrm{H}}^{(N)}(p),
\label{eq:BH_expansion}
\end{equation}
with operator norms uniformly controlled on the allowed compact low-energy region.

Therefore one can bound
\begin{equation}
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{H},p}[\psi]|
\le
\alpha_{\mathrm{H}}\,K\,\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
\beta_{\mathrm{H},\rho}\,\|\psi\|^2,
\label{eq:BH_bound}
\end{equation}
with schematic size
\begin{equation}
\alpha_{\mathrm{H}}
=
O(M_\sigma^{-2}),
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{H},\rho}
=
O(M_\sigma^{-4})
\quad
\text{or smaller,}
\label{eq:BH_scaling}
\end{equation}
provided the low-energy domain stays inside the uniform convergence region of the expansion.

Thus \(B_{\mathrm{H}}\) is naturally a suppressed lower-order perturbation.

\subsubsection*{E. Piecewise table}

The resulting lower-order remainder table is:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{piece }B_{\mathrm{lo}}^{(\ell)}
&
\text{microscopic origin}
&
\text{relative-form role}
&
\text{natural contribution}
\\
\hline
B_{\mathrm{cub}}
&
\Delta D_{ij}(k)
&
\text{anisotropic differential remainder}
&
(\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}},\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho})
\\
\hline
B_{\mathrm{pot}}
&
W_B(\xi)-\rho\theta'(\xi)^2\mathrm{diag}(2,1)+B_{\mathrm{bd}}
&
\text{bounded zeroth-order endomorphism}
&
(0,\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho})
\\
\hline
B_{\mathrm{tr}}
&
-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
&
\text{first-order transport}
&
(\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}},\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho})
\\
\hline
B_{\mathrm{H}}
&
1/M_\sigma^2\text{ local heavy-induced terms}
&
\text{suppressed derivative/zeroth-order correction}
&
(\alpha_{\mathrm{H}},\beta_{\mathrm{H},\rho})
\end{array}
\]

\subsubsection*{F. Summed bound}

Summing the piecewise estimates gives
\begin{equation}
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}
=
\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}
+
\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\alpha_{\mathrm{H}},
\label{eq:alpha_sum_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{H},\rho}.
\label{eq:beta_sum_final}
\end{equation}
The coercive lower bound becomes
\begin{equation}
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\Bigl(
1-\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}-\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}-\alpha_{\mathrm{H}}
\Bigr)
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\Bigl(
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{H},\rho}
\Bigr).
\label{eq:cextra_piecewise_final}
\end{equation}

Hence a sufficient positivity condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}+\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}+\alpha_{\mathrm{H}}<1
}
\label{eq:alpha_less_one_piecewise}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{H},\rho}
<
\Bigl(
1-\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}-\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}-\alpha_{\mathrm{H}}
\Bigr)
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2.
}
\label{eq:beta_budget_piecewise}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection*{G. Final benchmark replacement}

Thus the extra-sector slot is replaced by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\leadsto
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
}
\label{eq:extra_slot_piecewise_replace}
\end{equation}
with \(c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\) given explicitly by \eqref{eq:cextra_piecewise_final}.

Therefore the fully analytic BCC benchmark becomes
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{piece}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:bench_piece_final}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{piece}},
\label{eq:piece_master_condition}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}>0.
\label{eq:piece_final_gap}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Honest status.}
At this stage, the analytic closure problem is no longer abstract.
It has been reduced to estimating four concrete microscopic remainder pieces:
\[
B_{\mathrm{cub}},\quad
B_{\mathrm{pot}},\quad
B_{\mathrm{tr}},\quad
B_{\mathrm{H}}.
\]
The only remaining work is to extract the actual constants
\[
\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}},\ \beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho},\ 
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho},\ 
\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}},\ \beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho},\ 
\alpha_{\mathrm{H}},\ \beta_{\mathrm{H},\rho},\ 
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\]

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p)
=
B_{\mathrm{cub}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm{H}}(p).
}
\]

with

\[
B_{\mathrm{cub}}
=
\Delta D_{ij}(k),
\]
\[
B_{\mathrm{pot}}
=
W_B(\xi)-\rho\theta'(\xi)^2
\begin{pmatrix}
2&0\\0&1
\end{pmatrix}
+
B_{\mathrm{bd}},
\]
\[
B_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\]
\[
B_{\mathrm{H}}
=
\text{heavy-induced local }1/M_\sigma^2\text{ correction}.
\]

Piecewise relative-form roles:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c}
\text{piece} & \text{natural contribution} \\
\hline
B_{\mathrm{cub}} & (\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}},\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}) \\
B_{\mathrm{pot}} & (0,\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}) \\
B_{\mathrm{tr}} & (\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}},\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}) \\
B_{\mathrm{H}} & (\alpha_{\mathrm{H}},\beta_{\mathrm{H},\rho})
\end{array}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}
=
\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}+\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}+\alpha_{\mathrm{H}},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{H},\rho}.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\Bigl(
1-\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}-\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}-\alpha_{\mathrm{H}}
\Bigr)
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\Bigl(
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{H},\rho}
\Bigr).
}
\]

A sufficient positivity condition is
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}+\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}+\alpha_{\mathrm{H}}<1,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{H},\rho}
<
\Bigl(
1-\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}-\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}-\alpha_{\mathrm{H}}
\Bigr)
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2.
}
\]

So the extra-sector slot becomes
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\leadsto
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
}
\]

This reduces the remaining analytic problem to estimating the concrete microscopic constants attached to
\[
B_{\mathrm{cub}},\quad
B_{\mathrm{pot}},\quad
B_{\mathrm{tr}},\quad
B_{\mathrm{H}}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Explicit bound lemma for \texorpdfstring{$B_{\mathrm{pot}}$}{Bpot} and \texorpdfstring{$B_{\mathrm H}$}{BH}}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now close the two easiest lower-order pieces in the decomposition
\[
B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p)
=
B_{\mathrm{cub}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm H}(p),
\]
namely the bounded zeroth-order endomorphism sector \(B_{\mathrm{pot}}\) and the heavy-induced local correction \(B_{\mathrm H}\).

\subsubsection*{A. Bound for the bounded potential / endomorphism piece}

The projector-Hessian theorem gives the fluctuation operator in the schematic form
\[
H_B
=
-\rho D_\xi^{(B)2}
-
\rho D_y^{(B)2}
+
M_B(\xi),
\]
where \(M_B(\xi)\) is a Hermitian \(2\times 2\) endomorphism built from the background and its derivatives. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

Restricting to the extra sector and allowing additional bounded shell/Bloch zeroth-order corrections, define
\begin{equation}
B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p):=
P_{\mathrm{extra}}\,M_B(\xi)\,P_{\mathrm{extra}}
+
B_{\mathrm{bd}}(p),
\label{eq:Bpot_def_final}
\end{equation}
where \(B_{\mathrm{bd}}(p)\) is any further bounded symmetric zeroth-order endomorphism term on the extra sector.

Let
\[
\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{pot},p}[\psi]
=
\langle \psi,B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)\psi\rangle.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{pot},p}[\psi]|
\le
\|B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)\|\,\|\psi\|^2.
\label{eq:Bpot_norm_bound_final}
\end{equation}
Hence the natural relative-form constants are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{pot}}=0,
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)\|.
}
\label{eq:Bpot_alpha_beta_final}
\end{equation}

So \(B_{\mathrm{pot}}\) contributes only to the \(\beta\)-budget and does not consume any principal coercivity fraction.

\subsubsection*{B. Bound for the heavy-induced local correction}

The heavy-sector covariance satisfies
\begin{equation}
C_\sigma
=
(M_\sigma^2-\partial_t^2+c_\sigma^2\nabla^2)^{-1},
\qquad
\|C_\sigma\|_{L^2\to L^2}\le \frac1{M_\sigma^2},
\label{eq:Csigma_norm_final}
\end{equation}
and admits the convergent derivative expansion
\begin{equation}
C_\sigma
=
\frac1{M_\sigma^2}
\sum_{n=0}^{R}
\left(
-\frac{c_\sigma^2\nabla^2-\partial_t^2}{M_\sigma^2}
\right)^n
+
R_{\sigma}^{(R)},
\label{eq:Csigma_expansion_final}
\end{equation}
with remainder bounded by
\begin{equation}
\|R_{\sigma}^{(R)}\|
\le
\frac{C_R}{M_\sigma^{2(R+1)}}(1+|p|/\Lambda)^\kappa
\qquad
\text{on the low-energy region}.
\label{eq:Csigma_remainder_final}
\end{equation}
This is the standard heavy-field local expansion with explicit remainder control. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

In the TECT refined model, the projector stiffness term does not generically generate a tree-level shell-enriched tensor on the locked constant-projector background, but it makes projector tangent modes heavy and after elimination induces corrections of order
\[
O\!\left(\frac1{\chi \bar\rho^2 q_*^2}\right),
\]
while enhancing the remote gap. 

Accordingly, define the heavy-induced lower-order piece on the extra sector by
\begin{equation}
B_{\mathrm H}(p)
=
\frac1{M_\sigma^2}\mathcal O_{2}(p,D)
+
\frac1{M_\sigma^4}\mathcal O_{4}(p,D)
+
R_{\mathrm H}^{(R)}(p),
\label{eq:BH_expansion_final}
\end{equation}
where \(R_{\mathrm H}^{(R)}\) is uniformly controlled by \eqref{eq:Csigma_remainder_final}.

Let
\[
\mathfrak b_{\mathrm H,p}[\psi]
=
\langle \psi,B_{\mathrm H}(p)\psi\rangle.
\]
Using standard Sobolev interpolation / relative-form estimates for lower-order differential operators, one gets
\begin{equation}
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm H,p}[\psi]|
\le
\alpha_{\mathrm H}\,K\,\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}\,\|\psi\|^2,
\label{eq:BH_relative_final}
\end{equation}
with the safe scaling
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm H}=O(M_\sigma^{-2}),
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}=O(M_\sigma^{-2}),
}
\label{eq:BH_safe_scaling_final}
\end{equation}
and higher-order remainder contribution
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm H,\rho}^{(R)}
=
O(M_\sigma^{-2(R+1)}).
}
\label{eq:BH_remainder_scaling_final}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Important honesty clause.}
Without additional cancellations, one should \emph{not} claim in general that
\[
\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}=O(M_\sigma^{-4}).
\]
The document directly supports \(1/M_\sigma^2\)-type suppression of the heavy-induced local expansion and of the induced shell corrections, while the higher-order truncation remainder is \(O(M_\sigma^{-2(R+1)})\). :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11} :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12} :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

\subsubsection*{C. Piecewise contribution to the extra-sector coercivity budget}

Therefore the two easiest pieces contribute as follows:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{pot}}=0,
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)\|,
}
\label{eq:piece_pot_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm H}=O(M_\sigma^{-2}),
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}=O(M_\sigma^{-2}),
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm H,\rho}^{(R)}=O(M_\sigma^{-2(R+1)}).
}
\label{eq:piece_H_final}
\end{equation}

Hence the partial extra-sector coercivity constant becomes
\begin{equation}
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(\mathrm{partial})}
=
\Bigl(
1-\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}-\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}-\alpha_{\mathrm H}
\Bigr)
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\Bigl(
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}
\Bigr).
\label{eq:partial_cextra_final}
\end{equation}

Thus the analytic bottleneck is now sharply reduced:
the two easiest pieces are already in canonical bounded form, while the difficult work remains in
\[
B_{\mathrm{cub}},
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\]

\paragraph{Conclusion.}
The operator-level lower-order remainder problem has now been partially closed in explicit form:
\[
B_{\mathrm{pot}}
\text{ contributes only to }
\beta,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm H}
\text{ contributes a heavy-suppressed }(\alpha,\beta)\text{ pair.}
\]
This is the natural orthodox next step in the analytic coercivity program.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{First explicit lower-order remainder bounds}
}
\]

For the extra-sector remainder
\[
B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p)
=
B_{\mathrm{cub}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm H}(p),
\]
the two easiest pieces are:

\[
\textbf{(i) bounded potential / endomorphism piece}
\]
\[
B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)
=
P_{\mathrm{extra}}M_B(\xi)P_{\mathrm{extra}}
+
B_{\mathrm{bd}}(p),
\]
with
\[
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{pot},p}[\psi]|
\le
\|B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)\|\,\|\psi\|^2.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{pot}}=0,
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)\|.
}
\]

\[
\textbf{(ii) heavy-induced local correction}
\]
\[
C_\sigma
=
(M_\sigma^2-\partial_t^2+c_\sigma^2\nabla^2)^{-1},
\qquad
\|C_\sigma\|_{L^2\to L^2}\le \frac1{M_\sigma^2},
\]
and
\[
C_\sigma
=
\frac1{M_\sigma^2}\sum_{n=0}^{R}
\left(
-\frac{c_\sigma^2\nabla^2-\partial_t^2}{M_\sigma^2}
\right)^n
+
R_\sigma^{(R)},
\qquad
\|R_\sigma^{(R)}\|
=
O(M_\sigma^{-2(R+1)}).
\]
So
\[
B_{\mathrm H}(p)
=
\frac1{M_\sigma^2}\mathcal O_2
+
\frac1{M_\sigma^4}\mathcal O_4
+
R_{\mathrm H}^{(R)}(p)
\]
satisfies
\[
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm H,p}[\psi]|
\le
\alpha_{\mathrm H}K\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}\|\psi\|^2,
\]
with safe scaling
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm H}=O(M_\sigma^{-2}),
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}=O(M_\sigma^{-2}),
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm H,\rho}^{(R)}=O(M_\sigma^{-2(R+1)}).
}
\]

Important honesty clause:
\[
\boxed{
\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}=O(M_\sigma^{-4})
\text{ is not justified in general without extra cancellations.}
}
\]

Thus the partial coercivity budget becomes
\[
\boxed{
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(\mathrm{partial})}
=
\Bigl(
1-\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}-\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}-\alpha_{\mathrm H}
\Bigr)
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\Bigl(
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}
\Bigr).
}
\]

So the remaining analytic bottleneck is now concentrated in
\[
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{cub}},\qquad B_{\mathrm{tr}}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Fiberwise transport bound lemma}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now sharpen the treatment of the transport remainder
\[
B_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\]
At the PDE level, one may always use a conservative \(\varepsilon\)-Sobolev estimate for the first-order operator
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
\]
However, at the present stage of the program the operator has already been reduced to a fixed low-momentum Bloch/worldvolume fiber.
In that representation, the transport term is no longer an unbounded first-order differential operator in \(y\), but a bounded zeroth-order operator depending on the fiber momentum \(p\).

\paragraph{Structural input.}
The local projector-defect analysis establishes that the leading transport kernel has the form
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\label{eq:L1_transport_fiber}
\end{equation}
and, more sharply,
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\in \mathrm{Herm}(Q_B).
\label{eq:Vmu_theta_factor_fiber}
\end{equation}
Thus \(V^\mu(\xi)\) is a Hermitian bundle endomorphism on the rank-two transverse bundle \(Q_B\), multiplied by the odd scalar profile \(\theta'(\xi)\). 

The shell-valley/Bloch analysis also fixes that the relevant operator is studied fiberwise near
\[
k=G_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\le \rho,
\]
through the finite shell-projected Bloch matrix. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\paragraph{Fiber reduction of the transport operator.}
On a fixed worldvolume/Bloch fiber of momentum \(p\), one has
\[
-i\partial_{y^\mu}\ \mapsto\ p_\mu.
\]
Therefore the transport operator becomes
\begin{equation}
B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)
=
p_\mu V^\mu(\xi).
\label{eq:Btr_fiber_def}
\end{equation}
This is now a zeroth-order multiplication operator on the \(\xi\)-dependent bundle fiber, not an unbounded first-order differential operator.

\paragraph{Operator norm bound.}
Define
\begin{equation}
C_V(\rho)
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\left\|
\sum_\mu \frac{p_\mu}{|p|}V^\mu(\xi)
\right\|_{L^2_\xi\to L^2_\xi},
\label{eq:CV_def}
\end{equation}
with the convention that the unit vector is arbitrary at \(p=0\), or equivalently use the simpler sufficient bound
\begin{equation}
\widetilde C_V
:=
\left(
\sum_\mu
\sup_\xi \|V^\mu(\xi)\|^2
\right)^{1/2}.
\label{eq:CV_tilde_def}
\end{equation}
Then for every \(|p|\le \rho\),
\begin{equation}
\|B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\|
=
\|p_\mu V^\mu(\xi)\|
\le
|p|\,C_V(\rho)
\le
\rho\,C_V(\rho),
\label{eq:Btr_norm_bound}
\end{equation}
and in particular
\begin{equation}
\|B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\|
\le
\rho\,\widetilde C_V.
\label{eq:Btr_norm_bound_tilde}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Quadratic-form consequence.}
Let
\[
\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{tr},p}[\psi]
=
\langle \psi,B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\psi\rangle.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{tr},p}[\psi]|
\le
\|B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\|\,\|\psi\|^2
\le
\rho\,C_V(\rho)\,\|\psi\|^2.
\label{eq:btr_form_bound}
\end{equation}
Hence the transport remainder contributes only to the bounded \(\beta\)-budget:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}=0,
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
=
\rho\,C_V(\rho),
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_transport_final}
\end{equation}
or with the rougher sufficient constant,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}=0,
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
\le
\rho\,\widetilde C_V.
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_transport_rough}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Oddness and selection rule.}
The reflection-oddness
\[
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi)
\]
remains essential for the graded low-mode selection rule:
same-parity matrix elements vanish while mixed even/odd overlaps survive generically. 
However, for the present extra-sector coercivity estimate, oddness is not used to gain smallness.
The actual smallness comes from the fiber momentum factor \(p_\mu\), hence from the neighborhood size \(\rho\).

\paragraph{Important correction to the previous conservative bound.}
At the PDE level, before fixing the Bloch/worldvolume fiber, it is always legitimate to use the standard estimate
\[
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{tr},p}[\psi]|
\le
\varepsilon K\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
C_{\mathrm{tr}}(\varepsilon,\rho)\|\psi\|^2.
\]
But after fiber reduction, this is no longer optimal.
The stronger and more honest bound is \eqref{eq:alpha_beta_transport_final}:
the transport piece is a bounded zeroth-order operator with \(\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}=0\).

\paragraph{Updated piecewise decomposition.}
With this sharpening, the lower-order remainder decomposition becomes
\[
B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p)
=
B_{\mathrm{cub}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm{pot}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)
+
B_{\mathrm H}(p),
\]
with contributions
\begin{equation}
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}
=
\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}
+
\alpha_{\mathrm H},
\label{eq:alpha_sum_updated}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}.
\label{eq:beta_sum_updated}
\end{equation}
So the coercivity constant is sharpened to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\bigl(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}-\alpha_{\mathrm H}\bigr)
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\bigl(
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
+\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:cextra_updated_transport}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Conclusion.}
Thus the transport remainder is no longer part of the genuinely difficult relative-principal-form budget.
After fiber reduction it is simply a bounded \(O(\rho)\) perturbation.
Therefore the only genuinely difficult analytic remainder piece left is the cubic anisotropy sector \(B_{\mathrm{cub}}\).

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
}
\]

After Bloch/worldvolume fiber reduction near
\[
k=G_*+p,\qquad |p|\le \rho,
\]
one has
\[
-i\partial_{y^\mu}\mapsto p_\mu.
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)=p_\mu V^\mu(\xi),
}
\]
which is a bounded zeroth-order operator on the \(\xi\)-fiber.

Define
\[
C_V(\rho)
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\left\|
\sum_\mu \frac{p_\mu}{|p|}V^\mu(\xi)
\right\|,
\]
or more crudely
\[
\widetilde C_V
:=
\left(\sum_\mu \sup_\xi \|V^\mu(\xi)\|^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]
Then
\[
\|B_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\|
\le
|p|\,C_V(\rho)
\le
\rho\,C_V(\rho)
\le
\rho\,\widetilde C_V.
\]

Hence the quadratic-form bound is
\[
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{tr},p}[\psi]|
\le
\rho\,C_V(\rho)\,\|\psi\|^2,
\]
so the transport piece contributes only to the bounded \(\beta\)-budget:
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{tr}}=0,
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
=
\rho\,C_V(\rho)
\quad
(\text{or }\le \rho\,\widetilde C_V).
}
\]

Therefore the piecewise lower-order constants sharpen to
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}
=
\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}+\alpha_{\mathrm H},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}.
}
\]

Thus
\[
\boxed{
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}-\alpha_{\mathrm H})
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
(\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
+\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}).
}
\]

So the transport term is no longer part of the difficult relative-principal-form budget.
After fiber reduction it is only an \(O(\rho)\) bounded perturbation.
The only genuinely hard analytic remainder left is
\[
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{cub}}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Cubic anisotropy relative-bound theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now treat the last genuinely difficult lower-order remainder
\[
B_{\mathrm{cub}}=\Delta D_{ij}(k).
\]
The orthodox route is not to overclaim its smallness, but to separate the redundant part from the truly physical anisotropy and to state exactly what is proved, what is conditional, and what remains open.

\subsubsection*{A. Exact decomposition of quadratic derivative anisotropy}

The quadratic derivative anisotropy tensor admits the exact decomposition
\begin{equation}
\delta K^{ij}_{IJ}
=
\delta^{ij}\,\delta Z_{IJ}
+
\delta_{IJ}\,h^{ij}
+
\widehat K^{ij}_{IJ},
\label{eq:dK_exact_decomp_user}
\end{equation}
with
\[
h_{ii}=0,
\qquad
\widehat K^{ii}_{IJ}=0,
\qquad
\widehat K^{ij}_{II}=0.
\]
Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\delta Z_{IJ}\) is an internal metric deformation,
\item \(h^{ij}\) is a common spatial metric anisotropy,
\item \(\widehat K^{ij}_{IJ}\) is the genuine mixed traceless anisotropy.
\end{itemize}
This decomposition is exact at quadratic order. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

Therefore the cubic anisotropy remainder must be split as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{cub}}
=
B_{\mathrm{red}}
+
B_{\mathrm{phys}},
}
\label{eq:Bcub_split_user}
\end{equation}
where \(B_{\mathrm{red}}\) is the redundant common metric part and \(B_{\mathrm{phys}}\) is the physical relative anisotropy.

\subsubsection*{B. Redundant anisotropy is exactly removable}

The common spatial anisotropy term has the form
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_h
=
\frac12
\int d^d x\,
(Z\delta^{ij}+h^{ij})
\sum_I
\partial_i\Phi_I\,\partial_j\Phi_I,
\qquad
h^i{}_i=0.
\label{eq:Gamma_h_user}
\end{equation}
If \(Z\delta+h\) is positive definite, then there exists an invertible linear coordinate transformation \(y= Mx\) such that
\[
(Z\delta+h)=M^T M,
\]
and therefore
\[
\Gamma_h
\mapsto
\frac12
\int d^d y\,
\delta^{ab}
\sum_I
\partial_{y^a}\Phi_I\,\partial_{y^b}\Phi_I
\]
up to an overall constant Jacobian factor.
Hence \(B_{\mathrm{red}}\) is not a physical coupling and should be removed exactly rather than estimated as a perturbation. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

Thus:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{red}}\ \text{is exactly removable and contributes neither to }\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}\text{ nor to }\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:Bred_removed_user}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection*{C. What remains physically meaningful}

After removing the redundant common metric anisotropy, the physically meaningful derivative anisotropy is
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{\mathrm{phys}}
=
\frac12
\int d^d x\,
\Bigl[
\delta^{ij}\delta Z_{IJ}
+
\widehat K^{ij}_{IJ}
\Bigr]
\partial_i\Phi_I\,\partial_j\Phi_J.
\label{eq:Gamma_phys_user}
\end{equation}
In the block-diagonal TECT truncation this reduces to relative stiffness anisotropies
\[
\delta_T,\qquad \delta_O,\qquad \delta_D,
\]
subject to
\[
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
\]
These are the true velocity-locking / derivative-anisotropy variables. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

At the Gaussian level they are classically marginal:
\begin{equation}
y_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}^{\mathrm{tree}}=0.
\label{eq:y_tree_zero_user}
\end{equation}
Therefore their infrared fate is determined entirely by the loop-level kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\). 

\subsubsection*{D. Honest status of the physical derivative anisotropy}

The document proves the following reduction:

\[
\text{common spatial anisotropy is redundant},
\]
\[
\text{the only physical derivative anisotropy is the relative sectoral velocity anisotropy},
\]
\[
\text{its tree-level scaling is marginal},
\]
\[
\text{its infrared relevance/irrelevance is controlled by the loop-level matrix }M_Z.
\]

What remains open is precisely:
\begin{enumerate}
\item derive the full TECT Hessian including interaction vertices,
\item project the Wetterich flow onto the sectoral kinetic terms,
\item compute the matrix \(M_Z\),
\item verify that its nontrivial eigenvalues are negative.
\end{enumerate}
Thus the sign of the physical derivative anisotropy flow is not yet fixed rigorously from the available TECT data. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

Therefore one must \emph{not} currently claim an unconditional small relative-form bound for \(B_{\mathrm{phys}}\).

\subsubsection*{E. Conditional infrared smallness theorem}

There is nevertheless a correct conditional theorem.

Assume that the physical cubic anisotropy couplings are governed in the infrared by running couplings \(g_a(\Lambda)\) with RG eigenvalues \(y_a<0\), so that
\begin{equation}
g_a(\Lambda)\to 0
\qquad
(\Lambda\to 0).
\label{eq:ga_to_zero_user}
\end{equation}
Then, after removing the redundant part, the physical anisotropy remainder has the representation
\begin{equation}
B_{\mathrm{phys}}(\Lambda,p)
=
\sum_a g_a(\Lambda)\,\mathcal O_a(p,D),
\label{eq:Bphys_expansion_user}
\end{equation}
and for every \(\varepsilon>0\) there exists \(\Lambda_\varepsilon\) such that for all \(\Lambda<\Lambda_\varepsilon\),
\begin{equation}
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{phys},p}[\psi]|
\le
\varepsilon\,K\,\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
C_{\mathrm{phys},\rho}(\varepsilon,\Lambda)\,\|\psi\|^2.
\label{eq:Bphys_relative_cond_user}
\end{equation}
Hence one may set
\begin{equation}
\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}(\Lambda)=\varepsilon,
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}(\Lambda)=C_{\mathrm{phys},\rho}(\varepsilon,\Lambda),
\label{eq:alpha_beta_cub_cond_user}
\end{equation}
with \(\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}(\Lambda)\to 0\) and \(\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}(\Lambda)\to 0\) as \(\Lambda\to 0\), provided the anisotropy operators are indeed IR-irrelevant.

This is the correct conditional relative-bound statement.

\subsubsection*{F. Canonical RG support and its limitation}

In the gauge-covariant infrared EFT, cubic anisotropy operators satisfy canonical dimension
\[
[O_n^{\mathrm{cub}}]\ge 6,
\]
so their linearized RG eigenvalues obey
\[
y_n=4-[O_n^{\mathrm{cub}}]\le -2.
\]
Therefore, at the level of canonical power counting near the Maxwell fixed point, cubic anisotropy operators are IR-irrelevant and their dimensionless couplings vanish as \(\Lambda\to 0\). 

However, the document is explicit that a complete one-loop verification still requires:
\begin{enumerate}
\item identifying the full operator basis generated by the microscopic BCC condensate,
\item computing the anomalous-dimension matrix,
\item checking that all eigenvalues remain negative.
\end{enumerate}
So this is not yet a full microscopic theorem. 

Moreover, in the derivative anisotropy sector the sign of the physical kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\) is still open. Thus the physically most relevant piece of \(B_{\mathrm{phys}}\) is not yet unconditionally controlled. :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

\subsubsection*{G. Final honest bound for the cubic piece}

Therefore the correct present status is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{cub}}
=
B_{\mathrm{red}}
+
B_{\mathrm{phys}},
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{red}}\ \text{exactly removable},
}
\label{eq:Bcub_status1_user}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{phys}}
\text{ admits a small relative-form bound only conditionally on IR irrelevance of the physical anisotropy couplings.}
}
\label{eq:Bcub_status2_user}
\end{equation}

Hence, in the current orthodox analytic program, the cubic contribution may be entered as
\begin{equation}
\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}
=
\alpha_{\mathrm{phys}},
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}
=
\beta_{\mathrm{phys},\rho},
\label{eq:alpha_beta_cub_final_user}
\end{equation}
with the understanding that these are:
\begin{itemize}
\item \emph{not yet explicitly fixed microscopically},
\item but reduced to the RG problem of the physical anisotropy operators / the sign of \(M_Z\).
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{H. Updated extra-sector coercivity statement}

Thus the fully honest extra-sector coercivity constant is
\begin{equation}
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\bigl(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{phys}}-\alpha_{\mathrm H}\bigr)
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\bigl(
\beta_{\mathrm{phys},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+
\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}
\bigr),
\label{eq:cextra_honest_cub_user}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}\) is explicit,
\item \(\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}=O(\rho)\) is explicit,
\item \((\alpha_{\mathrm H},\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho})\) are heavy-suppressed,
\item \((\alpha_{\mathrm{phys}},\beta_{\mathrm{phys},\rho})\) remain open unless the physical cubic anisotropy is proved IR-irrelevant.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Conclusion.}
The last hard analytic remainder is now isolated exactly:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the true unresolved cubic piece is not the redundant common metric anisotropy, but the physical relative derivative anisotropy.}
}
\]
Its control is equivalent to the RG fate of the physical anisotropy operators, or more concretely in the current TECT truncation, to the sign of the kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\).

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{cub}}
=
B_{\mathrm{red}}
+
B_{\mathrm{phys}}.
}
\]

Here
\[
B_{\mathrm{red}}
\]
is the common spatial metric anisotropy, and
\[
B_{\mathrm{phys}}
\]
is the physical relative derivative anisotropy.

The exact quadratic decomposition is
\[
\delta K^{ij}_{IJ}
=
\delta^{ij}\delta Z_{IJ}
+
\delta_{IJ}h^{ij}
+
\widehat K^{ij}_{IJ},
\]
with
\[
h_{ii}=0,\qquad
\widehat K^{ii}_{IJ}=0,\qquad
\widehat K^{ij}_{II}=0.
\]

Redundant part:
\[
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{red}}\ \text{is exactly removable by a linear coordinate transformation,}
}
\]
so it contributes neither to \(\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}\) nor to \(\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}\).

Physical part:
\[
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{phys}}
\text{ is the true derivative/velocity anisotropy sector.}
}
\]
It is classically marginal, and its infrared fate is controlled by the loop-level kinetic-flow matrix
\[
M_Z.
\]

Hence the honest current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Unconditional control of }B_{\mathrm{cub}}\text{ is not yet proved microscopically.}
}
\]

Conditional theorem:
if the physical cubic anisotropy couplings are IR-irrelevant, then for every \(\varepsilon>0\),
\[
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{phys},p}[\psi]|
\le
\varepsilon\,K\,\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
C_{\mathrm{phys},\rho}(\varepsilon,\Lambda)\,\|\psi\|^2,
\]
so that
\[
\alpha_{\mathrm{cub}}(\Lambda)\to 0,
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{cub},\rho}(\Lambda)\to 0
\qquad
(\Lambda\to 0).
\]

Canonical RG support:
\[
[O_n^{\mathrm{cub}}]\ge 6
\Longrightarrow
y_n=4-[O_n^{\mathrm{cub}}]\le -2,
\]
so cubic anisotropy operators are canonically irrelevant at the Maxwell fixed point.

But the full microscopic completion still requires:
\[
\boxed{
\text{identify the full anisotropy operator basis,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute the anomalous-dimension matrix / }M_Z,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{and verify that all physical anisotropy eigenvalues are negative.}
}
\]

Therefore the honest extra-sector coercivity constant is
\[
\boxed{
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{phys}}-\alpha_{\mathrm H})
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
(\beta_{\mathrm{phys},\rho}
+\beta_{\mathrm{pot},\rho}
+\beta_{\mathrm{tr},\rho}
+\beta_{\mathrm H,\rho}).
}
\]

So the final unresolved analytic bottleneck is exactly:
\[
\boxed{
\text{control the physical derivative anisotropy sector }B_{\mathrm{phys}},
\text{ equivalently the sign of }M_Z.
}
\]

\section*{Explicit kinetic-flow matrix derivation roadmap for \texorpdfstring{$M_Z$}{MZ}}

\subsection*{1. Physical derivative-anisotropy variables}

After removing the redundant common spatial metric anisotropy, the physically meaningful derivative anisotropy is the relative sectoral kinetic anisotropy among the three TECT soft sectors:
\[
A,\qquad n,\qquad \chi.
\]
In the block-diagonal TECT truncation this is parameterized by
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{\mathrm{rel}}
=
\frac12
\int d^d x\,
\Bigl[
Z_T \sum_{\alpha=1}^2 (\partial_i A_\alpha)^2
+
Z_O \sum_{a=1}^2 (\partial_i n_a)^2
+
Z_D \sum_{r=1}^2 (\partial_i \chi_r)^2
\Bigr].
\label{eq:Gamma_rel_MZ}
\end{equation}
Define the relative anisotropy variables
\begin{equation}
\delta_T:=\frac{Z_T-Z}{Z},
\qquad
\delta_O:=\frac{Z_O-Z}{Z},
\qquad
\delta_D:=\frac{Z_D-Z}{Z},
\label{eq:deltaZ_def_MZ}
\end{equation}
with the traceless constraint
\begin{equation}
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
\label{eq:traceless_constraint_MZ}
\end{equation}
These are the true velocity-locking variables. They are classically marginal at the Gaussian level, so their infrared fate is determined entirely by the loop-level kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\). 

\subsection*{2. FRG truncation to be used}

The TECT-adapted infrared effective average action must contain, at minimum,
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k[A,n,\chi]
=
\int d^d x\,
\Bigl[
\frac{Z_{T,k}}{2}(\partial A)^2
+
\frac{Z_{O,k}}{2}(\partial n)^2
+
\frac{Z_{D,k}}{2}(\partial \chi)^2
+
U_k(\rho,\tau,\ldots)
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{int}}[A,n,\chi]
\Bigr],
\label{eq:TECT_truncation_MZ}
\end{equation}
where \(\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{int}}\) contains all interaction vertices relevant to the wavefunction renormalization flow. The exact sign of the derivative-anisotropy eigenvalues cannot be determined without these vertices, the regulator, the detailed tensor contractions, and the gauge/constraint structure of the \(A\)-sector. 

\subsection*{3. Starting Wetterich equation}

The flow is governed by the Wetterich equation
\begin{equation}
\partial_t \Gamma_k
=
\frac12
\mathrm{STr}
\left[
\bigl(\Gamma_k^{(2)}+R_k\bigr)^{-1}\partial_t R_k
\right].
\label{eq:Wetterich_MZ}
\end{equation}
To extract \(M_Z\), the required object is the exact Hessian
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[A,n,\chi],
\label{eq:Hessian_MZ}
\end{equation}
including all interaction vertices coupling the three soft sectors. Without this Hessian the sign of \(M_Z\) is underdetermined. 

\subsection*{4. Sectoral kinetic projectors}

Introduce the three kinetic projectors
\begin{equation}
\Pi_T,\qquad \Pi_O,\qquad \Pi_D,
\label{eq:PiTOD_MZ}
\end{equation}
which project onto the spatial two-derivative operators of the three soft sectors:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal O_T
=
\frac12\sum_{\alpha=1}^2(\partial_i A_\alpha)^2,
\qquad
\mathcal O_O
=
\frac12\sum_{a=1}^2(\partial_i n_a)^2,
\qquad
\mathcal O_D
=
\frac12\sum_{r=1}^2(\partial_i \chi_r)^2.
\label{eq:kinetic_ops_MZ}
\end{equation}
Then define the sectoral wavefunction flows by
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_T
=
\Pi_T\bigl[\partial_t\Gamma_k\bigr],
\qquad
\partial_t Z_O
=
\Pi_O\bigl[\partial_t\Gamma_k\bigr],
\qquad
\partial_t Z_D
=
\Pi_D\bigl[\partial_t\Gamma_k\bigr].
\label{eq:sectoral_Z_flows}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, one can extract these by taking the second derivative of the two-point functions and differentiating with respect to spatial momentum:
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_I
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
\label{eq:Z_projection_2pt}
\end{equation}
This is the standard route to the kinetic-flow matrix.

\subsection*{5. Linearization around the isotropic point}

Let
\[
Z_{T,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_T),\qquad
Z_{O,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_O),\qquad
Z_{D,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_D),
\]
with \(\delta_I\) small and subject to \eqref{eq:traceless_constraint_MZ}. Linearizing the three sectoral flows around the isotropic point gives
\begin{equation}
\partial_t
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
=
M_Z
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^2).
\label{eq:MZ_linearized}
\end{equation}
The matrix entries are the Jacobian
\begin{equation}
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\bigl(\partial_t \delta_I\bigr)
\right|_{\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{T,O,D\}.
\label{eq:MZ_Jacobian}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Equivalent traceless-basis reduction}

Since the common rescaling direction is unphysical, it is often cleaner to pass to a traceless basis:
\begin{equation}
u_1=\delta_T-\delta_O,
\qquad
u_2=\delta_T-\delta_D.
\label{eq:traceless_basis_MZ}
\end{equation}
Then the physical derivative-anisotropy flow is the \(2\times2\) matrix obtained by restricting \(M_Z\) to the subspace
\[
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
\]
Negative eigenvalues on this subspace are exactly the criterion for velocity locking and derivative-anisotropy irrelevance. 

\subsection*{7. Algebraic target}

A controlled sufficient target already identified in the document is
\begin{equation}
M_Z
=
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
2 & -1 & -1\\
-1 & 2 & -1\\
-1 & -1 & 2
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0.
\label{eq:MZ_target}
\end{equation}
This matrix has one zero mode corresponding to the unphysical common rescaling direction
\[
\delta_T=\delta_O=\delta_D,
\]
and two negative eigenvalues
\[
-3\lambda,\qquad -3\lambda
\]
on the traceless physical subspace. Therefore if the explicit FRG projection yields \eqref{eq:MZ_target} with \(\lambda>0\), derivative anisotropy is strictly irrelevant. 

\subsection*{8. Minimal loop ingredients}

The explicit computation of \(M_Z\) requires the following loop data:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact Hessian \(\Gamma_k^{(2)}\) including vertices coupling \(A,n,\chi\);
\item a fixed regulator \(R_k\);
\item the tensor contractions entering the momentum-dependent two-point functions;
\item the gauge/constraint structure of the \(A\)-sector.
\end{enumerate}

This is precisely where the current proof stops honestly: with present TECT truncation data, the sign of \(M_Z\) is not yet fixed. 

\subsection*{9. Conditional theorem and roadmap conclusion}

The exact current theorem-level status is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{If the nontrivial eigenvalues of }M_Z\text{ are negative, then }
\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D\to 0
\text{ in the infrared.}
}
\label{eq:conditional_MZ_theorem}
\end{equation}
Thus the remaining derivation task is no longer conceptual. It is the explicit FRG projection problem:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[A,n,\chi]
\ \Longrightarrow\
\partial_t Z_T,\ \partial_t Z_O,\ \partial_t Z_D
\ \Longrightarrow\
M_Z
\ \Longrightarrow\
\operatorname{sign}\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathrm{traceless}}).
}
\label{eq:MZ_roadmap_chain}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\delta_T=\frac{Z_T-Z}{Z},
\qquad
\delta_O=\frac{Z_O-Z}{Z},
\qquad
\delta_D=\frac{Z_D-Z}{Z},
\qquad
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
}
\]

These are the true physical derivative-anisotropy variables.
They are classically marginal, so their infrared fate is controlled entirely by the loop-level kinetic-flow matrix
\[
\boxed{
\partial_t
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
=
M_Z
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
+\cdots .
}
\]

To derive \(M_Z\), one must:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(1) write } \Gamma_k[A,n,\chi],
\quad
\text{(2) compute } \Gamma_k^{(2)},
\quad
\text{(3) insert into the Wetterich equation,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(4) project onto } \mathcal O_T,\mathcal O_O,\mathcal O_D,
\quad
\text{(5) linearize the flows of } Z_T,Z_O,Z_D.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\partial_t Z_I
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\},
\]
and
\[
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
(\partial_t \delta_I)
\right|_{\delta=0}.
\]

The algebraic target is
\[
\boxed{
M_Z
=
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
2 & -1 & -1\\
-1 & 2 & -1\\
-1 & -1 & 2
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0.
}
\]
Then the unphysical common-rescaling mode is the unique zero mode, and the two physical eigenvalues are
\[
\boxed{
-3\lambda,\qquad -3\lambda.
}
\]
Hence derivative anisotropy is strictly irrelevant.

Honest status:
\[
\boxed{
\text{with the currently available TECT truncation data, sign}(M_Z)\text{ is still not fixed.}
}
\]
What is still required is:
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[A,n,\chi],\quad
R_k,\quad
\text{tensor contractions},\quad
\text{A-sector gauge/constraint projection}.
}
\]
