\section*{TECT-adapted minimal FRG truncation for the kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\)}

\subsection*{1. Physical derivative-anisotropy variables}

After removing the redundant common spatial metric anisotropy, the physically meaningful quadratic derivative anisotropy is the \emph{relative} sectoral kinetic anisotropy among the three TECT soft sectors:
\[
A,\qquad n,\qquad \chi.
\]
The block-diagonal kinetic sector is parameterized as
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{\mathrm{kin}}
=
\frac12
\int d^d x\,
\Biggl[
Z_{T,k}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}(\partial_i A_\alpha)^2
+
Z_{O,k}\sum_{a=1}^{2}(\partial_i n_a)^2
+
Z_{D,k}\sum_{r=1}^{2}(\partial_i \chi_r)^2
\Biggr].
\label{eq:Gamma_kin_MZ_min}
\end{equation}
Define the relative anisotropy variables
\begin{equation}
\delta_T:=\frac{Z_{T,k}-Z_k}{Z_k},
\qquad
\delta_O:=\frac{Z_{O,k}-Z_k}{Z_k},
\qquad
\delta_D:=\frac{Z_{D,k}-Z_k}{Z_k},
\label{eq:delta_TOD_def}
\end{equation}
with the traceless constraint
\begin{equation}
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
\label{eq:traceless_TOD}
\end{equation}
These are the true physical velocity-locking variables. They are classically marginal at the Gaussian level, so their infrared fate is determined entirely by the loop-level kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\). :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection*{2. Minimal TECT-adapted FRG ansatz}

A minimal infrared FRG truncation adapted to the TECT soft sector is
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k[A,n,\chi]
=
\int d^d x\,
\Biggl[
\frac{Z_{T,k}}{2}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}(\partial_i A_\alpha)^2
+
\frac{Z_{O,k}}{2}\sum_{a=1}^{2}(\partial_i n_a)^2
+
\frac{Z_{D,k}}{2}\sum_{r=1}^{2}(\partial_i \chi_r)^2
+
Y_k\,O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}
+
U_k(\rho,\tau)
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{int}}[A,n,\chi]
\Biggr].
\label{eq:Gamma_k_minimal_MZ}
\end{equation}
Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(Z_{T,k},Z_{O,k},Z_{D,k}\) are the sectoral wavefunction renormalizations,
\item \(O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}\) is the leading derivative-anisotropy operator allowed by the BCC background,
\item \(U_k(\rho,\tau)\) is the local isotropic-plus-leading-anisotropy potential truncation,
\item \(\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{int}}[A,n,\chi]\) contains all interaction vertices required to generate the momentum-dependent two-point flow.
\end{itemize}
A minimal polynomial potential truncation is
\begin{equation}
U_k(\rho,\tau)=r_k\,\rho+\frac{u_k}{2}\rho^2+g_{\tau,k}\,\tau.
\label{eq:Uk_poly_MZ}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the TECT-adapted FRG structure already identified in the document. 

\subsection*{3. Wetterich equation and regulator}

The flow is governed by the Wetterich equation
\begin{equation}
\partial_t\Gamma_k
=
\frac12
\mathrm{Tr}
\Bigl[
(\Gamma_k^{(2)}+R_k)^{-1}\,\partial_t R_k
\Bigr],
\qquad
t=\ln(k/\Lambda).
\label{eq:Wetterich_MZ_min}
\end{equation}
A standard optimized regulator choice is
\begin{equation}
R_k(q)=Z_k(k^2-q^2)\Theta(k^2-q^2),
\label{eq:Rk_optimized_MZ}
\end{equation}
or, more carefully in the sectoral setting,
\begin{equation}
R_k(q)
=
\mathrm{diag}
\Bigl(
Z_{T,k}\,r_k(q),
\,Z_{O,k}\,r_k(q),
\,Z_{D,k}\,r_k(q)
\Bigr),
\label{eq:Rk_sectoral_MZ}
\end{equation}
with the same shape function \(r_k\) on the three soft sectors.
The exact sign of the derivative-anisotropy flow cannot be fixed without specifying \(\Gamma_k^{(2)}\), \(R_k\), the tensor contractions, and the gauge/constraint structure of the \(A\)-sector. 

\subsection*{4. Sectoral kinetic projectors}

Introduce the three kinetic projection operators
\begin{equation}
\Pi_T,\qquad \Pi_O,\qquad \Pi_D,
\label{eq:Pi_TOD}
\end{equation}
defined by projection onto the three spatial kinetic operators
\begin{equation}
\mathcal O_T
=
\frac12\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}(\partial_i A_\alpha)^2,
\qquad
\mathcal O_O
=
\frac12\sum_{a=1}^{2}(\partial_i n_a)^2,
\qquad
\mathcal O_D
=
\frac12\sum_{r=1}^{2}(\partial_i \chi_r)^2.
\label{eq:O_TOD}
\end{equation}
Then the sectoral wavefunction flows are defined by
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_{T,k}=\Pi_T[\partial_t\Gamma_k],
\qquad
\partial_t Z_{O,k}=\Pi_O[\partial_t\Gamma_k],
\qquad
\partial_t Z_{D,k}=\Pi_D[\partial_t\Gamma_k].
\label{eq:Z_flows_projected}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the two-point-function language, let
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}_{k,TT}(p),\qquad
\Gamma^{(2)}_{k,OO}(p),\qquad
\Gamma^{(2)}_{k,DD}(p)
\]
denote the diagonal two-point blocks of the three sectors.
Then
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_{I,k}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
\label{eq:Z_projection_2pt_MZ}
\end{equation}
This is the standard projection formula for extracting sectoral wavefunction renormalization flows.

\subsection*{5. Linearization around the isotropic point}

Write
\begin{equation}
Z_{T,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_T),
\qquad
Z_{O,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_O),
\qquad
Z_{D,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_D),
\label{eq:Z_expand_delta}
\end{equation}
with small \(\delta_I\) and constraint \eqref{eq:traceless_TOD}.
Linearizing the sectoral kinetic flows around the isotropic point gives
\begin{equation}
\partial_t
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
=
M_Z
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
+
O(\delta^2).
\label{eq:MZ_linearized_final}
\end{equation}
The matrix entries are the Jacobian
\begin{equation}
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\bigl(\partial_t\delta_I\bigr)
\right|_{\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{T,O,D\}.
\label{eq:MZ_Jacobian_final}
\end{equation}
Thus \(M_Z\) is not guessed: it is \emph{defined} by the linearization of the projected Wetterich flow.

\subsection*{6. Traceless-basis reduction}

Since the common rescaling direction is unphysical, it is convenient to pass to a traceless basis:
\begin{equation}
u_1=\delta_T-\delta_O,
\qquad
u_2=\delta_T-\delta_D.
\label{eq:u12_traceless}
\end{equation}
Let
\[
M_Z^{\mathrm{phys}}
\]
denote the restriction of \(M_Z\) to the two-dimensional traceless subspace
\[
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
\]
Then:
\[
\boxed{
\text{derivative anisotropy is infrared-irrelevant}
\iff
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z^{\mathrm{phys}})\subset(-\infty,0).
}
\]
This is the exact physical criterion.

\subsection*{7. Algebraic target}

A controlled sufficient target already identified in the document is
\begin{equation}
M_Z
=
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
2 & -1 & -1\\
-1 & 2 & -1\\
-1 & -1 & 2
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0.
\label{eq:MZ_target_final}
\end{equation}
This matrix has:
\begin{itemize}
\item one zero mode corresponding to the unphysical common-rescaling direction
\[
\delta_T=\delta_O=\delta_D,
\]
\item two negative eigenvalues
\[
-3\lambda,\qquad -3\lambda
\]
on the traceless physical subspace.
\end{itemize}
Hence, if the explicit FRG projection yields \eqref{eq:MZ_target_final} with \(\lambda>0\), then the physical derivative anisotropy is strictly irrelevant and velocity locking follows. 

\subsection*{8. What must still be specified}

To turn this roadmap into an actual sign computation, the following microscopic ingredients are still required:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact Hessian \(\Gamma_k^{(2)}[A,n,\chi]\) including all interaction vertices coupling the three soft sectors,
\item a fixed regulator choice \(R_k\),
\item the explicit tensor contractions contributing to the momentum derivative of the two-point functions,
\item the gauge/constraint projection in the \(A\)-sector.
\end{enumerate}
This is exactly where the honest proof presently stops: with currently available TECT truncation data, the sign of the nontrivial eigenvalues of \(M_Z\) is not yet fixed. 

\subsection*{9. Final roadmap theorem}

Therefore the correct final theorem-level roadmap is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_k[A,n,\chi]
\ \Longrightarrow\
\Gamma_k^{(2)}
\ \Longrightarrow\
\partial_t Z_T,\ \partial_t Z_O,\ \partial_t Z_D
\ \Longrightarrow\
M_Z
\ \Longrightarrow\
\operatorname{sign}\operatorname{spec}(M_Z^{\mathrm{phys}}).
}
\label{eq:MZ_roadmap_final}
\end{equation}
And the correct conditional theorem is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{If }
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z^{\mathrm{phys}})\subset(-\infty,0),
\text{ then }
\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D\to 0
\text{ in the infrared.}
}
\label{eq:MZ_conditional_velocity_locking}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_k[A,n,\chi]
=
\int d^d x\,
\Biggl[
\frac{Z_{T,k}}{2}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}(\partial_i A_\alpha)^2
+
\frac{Z_{O,k}}{2}\sum_{a=1}^{2}(\partial_i n_a)^2
+
\frac{Z_{D,k}}{2}\sum_{r=1}^{2}(\partial_i \chi_r)^2
+
Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}
+
U_k(\rho,\tau)
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{int}}
\Biggr].
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\delta_T=\frac{Z_{T,k}-Z_k}{Z_k},
\qquad
\delta_O=\frac{Z_{O,k}-Z_k}{Z_k},
\qquad
\delta_D=\frac{Z_{D,k}-Z_k}{Z_k},
\qquad
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
}
\]

Sectoral wavefunction flows are extracted by
\[
\boxed{
\partial_t Z_{I,k}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
}
\]

Linearizing around the isotropic point gives
\[
\boxed{
\partial_t
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
=
M_Z
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^2),
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
(\partial_t \delta_I)
\right|_{\delta=0}.
}
\]

The physical criterion is negativity on the traceless subspace.
A sufficient algebraic target is
\[
\boxed{
M_Z
=
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
2 & -1 & -1\\
-1 & 2 & -1\\
-1 & -1 & 2
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0,
}
\]
for which the two physical eigenvalues are
\[
\boxed{
-3\lambda,\qquad -3\lambda.
}
\]

Hence the remaining frontier is exactly:
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[A,n,\chi],\quad
R_k,\quad
\text{tensor contractions},\quad
\text{\(A\)-sector gauge/constraint projection}.
}
\]

And the honest final conditional theorem is:
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z^{\mathrm{phys}})\subset(-\infty,0)
\Longrightarrow
\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D\to 0
\text{ in the infrared.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Minimal vertex-complete truncation for the kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\)}

\subsection*{A. Why the schematic truncation is not enough}

The schematic TECT infrared truncation already identified in the document is
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k[\Phi]
=
\int d^d x
\left[
\frac{Z_{T,k}}{2}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}(\partial_iA_\alpha)^2
+
\frac{Z_{O,k}}{2}\sum_{a=1}^{2}(\partial_i n_a)^2
+
\frac{Z_{D,k}}{2}\sum_{r=1}^{2}(\partial_i\chi_r)^2
+
Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}
+
U_k(\rho,\tau)
\right],
\label{eq:schematic_truncation_MZ}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\Phi=(A_1,A_2,n_1,n_2,\chi_1,\chi_2),
\qquad
N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6.
\]
This truncation is sufficient to state the \emph{schematic} isotropy theorem and to identify the derivative-anisotropy problem. 

However, it is not yet sufficient to determine the sign of the linearized kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\), because the document is explicit that \(M_Z\) depends on:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact Hessian \(\Gamma_k^{(2)}\),
\item the interaction vertices coupling \(A,n,\chi\),
\item the regulator choice,
\item the detailed tensor contractions,
\item the gauge/constraint structure of the \(A\)-sector.
\end{enumerate}
Therefore, to compute \(M_Z\), one needs a \emph{vertex-complete} truncation for the sectoral two-point flows. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection*{B. Sectoral invariants}

Define the three quadratic sectoral invariants
\begin{equation}
\rho_T:=\frac12\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}A_\alpha^2,
\qquad
\rho_O:=\frac12\sum_{a=1}^{2}n_a^2,
\qquad
\rho_D:=\frac12\sum_{r=1}^{2}\chi_r^2,
\label{eq:rho_TOD}
\end{equation}
so that
\[
\rho=\rho_T+\rho_O+\rho_D.
\]

The leading quartic cubic anisotropy already used in the isotropy analysis is encoded by the traceless quartic invariant
\[
\tau(\Phi)=\sum_{I=1}^{6}\Phi_I^4-\frac{3}{N_{\mathrm{eff}}+2}(\Phi_J\Phi_J)^2,
\qquad N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6.
\]
Thus \(U_k(\rho,\tau)\) captures the isotropic quartic sector plus the leading quartic cubic anisotropy. 

\subsection*{C. Minimal sufficient vertex-complete ansatz}

A minimal \emph{sufficient} vertex-complete truncation for extracting \(M_Z\) is:
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k^{\mathrm{VC}}[A,n,\chi]
=
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{kin}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{pot}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}}.
\label{eq:Gamma_VC_split}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(i) Sectoral kinetic part}
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{kin}}
=
\frac12\int d^d x
\Biggl[
Z_{T,k}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}(\partial_iA_\alpha)^2
+
Z_{O,k}\sum_{a=1}^{2}(\partial_i n_a)^2
+
Z_{D,k}\sum_{r=1}^{2}(\partial_i\chi_r)^2
\Biggr].
\label{eq:Gamma_kin_VC}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(ii) Minimal quartic potential sector}
Instead of keeping only \(U_k(\rho,\tau)\) abstractly, write the minimal explicit quartic sector as
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{pot}}
=
\int d^d x\,
\Bigl[
r_{T,k}\rho_T+r_{O,k}\rho_O+r_{D,k}\rho_D
+
\frac{\lambda_{T,k}}{2}\rho_T^2
+
\frac{\lambda_{O,k}}{2}\rho_O^2
+
\frac{\lambda_{D,k}}{2}\rho_D^2
+
\lambda_{TO,k}\rho_T\rho_O
+
\lambda_{TD,k}\rho_T\rho_D
+
\lambda_{OD,k}\rho_O\rho_D
+
g_{\tau,k}\,\tau(\Phi)
\Bigr].
\label{eq:Gamma_pot_VC}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal explicit potential completion needed so that:
\begin{enumerate}
\item each sector has its own self-interaction,
\item each sector can renormalize the kinetic term of the others through one-loop mixed self-energies,
\item the leading cubic quartic anisotropy is retained.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{(iii) Leading derivative anisotropy}
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k,\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
=
Y_k\int d^d x\,O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}[A,n,\chi].
\label{eq:Gamma_gradani_VC}
\end{equation}
Here \(O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}\) is the leading BCC-allowed derivative anisotropy operator already isolated in the isotropy analysis. 

\paragraph{(iv) Gauge / constraint projection in the \(A\)-sector}
Because the sign of \(M_Z\) depends on the gauge or constraint structure of the \(A\)-sector, one must include either:
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}}
=
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf}}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{proj}}
\end{equation}
so that the \(A\)-sector Hessian entering the Wetterich trace is already projected onto the physical transverse/allowed subspace. The current data do not yet fix this uniquely, but some explicit gauge/constraint implementation is mandatory. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection*{D. Why these vertices are minimally necessary}

To compute
\[
\partial_t Z_T,\qquad \partial_t Z_O,\qquad \partial_t Z_D,
\]
one must project the momentum derivative of the one-loop two-point functions in each sector:
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_{I,k}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
\label{eq:Z_projection_VC}
\end{equation}
At one loop, these flows receive contributions from any quartic or derivative vertex that couples the \(I\)-sector to itself or to one of the other sectors. Therefore:

\begin{itemize}
\item omitting \(\lambda_{TO},\lambda_{TD},\lambda_{OD}\) would miss mixed-loop contributions to the sectoral two-point functions;
\item omitting \(g_{\tau,k}\tau\) would miss the leading quartic cubic-anisotropy contribution;
\item omitting \(Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}\) would miss the derivative-anisotropy insertion itself;
\item omitting the \(A\)-sector projection/gauge treatment would leave the \(A\)-sector Hessian ambiguous.
\end{itemize}

Thus \eqref{eq:Gamma_VC_split}--\eqref{eq:Gamma_gradani_VC} is the minimal \emph{sufficient} truncation to define \(M_Z\) unambiguously at the formal one-loop projection level.

\subsection*{E. Projectors and Jacobian definition of \(M_Z\)}

Define the three kinetic projectors
\[
\Pi_T,\qquad \Pi_O,\qquad \Pi_D,
\]
onto
\[
\mathcal O_T=\frac12\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}(\partial_iA_\alpha)^2,
\quad
\mathcal O_O=\frac12\sum_{a=1}^{2}(\partial_i n_a)^2,
\quad
\mathcal O_D=\frac12\sum_{r=1}^{2}(\partial_i\chi_r)^2.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_{T,k}=\Pi_T[\partial_t\Gamma_k^{\mathrm{VC}}],
\qquad
\partial_t Z_{O,k}=\Pi_O[\partial_t\Gamma_k^{\mathrm{VC}}],
\qquad
\partial_t Z_{D,k}=\Pi_D[\partial_t\Gamma_k^{\mathrm{VC}}].
\label{eq:Pi_projected_Zflows_VC}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\[
\partial_t Z_{I,k}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
\]

Write
\[
Z_{T,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_T),\qquad
Z_{O,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_O),\qquad
Z_{D,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_D),
\]
with
\[
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
\]
Then the kinetic-flow matrix is defined by linearization:
\begin{equation}
\partial_t
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
=
M_Z
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^2),
\qquad
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
(\partial_t\delta_I)
\right|_{\delta=0}.
\label{eq:MZ_from_VC}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{F. Honest status}

The exact honest statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The truncation } \Gamma_k^{\mathrm{VC}}
\text{ above is a minimal sufficient vertex-complete ansatz for formally defining }M_Z.
}
\]

What is still \emph{not} closed is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact tensor structure of \(O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}\) in the full corrected microscopic TECT model,
\item the exact \(A\)-sector gauge/constraint projector,
\item the actual evaluation of the one-loop tensor contractions,
\item the sign of the nontrivial eigenvalues of \(M_Z\).
\end{enumerate}

So this step closes the formal truncation problem, but not yet the sign computation itself.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\Phi=(A_1,A_2,n_1,n_2,\chi_1,\chi_2),\qquad N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6.
}
\]

The schematic TECT truncation
\[
\Gamma_k[\Phi]
=
\int d^d x
\left[
\frac{Z_{T,k}}{2}(\partial A)^2
+
\frac{Z_{O,k}}{2}(\partial n)^2
+
\frac{Z_{D,k}}{2}(\partial \chi)^2
+
Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}
+
U_k(\rho,\tau)
\right]
\]
is sufficient for the \emph{schematic} isotropy theorem, but not sufficient to determine \(\operatorname{sign}(M_Z)\).

A minimal \emph{sufficient} vertex-complete ansatz for the formal \(M_Z\) projection is
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_k^{\mathrm{VC}}
=
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{kin}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{pot}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}},
}
\]
with
\[
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{kin}}
=
\frac12\int d^d x
\Bigl[
Z_{T,k}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}(\partial_iA_\alpha)^2
+
Z_{O,k}\sum_{a=1}^{2}(\partial_i n_a)^2
+
Z_{D,k}\sum_{r=1}^{2}(\partial_i\chi_r)^2
\Bigr],
\]
\[
\rho_T=\frac12\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}A_\alpha^2,\qquad
\rho_O=\frac12\sum_{a=1}^{2}n_a^2,\qquad
\rho_D=\frac12\sum_{r=1}^{2}\chi_r^2,
\]
\[
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{pot}}
=
\int d^d x\,
\Bigl[
r_{T,k}\rho_T+r_{O,k}\rho_O+r_{D,k}\rho_D
+
\frac{\lambda_{T,k}}{2}\rho_T^2
+
\frac{\lambda_{O,k}}{2}\rho_O^2
+
\frac{\lambda_{D,k}}{2}\rho_D^2
+
\lambda_{TO,k}\rho_T\rho_O
+
\lambda_{TD,k}\rho_T\rho_D
+
\lambda_{OD,k}\rho_O\rho_D
+
g_{\tau,k}\tau(\Phi)
\Bigr],
\]
\[
\Gamma_{k,\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
=
Y_k\int d^d x\,O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}[A,n,\chi].
\]

Then
\[
\partial_t Z_{I,k}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\},
\]
and with
\[
Z_{T,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_T),\quad
Z_{O,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_O),\quad
Z_{D,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_D),
\quad
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0,
\]
the kinetic-flow matrix is
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
(\partial_t\delta_I)
\right|_{\delta=0}.
}
\]

Thus the truncation problem is formally closed.

What remains open is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the explicit evaluation of the Hessian, regulator contractions, and \(A\)-sector projection needed to compute the sign of }M_Z.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Formal block Hessian of the minimal vertex-complete TECT truncation}

\subsection*{1. Field organization}

Introduce the three soft-sector vectors
\[
A=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1\\ A_2
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
n=
\begin{pmatrix}
n_1\\ n_2
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\chi=
\begin{pmatrix}
\chi_1\\ \chi_2
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and collect them into the six-component multiplet
\[
\Phi=
\begin{pmatrix}
A\\ n\\ \chi
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
This is the \(N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6\) soft TECT infrared multiplet already identified in the document. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

Define the sectoral quadratic invariants
\[
\rho_T=\frac12 A^T A,
\qquad
\rho_O=\frac12 n^T n,
\qquad
\rho_D=\frac12 \chi^T \chi,
\qquad
\rho=\rho_T+\rho_O+\rho_D.
\]

\subsection*{2. Minimal vertex-complete ansatz}

A minimal sufficient vertex-complete truncation for the formal \(M_Z\) projection is
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k^{\mathrm{VC}}[A,n,\chi]
=
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{kin}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{pot}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}},
\label{eq:GammaVC_block}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{kin}}
=
\frac12
\int d^d x
\Bigl[
Z_{T,k}\,(\partial_i A)^T(\partial_i A)
+
Z_{O,k}\,(\partial_i n)^T(\partial_i n)
+
Z_{D,k}\,(\partial_i \chi)^T(\partial_i \chi)
\Bigr],
\label{eq:Gamma_kin_block}
\end{equation}
\begin{align}
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{pot}}
=
\int d^d x\,
\Bigl[
&r_{T,k}\rho_T+r_{O,k}\rho_O+r_{D,k}\rho_D
+\frac{\lambda_{T,k}}{2}\rho_T^2
+\frac{\lambda_{O,k}}{2}\rho_O^2
+\frac{\lambda_{D,k}}{2}\rho_D^2 \nonumber\\
&+\lambda_{TO,k}\rho_T\rho_O
+\lambda_{TD,k}\rho_T\rho_D
+\lambda_{OD,k}\rho_O\rho_D
+g_{\tau,k}\,\tau(\Phi)
\Bigr],
\label{eq:Gamma_pot_block}
\end{align}
and
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k,\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
=
Y_k\int d^d x\,
O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}[A,n,\chi].
\label{eq:Gamma_gradani_block}
\end{equation}
Here \(\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}}\) is whatever gauge-fixing or physical projector is needed to define the \(A\)-sector Hessian unambiguously. The document is explicit that some such gauge/constraint treatment is required before the sign of \(M_Z\) can be fixed. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection*{3. General block Hessian}

The full Hessian is the \(6\times 6\) block operator
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k^{(2)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_{TT}^{(2)}(p) & \Gamma_{TO}^{(2)}(p) & \Gamma_{TD}^{(2)}(p)\\[1mm]
\Gamma_{OT}^{(2)}(p) & \Gamma_{OO}^{(2)}(p) & \Gamma_{OD}^{(2)}(p)\\[1mm]
\Gamma_{DT}^{(2)}(p) & \Gamma_{DO}^{(2)}(p) & \Gamma_{DD}^{(2)}(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Gamma2_block_matrix}
\end{equation}
where each entry is a \(2\times2\) matrix differential operator (or, after Fourier/Bloch reduction, a \(2\times2\) matrix-valued symbol).

\subsubsection*{A. Diagonal blocks}

Differentiating \eqref{eq:GammaVC_block} twice gives the formal diagonal blocks
\begin{align}
\Gamma_{TT}^{(2)}(p)
&=
\Bigl[
Z_{T,k}\,p^2
+r_{T,k}
+\lambda_{T,k}\rho_T
+\lambda_{TO,k}\rho_O
+\lambda_{TD,k}\rho_D
\Bigr]\mathbf 1_2
+\lambda_{T,k}\,A A^T
\nonumber\\
&\qquad
+g_{\tau,k}\,
\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial A\,\partial A}
+
Y_k\,\mathcal K_{TT}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(p)
+
\mathcal G_A(p),
\label{eq:GTT_formal}
\\[1mm]
\Gamma_{OO}^{(2)}(p)
&=
\Bigl[
Z_{O,k}\,p^2
+r_{O,k}
+\lambda_{O,k}\rho_O
+\lambda_{TO,k}\rho_T
+\lambda_{OD,k}\rho_D
\Bigr]\mathbf 1_2
+\lambda_{O,k}\,n n^T
\nonumber\\
&\qquad
+g_{\tau,k}\,
\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial n\,\partial n}
+
Y_k\,\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(p),
\label{eq:GOO_formal}
\\[1mm]
\Gamma_{DD}^{(2)}(p)
&=
\Bigl[
Z_{D,k}\,p^2
+r_{D,k}
+\lambda_{D,k}\rho_D
+\lambda_{TD,k}\rho_T
+\lambda_{OD,k}\rho_O
\Bigr]\mathbf 1_2
+\lambda_{D,k}\,\chi\chi^T
\nonumber\\
&\qquad
+g_{\tau,k}\,
\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial \chi\,\partial \chi}
+
Y_k\,\mathcal K_{DD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(p).
\label{eq:GDD_formal}
\end{align}
Here \(\mathcal G_A(p)\) denotes the \(A\)-sector gauge-fixing / constraint projection contribution.

\subsubsection*{B. Off-diagonal blocks}

The mixed Hessian blocks are
\begin{align}
\Gamma_{TO}^{(2)}(p)
&=
\lambda_{TO,k}\,A n^T
+
g_{\tau,k}\,
\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial A\,\partial n}
+
Y_k\,\mathcal K_{TO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(p),
\label{eq:GTO_formal}
\\[1mm]
\Gamma_{TD}^{(2)}(p)
&=
\lambda_{TD,k}\,A \chi^T
+
g_{\tau,k}\,
\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial A\,\partial \chi}
+
Y_k\,\mathcal K_{TD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(p),
\label{eq:GTD_formal}
\\[1mm]
\Gamma_{OD}^{(2)}(p)
&=
\lambda_{OD,k}\,n \chi^T
+
g_{\tau,k}\,
\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial n\,\partial \chi}
+
Y_k\,\mathcal K_{OD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(p),
\label{eq:GOD_formal}
\end{align}
with the transpose/Hermitian-conjugate relations
\[
\Gamma_{OT}^{(2)}=(\Gamma_{TO}^{(2)})^T,
\qquad
\Gamma_{DT}^{(2)}=(\Gamma_{TD}^{(2)})^T,
\qquad
\Gamma_{DO}^{(2)}=(\Gamma_{OD}^{(2)})^T.
\]

\subsection*{4. Specialization to the isotropic symmetric point}

For the linearized \(M_Z\) analysis one expands around the isotropic symmetric point
\[
A=0,\qquad n=0,\qquad \chi=0,
\qquad
Z_{T,k}=Z_{O,k}=Z_{D,k}=Z_k.
\]
At that point,
\[
\rho_T=\rho_O=\rho_D=0,
\]
and the quartic cross terms do not contribute directly to the mixed Hessian entries. Therefore the block Hessian simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k^{(2)}(p)\Big|_{\Phi=0}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
(Z_kp^2+r_{T,k})\mathbf 1_2 + g_{\tau,k}\tau_{AA}^{\prime\prime} + Y_k\mathcal K_{TT}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}} + \mathcal G_A
&
g_{\tau,k}\tau_{An}^{\prime\prime} + Y_k\mathcal K_{TO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
&
g_{\tau,k}\tau_{A\chi}^{\prime\prime} + Y_k\mathcal K_{TD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
\\[1mm]
\ast
&
(Z_kp^2+r_{O,k})\mathbf 1_2 + g_{\tau,k}\tau_{nn}^{\prime\prime} + Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
&
g_{\tau,k}\tau_{n\chi}^{\prime\prime} + Y_k\mathcal K_{OD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
\\[1mm]
\ast & \ast &
(Z_kp^2+r_{D,k})\mathbf 1_2 + g_{\tau,k}\tau_{\chi\chi}^{\prime\prime} + Y_k\mathcal K_{DD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Gamma2_at_zero}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Honest caution.}
If the quartic anisotropy \(\tau(\Phi)\) and the derivative-anisotropy operator \(O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}\) are chosen so that their mixed second derivatives vanish at \(\Phi=0\), then the Hessian at the symmetric point becomes block diagonal.
This does \emph{not} mean that mixed couplings are irrelevant for \(M_Z\). It means only that they enter the flow of the two-point functions through higher vertices \(\Gamma_k^{(3)}\) and \(\Gamma_k^{(4)}\), not directly through off-diagonal entries of \(\Gamma_k^{(2)}|_{\Phi=0}\).

\subsection*{5. Why mixed quartic vertices are still needed}

The Wetterich equation for the two-point function flow schematically gives
\begin{equation}
\partial_t \Gamma_k^{(2)}
=
-\frac12 \mathrm{Tr}\bigl[G_k\,\Gamma_k^{(4)}\,G_k\,\partial_t R_k\bigr]
+
\mathrm{Tr}\bigl[
G_k\,\Gamma_k^{(3)}\,G_k\,\Gamma_k^{(3)}\,G_k\,\partial_t R_k
\bigr],
\label{eq:flow_2pt_schematic}
\end{equation}
with
\[
G_k=(\Gamma_k^{(2)}+R_k)^{-1}.
\]
Therefore, even if the block Hessian at \(\Phi=0\) is diagonal, the flow of
\[
\Gamma_{TT}^{(2)},\qquad
\Gamma_{OO}^{(2)},\qquad
\Gamma_{DD}^{(2)}
\]
still depends on the quartic cross vertices
\[
\lambda_{TO,k},\qquad
\lambda_{TD,k},\qquad
\lambda_{OD,k},
\]
as well as on \(g_{\tau,k}\) and \(Y_k\), because these enter \(\Gamma_k^{(4)}\) and \(\Gamma_k^{(3)}\).
This is exactly why the sign of \(M_Z\) cannot be fixed from the structural truncation alone. The document states that one needs the exact Hessian including the interaction vertices coupling \(A,n,\chi\), the regulator, tensor contractions, and the \(A\)-sector gauge/constraint structure. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection*{6. Sectoral kinetic projection}

Once \(\Gamma_k^{(2)}\) is fixed, the sectoral wavefunction flows are extracted by
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_{I,k}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
\label{eq:ZI_projection_block}
\end{equation}
Then, writing
\[
Z_{T,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_T),\qquad
Z_{O,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_O),\qquad
Z_{D,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_D),
\qquad
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0,
\]
the kinetic-flow matrix is defined by
\begin{equation}
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\bigl(\partial_t\delta_I\bigr)
\right|_{\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{T,O,D\}.
\label{eq:MZ_from_block_Hessian}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Honest conclusion}

Thus the formal block-Hessian problem is now closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the six-component soft multiplet \(\Phi=(A,n,\chi)\) is fixed;
\item the minimal sufficient vertex-complete truncation is fixed;
\item the block Hessian \(\Gamma_k^{(2)}\) is fixed formally;
\item the projection formula defining \(M_Z\) is fixed.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is the actual evaluation:
\[
\Gamma_k^{(2)},\ \Gamma_k^{(3)},\ \Gamma_k^{(4)},\ R_k
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\partial_t Z_T,\partial_t Z_O,\partial_t Z_D
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
M_Z.
\]
So the proof frontier is no longer structural. It is now a concrete one-loop tensor-contraction computation.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\Phi=
(A_1,A_2,n_1,n_2,\chi_1,\chi_2)^T,
\qquad
\rho_T=\frac12A^TA,\ 
\rho_O=\frac12n^Tn,\ 
\rho_D=\frac12\chi^T\chi.
}
\]

A minimal sufficient vertex-complete truncation is
\[
\Gamma_k^{\mathrm{VC}}
=
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{kin}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{pot}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}},
\]
with
\[
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{kin}}
=
\frac12\int d^d x
\Bigl[
Z_{T,k}(\partial A)^2+Z_{O,k}(\partial n)^2+Z_{D,k}(\partial \chi)^2
\Bigr],
\]
\[
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{pot}}
=
\int d^d x\,
\Bigl[
r_T\rho_T+r_O\rho_O+r_D\rho_D
+\frac{\lambda_T}{2}\rho_T^2
+\frac{\lambda_O}{2}\rho_O^2
+\frac{\lambda_D}{2}\rho_D^2
+\lambda_{TO}\rho_T\rho_O
+\lambda_{TD}\rho_T\rho_D
+\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
+g_\tau \tau(\Phi)
\Bigr],
\]
\[
\Gamma_{k,\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
=
Y_k\int d^d x\,O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}[A,n,\chi].
\]

The formal block Hessian is
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_k^{(2)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_{TT}^{(2)} & \Gamma_{TO}^{(2)} & \Gamma_{TD}^{(2)}\\
\Gamma_{OT}^{(2)} & \Gamma_{OO}^{(2)} & \Gamma_{OD}^{(2)}\\
\Gamma_{DT}^{(2)} & \Gamma_{DO}^{(2)} & \Gamma_{DD}^{(2)}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

At the isotropic symmetric point \(A=n=\chi=0\), the Hessian may simplify drastically, possibly even to block diagonal form.
But this does \emph{not} remove the mixed couplings from the \(M_Z\) problem, because the two-point flow depends on
\[
\Gamma_k^{(3)},\qquad \Gamma_k^{(4)},
\]
not only on \(\Gamma_k^{(2)}|_{\Phi=0}\).

The sectoral wavefunction flows are
\[
\boxed{
\partial_t Z_{I,k}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
}
\]

Then, with
\[
Z_{T,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_T),\quad
Z_{O,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_O),\quad
Z_{D,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_D),
\quad
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0,
\]
the kinetic-flow matrix is
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
(\partial_t\delta_I)
\right|_{\delta=0}.
}
\]

So the structural problem is now reduced to the actual one-loop evaluation of
\[
\Gamma_k^{(2)},\ \Gamma_k^{(3)},\ \Gamma_k^{(4)},\ R_k.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Diagrammatic contribution table for the kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\)}

\subsection*{1. General one-loop flow of the two-point function}

Let
\[
G_k=(\Gamma_k^{(2)}+R_k)^{-1}.
\]
The formal Wetterich flow of the two-point function has the standard schematic structure
\begin{equation}
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,IJ}^{(2)}
=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[
G_k\,\Gamma_{k,IJ}^{(4)}\,G_k\,\partial_t R_k
\right]
-
\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[
G_k\,\Gamma_{k,I}^{(3)}\,G_k\,\Gamma_{k,J}^{(3)}\,G_k\,\partial_t R_k
\right],
\label{eq:flow_2pt_diagtable}
\end{equation}
where \(I,J\in\{T,O,D\}\) denote the three soft sectors.
This is the formal starting point for extracting
\[
\partial_t Z_T,\qquad \partial_t Z_O,\qquad \partial_t Z_D.
\]

The sectoral kinetic projections are
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_{I,k}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
\label{eq:Zi_proj_diagtable}
\end{equation}
Therefore only those one-loop terms that generate a nontrivial \(p^2\)-dependence in the diagonal two-point blocks contribute to \(M_Z\).

\subsection*{2. Vertex inventory in the minimal vertex-complete truncation}

The minimal sufficient truncation contains the following interaction data:

\paragraph{(a) Quartic sectoral self-couplings}
\[
\lambda_T\,\rho_T^2,\qquad
\lambda_O\,\rho_O^2,\qquad
\lambda_D\,\rho_D^2.
\]

\paragraph{(b) Quartic mixed couplings}
\[
\lambda_{TO}\,\rho_T\rho_O,\qquad
\lambda_{TD}\,\rho_T\rho_D,\qquad
\lambda_{OD}\,\rho_O\rho_D.
\]

\paragraph{(c) Leading quartic cubic anisotropy}
\[
g_{\tau,k}\,\tau(\Phi).
\]

\paragraph{(d) Leading derivative anisotropy insertion}
\[
Y_k\,O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}[A,n,\chi].
\]

\paragraph{(e) \(A\)-sector gauge/constraint structure}
\[
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}}.
\]

These are precisely the kinds of interaction vertices the document says are required to determine \(M_Z\). 

\subsection*{3. Which diagrams can contribute to \(\partial_t Z_T,\partial_t Z_O,\partial_t Z_D\)}

\paragraph{Important honesty clause.}
At the symmetric point
\[
A=n=\chi=0,
\]
the pure quartic potential sector typically yields only tadpole-type one-loop corrections from \(\Gamma^{(4)}\).
These often renormalize the mass terms \(r_T,r_O,r_D\), but do \emph{not} by themselves generate nontrivial \(p^2\)-dependence in the two-point function.
Hence, unless derivative vertices, gauge exchange, or effective cubic vertices are present, the direct one-loop contribution to \(Z_I\) may vanish.

Therefore the correct table must separate:
\begin{enumerate}
\item diagrams that certainly renormalize the two-point block,
\item diagrams that actually contribute to its momentum derivative,
\item diagrams whose contribution depends on whether one expands around a nonzero background or includes derivative/gauge structures.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{4. Sectorwise diagrammatic table}

\[

\end{array}
\]

\subsection*{5. Minimal practical interpretation}

The table implies the following.

\paragraph{(i) Pure quartic self/mixed couplings}
The couplings
\[
\lambda_T,\lambda_O,\lambda_D,\lambda_{TO},\lambda_{TD},\lambda_{OD}
\]
are necessary because they determine which sectors can appear in the loop of each two-point flow.
However, at the symmetric point they may feed primarily into \emph{mass} renormalization rather than directly into the \(p^2\)-coefficient.

\paragraph{(ii) Quartic anisotropy \(g_{\tau,k}\tau(\Phi)\)}
This term is necessary because it is the leading explicit cubic-symmetry-breaking quartic interaction.
It modifies both diagonal and mixed four-point vertices and can therefore enter the linearized anisotropy flow.

\paragraph{(iii) Derivative anisotropy insertion \(Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}\)}
This is the most direct source of momentum-dependent anisotropic corrections.
Even when pure potential tadpoles do not generate wavefunction flow, the derivative-anisotropy vertex can feed directly into \(\partial_t Z_T,\partial_t Z_O,\partial_t Z_D\).

\paragraph{(iv) \(A\)-sector gauge/constraint structure}
Because the sign of \(M_Z\) explicitly depends on the \(A\)-sector gauge or constraint projection, loops involving the projected \(A\)-sector are potentially indispensable for \(\partial_t Z_T\). This is not optional in an honest computation. 

\subsection*{6. Formal decomposition of the \(M_Z\) entries}

Accordingly, each matrix entry should be written schematically as
\begin{equation}
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\lambda)}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\tau)}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})},
\label{eq:MZ_entry_decomp}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \((M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\lambda)}\) comes from the sectoral quartic self/mixed couplings,
\item \((M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\tau)}\) comes from the quartic cubic-anisotropy vertex,
\item \((M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}\) comes from the derivative-anisotropy operator,
\item \((M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}\) comes from the \(A\)-sector gauge/constraint contribution.
\end{itemize}

This is the correct formal bookkeeping for the explicit FRG sign computation.

\subsection*{7. Honest conclusion}

Thus the one-loop \(M_Z\) problem is no longer structurally ambiguous.

What is now fixed is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the field content,
\item the minimal sufficient truncation,
\item the block Hessian structure,
\item the sectoral projection formula,
\item the list of diagram classes that can contribute to each \(\partial_t Z_I\).
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is the actual evaluation of these diagrams and their tensor contractions.
That is the first point at which the proof becomes genuinely computational rather than merely structural.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,IJ}^{(2)}
=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[
G_k\,\Gamma_{k,IJ}^{(4)}\,G_k\,\partial_t R_k
\right]
-
\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[
G_k\,\Gamma_{k,I}^{(3)}\,G_k\,\Gamma_{k,J}^{(3)}\,G_k\,\partial_t R_k
\right].
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\partial_t Z_{I,k}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
}
\]

The minimal diagrammatic sources are:

\[
\textbf{quartic self/mixed sector: }
\lambda_T,\lambda_O,\lambda_D,\lambda_{TO},\lambda_{TD},\lambda_{OD},
\]
\[
\textbf{quartic cubic anisotropy: } g_{\tau,k}\tau(\Phi),
\]
\[
\textbf{derivative anisotropy insertion: } Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}},
\]
\[
\textbf{\(A\)-sector gauge/constraint contribution: } \Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}}.
\]

For each sector \(I=T,O,D\), the one-loop flow receives contributions from:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(a) tadpole-type } \Gamma^{(4)}_{IIII},
\quad
\text{(b) mixed tadpole-type } \Gamma^{(4)}_{IIJJ},
\quad
\text{(c) sunset/bubble-type } \Gamma^{(3)}\Gamma^{(3)},
\quad
\text{(d) gauge/constraint loops for }I=T.
}
\]

Important honesty clause:
at the symmetric point \(A=n=\chi=0\), pure quartic tadpoles may renormalize mainly the mass terms, not directly the \(p^2\)-coefficient. Therefore nontrivial wavefunction flow may rely crucially on derivative vertices, gauge/constraint structure, or effective cubic vertices.

Accordingly,
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\lambda)}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\tau)}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}.
}
\]

So the structural part is now fixed.
What remains is the actual one-loop tensor-contraction evaluation of these contributions.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Symmetric-point survival table for \texorpdfstring{$\Gamma^{(3)}$ and $\Gamma^{(4)}$}{Gamma(3), Gamma(4)}}

\subsection*{1. Starting minimal truncation}

We work with the TECT-adapted minimal soft-sector truncation
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k[\Phi]
=
\int d^d x
\left[
\frac{Z_{T,k}}{2}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}(\partial_iA_\alpha)^2
+
\frac{Z_{O,k}}{2}\sum_{a=1}^{2}(\partial_i n_a)^2
+
\frac{Z_{D,k}}{2}\sum_{r=1}^{2}(\partial_i\chi_r)^2
+
Y_k\,O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}
+
U_k(\rho,\tau)
\right],
\label{eq:Gamma_min_survival}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\Phi=(A_1,A_2,n_1,n_2,\chi_1,\chi_2),
\qquad
N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6,
\]
\[
\rho_T=\frac12A^TA,\qquad
\rho_O=\frac12n^Tn,\qquad
\rho_D=\frac12\chi^T\chi,\qquad
\rho=\rho_T+\rho_O+\rho_D,
\]
and
\begin{equation}
U_k(\rho,\tau)
=
r_{T,k}\rho_T+r_{O,k}\rho_O+r_{D,k}\rho_D
+\frac{\lambda_{T,k}}{2}\rho_T^2
+\frac{\lambda_{O,k}}{2}\rho_O^2
+\frac{\lambda_{D,k}}{2}\rho_D^2
+\lambda_{TO,k}\rho_T\rho_O
+\lambda_{TD,k}\rho_T\rho_D
+\lambda_{OD,k}\rho_O\rho_D
+g_{\tau,k}\tau(\Phi).
\label{eq:Uk_explicit_survival}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the soft-sector FRG structure already identified in the uploaded derivations. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection*{2. Symmetric point}

We expand around the isotropic symmetric point
\begin{equation}
A=0,\qquad n=0,\qquad \chi=0.
\label{eq:symmetric_point_survival}
\end{equation}
At this point,
\[
\rho_T=\rho_O=\rho_D=\rho=0,
\qquad
\tau(0)=0.
\]

We now ask: which functional derivatives
\[
\Gamma_k^{(3)}\big|_{\Phi=0},
\qquad
\Gamma_k^{(4)}\big|_{\Phi=0}
\]
survive?

\subsection*{3. Quadratic sector: contributes only to \(\Gamma^{(2)}\)}

The sectoral kinetic terms
\[
\frac{Z_{T,k}}{2}(\partial A)^2,\qquad
\frac{Z_{O,k}}{2}(\partial n)^2,\qquad
\frac{Z_{D,k}}{2}(\partial \chi)^2
\]
are purely quadratic in the fields.
Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\mathrm{kin}}\big|_{\Phi=0}=0,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}_{\mathrm{kin}}\big|_{\Phi=0}=0.
\label{eq:kin_zero_survival}
\end{equation}

The same holds for the linear mass sector
\[
r_{T,k}\rho_T+r_{O,k}\rho_O+r_{D,k}\rho_D,
\]
which is also purely quadratic:
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\mathrm{mass}}\big|_{\Phi=0}=0,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}_{\mathrm{mass}}\big|_{\Phi=0}=0.
\label{eq:mass_zero_survival}
\end{equation}

So the entire quadratic part contributes only to \(\Gamma^{(2)}\).

\subsection*{4. Quartic sector: \(\Gamma^{(4)}\) survives, \(\Gamma^{(3)}\) vanishes}

Every quartic monomial in \eqref{eq:Uk_explicit_survival} is homogeneous of degree four in the fields.
Therefore:

\paragraph{Third derivative at the origin.}
For any quartic polynomial \(Q_4(\Phi)\),
\[
\partial^3 Q_4(\Phi)\big|_{\Phi=0}=0.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\mathrm{quartic}}\big|_{\Phi=0}=0.
\label{eq:quartic_Gamma3_zero}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Fourth derivative at the origin.}
For any nonzero quartic polynomial \(Q_4(\Phi)\),
\[
\partial^4 Q_4(\Phi)\big|_{\Phi=0}\neq 0
\]
in general.
Hence
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(4)}_{\mathrm{quartic}}\big|_{\Phi=0}\neq 0
\label{eq:quartic_Gamma4_nonzero}
\end{equation}
for the self-couplings
\[
\lambda_T,\ \lambda_O,\ \lambda_D,
\]
the mixed quartic couplings
\[
\lambda_{TO},\ \lambda_{TD},\ \lambda_{OD},
\]
and also for the quartic cubic-anisotropy vertex
\[
g_{\tau,k}\tau(\Phi),
\]
provided the corresponding coefficient is nonzero.

Thus, at the symmetric point:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\mathrm{pot}}\big|_{\Phi=0}=0,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}_{\mathrm{pot}}\big|_{\Phi=0}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:pot_survival_box}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Derivative-anisotropy insertion}

The leading derivative anisotropy operator \(O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}\) is explicitly included in the truncation as a distinct coupling:
\[
Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}.
\]
In the current minimal truncation, this operator is treated as a leading bilinear two-derivative anisotropic kinetic deformation, not as a higher-field interaction polynomial. This is exactly how the soft-sector FRG truncation is written in the document. 

Under this minimal interpretation,
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}\big|_{\Phi=0}=0,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}_{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}\big|_{\Phi=0}=0,
\label{eq:gradani_survival_minimal}
\end{equation}
while
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}\big|_{\Phi=0}\neq 0
\]
in general.

\paragraph{Honest caveat.}
If one later refines \(O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}\) into field-dependent derivative vertices beyond the bilinear level, then additional \(\Gamma^{(3)}\) and/or \(\Gamma^{(4)}\) pieces may survive. That is not part of the current minimal truncation.

\subsection*{6. Gauge/constraint sector}

The \(A\)-sector requires a gauge-fixing or physical projection structure to define the Hessian and the projected loops unambiguously. The document explicitly states that the sign of \(M_Z\) depends on the gauge/constraint structure of the \(A\)-sector. 

Therefore, in full honesty:
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}\big|_{\Phi=0},
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}\big|_{\Phi=0}
\]
cannot be declared zero or nonzero until a concrete gauge/constraint realization is chosen.

\subsection*{7. Survival table}

The symmetric-point survival table is therefore:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{source term}
&
\Gamma^{(2)}|_{\Phi=0}
&
\Gamma^{(3)}|_{\Phi=0}
&
\Gamma^{(4)}|_{\Phi=0}
\\
\hline
Z_{T,k}(\partial A)^2,\ Z_{O,k}(\partial n)^2,\ Z_{D,k}(\partial \chi)^2
&
\text{nonzero}
&
0
&
0
\\
\hline
r_{T,k}\rho_T+r_{O,k}\rho_O+r_{D,k}\rho_D
&
\text{nonzero}
&
0
&
0
\\
\hline
\frac{\lambda_{T,k}}{2}\rho_T^2,\ \frac{\lambda_{O,k}}{2}\rho_O^2,\ \frac{\lambda_{D,k}}{2}\rho_D^2
&
0
&
0
&
\text{nonzero}
\\
\hline
\lambda_{TO,k}\rho_T\rho_O,\ \lambda_{TD,k}\rho_T\rho_D,\ \lambda_{OD,k}\rho_O\rho_D
&
0
&
0
&
\text{nonzero}
\\
\hline
g_{\tau,k}\tau(\Phi)
&
0
&
0
&
\text{nonzero}
\\
\hline
Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}
\text{ (minimal bilinear interpretation)}
&
\text{nonzero}
&
0
&
0
\\
\hline
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}}
&
\text{depends on implementation}
&
\text{undetermined}
&
\text{undetermined}
\end{array}
\]

\subsection*{8. Consequence for one-loop \(M_Z\) extraction}

The formal one-loop flow of the two-point function is
\begin{equation}
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,IJ}^{(2)}
=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[
G_k\,\Gamma_{k,IJ}^{(4)}\,G_k\,\partial_t R_k
\right]
-
\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[
G_k\,\Gamma_{k,I}^{(3)}\,G_k\,\Gamma_{k,J}^{(3)}\,G_k\,\partial_t R_k
\right].
\label{eq:flow_2pt_survival}
\end{equation}

Since the minimal truncation at the symmetric point gives
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}|_{\Phi=0}=0
\]
for the kinetic, mass, quartic-potential, and minimal derivative-anisotropy pieces, the sunset/bubble-type
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}\Gamma^{(3)}
\]
contribution vanishes \emph{unless} it is regenerated by the gauge/constraint sector or by a refined field-dependent derivative truncation.

Therefore, in the current minimal truncation, the direct one-loop source for the two-point flow is predominantly the tadpole-type
\[
\Gamma^{(4)}
\]
sector.

\paragraph{Final honesty clause.}
Whether these tadpole-type terms actually contribute to
\[
\left.\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}\partial_t\Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p)\right|_{p=0}
\]
depends on the regulator, the momentum routing, the tensor contractions, and the gauge/projector structure.
So this table fixes \emph{which vertices survive}, but not yet \emph{which of them give a nonzero wavefunction flow}.
That is the next explicit contraction step.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Symmetric point: }A=n=\chi=0.
}
\]

At the current minimal TECT-adapted truncation:

\[
\textbf{quadratic kinetic + mass sector}
\]
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}|_{\Phi=0}\neq 0,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}|_{\Phi=0}=0,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}|_{\Phi=0}=0.
\]

\[
\textbf{quartic self/mixed potential sector}
\]
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}|_{\Phi=0}=0,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}|_{\Phi=0}\neq 0.
\]

\[
\textbf{quartic cubic anisotropy }g_{\tau,k}\tau(\Phi)
\]
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}|_{\Phi=0}=0,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}|_{\Phi=0}\neq 0.
\]

\[
\textbf{leading derivative anisotropy }Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}
\]
under the current minimal bilinear interpretation,
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}|_{\Phi=0}\neq 0,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}|_{\Phi=0}=0,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}|_{\Phi=0}=0.
\]

\[
\textbf{\(A\)-sector gauge/constraint contribution}
\]
\[
\Gamma^{(2)},\Gamma^{(3)},\Gamma^{(4)}
\text{ are implementation-dependent and cannot yet be fixed abstractly.}
\]

Therefore the survival table is:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{source} & \Gamma^{(2)}|_{\Phi=0} & \Gamma^{(3)}|_{\Phi=0} & \Gamma^{(4)}|_{\Phi=0} \\
\hline
\text{kinetic} & \neq 0 & 0 & 0 \\
\text{mass} & \neq 0 & 0 & 0 \\
\text{quartic self/mixed} & 0 & 0 & \neq 0 \\
g_{\tau,k}\tau(\Phi) & 0 & 0 & \neq 0 \\
Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}} & \neq 0 & 0 & 0 \\
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}} & \text{depends} & \text{depends} & \text{depends}
\end{array}
\]

Hence, in the current minimal truncation, the dominant direct one-loop source for the two-point flow is the tadpole-type
\[
\Gamma^{(4)}
\]
sector, while the sunset/bubble
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}\Gamma^{(3)}
\]
sector vanishes unless regenerated by gauge/constraint structure or a refined derivative vertex truncation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Tadpole momentum-derivative test table for \(M_Z\)}

\subsection*{1. Projection target}

The kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\) is extracted from
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_{I,k}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
\label{eq:Zi_target_tadpole}
\end{equation}
Therefore a one-loop diagram contributes to \(M_Z\) only if it generates a nontrivial dependence on the external momentum \(p\) in the diagonal two-point function.

\subsection*{2. One-loop two-point flow at the symmetric point}

At the symmetric point
\[
A=n=\chi=0,
\]
the minimal truncation survival table gives:
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}|_{\Phi=0}=0
\]
for the quadratic sector, the quartic potential sector, and the minimal bilinear derivative-anisotropy insertion, while
\[
\Gamma^{(4)}|_{\Phi=0}\neq 0
\]
for the quartic self/mixed potential sector and for the quartic cubic-anisotropy vertex.
Hence the surviving direct one-loop source is predominantly the tadpole-type term
\begin{equation}
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p)
\supset
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[
G_k(q)\,\Gamma_{k,II}^{(4)}(p,-p,q,-q)\,G_k(q)\,\partial_t R_k(q)
\right].
\label{eq:tadpole_source_test}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{3. Momentum-derivative test}

We now test whether the surviving tadpole source contributes to
\[
\partial_{p^2}\partial_t\Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p)\big|_{p=0}.
\]

\paragraph{Criterion.}
A tadpole contributes to \(Z_I\) only if the integrand in \eqref{eq:tadpole_source_test} has explicit nontrivial dependence on the external momentum \(p\) near \(p=0\).

If
\[
\Gamma_{k,II}^{(4)}(p,-p,q,-q)
\]
is momentum-independent (or depends only on loop momentum \(q\) but not on \(p\)),
and if the regulated propagator factors in the tadpole topology also depend only on \(q\),
then
\[
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t\Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p)\Big|_{p=0}=0.
\]
In that case the tadpole renormalizes only the mass-like term, not the wavefunction coefficient.

\subsection*{4. Tadpole momentum-derivative test table}

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c|c}
\text{surviving source}
&
\Gamma^{(4)}|_{\Phi=0}\neq 0?
&
\text{explicit }p\text{-dependence in the vertex?}
&
\partial_{p^2}\text{ contribution?}
&
\text{verdict}
\\
\hline
\lambda_T\rho_T^2,\ \lambda_O\rho_O^2,\ \lambda_D\rho_D^2
&
\text{yes}
&
\text{no (local quartic)}
&
\text{generically no}
&
\text{mass-flow only}
\\
\hline
\lambda_{TO}\rho_T\rho_O,\ \lambda_{TD}\rho_T\rho_D,\ \lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
&
\text{yes}
&
\text{no (local quartic)}
&
\text{generically no}
&
\text{mass mixing only}
\\
\hline
g_{\tau,k}\tau(\Phi)
&
\text{yes}
&
\text{no, if }\tau\text{ is local quartic only}
&
\text{generically no}
&
\text{mass-type anisotropic correction}
\\
\hline
Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}
\text{ (minimal bilinear interpretation)}
&
\Gamma^{(4)}=0
&
\text{not applicable}
&
\text{no tadpole source}
&
\text{enters only via }\Gamma^{(2)}
\\
\hline
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}}
&
\text{implementation-dependent}
&
\text{possibly yes}
&
\text{possibly yes}
&
\text{must be checked explicitly}
\\
\hline
\text{refined field-dependent derivative vertex}
&
\text{possibly yes}
&
\text{yes}
&
\text{yes}
&
\text{candidate source of }Z_I\text{-flow}
\\
\hline
\text{background-generated effective cubic vertices}
&
\Gamma^{(3)}\neq 0\text{ if background }\neq 0
&
\text{yes via sunset/bubble}
&
\text{yes}
&
\text{candidate source of }Z_I\text{-flow}
\end{array}
\]

\subsection*{5. Formal consequence}

The test table implies:

\begin{enumerate}
\item In the current minimal symmetric-point truncation, the surviving local quartic tadpoles are generically \(p^2\)-silent.
They renormalize the masses \(r_T,r_O,r_D\), and possibly anisotropic mass splittings, but not necessarily the wavefunction factors \(Z_T,Z_O,Z_D\).

\item Therefore, the one-loop sign of \(M_Z\) is not expected to be fixed by the local quartic potential sector alone.

\item A nontrivial \(p^2\)-flow must come from one of the following:
\begin{enumerate}
\item field-dependent derivative vertices beyond the minimal bilinear \(Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}\) truncation,
\item gauge/constraint-sector loops in the \(A\)-sector,
\item expansion around a nonzero background generating effective cubic vertices and hence nonzero \(\Gamma^{(3)}\Gamma^{(3)}\) contributions.
\end{enumerate}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{6. Honest theorem-level statement}

Thus the correct theorem-level conclusion is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Within the current minimal symmetric-point truncation, surviving local quartic tadpoles are insufficient in general to fix }M_Z.
}
\label{eq:minimal_tadpole_insufficient}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the current truncation is structurally sufficient to define the \(M_Z\) problem,
but not yet dynamically rich enough to guarantee a nontrivial wavefunction-anisotropy flow.

\subsection*{7. What must be refined next}

The next refinement must therefore enlarge the truncation in one of two ways:

\paragraph{Route A: derivative-vertex completion}
Promote
\[
Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}
\]
from a purely bilinear insertion to a field-dependent derivative interaction sector so that nontrivial momentum-dependent \(\Gamma^{(3)}\) and/or \(\Gamma^{(4)}\) survive at the symmetric point.

\paragraph{Route B: background-field completion}
Perform the FRG expansion not around the strict symmetric point \(\Phi=0\), but around the relevant background that generates effective cubic vertices.
Then the \(\Gamma^{(3)}\Gamma^{(3)}\) contribution in the two-point flow can become nonzero and feed the sectoral \(Z_I\)-flows.

\paragraph{Gauge-sector completion}
In either route, the \(A\)-sector gauge/constraint projection must be implemented explicitly, since the document states that the sign of \(M_Z\) depends on it.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\partial_t Z_{I,k}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
}
\]

So a surviving one-loop diagram contributes to \(M_Z\) only if it carries nontrivial external momentum dependence.

At the symmetric point \(A=n=\chi=0\), in the current minimal truncation:

\[
\Gamma^{(3)}|_{\Phi=0}=0
\]
for the kinetic, mass, quartic-potential, and minimal bilinear derivative-anisotropy sectors, while
\[
\Gamma^{(4)}|_{\Phi=0}\neq 0
\]
for the local quartic self/mixed couplings and for \(g_{\tau,k}\tau(\Phi)\).

However, these surviving quartic vertices are local and generically do not carry explicit external momentum \(p\).
Therefore their tadpole contribution is typically
\[
\boxed{
\partial_{p^2}\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{k,II}(p)\Big|_{p=0}=0,
}
\]
so they feed mainly mass renormalization, not wavefunction renormalization.

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the current minimal symmetric-point truncation is generally insufficient to determine }M_Z.
}
\]

A nontrivial \(M_Z\)-flow requires at least one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(i) field-dependent derivative vertices,}
\quad
\text{(ii) explicit gauge/constraint loops,}
\quad
\text{(iii) background-generated effective cubic vertices.}
}
\]

So the next necessary refinement is not another potential term,
but a truncation refinement that generates genuine external-momentum dependence in the two-point flow.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Background-field FRG completion for a nontrivial kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\)}

\subsection*{1. Why the symmetric-point truncation is insufficient}

At the strict symmetric point
\[
\Phi=0,
\qquad
\Phi=(A_1,A_2,n_1,n_2,\chi_1,\chi_2),
\]
the current minimal TECT-adapted truncation has the following schematic property:

\begin{itemize}
\item the kinetic and mass sectors are purely quadratic, hence contribute only to \(\Gamma^{(2)}\);
\item the quartic potential sector contributes nonzero \(\Gamma^{(4)}\), but \(\Gamma^{(3)}|_{\Phi=0}=0\);
\item the minimal bilinear derivative-anisotropy insertion contributes to \(\Gamma^{(2)}\), but not to \(\Gamma^{(3)}\) or \(\Gamma^{(4)}\).
\end{itemize}

Therefore the sunset/bubble contribution
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}G\Gamma^{(3)}
\]
vanishes at the symmetric point, and the surviving local quartic tadpoles are generically \(p^2\)-silent, contributing mainly to mass renormalization rather than to wavefunction renormalization.
Hence the strict symmetric-point truncation is generally insufficient to generate a nontrivial kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\).

\subsection*{2. Background-field completion idea}

To generate nontrivial momentum-dependent two-point flows, introduce a nonzero background
\[
\bar\Phi=(\bar A,\bar n,\bar\chi),
\]
and decompose
\begin{equation}
\Phi=\bar\Phi+\varphi,
\label{eq:Phi_background_split}
\end{equation}
where \(\varphi\) denotes the fluctuation field.

Expanding the action around \(\bar\Phi\), one obtains the background-dependent vertices
\[
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi],\qquad
\Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi],\qquad
\Gamma_k^{(4)}[\bar\Phi],\ \ldots
\]
Even if the original truncation contains only quartic local interactions, the expansion around \(\bar\Phi\neq 0\) generates effective cubic fluctuation vertices:
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi]\neq 0.
\label{eq:Gamma3_background_nonzero}
\end{equation}
This reactivates the bubble/sunset topology in the two-point flow.

\subsection*{3. Background-field Wetterich equation}

The background-field effective average action is taken as
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k[\bar\Phi,\varphi]
=
\Gamma_k[\bar\Phi+\varphi],
\label{eq:Gamma_background_functional}
\end{equation}
with flow
\begin{equation}
\partial_t\Gamma_k[\bar\Phi,\varphi]
=
\frac12
\mathrm{Tr}
\left[
\bigl(\Gamma_k^{(2,0)}[\bar\Phi,\varphi]+R_k[\bar\Phi]\bigr)^{-1}
\partial_t R_k[\bar\Phi]
\right],
\label{eq:Wetterich_background}
\end{equation}
where \(\Gamma_k^{(2,0)}\) denotes the fluctuation Hessian at fixed background.

A background-adapted regulator \(R_k[\bar\Phi]\) is required so that:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the fluctuation spectrum is regularized in the correct background sector,
\item the \(A\)-sector gauge/constraint projection is implemented on the physical fluctuation subspace,
\item the sectoral kinetic projection remains compatible with the background decomposition.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{4. Minimal background choice}

The orthodox minimal choice is not a completely arbitrary \(\bar\Phi\), but a background adapted to the shell/defect structure already present in the TECT derivation. The natural options are:

\paragraph{(a) Uniform soft-sector background}
\[
\bar\Phi
=
(\bar A,\bar n,\bar\chi)=\text{const.}
\]
This is algebraically simplest, but may still fail to generate the physically relevant momentum structure if it ignores the shell geometry.

\paragraph{(b) Shell-adapted background}
Choose \(\bar\Phi\) aligned with the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\), so that the fluctuation Hessian is already adapted to the TECT shell geometry.

\paragraph{(c) Defect-adapted background}
Use the actual defect/worldvolume background already appearing in the local transport derivation, so that the fluctuation sectors inherit the odd/even selection structure and the transport kernels \(V^\mu(\xi)\).

Among these, the most faithful TECT choice is the shell-/defect-adapted background, because the Dirac-emergence program already singles out a defect/shell geometry rather than the strict homogeneous vacuum.

\subsection*{5. Generation of effective cubic vertices}

Let the quartic sector schematically contain
\[
\lambda_{IJ}\,\rho_I\rho_J,
\qquad
g_{\tau,k}\tau(\Phi),
\qquad
Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}[\Phi].
\]
Expanding around \(\Phi=\bar\Phi+\varphi\), one gets terms of the form
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k[\bar\Phi+\varphi]
=
\Gamma_k[\bar\Phi]
+
\Gamma_k^{(1)}[\bar\Phi]\varphi
+
\frac12\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi]\varphi^2
+
\frac{1}{3!}\Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi]\varphi^3
+
\frac{1}{4!}\Gamma_k^{(4)}[\bar\Phi]\varphi^4
+\cdots.
\label{eq:background_expansion_vertices}
\end{equation}
In particular:
\begin{itemize}
\item quartic local terms produce cubic fluctuation vertices proportional to \(\bar\Phi\),
\item derivative anisotropy terms may produce momentum-dependent cubic fluctuation vertices proportional to \(\bar\Phi\),
\item gauge/constraint terms may produce background-dependent projected vertices in the \(A\)-sector.
\end{itemize}
Thus \(\Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi]\) becomes nonzero and can source nontrivial \(p^2\)-flows in the two-point functions.

\subsection*{6. Two-point flow in the background-field scheme}

The fluctuation two-point flow now has the formal structure
\begin{equation}
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p;\bar\Phi)
=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}
\Bigl[
G_k(\bar\Phi)\,\Gamma_{k,II}^{(4)}(\bar\Phi)\,G_k(\bar\Phi)\,\partial_tR_k(\bar\Phi)
\Bigr]
-
\mathrm{Tr}
\Bigl[
G_k(\bar\Phi)\,\Gamma_{k,I}^{(3)}(\bar\Phi)\,G_k(\bar\Phi)\,\Gamma_{k,I}^{(3)}(\bar\Phi)\,G_k(\bar\Phi)\,\partial_tR_k(\bar\Phi)
\Bigr].
\label{eq:background_2pt_flow}
\end{equation}
Unlike the strict symmetric-point truncation, the second term is now generally nonzero.

Therefore the sectoral wavefunction flows are defined by
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_{I,k}(\bar\Phi)
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p;\bar\Phi)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
\label{eq:background_Zflows}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Definition of the background-dependent \(M_Z\)}

Write
\[
Z_{T,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_T),\qquad
Z_{O,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_O),\qquad
Z_{D,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_D),
\]
with the traceless constraint
\[
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
\]
Then, at fixed admissible background \(\bar\Phi\), define
\begin{equation}
\partial_t
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
=
M_Z(\bar\Phi)
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^2),
\label{eq:MZ_background}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
(M_Z(\bar\Phi))_{IJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\bigl(\partial_t\delta_I(\bar\Phi)\bigr)
\right|_{\delta=0}.
\label{eq:MZ_background_Jacobian}
\end{equation}
The physical question is then the sign of the nontrivial eigenvalues of \(M_Z(\bar\Phi)\) on the traceless subspace.

\subsection*{8. Honest gain and honest limitation}

The background-field completion achieves the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item it explains why the strict symmetric-point truncation can miss the \(Z_I\)-flow;
\item it reactivates effective cubic vertices;
\item it makes the sunset/bubble topology available;
\item it provides a mathematically honest mechanism for obtaining a nonzero \(M_Z\).
\end{enumerate}

However, it still does not determine the sign of \(M_Z\) automatically.
To do that one must still specify:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit admissible background \(\bar\Phi\),
\item the background-adapted regulator \(R_k[\bar\Phi]\),
\item the projected \(A\)-sector Hessian,
\item the actual tensor contractions in the one-loop flow.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{9. Final roadmap statement}

Therefore the correct next-stage roadmap is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar\Phi\neq 0
\ \Longrightarrow\
\Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi]\neq 0
\ \Longrightarrow\
\text{nontrivial } \Gamma^{(3)}G\Gamma^{(3)} \text{ contribution}
\ \Longrightarrow\
\partial_t Z_T,\partial_t Z_O,\partial_t Z_D
\ \Longrightarrow\
M_Z(\bar\Phi).
}
\label{eq:background_MZ_chain}
\end{equation}
This is the orthodox background-field completion of the TECT \(M_Z\)-problem.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Strict symmetric-point truncation can miss }M_Z
\text{ because } \Gamma^{(3)}|_{\Phi=0}=0.
}
\]

Hence the orthodox refinement is a background-field completion:
\[
\boxed{
\Phi=\bar\Phi+\varphi,
\qquad
\bar\Phi=(\bar A,\bar n,\bar\chi)\neq 0.
}
\]

Expanding around \(\bar\Phi\neq 0\) generates effective cubic vertices
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi]\neq 0,
}
\]
so the bubble/sunset topology
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}G\Gamma^{(3)}
\]
becomes active in the two-point flow.

The background-field flow is
\[
\boxed{
\partial_t\Gamma_k[\bar\Phi,\varphi]
=
\frac12
\mathrm{Tr}
\left[
(\Gamma_k^{(2,0)}[\bar\Phi,\varphi]+R_k[\bar\Phi])^{-1}
\partial_t R_k[\bar\Phi]
\right].
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\partial_t Z_{I,k}(\bar\Phi)
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p;\bar\Phi)
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\},
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z(\bar\Phi))_{IJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
(\partial_t\delta_I(\bar\Phi))
\right|_{\delta=0}.
}
\]

Thus the background-field route provides the first honest mechanism for a genuinely nonzero \(M_Z\).

The remaining concrete choices are:
\[
\boxed{
\text{(i) choose an admissible shell/defect-adapted background }\bar\Phi,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(ii) fix }R_k[\bar\Phi],
\quad
\text{(iii) fix the \(A\)-sector projector,}
\quad
\text{(iv) perform the one-loop tensor contractions.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Minimal admissible background for the background-field \(M_Z\) computation}

\subsection*{1. Selection principle}

The purpose of the background-field completion is to generate nonzero effective cubic fluctuation vertices
\[
\Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi]\neq 0
\]
so that the bubble/sunset topology
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}G\Gamma^{(3)}
\]
contributes nontrivially to the sectoral wavefunction flows
\[
\partial_t Z_T,\qquad \partial_t Z_O,\qquad \partial_t Z_D.
\]

A useful background \(\bar\Phi\) must therefore satisfy two conditions:

\begin{enumerate}
\item it must be \emph{admissible}, i.e. compatible with the actual shell/defect geometry already singled out by the TECT Dirac-emergence analysis;
\item it must be \emph{nontrivial enough} to generate effective cubic fluctuation vertices after expansion
\[
\Phi=\bar\Phi+\varphi.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{2. Why a constant homogeneous background is not the preferred choice}

A purely constant background
\[
\bar\Phi=\text{const.}
\]
is algebraically simple, but it ignores the two geometric structures that the present TECT derivation actually uses:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\),
\item the CP\(^2\) defect / projector background \(P_B(\xi)\).
\end{enumerate}

Since the local transport kernel and the projected Dirac symbol are already derived from the defect background and its odd derivative structure, a homogeneous constant background is not the most faithful choice for the \(M_Z\) computation.

\subsection*{3. Defect-adapted background data already established}

The projector-defect sector is built from a smooth rank-one projector
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi),
\label{eq:PB_background_MZ}
\end{equation}
with tangent fluctuations
\begin{equation}
\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger \eta=0,
\qquad
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb Cz_B(\xi))^\perp.
\label{eq:eta_QB_background_MZ}
\end{equation}
The quadratic fluctuation operator is a matrix Schrödinger operator on the rank-two bundle \(Q_B\), and the transport kernel is induced by the odd derivative of the background:
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
\label{eq:transport_background_MZ}
\end{equation}
Therefore the actual low-energy fluctuation problem is already background-adapted at the projector/defect level. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection*{4. Minimal admissible background}

The orthodox minimal choice is therefore a shell-/defect-adapted background rather than a homogeneous vacuum.
The smallest such choice is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}
=
(\bar A,\bar n,\bar\chi)
=
(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:Phi_min_background}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\bar n_B(\xi)\) is the defect-adapted orientational background in the low-energy CP\(^2\)/projector sector,
\item \(\bar\chi_B(\xi)\) is the corresponding defect-condensate hybrid background if the hybrid channels are retained in the minimal soft sector,
\item the gauge sector is initially set to \(\bar A=0\) unless an explicit background gauge field is required by the \(A\)-sector constraint analysis.
\end{itemize}

A slightly stronger but still admissible choice is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}^{\mathrm{full}}
=
(\bar A_B(\xi),\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:Phi_min_background_full}
\end{equation}
where \(\bar A_B(\xi)\) is the background gauge/connection field induced by the defect projector if one wants the \(A\)-sector projection already built into the background.

\subsection*{5. Why this is minimal}

This choice is minimal in the following precise sense:

\begin{enumerate}
\item it preserves the actual shell-/defect-adapted geometry used in the Dirac-emergence construction;
\item it is one-dimensional in the transverse coordinate \(\xi\), hence simpler than a fully space-dependent background;
\item it is nontrivial enough to generate effective cubic vertices after expansion
\[
\Phi=\bar\Phi+\varphi;
\]
\item it keeps the reflection-parity structure
\[
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi),\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\]
which is already central in the low-mode transport selection rules.
\end{enumerate}

Thus \eqref{eq:Phi_min_background} is the minimal admissible background that remains faithful to the present TECT derivation.

\subsection*{6. Background-generated vertices}

Expanding
\[
\Phi=\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi
\]
in the minimal vertex-complete FRG truncation generates:
\begin{itemize}
\item a background-dependent fluctuation Hessian
\[
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],
\]
\item effective cubic vertices
\[
\Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\neq 0,
\]
coming from the quartic potential and derivative-anisotropy sectors,
\item a background-dependent projected propagator
\[
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})=(\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]+R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}])^{-1}.
\]
\end{itemize}
Therefore the two-point flow acquires the nontrivial bubble contribution
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\,G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,\Gamma^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],
\]
which is the minimal mechanism for generating a nonzero \(M_Z\).

\subsection*{7. Admissibility conditions}

To be fully acceptable, the background \(\bar\Phi_{\min}\) should satisfy:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{shell compatibility:} it must be adapted to the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\);
\item \textbf{defect compatibility:} it must descend from the actual defect projector background \(P_B(\xi)\);
\item \textbf{reflection structure:} the induced transport kernel should retain the oddness selection rule;
\item \textbf{constraint compatibility:} the \(A\)-sector must still admit a well-defined gauge/constraint projection;
\item \textbf{spectral admissibility:} the background Hessian must preserve the isolated low-energy sector on which the \(M_Z\) projection is to be performed.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{8. Final roadmap consequence}

Once \(\bar\Phi_{\min}\) is fixed, the \(M_Z\)-computation chain becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}
\Longrightarrow
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],\ \Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],\ \Gamma_k^{(4)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\Longrightarrow
\partial_t Z_T,\partial_t Z_O,\partial_t Z_D
\Longrightarrow
M_Z(\bar\Phi_{\min}).
}
\label{eq:MZ_background_chain_min}
\end{equation}

Thus the problem is no longer to invent a background from scratch.
It is to use the defect/shell background that the TECT Dirac-emergence program has already singled out.

\subsection*{9. Honest status}

The exact current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The minimal admissible background can be identified structurally.}
}
\]
What is not yet done is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item writing the full background-dependent Hessian explicitly,
\item constructing the corresponding background-adapted regulator,
\item evaluating the one-loop tensor contractions.
\end{enumerate}
So the next step is not conceptual background selection, but explicit background-Hessian construction.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Minimal admissible background for }M_Z\text{ should be shell-/defect-adapted, not an arbitrary constant background.}
}
\]

The actual TECT low-energy geometry is already built on the defect projector background
\[
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi),
\]
with tangent fluctuations
\[
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb Cz_B(\xi))^\perp
\]
and odd transport kernel
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
\]

Hence the orthodox minimal background is
\[
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}
=
(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
}
\]
or, if the gauge sector is included explicitly,
\[
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}^{\mathrm{full}}
=
(\bar A_B(\xi),\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)).
}
\]

This choice is minimal because it:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(i) preserves shell/defect geometry,}
\quad
\text{(ii) keeps reflection selection structure,}
\quad
\text{(iii) generates }\Gamma^{(3)}[\bar\Phi]\neq 0.
}
\]

After the background split
\[
\Phi=\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi,
\]
one obtains
\[
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],\qquad
\Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],\qquad
\Gamma_k^{(4)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],
\]
and therefore a genuinely nontrivial two-point flow via
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}G\Gamma^{(3)}.
\]

So the computation chain becomes
\[
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}
\Longrightarrow
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],\Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],\Gamma_k^{(4)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\Longrightarrow
\partial_t Z_T,\partial_t Z_O,\partial_t Z_D
\Longrightarrow
M_Z(\bar\Phi_{\min}).
}
\]

Thus the background-selection problem is essentially closed.
The next real task is the explicit construction of the background-dependent Hessian and regulator.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Background-dependent block Hessian for \texorpdfstring{$\bar\Phi_{\min}$}{barPhi_min}}

\subsection*{1. Background split}

We choose the minimal admissible shell-/defect-adapted background
\begin{equation}
\bar\Phi_{\min}(\xi)
=
(\bar A,\bar n,\bar\chi)
=
(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\label{eq:Phi_bar_min_choice}
\end{equation}
and expand
\begin{equation}
\Phi=\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi,
\qquad
\varphi=(a,\nu,\zeta).
\label{eq:background_split_phi}
\end{equation}
Thus
\[
A=a,\qquad
n=\bar n_B+\nu,\qquad
\chi=\bar\chi_B+\zeta.
\]

Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(a\) is the fluctuation in the \(A\)-sector (with gauge/constraint projection still to be imposed),
\item \(\nu\) is the orientational fluctuation around \(\bar n_B(\xi)\),
\item \(\zeta\) is the defect-condensate / hybrid fluctuation around \(\bar\chi_B(\xi)\).
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{2. Background-adapted truncation}

The minimal vertex-complete truncation is taken in the form
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k^{\mathrm{VC}}[A,n,\chi]
=
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{kin}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{pot}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
+
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}},
\label{eq:Gamma_VC_background}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{kin}}
=
\frac12\int d^d x
\Bigl[
Z_{T,k}(\partial_i A)^T(\partial_i A)
+
Z_{O,k}(\partial_i n)^T(\partial_i n)
+
Z_{D,k}(\partial_i \chi)^T(\partial_i \chi)
\Bigr],
\label{eq:Gamma_kin_background}
\end{equation}
\begin{align}
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{pot}}
=
\int d^d x\,
\Bigl[
&r_{T,k}\rho_T+r_{O,k}\rho_O+r_{D,k}\rho_D
+\frac{\lambda_{T,k}}{2}\rho_T^2
+\frac{\lambda_{O,k}}{2}\rho_O^2
+\frac{\lambda_{D,k}}{2}\rho_D^2 \nonumber\\
&+\lambda_{TO,k}\rho_T\rho_O
+\lambda_{TD,k}\rho_T\rho_D
+\lambda_{OD,k}\rho_O\rho_D
+g_{\tau,k}\tau(A,n,\chi)
\Bigr],
\label{eq:Gamma_pot_background}
\end{align}
and
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k,\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
=
Y_k\int d^d x\,O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}[A,n,\chi].
\label{eq:Gamma_gradani_background}
\end{equation}

The sectoral quadratic invariants are
\[
\rho_T=\frac12 A^T A,
\qquad
\rho_O=\frac12 n^T n,
\qquad
\rho_D=\frac12 \chi^T\chi.
\]

\subsection*{3. Definition of the background-dependent Hessian}

The fluctuation Hessian at fixed background is
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\left.
\frac{\delta^2 \Gamma_k^{\mathrm{VC}}[\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi]}
{\delta\varphi\,\delta\varphi}
\right|_{\varphi=0}.
\label{eq:Hessian_def_background}
\end{equation}
With respect to the sector decomposition \(\varphi=(a,\nu,\zeta)\), it has the \(3\times 3\) block form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal H_{TT} & \mathcal H_{TO} & \mathcal H_{TD}\\
\mathcal H_{OT} & \mathcal H_{OO} & \mathcal H_{OD}\\
\mathcal H_{DT} & \mathcal H_{DO} & \mathcal H_{DD}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:block_Hessian_background}
\end{equation}

Each entry is now a \(\xi\)-dependent matrix differential operator on the worldvolume fluctuation bundle.

\subsection*{4. Diagonal blocks}

\subsubsection*{4.1 \(TT\)-block}

Since \(\bar A=0\), the \(A\)-sector diagonal block is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{TT}
=
-Z_{T,k}\,\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{TT}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\,\mathcal K_{TT}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal G_A(\xi,\partial),
\label{eq:HTT_background}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_{TT}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
=
r_{T,k}
+
\lambda_{TO,k}\rho_O^B(\xi)
+
\lambda_{TD,k}\rho_D^B(\xi)
+
g_{\tau,k}\,
\left.
\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial A\,\partial A}
\right|_{\bar\Phi_{\min}},
\label{eq:MTT_pot_background}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\rho_O^B(\xi)=\frac12 \bar n_B^T\bar n_B,
\qquad
\rho_D^B(\xi)=\frac12 \bar\chi_B^T\bar\chi_B.
\]
The term \(\mathcal G_A\) denotes the gauge-fixing / constraint projection contribution.

\subsubsection*{4.2 \(OO\)-block}

The orientational diagonal block is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\,\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\,\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y),
\label{eq:HOO_background}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{align}
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
&=
\Bigl[
r_{O,k}
+
3\lambda_{O,k}\rho_O^B(\xi)
+
\lambda_{OD,k}\rho_D^B(\xi)
\Bigr]\mathbf 1_2
+
\lambda_{O,k}\,\bar n_B(\xi)\bar n_B(\xi)^T
\nonumber\\
&\qquad
+
g_{\tau,k}
\left.
\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial n\,\partial n}
\right|_{\bar\Phi_{\min}}.
\label{eq:MOO_pot_background}
\end{align}
The transport term \(\mathcal T_{OO}\) is the background-induced first-order operator descending from the odd kernel \(V^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\).

\subsubsection*{4.3 \(DD\)-block}

Similarly,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{DD}
=
-Z_{D,k}\,\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{DD}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\,\mathcal K_{DD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{DD}(\xi,\partial_y),
\label{eq:HDD_background}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{align}
\mathcal M_{DD}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
&=
\Bigl[
r_{D,k}
+
3\lambda_{D,k}\rho_D^B(\xi)
+
\lambda_{OD,k}\rho_O^B(\xi)
\Bigr]\mathbf 1_2
+
\lambda_{D,k}\,\bar\chi_B(\xi)\bar\chi_B(\xi)^T
\nonumber\\
&\qquad
+
g_{\tau,k}
\left.
\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial \chi\,\partial \chi}
\right|_{\bar\Phi_{\min}}.
\label{eq:MDD_pot_background}
\end{align}

\subsection*{5. Off-diagonal blocks}

The essential gain of the background-field completion is that the mixed blocks no longer vanish generically.

\subsubsection*{5.1 \(TO\)-block}

\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{TO}
=
g_{\tau,k}
\left.
\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial A\,\partial n}
\right|_{\bar\Phi_{\min}}
+
Y_k\,\mathcal K_{TO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial).
\label{eq:HTO_background}
\end{equation}
Because \(\bar A=0\), no \(\lambda_{TO}\,A n^T\) term survives directly in the Hessian itself, but \(g_\tau\)- and derivative-anisotropy-induced mixing may survive on the nontrivial background.

\subsubsection*{5.2 \(TD\)-block}

\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{TD}
=
g_{\tau,k}
\left.
\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial A\,\partial \chi}
\right|_{\bar\Phi_{\min}}
+
Y_k\,\mathcal K_{TD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial).
\label{eq:HTD_background}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection*{5.3 \(OD\)-block}

Here the quartic mixed coupling is activated directly by the background:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{OD}
=
\lambda_{OD,k}\,\bar n_B(\xi)\bar\chi_B(\xi)^T
+
g_{\tau,k}
\left.
\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial n\,\partial \chi}
\right|_{\bar\Phi_{\min}}
+
Y_k\,\mathcal K_{OD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial).
\label{eq:HOD_background}
\end{equation}
Thus the \(O\)- and \(D\)-sector mixing is generically nonzero on the background.

The Hermitian transpose relations hold:
\[
\mathcal H_{OT}=\mathcal H_{TO}^\dagger,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{DT}=\mathcal H_{TD}^\dagger,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{DO}=\mathcal H_{OD}^\dagger.
\]

\subsection*{6. Background-generated cubic vertices}

Expanding \(\Gamma_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi]\) to third order in \(\varphi\), one obtains
\[
\Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\neq 0.
\]
Schematically:
\begin{itemize}
\item quartic self/mixed couplings produce cubic fluctuation vertices proportional to \(\bar n_B(\xi)\) or \(\bar\chi_B(\xi)\),
\item \(g_{\tau,k}\tau\) produces anisotropic cubic fluctuation vertices proportional to the background,
\item \(Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}\) may produce momentum-dependent cubic fluctuation vertices on the background.
\end{itemize}
Therefore the bubble/sunset contribution
\[
