\Gamma^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\,G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,\Gamma^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\]
is now generally nonzero.

\subsection*{7. Background-adapted propagator and sectoral projection}

Define the background propagator
\begin{equation}
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\bigl(
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
+
R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\bigr)^{-1}.
\label{eq:G_background}
\end{equation}
Then the background two-point flow is
\begin{align}
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
&=
\frac12\,
\mathrm{Tr}\Bigl[
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\Gamma_{k,II}^{(4)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\,
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\partial_t R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\Bigr]
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-
\mathrm{Tr}\Bigl[
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\Gamma_{k,I}^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\,
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\Gamma_{k,I}^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\,
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\partial_t R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\Bigr].
\label{eq:background_2pt_flow_explicit}
\end{align}
The sectoral wavefunction flows are then projected by
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_{I,k}(\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
\label{eq:ZI_background_proj}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{8. Final formal form of the \(M_Z\) problem}

Writing
\[
Z_{T,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_T),\qquad
Z_{O,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_O),\qquad
Z_{D,k}=Z_k(1+\delta_D),
\qquad
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0,
\]
the background-dependent kinetic-flow matrix is defined by
\begin{equation}
\partial_t
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
=
M_Z(\bar\Phi_{\min})
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^2),
\label{eq:MZ_background_final}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
(M_Z(\bar\Phi_{\min}))_{IJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\bigl(\partial_t\delta_I(\bar\Phi_{\min})\bigr)
\right|_{\delta=0}.
\label{eq:MZ_background_J_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{9. Honest status}

Thus the structural problem is now closed at the background-dependent level:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal admissible background is fixed;
\item the background-dependent block Hessian is fixed formally;
\item the source of nonzero cubic vertices is identified;
\item the projected background two-point flow defining \(M_Z(\bar\Phi_{\min})\) is fixed.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is the explicit evaluation of:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the background-adapted regulator \(R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\),
\item the gauge-projected \(A\)-sector block \(\mathcal G_A\),
\item the tensor contractions in \eqref{eq:background_2pt_flow_explicit},
\item the sign of the nontrivial eigenvalues of \(M_Z(\bar\Phi_{\min})\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi))
}
\]
is the minimal admissible shell-/defect-adapted background.

With
\[
\Phi=\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi,
\qquad
\varphi=(a,\nu,\zeta),
\]
the fluctuation Hessian is
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal H_{TT} & \mathcal H_{TO} & \mathcal H_{TD}\\
\mathcal H_{OT} & \mathcal H_{OO} & \mathcal H_{OD}\\
\mathcal H_{DT} & \mathcal H_{DO} & \mathcal H_{DD}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

Diagonal blocks:
\[
\mathcal H_{TT}
=
-Z_{T,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{TT}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{TT}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
+
\mathcal G_A,
\]
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
+
\mathcal T_{OO},
\]
\[
\mathcal H_{DD}
=
-Z_{D,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{DD}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{DD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
+
\mathcal T_{DD}.
\]

Mixed blocks:
\[
\mathcal H_{TO}
=
g_{\tau,k}\left.\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial A\,\partial n}\right|_{\bar\Phi_{\min}}
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{TO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}},
\]
\[
\mathcal H_{TD}
=
g_{\tau,k}\left.\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial A\,\partial\chi}\right|_{\bar\Phi_{\min}}
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{TD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}},
\]
\[
\mathcal H_{OD}
=
\lambda_{OD,k}\bar n_B\bar\chi_B^T
+
g_{\tau,k}\left.\frac{\partial^2\tau}{\partial n\,\partial\chi}\right|_{\bar\Phi_{\min}}
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}.
\]

Because \(\bar\Phi_{\min}\neq 0\), one has
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_k^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\neq 0,
}
\]
so the bubble/sunset topology
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}G\Gamma^{(3)}
\]
is activated.

The background propagator is
\[
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\bigl(\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]+R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\bigr)^{-1},
\]
and the sectoral kinetic flows are
\[
\boxed{
\partial_t Z_{I,k}(\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t\Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
M_Z(\bar\Phi_{\min})
\text{ is now formally well-defined.}
}
\]

What remains open is the actual contraction/evaluation:
\[
\boxed{
R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}],\qquad
\mathcal G_A,\qquad
\text{tensor contractions},\qquad
\operatorname{sign}\operatorname{spec}(M_Z(\bar\Phi_{\min})|_{\mathrm{traceless}}).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Background-adapted regulator and \(A\)-sector projector ansatz}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

To make the background-field definition of
\[
M_Z(\bar\Phi_{\min})
\]
actually operational, one must specify:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a background-adapted regulator \(R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\),
\item a physical projector in the \(A\)-sector,
\item the corresponding projected propagator.
\end{enumerate}

The document is explicit that the sign of \(M_Z\) depends on the regulator choice and on the gauge/constraint structure of the \(A\)-sector. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection*{2. Background-dependent Hessian blocks}

On the minimal admissible background
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\]
the fluctuation Hessian has the block form
\[
\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal H_{TT} & \mathcal H_{TO} & \mathcal H_{TD}\\
\mathcal H_{OT} & \mathcal H_{OO} & \mathcal H_{OD}\\
\mathcal H_{DT} & \mathcal H_{DO} & \mathcal H_{DD}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
The regulator should be adapted to these background-dependent kinetic blocks rather than to the strict symmetric-point operator.

\subsection*{3. Minimal background-adapted regulator ansatz}

A minimal sectoral regulator ansatz is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\mathrm{diag}\Bigl(
R_{T,k},\,R_{O,k},\,R_{D,k}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:Rk_diag_ansatz}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{align}
R_{T,k}
&=
Z_{T,k}\,\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}\,
r_k(\mathcal H_{TT}^{(0)}),
\label{eq:RTk_ansatz}
\\
R_{O,k}
&=
Z_{O,k}\,r_k(\mathcal H_{OO}^{(0)}),
\label{eq:ROk_ansatz}
\\
R_{D,k}
&=
Z_{D,k}\,r_k(\mathcal H_{DD}^{(0)}).
\label{eq:RDk_ansatz}
\end{align}
Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_{II}^{(0)}\) denotes the principal/background-diagonal part of the \(II\)-block,
\item \(r_k(\cdot)\) is a standard monotone cutoff profile,
\item \(\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}\) projects onto the physical \(A\)-sector fluctuation subspace before regularization.
\end{itemize}

This is the natural background-field analogue of the usual sectoral FRG regulator.

\subsection*{4. Optimized-profile version}

A concrete optimized-profile realization is
\begin{equation}
R_{I,k}
=
Z_{I,k}\,
\bigl(k^2-\mathcal H_{II}^{(0)}\bigr)\,
\Theta\!\bigl(k^2-\mathcal H_{II}^{(0)}\bigr),
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\},
\label{eq:optimized_profile_background}
\end{equation}
with the understanding that for \(I=T\) the operator acts only on the image of \(\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}\).

Equivalently, in momentum language for the worldvolume modes,
\begin{equation}
R_{I,k}(q)
=
Z_{I,k}(k^2-q^2)\Theta(k^2-q^2),
\label{eq:Rk_momentum_opt}
\end{equation}
but with the transverse/gauge projection imposed in the \(A\)-sector.

\subsection*{5. \(A\)-sector physical projector}

The emergent Abelian gauge chain in TECT is geometrically closed:
\[
z\in S^5
\Longrightarrow
S^5\to CP^2
\Longrightarrow
U(1)\text{ principal bundle}
\Longrightarrow
A_\mu=-iz^\dagger\partial_\mu z
\Longrightarrow
F_{\mu\nu}.
\]
Dynamical infrared consistency requires that the Proca mass vanish,
\[
m_{A,k}^2\to 0,
\]
so that only the genuine transverse gauge mode survives in the infrared. 

Therefore the \(A\)-sector must be projected onto the physical transverse/gauge-consistent subspace. The minimal abstract requirement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}
:
\mathcal H_A
\to
\mathcal H_A^{\mathrm{phys}},
}
\label{eq:PiA_phys_def}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal H_A^{\mathrm{phys}}\) contains only the transverse fluctuation modes compatible with the infrared gauge surface.

In momentum representation the standard transverse projector is
\begin{equation}
\Pi_{A,ij}^{\mathrm{T}}(p)
=
\delta_{ij}
-
\frac{p_i p_j}{p^2},
\label{eq:transverse_projector}
\end{equation}
and the minimal ansatz is that \(\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}\) reduces to \(\Pi_A^{\mathrm{T}}\) on the projected shell/worldvolume gauge block, possibly corrected by background-dependent constraint terms.

\subsection*{6. Background-adapted projected propagator}

With the regulator and the physical projector in place, define the projected background propagator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_k^{\mathrm{phys}}(\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\Bigl(
\Pi^{\mathrm{phys}}
\bigl[\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]+R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\bigr]
\Pi^{\mathrm{phys}}
\Bigr)^{-1},
}
\label{eq:Gphys_background}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\Pi^{\mathrm{phys}}
=
\mathrm{diag}\bigl(\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}},\,\mathbf 1_O,\,\mathbf 1_D\bigr).
\]
This ensures that unphysical \(A\)-sector directions do not contaminate the one-loop tensor contractions used to define \(M_Z\).

\subsection*{7. Background-field two-point flow with projection}

The projected two-point flow is then
\begin{align}
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
&=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{phys}}
\Bigl[
G_k^{\mathrm{phys}}(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\Gamma_{k,II}^{(4)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\,
G_k^{\mathrm{phys}}(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\partial_tR_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\Bigr]
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-
\mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{phys}}
\Bigl[
G_k^{\mathrm{phys}}(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\Gamma_{k,I}^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\,
G_k^{\mathrm{phys}}(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\Gamma_{k,I}^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\,
G_k^{\mathrm{phys}}(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\partial_tR_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\Bigr].
\label{eq:flow_projected_background}
\end{align}
Then
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_{I,k}(\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t\Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\},
\label{eq:Zflow_projected_background}
\end{equation}
and finally
\begin{equation}
(M_Z(\bar\Phi_{\min}))_{IJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\bigl(\partial_t\delta_I(\bar\Phi_{\min})\bigr)
\right|_{\delta=0}.
\label{eq:MZ_projected_background}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{8. Honest status}

At this point, the regulator/projector problem is structurally closed at the ansatz level:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the regulator is chosen background-adapted and sectoral,
\item the \(A\)-sector is projected to its physical transverse/gauge-consistent subspace,
\item the resulting projected propagator is well defined,
\item the projected two-point flow defining \(M_Z\) is formally fixed.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is not the structural form of the ansatz, but the explicit implementation:
\begin{enumerate}
\item determine the detailed background-corrected projector \(\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}\),
\item specify the exact regulator profile \(r_k\),
\item evaluate the corresponding one-loop tensor contractions,
\item extract the sign of the nontrivial eigenvalues of \(M_Z(\bar\Phi_{\min})\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\mathrm{diag}\bigl(
R_{T,k},R_{O,k},R_{D,k}
\bigr),
}
\]
with
\[
R_{T,k}
=
Z_{T,k}\,\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}\,r_k(\mathcal H_{TT}^{(0)}),
\qquad
R_{O,k}
=
Z_{O,k}\,r_k(\mathcal H_{OO}^{(0)}),
\qquad
R_{D,k}
=
Z_{D,k}\,r_k(\mathcal H_{DD}^{(0)}).
\]

A concrete optimized version is
\[
R_{I,k}
=
Z_{I,k}\bigl(k^2-\mathcal H_{II}^{(0)}\bigr)\Theta(k^2-\mathcal H_{II}^{(0)}),
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\},
\]
with the \(A\)-sector restricted to the physical projected subspace.

The \(A\)-sector physical projector is
\[
\boxed{
\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}:\mathcal H_A\to \mathcal H_A^{\mathrm{phys}},
}
\]
where \(\mathcal H_A^{\mathrm{phys}}\) contains only the transverse gauge-consistent fluctuation modes.
In momentum representation, the minimal transverse projector is
\[
\Pi_{A,ij}^{\mathrm T}(p)=\delta_{ij}-\frac{p_i p_j}{p^2}.
\]

The projected propagator is
\[
\boxed{
G_k^{\mathrm{phys}}(\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\Bigl(
\Pi^{\mathrm{phys}}
[\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]+R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]]
\Pi^{\mathrm{phys}}
\Bigr)^{-1},
}
\]
with
\[
\Pi^{\mathrm{phys}}
=
\mathrm{diag}\bigl(\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}},\mathbf 1_O,\mathbf 1_D\bigr).
\]

Then the projected background two-point flow is
\[
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{phys}}[G\Gamma^{(4)}G\partial_tR]
-
\mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{phys}}[G\Gamma^{(3)}G\Gamma^{(3)}G\partial_tR],
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\partial_t Z_{I,k}(\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0}.
}
\]

So the regulator/projector problem is structurally closed.
What remains open is the explicit implementation of
\[
\boxed{
\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}},\qquad
r_k,\qquad
\text{one-loop contractions},\qquad
\operatorname{sign}\operatorname{spec}(M_Z(\bar\Phi_{\min})|_{\mathrm{traceless}}).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Background-generated explicit vertex list on \texorpdfstring{$\bar\Phi_{\min}$}{barPhi_min}}

\subsection*{1. Background split}

Choose the minimal admissible shell-/defect-adapted background
\begin{equation}
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\label{eq:bg_vertex_barphi}
\end{equation}
and expand
\begin{equation}
\Phi=\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi,
\qquad
\varphi=(a,\nu,\zeta),
\label{eq:bg_vertex_split}
\end{equation}
so that
\[
A=a,\qquad
n=\bar n_B+\nu,\qquad
\chi=\bar\chi_B+\zeta.
\]

We now list the explicit background-generated cubic and quartic fluctuation vertices that can enter the projected one-loop flow of
\[
\partial_t Z_T,\qquad \partial_t Z_O,\qquad \partial_t Z_D.
\]

\subsection*{2. Potential-sector background-generated cubic vertices}

The minimal explicit potential sector is
\begin{align}
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{pot}}
=
\int d^d x\,
\Bigl[
&r_{T,k}\rho_T+r_{O,k}\rho_O+r_{D,k}\rho_D
+\frac{\lambda_{T,k}}{2}\rho_T^2
+\frac{\lambda_{O,k}}{2}\rho_O^2
+\frac{\lambda_{D,k}}{2}\rho_D^2
\nonumber\\
&+\lambda_{TO,k}\rho_T\rho_O
+\lambda_{TD,k}\rho_T\rho_D
+\lambda_{OD,k}\rho_O\rho_D
+g_{\tau,k}\tau(A,n,\chi)
\Bigr].
\label{eq:bg_vertex_potential}
\end{align}

Since \(\bar A=0\), but \(\bar n_B,\bar\chi_B\neq 0\), the expansion of the quartic terms yields the following cubic fluctuation vertices.

\subsubsection*{2.1 Orientational self-cubic}

From \(\frac{\lambda_{O,k}}{2}\rho_O^2\),
\begin{equation}
\rho_O=\frac12(\bar n_B+\nu)^T(\bar n_B+\nu)
=
\rho_O^B+\bar n_B^T\nu+\frac12\nu^T\nu.
\label{eq:rhoO_expand}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\frac{\lambda_{O,k}}{2}\rho_O^2
\supset
\lambda_{O,k}\,(\bar n_B^T\nu)\,\frac12\nu^T\nu,
\label{eq:nu3_vertex}
\end{equation}
which generates a cubic fluctuation vertex of the schematic type
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\nu}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{O,k}\,\bar n_B(\xi).
\]

\subsubsection*{2.2 Defect/hybrid self-cubic}

Similarly, from \(\frac{\lambda_{D,k}}{2}\rho_D^2\),
\begin{equation}
\rho_D=\rho_D^B+\bar\chi_B^T\zeta+\frac12\zeta^T\zeta,
\label{eq:rhoD_expand}
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\frac{\lambda_{D,k}}{2}\rho_D^2
\supset
\lambda_{D,k}\,(\bar\chi_B^T\zeta)\,\frac12\zeta^T\zeta,
\label{eq:zeta3_vertex}
\end{equation}
which gives
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\zeta\zeta\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{D,k}\,\bar\chi_B(\xi).
\]

\subsubsection*{2.3 Mixed \(O\)-\(D\) cubic vertices}

From the mixed quartic term \(\lambda_{OD,k}\rho_O\rho_D\),
\begin{align}
\lambda_{OD,k}\rho_O\rho_D
\supset\;
&\lambda_{OD,k}\,(\bar n_B^T\nu)\,\frac12\zeta^T\zeta
+
\lambda_{OD,k}\,(\bar\chi_B^T\zeta)\,\frac12\nu^T\nu
\nonumber\\
&+
\lambda_{OD,k}\,(\bar n_B^T\nu)(\bar\chi_B^T\zeta).
\label{eq:OD_cubic_vertices}
\end{align}
Thus one obtains the cubic fluctuation vertices
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD,k}\,\bar n_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD,k}\,\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\]
as well as background-dependent quadratic mixing.

\paragraph{Important note.}
Because \(\bar A=0\), the mixed quartic couplings \(\lambda_{TO,k}\rho_T\rho_O\) and \(\lambda_{TD,k}\rho_T\rho_D\) do not generate cubic vertices linear in \(a\) at this stage.
They remain relevant for higher derivatives of the action, but not as immediate background-generated cubic sources.

\subsection*{3. Quartic anisotropy background-generated vertices}

The quartic cubic-anisotropy term
\[
g_{\tau,k}\tau(A,n,\chi)
\]
is quartic in the fields.
Therefore, after the background split, it generates:
\begin{itemize}
\item background-dependent quadratic corrections to the Hessian,
\item background-dependent cubic fluctuation vertices,
\item background-dependent quartic fluctuation vertices.
\end{itemize}

Schematically,
\begin{equation}
g_{\tau,k}\tau(\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi)
=
g_{\tau,k}\tau(\bar\Phi_{\min})
+
g_{\tau,k}\,\tau^{(1)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\varphi
+
\frac12 g_{\tau,k}\,\tau^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\varphi^2
+
\frac1{3!}g_{\tau,k}\,\tau^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\varphi^3
+
\frac1{4!}g_{\tau,k}\,\tau^{(4)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\varphi^4.
\label{eq:tau_background_expand}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\tau}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\neq 0,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}_{\tau}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\neq 0,
\label{eq:tau_vertices_survive}
\end{equation}
in general.
These vertices are anisotropic and therefore can feed directly into the linearized anisotropy flow.

\subsection*{4. Derivative-anisotropy background-generated vertices}

The minimal truncation contains
\[
Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}[A,n,\chi].
\]
At the strict symmetric point and under the minimal bilinear interpretation, this term contributes only to \(\Gamma^{(2)}\).
But on the nontrivial background \(\bar\Phi_{\min}\), a field-dependent derivative operator generally expands as
\begin{equation}
O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}[\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi]
=
O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
+
O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}^{(1)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\varphi
+
\frac12 O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\varphi^2
+
\frac1{3!} O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\varphi^3+\cdots.
\label{eq:gradani_background_expand}
\end{equation}
Hence the background can generate momentum-dependent cubic fluctuation vertices
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\neq 0.
\label{eq:gradani_gamma3_nonzero}
\end{equation}
These are especially important, because they are natural candidates for generating genuine \(p^2\)-dependence in the two-point flow and therefore nontrivial contributions to \(M_Z\).

\subsection*{5. Gauge/projector background-generated vertices}

The \(A\)-sector requires a gauge-fixing or physical projector structure.
The sign of \(M_Z\) depends explicitly on this gauge/constraint sector.
Therefore, once the \(A\)-sector is formulated on the background-adapted projected space, the corresponding contribution
\[
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}}[\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi]
\]
may also generate:
\begin{itemize}
\item projected background-dependent quadratic corrections in \(\mathcal H_{TT}\),
\item mixed background-dependent cubic vertices involving \(a\) and \(\nu,\zeta\),
\item possibly additional quartic projected vertices.
\end{itemize}
Their explicit form depends on the chosen projector/gauge implementation and cannot be fixed abstractly at the present stage.

\subsection*{6. Survival table on the background}

The explicit background-generated survival table is:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{source}
&
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
&
\Gamma^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
&
\Gamma^{(4)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\\
\hline
\text{kinetic sector}
&
\text{yes}
&
\text{no}
&
\text{no}
\\
\hline
r_T\rho_T+r_O\rho_O+r_D\rho_D
&
\text{yes}
&
\text{no}
&
\text{no}
\\
\hline
\frac{\lambda_O}{2}\rho_O^2
&
\text{yes}
&
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\nu}\sim \lambda_O\bar n_B
&
\Gamma^{(4)}_{\nu\nu\nu\nu}\neq 0
\\
\hline
\frac{\lambda_D}{2}\rho_D^2
&
\text{yes}
&
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\zeta\zeta\zeta}\sim \lambda_D\bar\chi_B
&
\Gamma^{(4)}_{\zeta\zeta\zeta\zeta}\neq 0
\\
\hline
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
&
\text{yes}
&
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta},\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}\neq 0
&
\Gamma^{(4)}_{\nu\nu\zeta\zeta}\neq 0
\\
\hline
\lambda_{TO}\rho_T\rho_O,\ \lambda_{TD}\rho_T\rho_D
&
\text{yes}
&
\text{not directly if }\bar A=0
&
\Gamma^{(4)}\neq 0
\\
\hline
g_{\tau,k}\tau(A,n,\chi)
&
\text{yes}
&
\text{yes (background-anisotropic cubic)}
&
\text{yes}
\\
\hline
Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}
&
\text{yes}
&
\text{yes if field-dependent on background}
&
\text{possibly yes in refined completion}
\\
\hline
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{gf/proj}}
&
\text{yes}
&
\text{implementation-dependent}
&
\text{implementation-dependent}
\end{array}
\]

\subsection*{7. Consequence for the one-loop two-point flow}

Therefore, on the background \(\bar\Phi_{\min}\), the two-point flow
\begin{align}
\partial_t \Gamma_{k,II}^{(2)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
&=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\Bigl[
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})
\Gamma_{k,II}^{(4)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})
\partial_tR_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})
\Bigr]
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-
\mathrm{Tr}\Bigl[
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})
\Gamma_{k,I}^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})
\Gamma_{k,I}^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})
\partial_tR_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})
\Bigr]
\label{eq:bg_2pt_vertex_flow}
\end{align}
contains genuinely nonzero \(\Gamma^{(3)}G\Gamma^{(3)}\) terms.
This is the minimal honest mechanism by which the sectoral wavefunction flows
\[
\partial_t Z_T,\qquad
\partial_t Z_O,\qquad
\partial_t Z_D
\]
can become nontrivial.

\subsection*{8. Formal decomposition of the \(M_Z\) entries}

Accordingly, the physical kinetic-flow matrix should be decomposed as
\begin{equation}
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(O\text{-self})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(D\text{-self})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(OD\text{-mix})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\tau)}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})},
\label{eq:MZ_decomp_bg}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \((M_Z)^{(O\text{-self})}\) comes from \(\lambda_O\bar n_B\)-induced cubic vertices,
\item \((M_Z)^{(D\text{-self})}\) comes from \(\lambda_D\bar\chi_B\)-induced cubic vertices,
\item \((M_Z)^{(OD\text{-mix})}\) comes from the mixed coupling \(\lambda_{OD}\),
\item \((M_Z)^{(\tau)}\) comes from the quartic cubic-anisotropy background-generated vertices,
\item \((M_Z)^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}\) comes from the derivative-anisotropy background-generated vertices,
\item \((M_Z)^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}\) comes from the \(A\)-sector gauge/projector completion.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{9. Honest final status}

Thus the background-generated vertex problem is now structurally closed.

What is fixed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item which vertices vanish at the symmetric point,
\item which vertices are regenerated on the minimal admissible background,
\item which vertex classes can actually contribute to the one-loop kinetic flow.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit tensor form of \(O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}\) on the background,
\item the explicit gauge/projector completion in the \(A\)-sector,
\item the actual one-loop contraction signs and weights.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\Phi=\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi,
\qquad
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\qquad
\varphi=(a,\nu,\zeta).
}
\]

On this background, the quartic potential sector generates effective cubic fluctuation vertices:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\nu}\sim \lambda_O\,\bar n_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\zeta\zeta\zeta}\sim \lambda_D\,\bar\chi_B(\xi),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\,\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\,\bar n_B(\xi).
}
\]

The quartic anisotropy term generates
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\tau}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\neq 0,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}_{\tau}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\neq 0.
}
\]

The derivative-anisotropy sector can now generate
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\neq 0
}
\]
provided the operator is treated in its background-dependent field-sensitive form.

The gauge/projector sector may also generate background-dependent cubic and quartic vertices:
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],
}
\]
but these remain implementation-dependent.

Hence the one-loop two-point flow on the background now contains a genuinely nonzero bubble/sunset sector:
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\,G_k(\bar\Phi_{\min})\,\Gamma^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],
}
\]
which was absent at the strict symmetric point.

Accordingly, the kinetic-flow matrix decomposes schematically as
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(O\text{-self})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(D\text{-self})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(OD\text{-mix})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\tau)}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}.
}
\]

So the vertex-survival problem is now structurally closed.
The remaining frontier is the explicit sign/coupling evaluation of these background-generated one-loop contributions.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Sector-by-sector sign roadmap for the kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\)}

\subsection*{1. Physical problem}

After removing the redundant common metric anisotropy, the physical derivative-anisotropy problem is the flow of
\[
\delta_T,\qquad \delta_O,\qquad \delta_D,
\qquad
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
\]
These variables are classically marginal, so their infrared fate is controlled entirely by the loop-level kinetic-flow matrix
\[
\partial_t
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
=
M_Z
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\
\delta_O\\
\delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^2).
\]
The sign of the nontrivial eigenvalues of \(M_Z\) is not fixed by the currently available truncation data alone. It depends on the exact Hessian, interaction vertices coupling \(A,n,\chi\), the regulator, the tensor contractions, and the \(A\)-sector gauge/constraint structure. 

\subsection*{2. Background-generated decomposition of \(M_Z\)}

On the minimal admissible background
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\]
the background-generated cubic vertices imply the decomposition
\begin{equation}
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(O\text{-self})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(D\text{-self})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(OD\text{-mix})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\tau)}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}.
\label{eq:MZ_sector_decomp_sign}
\end{equation}
Each term corresponds to a specific class of one-loop background-induced vertices.

\subsection*{3. \(O\)-self contribution}

The self-quartic term
\[
\frac{\lambda_O}{2}\rho_O^2
\]
generates the background-induced cubic vertex
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\nu}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_O\,\bar n_B(\xi).
\]
Therefore it contributes to the two-point flow through
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\nu}G_O\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\nu}.
\]

\paragraph{Sign expectation.}
If the orientational sector is stable and its quartic self-coupling is positive,
\[
\lambda_O>0,
\]
then this loop typically acts as a self-stabilizing renormalization of the \(O\)-sector stiffness.
Hence the natural expectation is that
\[
(M_Z)^{(O\text{-self})}
\]
contributes predominantly to the diagonal part and tends to reduce relative anisotropy rather than amplify it.

\paragraph{Honest limitation.}
The actual sign depends on the precise momentum derivative of the projected self-energy and cannot be fixed without evaluating the loop kernel explicitly.

\subsection*{4. \(D\)-self contribution}

Similarly, the self-quartic term
\[
\frac{\lambda_D}{2}\rho_D^2
\]
generates
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\zeta\zeta\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_D\,\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\]
so that
\[
(M_Z)^{(D\text{-self})}
\]
comes from the corresponding \(D\)-sector bubble.

\paragraph{Sign expectation.}
Under the natural stability condition
\[
\lambda_D>0,
\]
the \(D\)-self contribution is again expected to be diagonally stabilizing and therefore consistent with isotropization.

\paragraph{Honest limitation.}
As with the \(O\)-sector, this is an expectation, not yet a theorem.

\subsection*{5. Mixed \(OD\) contribution}

The mixed quartic term
\[
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
\]
generates the background-induced cubic vertices
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar n_B(\xi).
\]
This sector is the first genuine source of off-diagonal kinetic mixing between the \(O\)- and \(D\)-channels.

\paragraph{Sign expectation.}
If the mixed interaction tends to lock the two sectors together, then
\[
(M_Z)^{(OD\text{-mix})}
\]
should have the Laplacian-type sign structure
\[
\sim
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
2 & -1\\
-1 & 2
\end{pmatrix}
\]
on the \(O\)-\(D\) traceless subspace.
This would favor isotropization.

\paragraph{Honest limitation.}
This is exactly one of the most dangerous unresolved sign sources.
The sign of the corresponding off-diagonal kernel is not fixed without explicit tensor contraction.

\subsection*{6. Quartic anisotropy contribution}

The quartic BCC anisotropy term
\[
g_{\tau,k}\tau(\Phi)
\]
generates anisotropic background-dependent cubic and quartic fluctuation vertices.
Its contribution to \(M_Z\) is denoted
\[
(M_Z)^{(\tau)}.
\]

\paragraph{RG support.}
In the TECT infrared truncation with
\[
N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6,
\]
the linearized quartic anisotropy eigenvalue is
\[
\theta_\tau=\epsilon\frac{4-N_{\mathrm{eff}}}{N_{\mathrm{eff}}+8}
=
-\frac{\epsilon}{7}<0.
\]
Hence the leading quartic cubic anisotropy is irrelevant in the infrared. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\paragraph{Sign expectation.}
Therefore it is natural to expect that
\[
(M_Z)^{(\tau)}
\]
acts in the isotropizing direction, i.e. contributes negative physical eigenvalues on the traceless anisotropy subspace.

\paragraph{Honest limitation.}
This does not yet prove that the full derivative-anisotropy matrix \(M_Z\) is negative, because the quartic anisotropy direction is not identical to the full sectoral wavefunction-anisotropy direction.

\subsection*{7. Derivative-anisotropy contribution}

The leading derivative anisotropy operator
\[
Y_k O_{\nabla,\mathrm{ani}}
\]
produces the contribution
\[
(M_Z)^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}.
\]

\paragraph{Why this is the core driver.}
Since \(M_Z\) is precisely the linearized flow matrix of the derivative anisotropy variables \(\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D\), this is the most direct source term for the physical anisotropy problem.

\paragraph{Expectation from the TECT FRG truncation.}
The document states that the derivative anisotropy has negative canonical part,
\[
-2+\eta_*<0,
\]
and that \(\theta_Y<0\) is the natural TECT expectation. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\paragraph{Honest limitation.}
The same document is equally explicit that the sign of the physical derivative-anisotropy flow is not yet rigorously fixed from current TECT data, because it requires the full kinetic-flow matrix \(M_Z\). 
Therefore:
\[
(M_Z)^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
\]
is the most important expected negative contribution, but not yet a proved one.

\subsection*{8. Gauge/projector contribution}

The gauge/projector completion contributes
\[
(M_Z)^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}.
\]

\paragraph{Structural expectation.}
The gauge-consistent IR sector must preserve transversality and avoid a generated Proca mass.
In the gauge-preserving reference EFT, the one-loop polarization tensor remains transverse,
\[
p^\mu \Pi_{\mu\nu}(p)=0,
\qquad
\Pi_{\mu\nu}(0)=0,
\]
even in the presence of Class II gauge-covariant corrections. 

This suggests that a properly projected \(A\)-sector should not generate uncontrolled gauge-breaking anisotropy, and therefore may be compatible with isotropization.

\paragraph{Honest limitation.}
However, the sign of its contribution to \(Z_T\) still depends on the detailed projector implementation and background-adapted contractions. Hence this is a second unresolved sign source.

\subsection*{9. Qualitative sign hierarchy}

The most honest current hierarchy is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z)^{(\tau)}\ \text{and}\ (M_Z)^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
\text{ are naturally expected to be isotropizing},
}
\label{eq:expected_negative_sources}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z)^{(OD\text{-mix})}\ \text{and}\ (M_Z)^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}
\text{ are the two main unresolved sign bottlenecks.}
}
\label{eq:bottleneck_sources}
\end{equation}

The self-sector pieces
\[
(M_Z)^{(O\text{-self})},\qquad
(M_Z)^{(D\text{-self})}
\]
are expected to be diagonally stabilizing, but their exact sign weight is not yet proved.

\subsection*{10. Algebraic target}

The exact algebraic target remains
\begin{equation}
M_Z
=
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
2 & -1 & -1\\
-1 & 2 & -1\\
-1 & -1 & 2
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0,
\label{eq:MZ_target_signroad}
\end{equation}
for which the physical eigenvalues are
\[
-3\lambda,\qquad -3\lambda
\]
on the traceless subspace. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

Thus the practical sign roadmap is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item show that the sum of the expected negative pieces
\[
(M_Z)^{(\tau)}+(M_Z)^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
\]
dominates,
\item show that the unresolved pieces
\[
(M_Z)^{(OD\text{-mix})}+(M_Z)^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}
\]
do not overturn negativity,
\item recover the Laplacian-type sign pattern \eqref{eq:MZ_target_signroad}.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{11. Honest conclusion}

Therefore the current status is not “\(M_Z\) is negative.”
The honest theorem-level status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the sign problem has been reduced to a finite list of background-generated one-loop sources.}
}
\]
Among these, the derivative-anisotropy and quartic-anisotropy sectors are the main expected isotropizing sources, while the mixed \(OD\) and gauge/projector sectors are the main unresolved sign bottlenecks.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
(M_Z)_{IJ}
=
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(O\text{-self})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(D\text{-self})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(OD\text{-mix})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\tau)}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
(M_Z)_{IJ}^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}.
}
\]

Current honest sign roadmap:

\[
\textbf{(1) Self-sector pieces}
\]
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\nu}\sim \lambda_O\bar n_B,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\zeta\zeta\zeta}\sim \lambda_D\bar\chi_B.
\]
These are naturally expected to be diagonally stabilizing, but their exact sign is not yet proved.

\[
\textbf{(2) Mixed \(OD\) piece}
\]
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar\chi_B,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar n_B.
\]
This is the first genuine off-diagonal anisotropy source and one of the main unresolved bottlenecks.

\[
\textbf{(3) Quartic anisotropy piece}
\]
For \(N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6\),
\[
\theta_\tau
=
\epsilon\frac{4-N_{\mathrm{eff}}}{N_{\mathrm{eff}}+8}
=
-\frac{\epsilon}{7}<0.
\]
Hence the quartic anisotropy direction is RG-irrelevant, so
\[
(M_Z)^{(\tau)}
\]
is naturally expected to favor isotropization.

\[
\textbf{(4) Derivative-anisotropy piece}
\]
This is the most direct driver of the physical anisotropy flow.
TECT expectation:
\[
\theta_Y<0
\]
is natural, but not yet rigorously proved.
So
\[
(M_Z)^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
\]
is expected to be negative, but remains open.

\[
\textbf{(5) Gauge/projector piece}
\]
Gauge-preserving EFT structure suggests compatibility with transversality and isotropization, but the actual sign depends on the detailed projector implementation.

Thus the most honest hierarchy is
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z)^{(\tau)}\text{ and }(M_Z)^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
\text{ are the main expected negative/isotropizing sources,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z)^{(OD\text{-mix})}\text{ and }(M_Z)^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}
\text{ are the main unresolved sign bottlenecks.}
}
\]

The algebraic target remains
\[
\boxed{
M_Z
=
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
2 & -1 & -1\\
-1 & 2 & -1\\
-1 & -1 & 2
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0,
}
\]
whose physical eigenvalues are
\[
\boxed{
-3\lambda,\qquad -3\lambda.
}
\]

So the sign problem is now reduced to checking whether the expected negative sources dominate the unresolved mixed/gauge contributions.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Explicit sign test formula for the \(OD\)-mixed contribution to \(M_Z\)}

\subsection*{1. Why the \(OD\)-mixed piece is the first genuine off-diagonal bottleneck}

After removing the redundant common anisotropy, the physical derivative-anisotropy problem reduces to the sign of the kinetic-flow matrix
\[
M_Z
\]
on the traceless sector
\[
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
\]
At the current stage, the full sign of \(M_Z\) is not fixed by the available TECT truncation data; what remains is an explicit FRG computation requiring the exact Hessian, regulator, tensor contractions, and the \(A\)-sector gauge/constraint projection. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

Among the sectorwise one-loop sources, the mixed \(OD\) piece is the first genuinely off-diagonal contribution, because it is generated by the quartic mixed coupling
\[
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D,
\]
and, on the minimal admissible background
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\]
it produces cubic fluctuation vertices coupling the \(O\)- and \(D\)-sectors.

\subsection*{2. Background-generated \(OD\) cubic vertices}

Write
\[
n=\bar n_B+\nu,
\qquad
\chi=\bar\chi_B+\zeta,
\qquad
\rho_O=\frac12 n^Tn,
\qquad
\rho_D=\frac12 \chi^T\chi.
\]
Then
\[
\rho_O
=
\rho_O^B+\bar n_B^T\nu+\frac12\nu^T\nu,
\qquad
\rho_D
=
\rho_D^B+\bar\chi_B^T\zeta+\frac12\zeta^T\zeta.
\]
Expanding the mixed quartic term gives
\begin{align}
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
\supset\;
&\lambda_{OD}\,(\bar n_B^T\nu)\,\frac12\zeta^T\zeta
+
\lambda_{OD}\,(\bar\chi_B^T\zeta)\,\frac12\nu^T\nu
\nonumber\\
&+
\lambda_{OD}\,(\bar n_B^T\nu)(\bar\chi_B^T\zeta).
\label{eq:OD_mixed_cubic_expand}
\end{align}
Hence the two relevant background-generated cubic vertices are
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar n_B(\xi).
\label{eq:OD_cubic_vertices_final}
\end{equation}
These are the minimal sources of \(OD\)-mixed bubble contributions.

\subsection*{3. Projected \(OD\)-mixed self-energies}

Let
\[
G_O(q;\bar\Phi_{\min}),
\qquad
G_D(q;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\]
denote the projected background propagators in the \(O\)- and \(D\)-sectors.
Then the \(OD\)-mixed contribution to the \(O\)-sector self-energy has the schematic form
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^{(OD)}_{O}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
-
\int_q
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}(p,q;\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
G_D(q;\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}(-p,q;\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
G_O(p+q;\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\partial_t R_k(q),
\label{eq:SigmaO_OD}
\end{equation}
and similarly for the \(D\)-sector
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^{(OD)}_{D}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
-
\int_q
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}(p,q;\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
G_O(q;\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}(-p,q;\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
G_D(p+q;\bar\Phi_{\min})\,
\partial_t R_k(q).
\label{eq:SigmaD_OD}
\end{equation}
Here \(\int_q\) denotes the loop integration together with any background spectral sum and physical projection.

These are the minimal \(OD\)-mixed bubble kernels whose momentum derivatives feed the sectoral kinetic flows.

\subsection*{4. Definition of the \(OD\)-mixed matrix entry}

The corresponding contribution to the kinetic-flow matrix is defined by linearization in the anisotropy variables:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma^{(OD)}_{I}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{O,D\}.
}
\label{eq:MZ_OD_def}
\end{equation}
This is the exact sign-test formula:
the sign of the \(OD\)-mixed block is the sign of the momentum-derivative Jacobian of the projected mixed self-energy.

\subsection*{5. Symmetry-reduced \(2\times 2\) \(OD\) block}

On the \(OD\) subspace, the physically relevant mixed block is
\begin{equation}
M_Z^{OD}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO} & (M_Z^{OD})_{OD}\\
(M_Z^{OD})_{DO} & (M_Z^{OD})_{DD}
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:MZ_OD_matrix}
\end{equation}
If the background and regulator preserve the \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry to leading order, one expects
\begin{equation}
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DD},
\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DO}.
\label{eq:OD_exchange_sym}
\end{equation}
Then the traceless \(OD\) anisotropy direction \(u=\delta_O-\delta_D\) evolves with eigenvalue
\begin{equation}
\lambda_{OD}^{\mathrm{phys}}
=
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}.
\label{eq:OD_phys_eig}
\end{equation}
Thus isotropization in the \(OD\)-subsector requires
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}<0.
}
\label{eq:OD_iso_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Laplacian-sign sufficient test}

A particularly clean sufficient condition is the Laplacian-type sign pattern
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}<0,\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{DD}<0,\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DO}>0,
}
\label{eq:OD_laplacian_sign}
\end{equation}
with row-sum balance
\begin{equation}
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}+(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}=0,
\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{DD}+(M_Z^{OD})_{DO}=0.
\label{eq:OD_rowsum_zero}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
M_Z^{OD}
=
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
1 & -1\\
-1 & 1
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0,
\label{eq:OD_laplacian_matrix}
\end{equation}
and the physical traceless \(OD\) eigenvalue is
\[
-2\lambda<0.
\]
This is exactly the sign pattern needed for the \(OD\)-mixed piece to be isotropizing rather than destabilizing.

\subsection*{7. Practical sign diagnostics}

The explicit sign test \eqref{eq:MZ_OD_def} can be reduced operationally to the following diagnostics.

\paragraph{(a) Vertex sign.}
Because each cubic vertex carries one factor of \(\lambda_{OD}\) and one background profile,
the bubble amplitude is quadratic in \(\lambda_{OD}\):
\[
\Sigma^{(OD)}\sim \lambda_{OD}^2\,(\bar n_B,\bar\chi_B)^2\times(\text{loop kernel}).
\]
Hence the overall sign is not fixed by \(\lambda_{OD}\) alone; it is controlled by the loop kernel and projector contractions.

\paragraph{(b) Propagator positivity.}
If the projected background propagators \(G_O,G_D\) are positive in the relevant Euclidean sector and the regulator insertion \(\partial_t R_k\) is positive, then the bubble carries the standard overall minus sign in \eqref{eq:SigmaO_OD}--\eqref{eq:SigmaD_OD}. This tends to favor negative diagonal contributions.

\paragraph{(c) Off-diagonal sign.}
The off-diagonal entries depend on whether the mixed background contraction
\[
\bar n_B(\xi)\bar\chi_B(\xi)
\]
enters the projected kernel with the same or opposite sign relative to the diagonal pieces. This is precisely where an explicit tensor-contraction computation is still needed.

\subsection*{8. Honest conclusion}

Therefore the current theorem-level status of the \(OD\)-mixed piece is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma^{(OD)}_{I}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0}
}
\label{eq:OD_sign_test_final}
\end{equation}
is the correct explicit sign-test formula.

What is \emph{not} yet proved is the actual sign of this expression.

The honest practical target is to verify the Laplacian-type sign structure
\[
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
1 & -1\\
-1 & 1
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0,
\]
for the \(OD\)-mixed subsector.
This is one of the two main remaining sign bottlenecks for the full matrix \(M_Z\).

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
\Longrightarrow
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar n_B(\xi).
}
\]

These background-generated cubic vertices define the mixed \(OD\)-bubble self-energies
\[
\Sigma^{(OD)}_{O}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min}),
\qquad
\Sigma^{(OD)}_{D}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min}),
\]
and the explicit sign-test formula is
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma^{(OD)}_{I}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{O,D\}.
}
\]

On the \(OD\) subsector,
\[
M_Z^{OD}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO} & (M_Z^{OD})_{OD}\\
(M_Z^{OD})_{DO} & (M_Z^{OD})_{DD}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
If exchange symmetry gives
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DD},
\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DO},
\]
then the physical traceless eigenvalue is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{OD}^{\mathrm{phys}}
=
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}.
}
\]
Thus isotropization requires
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}<0.
}
\]

A clean sufficient target is the Laplacian sign pattern
\[
\boxed{
M_Z^{OD}
=
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
1 & -1\\
-1 & 1
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0,
}
\]
for which the traceless \(OD\) eigenvalue is
\[
\boxed{
-2\lambda<0.
}
\]

So the \(OD\)-mixed sign bottleneck is now reduced to one explicit projected self-energy derivative test.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Explicit sign test formula for the \(A\)-sector gauge/projector contribution to \(M_Z\)}

\subsection*{1. Structural role of the gauge/projector sector}

The \(A\)-sector is special because the fluctuation space contains physical transverse modes together with unphysical longitudinal / gauge / constraint directions.
Therefore its contribution to the derivative-anisotropy flow cannot be defined directly from the unprojected two-point kernel.
It must first be projected onto the physical transverse subspace.

This is not optional: the document is explicit that the sign of the derivative-anisotropy flow depends on the gauge/constraint structure of the \(A\)-sector. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection*{2. Physical projected two-point kernel}

Let
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\]
denote the background-dependent \(A\)-sector two-point kernel.
Introduce the transverse projector
\begin{equation}
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)
=
\eta^{\mu\nu}-\frac{p^\mu p^\nu}{p^2},
\label{eq:PiT_gfproj}
\end{equation}
or, in purely spatial notation,
\[
\Pi_{T,ij}(p)=\delta_{ij}-\frac{p_i p_j}{p^2}.
\]

The physical projected inverse propagator is then
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2),\mathrm{phys}}_{A}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
:=
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min}).
\label{eq:Gamma2_phys_A}
\end{equation}

The corresponding projected flow is
\begin{equation}
\partial_t\Gamma^{(2),\mathrm{phys}}_{A}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,
\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min}).
\label{eq:dGamma2_phys_A}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{3. Explicit sign test formula}

The gauge/projector contribution to the kinetic-flow matrix is the response of the projected \(A\)-sector wavefunction renormalization to the sectoral anisotropy variables \(\delta_J\).
Therefore the correct explicit sign-test formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Bigl[
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,
\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\Bigr]
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
}
\label{eq:MZ_gfproj_test}
\end{equation}
for
\[
J\in\{T,O,D\}.
\]
This is the direct analogue of the \(OD\)-mixed sign test formula, but now with the physical transverse projection inserted first.

\subsection*{4. Consistency test preceding the sign test}

Before even asking for the sign of \((M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}\), one must verify that the projected gauge sector is dynamically admissible.

\paragraph{(i) Transversality test.}
The flow must satisfy
\begin{equation}
p^\mu \Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})=0
\qquad
\text{in the infrared projected sector.}
\label{eq:transversality_test}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(ii) No-Proca-mass test.}
The zero-momentum limit must obey
\begin{equation}
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(0)\,\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(0;\bar\Phi_{\min})=0,
\label{eq:no_Proca_test}
\end{equation}
equivalently,
\[
m_{A,k}^2\to 0
\qquad (k\to 0).
\]
The document is explicit that the gauge-consistent infrared surface is characterized precisely by the vanishing of the Proca mass and by the survival of only the transverse mode. 

\paragraph{(iii) Regulator consistency test.}
The regulator must preserve the Ward identity, or else gauge-restoring counterterms are required.
Gauge-preserving schemes keep
\[
p^\mu \Pi_{\mu\nu}(p)=0
\]
and avoid spurious longitudinal artifacts. 

Only after these three tests are passed does \eqref{eq:MZ_gfproj_test} become a physically meaningful sign test.

\subsection*{5. One-loop structure of the projected \(A\)-sector flow}

At one loop, the projected two-point flow has the generic form
\begin{align}
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
&=
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,
\Biggl\{
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{phys}}
\bigl[
G\,\Gamma^{(4)}_{\mu\nu}\,G\,\partial_tR
\bigr]
\nonumber\\
&\qquad
-
\mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{phys}}
\bigl[
G\,\Gamma^{(3)}_\mu\,G\,\Gamma^{(3)}_\nu\,G\,\partial_tR
\bigr]
\Biggr\},
\label{eq:projected_A_flow}
\end{align}
where all propagators and vertices are background-adapted and physically projected.

Thus the gauge/projector contribution decomposes schematically as
\begin{equation}
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj},4})_{TJ}
+
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj},33})_{TJ},
\label{eq:MZ_gfproj_split}
\end{equation}
coming respectively from:
\begin{itemize}
\item projected tadpole-type gauge-sector contributions,
\item projected bubble/sunset-type gauge-sector contributions.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{6. Sufficient isotropizing criterion}

A clean sufficient condition that the gauge/projector sector does not destabilize isotropy is the following.

\paragraph{Sufficient criterion.}
If:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the projected two-point function is transverse,
\[
p^\mu\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p)=0;
\]
\item no Proca mass is generated,
\[
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(0)\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(0)=0;
\]
\item the projected \(p^2\)-coefficient is nonnegative in the Euclidean sign convention,
\[
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p)
\right|_{p=0}
\ge 0;
\]
\end{enumerate}
then the \(A\)-sector gauge/projector contribution is compatible with isotropization and does not act as a dangerous source of physical anisotropy.

\paragraph{Honest warning.}
This is a sufficient criterion, not a derived theorem for the current microscopic TECT data.
The actual sign still depends on the detailed projector implementation.

\subsection*{7. Operator-classification refinement}

The document provides a sharp classification of lattice-induced operators:

\begin{itemize}
\item Class I and II operators preserve local emergent \(U(1)\) and cannot generate a gauge mass,
\item Class III operators explicitly break local \(U(1)\) and can generate \(m_A^2\neq 0\).
\end{itemize}
Therefore an immediate necessary condition for a healthy gauge/projector contribution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the projected \(A\)-sector EFT must contain only Class I and Class II operators.}
}
\label{eq:ClassI_II_only}
\end{equation}
Otherwise the sign test is moot, because the gauge-consistent infrared surface is already destroyed. 

\subsection*{8. Honest conclusion}

Therefore the exact sign-test problem for the gauge/projector bottleneck is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Bigl[
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,
\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\Bigr]
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
}
\label{eq:final_gfproj_sign_test}
\end{equation}
subject to the preconditions:
\[
\text{transversality},\qquad
m_{A,k}^2\to 0,\qquad
\text{gauge-preserving regulator},\qquad
\text{Class I/II only}.
\]

This is the correct explicit sign-test formula.
What remains open is its actual evaluation.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{

This is the explicit sign-test formula for the \(A\)-sector gauge/projector contribution.

\section*{TECT Dirac / IR-isotropy / \(M_Z\) frontier Master Verification Map}

\subsection*{A. Global logical status}

The present status of the TECT program is:

whereas

\boxed{
\text{the final microscopic realization is reduced to a finite list of explicit verification problems.}
}

This is exactly the logical separation already emphasized in the current TECT notes:
the closed core is no longer conceptual, and the remaining frontier is a finite checklist of microscopic inputs. 

\subsection*{B. Layer I: theorem-level closed core}

\paragraph{B1. UV and shell structure.}
The BCC phase is selected at the structural level, and the shell-based local reduction is closed.
The shell-reduced soft sector admits the effective infrared multiplet
\[
\Phi=(A_1,A_2,n_1,n_2,\chi_1,\chi_2),
\qquad
N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6.
\]
This is the theorem-level starting point for the IR isotropy and Dirac-emergence chain. 

\paragraph{B2. Local shell-enriched Dirac architecture.}
The local projector-defect transport analysis reduces the actual Weyl/Dirac nondegeneracy problem to a finite coefficient test.
The microscopic transport ansatz has the form
\[
i\partial_t\eta
=
\Bigl[
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2+U_B(\xi)
-i\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi))\partial_{y^\mu}
\Bigr]\eta
+O(\partial_y^2)\eta,
\]
and the shell witnesses are determined by a finite matrix \(\Lambda_i{}^\mu\). 

\paragraph{B3. Quartic anisotropy irrelevance.}
At the TECT soft-sector level, the leading quartic cubic anisotropy has
\[
\theta_\tau
=
\epsilon\frac{4-N_{\mathrm{eff}}}{N_{\mathrm{eff}}+8}
=
-\frac{\epsilon}{7}<0
\qquad
(N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6),
\]
so the quartic anisotropy coupling flows to zero in the infrared. This part of the isotropy mechanism is structurally closed. 

\paragraph{B4. Gauge-consistent transverse sector.}
In the gauge-preserving reference EFT, the polarization tensor is transverse:
\[
p^\mu \Pi_{\mu\nu}(p)=0,
\]
and the emergent gauge sector is massless provided the regulator preserves the Ward identity and no explicit Class III symmetry-breaking operator is present. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\paragraph{B5. Mass-space classification.}
For the minimal doubled Dirac block, the constant mass space is exactly two-dimensional, and valley-charge \(U(1)\) is a sufficient symmetry to forbid all constant masses. Thus the mass-protection problem is reduced to a finite residual-symmetry algebra check. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\subsection*{C. Layer II: problems already reduced to explicit finite tests}

\paragraph{C1. Dirac nondegeneracy witness test.}
The Weyl/Dirac nondegeneracy problem is reduced to the finite coefficient condition
\[
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
So the full PDE problem is already reduced to determining finitely many transport coefficients. 

\paragraph{C2. Remote-gap / zero-mixing check.}
The local shell-reduced fermion framework is structurally closed, but the final microscopic TECT realization still requires finite checks such as:
\[
\Delta>0,
\qquad
V(0)=0.
\]
These are no longer conceptual problems; they are explicit spectral/projection tests inside the microscopic linearization. 

\paragraph{C3. Mass-protection residual symmetry audit.}
The final massless Dirac closure requires determining the actual residual constant algebra
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\]
and verifying that it excludes the two constant mass generators.
Again, this is reduced to a finite symmetry-algebra check. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

\paragraph{C4. IR isotropy beyond quartic anisotropy.}
What remains after quartic anisotropy irrelevance is the derivative-anisotropy and sectoral velocity-mismatch problem.
This is encoded in the kinetic-flow matrix
\[
M_Z.
\]
The document is explicit that what remains is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item derive the precise soft-mode spectrum,
\item compute the threshold functions and anomalous dimensions in a TECT-specific FRG truncation,
\item evaluate the derivative-anisotropy stability matrix \(M_Z\) explicitly,
\item solve the full Wetterich flow numerically.
\end{enumerate}
Thus the isotropy frontier is already reduced to the explicit FRG computation of \(M_Z\). :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\subsection*{D. Layer III: current \(M_Z\) frontier}

\paragraph{D1. Physical derivative-anisotropy variables.}
The physical anisotropy variables are
\[
\delta_T,\qquad \delta_O,\qquad \delta_D,
\qquad
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
\]
They are classically marginal, so their infrared fate is controlled entirely by
\[
\partial_t
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\ \delta_O\\ \delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
=
M_Z
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta_T\\ \delta_O\\ \delta_D
\end{pmatrix}
+\cdots.
\]

\paragraph{D2. Minimal FRG truncation.}
The TECT-adapted FRG truncation is
\[
\Gamma_k[\Phi]
=
\int d^d x
\left[
\frac{Z_{T,k}}{2}(\partial A)^2
+

+

\right].

This defines the formal \(M_Z\) problem, but not yet its sign. 

\paragraph{D3. Why the strict symmetric-point truncation is insufficient.}
At the strict symmetric point \(\Phi=0\), one typically has
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}|_{\Phi=0}=0,
\]
while only the local quartic \(\Gamma^{(4)}\) survives. Such tadpoles are generically \(p^2\)-silent and may fail to generate a nontrivial \(Z_I\)-flow.
Therefore the orthodox completion requires a nontrivial background field:
\[
\Phi=\bar\Phi+\varphi,
\qquad
\bar\Phi\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{D4. Minimal admissible background.}
The most faithful minimal choice is shell-/defect-adapted:
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\]
built on the actual projector-defect background
\[
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi),
\]
with odd transport kernel
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
\]
This background reactivates
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\neq 0
\]
and hence the bubble/sunset sector in the two-point flow. 

\paragraph{D5. Background-generated vertex inventory.}
On \(\bar\Phi_{\min}\), the relevant cubic fluctuation vertices are generated by:
\begin{itemize}
\item self quartics:

\item mixed quartic:

\]
\item quartic anisotropy:
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_\tau[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\neq 0;
\]
\item derivative anisotropy:
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\neq 0
\]
in the field-dependent background completion;
\item gauge/projector completion:
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\]
implementation-dependent.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{D6. Background-adapted regulator and projector.}
To define the projected flow honestly, one needs:
\[
R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=

R_{T,k},R_{O,k},R_{D,k}

with the \(A\)-sector regulator acting only on the physical projected subspace
