\section*{Projected loop-kernel formula for \texorpdfstring{$\Sigma_O^{(OD)}$}{SigmaO(OD)} and \texorpdfstring{$\Sigma_D^{(OD)}$}{SigmaD(OD)}}

\subsection*{1. Background-generated mixed cubic vertices}

On the minimal admissible background
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\]
the mixed quartic interaction
\[
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
\]
generates the cubic fluctuation vertices
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar n_B(\xi).
\label{eq:OD_vertices_kernel}
\end{equation}
These are the minimal background-generated sources of the mixed \(OD\) bubble/sunset contribution to the two-point flow.

\subsection*{2. Projected propagators and mode basis}

Let
\[
\mathcal H_{OO},\qquad \mathcal H_{DD}
\]
be the background-dependent \(O\)- and \(D\)-sector Hessian blocks.
Choose orthonormal eigenmode bases
\[
\mathcal H_{OO} u_m = E^O_m u_m,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{DD} v_n = E^D_n v_n,
\]
with projectors
\[
P_O=\sum_m |u_m\rangle\langle u_m|,
\qquad
P_D=\sum_n |v_n\rangle\langle v_n|.
\]
The regulated projected propagators are
\begin{equation}
G_O(q;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\Bigl(
P_O[\mathcal H_{OO}+R_{O,k}]P_O
\Bigr)^{-1},
\qquad
G_D(q;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\Bigl(
P_D[\mathcal H_{DD}+R_{D,k}]P_D
\Bigr)^{-1}.
\label{eq:OD_projected_props}
\end{equation}

In the mixed kernel formulas below, the loop trace includes:
\begin{enumerate}
\item worldvolume momentum integration \(q\),
\item summation over the background transverse-mode indices \(m,n\),
\item any residual internal \(2\times2\) bundle contraction.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{3. Explicit projected kernel for \(\Sigma_O^{(OD)}\)}

The \(OD\)-mixed contribution to the \(O\)-sector two-point function is generated by the cubic vertex
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}.
\]
Its projected self-energy has the form
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
-
\int\!\frac{d^d q}{(2\pi)^d}
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;mn}(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;nm}(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)\,
\partial_t R_k(q),
\label{eq:SigmaO_kernel_main}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;mn}(p,q)
:=
\left\langle
u_m
\middle|
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}(p,q;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\middle|
v_n
\right\rangle.
\label{eq:VO_kernel_def}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:OD_vertices_kernel}, this matrix element is schematically
\begin{equation}
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;mn}(p,q)
=
\lambda_{OD}\,
\mathcal B^{\chi}_{mn}(\xi)\,
\mathcal P_O(p,q),
\label{eq:VO_factorized}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\mathcal B^{\chi}_{mn}(\xi)
\sim
\langle u_m,\bar\chi_B(\xi) v_n\rangle,
\]
and \(\mathcal P_O(p,q)\) collecting momentum/projector structure.

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^{\chi}_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_O(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^{\chi}_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_O(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q).
}
\label{eq:SigmaO_factorized_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Explicit projected kernel for \(\Sigma_D^{(OD)}\)}

Similarly, the \(D\)-sector mixed self-energy is generated by
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}.
\]
Its projected form is
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
-
\int\!\frac{d^d q}{(2\pi)^d}
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{D;mn}(p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(q)\,
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{D;nm}(-p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(p+q)\,
\partial_t R_k(q),
\label{eq:SigmaD_kernel_main}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{D;mn}(p,q)
:=
\left\langle
v_n
\middle|
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}(p,q;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\middle|
u_m
\right\rangle
=
\lambda_{OD}\,
\mathcal B^{n}_{nm}(\xi)\,
\mathcal P_D(p,q),
\label{eq:VD_factorized}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathcal B^{n}_{nm}(\xi)\sim \langle v_n,\bar n_B(\xi)u_m\rangle.
\]
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^{n}_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_D(p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^{n}_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_D(-p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q).
}
\label{eq:SigmaD_factorized_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Momentum-derivative extraction}

The \(OD\)-mixed contribution to the sectoral wavefunction flows is obtained by
\begin{equation}
\partial_t Z_O^{(OD)}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_t Z_D^{(OD)}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0}.
\label{eq:OD_Z_extract}
\end{equation}
Then the \(OD\)-mixed block of the anisotropy-flow matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{O,D\}.
}
\label{eq:MZOD_sign_formula_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Sign separation}

The projected kernel formulas \eqref{eq:SigmaO_factorized_final} and \eqref{eq:SigmaD_factorized_final} show that the sign problem separates into three pieces.

\paragraph{(i) Overall loop sign.}
Both self-energies carry the standard bubble minus sign:
\[
\Sigma^{(OD)}\sim -(\text{positive kernel}) \quad \text{if all projected propagators and }\partial_tR_k\text{ are positive.}
\]
This tends to favor negative diagonal contributions.

\paragraph{(ii) Background-overlap sign.}
The products
\[
\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}\mathcal B^\chi_{nm},
\qquad
\mathcal B^n_{nm}\mathcal B^n_{mn}
\]
are positive-semidefinite if the relevant background overlap matrices are Hermitian.
This again tends to favor negative diagonal terms.

\paragraph{(iii) Off-diagonal anisotropy response.}
The sign of
\[
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_D}\Sigma_O^{(OD)},
\qquad
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_O}\Sigma_D^{(OD)}
\]
depends on how the anisotropy variables deform the propagators and projected vertices.
This is the genuine mixed sign bottleneck and cannot be fixed without explicit contraction.

\subsection*{7. Exchange-symmetric simplification}

If the background and projected regulator are symmetric under the exchange
\[
O \leftrightarrow D,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DD},
\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DO}.
\label{eq:OD_exchange_final}
\end{equation}
The physical traceless \(OD\) anisotropy direction
\[
u=\delta_O-\delta_D
\]
then has eigenvalue
\begin{equation}
\lambda_{OD}^{\mathrm{phys}}
=
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}.
\label{eq:OD_eigen_final}
\end{equation}
Therefore the isotropizing sign condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}<0.
}
\label{eq:OD_iso_sign_final}
\end{equation}

A sufficient Laplacian-type target is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_Z^{OD}
=
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
1 & -1\\
-1 & 1
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0,
}
\label{eq:OD_laplacian_final}
\end{equation}
for which the physical eigenvalue is
\[
-2\lambda<0.
\]

\subsection*{8. Honest conclusion}

Thus the \(OD\)-mixed bottleneck is now reduced completely to the projected loop-kernel sign test:

\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min}),
\qquad
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
}
\]
are known formally, and
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0}
}
\]
is the exact sign-test formula.

What remains open is no longer the structure, but the explicit sign of the projected contraction kernel.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
\Longrightarrow
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar n_B(\xi).
}
\]

These generate the projected mixed self-energies
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^{\chi}_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_O(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^{\chi}_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_O(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^{n}_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_D(p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^{n}_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_D(-p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q).
}
\]

Then the exact \(OD\)-mixed sign-test formula is
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{O,D\}.
}
\]

If exchange symmetry gives
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DD},
\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DO},
\]
then the physical traceless eigenvalue is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{OD}^{\mathrm{phys}}
=
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}.
}
\]
Hence isotropization requires
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}<0.
}
\]

A clean sufficient target is the Laplacian form
\[
\boxed{
M_Z^{OD}
=
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
1 & -1\\
-1 & 1
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0,
}
\]
for which
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{OD}^{\mathrm{phys}}=-2\lambda<0.
}
\]

So the \(OD\)-mixed bottleneck is now reduced to one explicit projected loop-kernel derivative test.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Minimal calculable form of the projected \(OD\)-mixed loop kernel}

\subsection*{1. Starting point}

From the background split
\[
\Phi=\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi,
\qquad
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\qquad
\varphi=(a,\nu,\zeta),
\]
the mixed quartic interaction
\[
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
\]
generates the background-induced cubic fluctuation vertices
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar n_B(\xi).
\]

Hence the \(OD\)-mixed self-energies take the projected bubble form
\[
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min}),
\qquad
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min}),
\]
and the exact sign-test formula is
\begin{equation}
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{O,D\}.
\label{eq:MZOD_exact_again}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Rank-one overlap reduction}

Let
\[
\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}:=\langle u_m,\bar\chi_B v_n\rangle,
\qquad
\mathcal B^n_{nm}:=\langle v_n,\bar n_B u_m\rangle,
\]
where \(\{u_m\}\) and \(\{v_n\}\) are orthonormal eigenmodes of the projected \(O\)- and \(D\)-sector Hessians.

Then the factorized kernels are
\begin{align}
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p)
&=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_O(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^\chi_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_O(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q),
\label{eq:SigmaO_fact_rank1}
\\
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p)
&=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^n_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_D(p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^n_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_D(-p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q).
\label{eq:SigmaD_fact_rank1}
\end{align}

If the background overlaps are Hermitian,
\[
\mathcal B^\chi_{nm}=(\mathcal B^\chi_{mn})^\ast,
\qquad
\mathcal B^n_{mn}=(\mathcal B^n_{nm})^\ast,
\]
then the overlap products become positive semidefinite:
\[
\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}\mathcal B^\chi_{nm}=|\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}|^2\ge 0,
\qquad
\mathcal B^n_{nm}\mathcal B^n_{mn}=|\mathcal B^n_{nm}|^2\ge 0.
\]

Thus the sign problem is reduced to the momentum/projector part of the loop kernel.

\subsection*{3. Small-\(p\) expansion}

Assume the projected momentum structure is smooth near \(p=0\):
\[
\mathcal P_I(p,q)=\mathcal P_I^{(0)}(q)+p_\mu \mathcal P_I^{(1)\mu}(q)+\frac12 p_\mu p_\nu \mathcal P_I^{(2)\mu\nu}(q)+\cdots.
\]
Also expand the propagator:
\[
G_I^{(m)}(p+q)
=
G_I^{(m)}(q)
+
p_\mu \partial_{q_\mu}G_I^{(m)}(q)
+
\frac12 p_\mu p_\nu \partial_{q_\mu}\partial_{q_\nu}G_I^{(m)}(q)
+\cdots.
\]

Then
\[
\left.\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p)\right|_{p=0}
\]
is a finite linear combination of the following three kernel types:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{vertex-curvature term}
\[
K^{(V)}_I(q)
\sim
\mathcal P_I^{(2)}(q)\,G_{\bar I}(q)\,G_I(q)\,\partial_tR_k(q);
\]

\item \textbf{propagator-curvature term}
\[
K^{(G)}_I(q)
\sim
\mathcal P_I^{(0)}(q)\,G_{\bar I}(q)\,\partial_q^2 G_I(q)\,\partial_tR_k(q);
\]

\item \textbf{mixed derivative term}
\[
K^{(VG)}_I(q)
\sim
\mathcal P_I^{(1)}(q)\,G_{\bar I}(q)\,\partial_q G_I(q)\,\partial_tR_k(q).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the sign-test formula becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left.\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p)\right|_{p=0}
=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
W^{(I)}_{mn}(q)\,
\Bigl[
K^{(V)}_I(q)+K^{(G)}_I(q)+K^{(VG)}_I(q)
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:SigmaI_smallp_kernel}
\end{equation}
where
\[
W^{(O)}_{mn}(q)=|\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}|^2\,\partial_tR_k(q),
\qquad
W^{(D)}_{mn}(q)=|\mathcal B^n_{nm}|^2\,\partial_tR_k(q).
\]

\subsection*{4. Minimal sign criterion}

A clean sufficient criterion for the diagonal part is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_tR_k(q)\ge 0,
\qquad
G_O^{(m)}(q)\ge 0,
\qquad
G_D^{(n)}(q)\ge 0,
\qquad
K^{(V)}_I+K^{(G)}_I+K^{(VG)}_I\ge 0
}
\label{eq:diag_sign_sufficient}
\end{equation}
for the relevant projected Euclidean kernel region.

Then
\[
\left.\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p)\right|_{p=0}\le 0,
\]
and hence the diagonal entries tend to satisfy
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}<0,
\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{DD}<0.
\]

This is not yet a theorem for the actual TECT data, but it gives the exact sign target of the projected contraction.

\subsection*{5. Off-diagonal response test}

The off-diagonal entries arise from the anisotropy response:
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_D}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p)
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\]
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{DO}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_O}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p)
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0}.
\]
These derivatives act on:
\begin{itemize}
\item the projected propagators \(G_O,G_D\),
\item possibly the projected vertices \(\mathcal P_O,\mathcal P_D\),
\item the regulator \(R_k\) if it is sector-dependent.
\end{itemize}

Therefore the explicit off-diagonal sign test is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}>0,\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{DO}>0
}
\label{eq:offdiag_positive_target}
\end{equation}
together with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}+(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}=0,
\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{DD}+(M_Z^{OD})_{DO}=0
}
\label{eq:rowsum_balance_target}
\end{equation}
if one wants the exact Laplacian target
\[
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
1 & -1\\
-1 & 1
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

\subsection*{6. Exchange-symmetric reduction}

If the projected background and regulator respect \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry, then
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DD},
\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DO},
\]
and the physical traceless eigenvalue is
\[
\lambda_{OD}^{\mathrm{phys}}
=
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}.
\]
Thus the final sign test reduces to a single inequality:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}<0.
}
\label{eq:single_OD_test}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Honest status}

At this point the \(OD\)-mixed bottleneck is reduced as far as one can go without actually performing the projected contraction.

What is now explicit:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact bubble self-energy formulas \(\Sigma_O^{(OD)},\Sigma_D^{(OD)}\),
\item the small-\(p\) kernel decomposition,
\item the sufficient sign pattern for isotropization,
\item the final one-inequality reduction under \(O\leftrightarrow D\) symmetry.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the detailed form of the projected momentum structures \(\mathcal P_O,\mathcal P_D\),
\item the actual sign of the anisotropy response derivatives,
\item the numerical or analytic evaluation of the loop kernels.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p)
=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^{\chi}_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_O(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^{\chi}_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_O(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p)
=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^{n}_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_D(p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^{n}_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_D(-p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q).
}
\]

The exact sign-test formula is
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p)
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{O,D\}.
}
\]

After small-\(p\) expansion,
\[
\left.\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p)\right|_{p=0}
=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q\sum_{m,n}
W^{(I)}_{mn}(q)\,
\bigl[
K_I^{(V)}(q)+K_I^{(G)}(q)+K_I^{(VG)}(q)
\bigr].
\]

A sufficient diagonal sign criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\partial_tR_k\ge 0,\qquad
G_O\ge 0,\qquad
G_D\ge 0,\qquad
K_I^{(V)}+K_I^{(G)}+K_I^{(VG)}\ge 0,
}
\]
which implies
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}<0,\qquad (M_Z^{OD})_{DD}<0.
}
\]

The off-diagonal target is
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}>0,\qquad (M_Z^{OD})_{DO}>0,
}
\]
and with row-sum balance one recovers the Laplacian form
\[
\boxed{
M_Z^{OD}
=
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
1 & -1\\
-1 & 1
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0.
}
\]

If \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry holds, the whole test reduces to
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}<0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Projected polarization-kernel formula for the gauge/projector contribution to \(M_Z\)}

\subsection*{1. Physical starting point}

The \(A\)-sector contribution to the derivative-anisotropy flow must be defined on the physical transverse subspace.
Let
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\]
denote the background-dependent gauge-sector two-point kernel, and let
\begin{equation}
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)
=
\eta^{\mu\nu}
-
\frac{p^\mu p^\nu}{p^2}
\label{eq:PiT_phys_kernel}
\end{equation}
be the transverse projector.

The physical projected inverse propagator is
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2),\mathrm{phys}}_{A}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
:=
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min}).
\label{eq:Gamma2_phys_gfproj}
\end{equation}

The corresponding kinetic-flow contribution is
\begin{equation}
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Bigl[
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,
\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\Bigr]
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\qquad
J\in\{T,O,D\}.
\label{eq:MZ_gfproj_exact}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Preconditions for a meaningful sign test}

The projected sign test \eqref{eq:MZ_gfproj_exact} is meaningful only if the \(A\)-sector lies on the gauge-consistent infrared surface:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{transversality:}
\begin{equation}
p^\mu \Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})=0;
\label{eq:gfproj_transverse}
\end{equation}

\item \textbf{no Proca mass:}
\begin{equation}
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(0)\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(0;\bar\Phi_{\min})=0,
\qquad
m_{A,k}^2\to 0;
\label{eq:gfproj_noProca}
\end{equation}

\item \textbf{gauge-preserving regulator:}
\begin{equation}
p^\mu \Pi_{\mu\nu}(p)=0
\quad\text{is preserved by the regulator/renormalization scheme;}
\label{eq:gfproj_regulator}
\end{equation}

\item \textbf{operator-class restriction:}
\begin{equation}
\text{the projected infrared EFT contains only Class I and Class II operators.}
\label{eq:gfproj_ClassI_II}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

These are precisely the conditions under which the one-loop polarization remains transverse and no gauge mass is generated. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5} :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6} :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\subsection*{3. Projected one-loop polarization decomposition}

Let
\[
G_A^{\mathrm{phys}}(\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\Bigl(
\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}
[\Gamma_A^{(2)}+R_{A,k}]
\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}
\Bigr)^{-1}
\]
be the projected gauge-sector propagator, and let
\[
G_{\mathrm{mat}}(\bar\Phi_{\min})
\]
denote the projected matter propagators in the coupled soft sectors.

Then the projected one-loop flow of the gauge two-point function has the standard decomposition
\begin{align}
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
&=
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,
\Biggl\{
\frac12\,
\mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{phys}}
\bigl[
G\,\Gamma^{(4)}_{\mu\nu}\,G\,\partial_tR_k
\bigr]
\nonumber\\
&\qquad
-
\mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{phys}}
\bigl[
G\,\Gamma^{(3)}_{\mu}\,G\,\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu}\,G\,\partial_tR_k
\bigr]
\Biggr\}
\nonumber\\
&=:
\Pi_T^{(4)}(p)+\Pi_T^{(33)}(p).
\label{eq:projected_pol_decomp}
\end{align}
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj},4})_{TJ}
+
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj},33})_{TJ},
}
\label{eq:MZ_gfproj_split_final}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj},4})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Pi_T^{(4)}(p)
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\label{eq:MZ_gfproj_4}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj},33})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Pi_T^{(33)}(p)
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0}.
\label{eq:MZ_gfproj_33}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Minimal calculable kernel form}

In a gauge-preserving scheme with minimally coupled charged transverse matter, the one-loop vacuum polarization has the standard form
\begin{equation}
\Pi^{(\psi)}_{\mu\nu}(p)
=
e^2
\int\!\frac{d^Dk}{(2\pi)^D}
\frac{(2k+p)_\mu(2k+p)_\nu}{
(k^2-m_T^2+i0^+)\bigl((k+p)^2-m_T^2+i0^+\bigr)
},
\label{eq:charged_scalar_pol}
\end{equation}
which can be rewritten as
\begin{equation}
\Pi^{(\psi)}_{\mu\nu}(p)
=
(p_\mu p_\nu-p^2\eta_{\mu\nu})\,\Pi_R(p^2).
\label{eq:transverse_form_standard}
\end{equation}
This is the model template for the projected gauge-sector kernel. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

Accordingly, the projected background-adapted polarization kernel should be written schematically as
\begin{equation}
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
p^2\,\mathcal K_A(p^2;\bar\Phi_{\min}),
\label{eq:projected_scalar_kernel}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal K_A
=
\mathcal K_A^{(4)}
+
\mathcal K_A^{(33)}.
\label{eq:KA_split}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\mathcal K_A(0;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{\delta=0}.
}
\label{eq:MZ_gfproj_reduced}
\end{equation}
This is the minimal calculable reduction of the gauge/projector bottleneck.

\subsection*{5. Small-\(p\) sign decomposition}

Expand
\[
\mathcal K_A(p^2;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\mathcal K_A^{(0)}+\mathcal K_A^{(1)}p^2+\cdots.
\]
Then only the \(p^2\)-coefficient of the projected polarization matters.
The sign test separates into:

\paragraph{(i) Tadpole-like projected contribution}
\[
\mathcal K_A^{(4)}(0;\bar\Phi_{\min}).
\]
This often contributes only to local mass-like terms or vanishes after transversality is imposed.
Hence it is usually subleading for the kinetic-flow sign, unless the background-dependent gauge projector produces nontrivial momentum dependence.

\paragraph{(ii) Bubble/sunset projected contribution}
\[
\mathcal K_A^{(33)}(0;\bar\Phi_{\min}).
\]
This is the main candidate for a genuine \(p^2\)-flow, because background-generated cubic vertices can produce a nontrivial momentum-dependent projected polarization.

Thus the practical sign hierarchy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj},33})_{TJ}
\text{ is the dominant sign carrier,}
\qquad
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj},4})_{TJ}
\text{ is usually kinematically constrained.}
}
\label{eq:gfproj_hierarchy}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Sufficient non-dangerous criterion}

A sufficient criterion that the gauge/projector sector is \emph{not} a dangerous anisotropy source is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the projected polarization is transverse;
\item the zero-momentum limit vanishes:
\[
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(0)\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(0)=0;
\]
\item the projected kernel satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\mathcal K_A(0;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{\delta=0}
\ge 0
\quad\text{for the Euclidean sign convention.}
}
\label{eq:gfproj_sufficient_safe}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

Under these conditions, the gauge/projector sector is compatible with isotropization and does not overturn the negative contributions expected from the quartic- and derivative-anisotropy sectors.

\subsection*{7. Honest conclusion}

Thus the gauge/projector bottleneck is now reduced completely to the projected polarization-kernel test:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\mathcal K_A(0;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{\delta=0},
}
\label{eq:gfproj_final_kernel_test}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal K_A\) is defined by the small-\(p\) transverse projected polarization kernel
\[
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
p^2\mathcal K_A(p^2;\bar\Phi_{\min}).
\]

At this point, both remaining sign bottlenecks are reduced to explicit projected kernel derivative tests.
What remains open is their actual evaluation.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Bigl[
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,
\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\Bigr]
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0}.
}
\]

The projected polarization splits as
\[
\boxed{
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\Pi_T^{(4)}(p)+\Pi_T^{(33)}(p),
}
\]
so that
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj},4})_{TJ}
+
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj},33})_{TJ}.
}
\]

Using the standard transverse form,
\[
\Pi^{(\psi)}_{\mu\nu}(p)
=
(p_\mu p_\nu-p^2\eta_{\mu\nu})\,\Pi_R(p^2),
\]
the background-adapted projected kernel should be written as
\[
\boxed{
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
p^2\,\mathcal K_A(p^2;\bar\Phi_{\min}),
}
\]
with
\[
\mathcal K_A=\mathcal K_A^{(4)}+\mathcal K_A^{(33)}.
\]

Therefore the gauge/projector sign test reduces to
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\mathcal K_A(0;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{\delta=0}.
}
\]

Its consistency preconditions are:
\[
\boxed{
p^\mu\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}=0,\qquad
m_{A,k}^2\to 0,\qquad
\text{gauge-preserving regulator},\qquad
\text{Class I/II only}.
}
\]

The practical sign hierarchy is
\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj},33})_{TJ}
\text{ is the main sign carrier,}
\qquad
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj},4})_{TJ}
\text{ is usually kinematically constrained.}
}
\]

Thus the gauge/projector bottleneck is now reduced to one explicit projected polarization-kernel derivative test.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Final sufficient criterion for \texorpdfstring{$\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathrm{traceless}})<0$}{spec(MZ|traceless)<0}}

\subsection*{1. Physical setting}

The physical derivative-anisotropy variables are
\[
\delta_T,\qquad \delta_O,\qquad \delta_D,
\qquad
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
\]
Let
\[
\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}
:=
\left\{
u=(\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D)^T\in \mathbb R^3:
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0
\right\}
\]
denote the two-dimensional traceless physical anisotropy subspace.

The loop-level flow is
\[
\partial_t u = M_Z u + O(u^2).
\]
The problem is to guarantee
\[
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}})\subset(-\infty,0).
\]

\subsection*{2. Canonical decomposition of the kinetic-flow matrix}

At the present stage, the physically relevant decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_Z
=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}
+
M_Z^{(OD)}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}.
}
\label{eq:MZ_final_decomp}
\end{equation}
Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(M_Z^{(\tau)}\) is induced by the quartic cubic-anisotropy sector,
\item \(M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}\) is induced by the derivative-anisotropy sector,
\item \(M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}\) collects the self-sector \(O\)- and \(D\)-stabilizing pieces,
\item \(M_Z^{(OD)}\) is the mixed \(OD\)-bubble contribution,
\item \(M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}\) is the projected gauge/projector contribution.
\end{itemize}

The current theorem-level status is:
\[
M_Z^{(\tau)}\ \text{and}\ M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
\]
are the main expected isotropizing sources, whereas
\[
M_Z^{(OD)}\ \text{and}\ M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}
\]
are the two main remaining sign bottlenecks. This is consistent with the current TECT FRG notes: quartic anisotropy is explicitly irrelevant for \(N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6\), while the derivative-anisotropy sector is reduced to the explicit sign of \(M_Z\). :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection*{3. Good/bad split}

Define the \emph{good} and \emph{bad} parts by
\begin{equation}
M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}
:=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})},
\label{eq:MZ_good_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
M_Z^{\mathrm{bad}}
:=
M_Z^{(OD)}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}.
\label{eq:MZ_bad_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
M_Z = M_Z^{\mathrm{good}} + M_Z^{\mathrm{bad}}.
\]

\subsection*{4. Coercive negativity of the good part}

Assume that on the traceless subspace \(\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}\), the good part satisfies the quadratic-form bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle u,M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}u\rangle
\le
-\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\|u\|^2
\qquad
\forall u\in \mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>0.
}
\label{eq:good_negative_bound}
\end{equation}
This is the coercive negativity input.

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
It means that the combined quartic-anisotropy, derivative-anisotropy, and self-sector contributions are already strictly isotropizing on the physical anisotropy sector.

\paragraph{Support from current TECT status.}
The quartic anisotropy piece has explicit negative RG eigenvalue
\[
\theta_\tau
=
\epsilon\frac{4-N_{\mathrm{eff}}}{N_{\mathrm{eff}}+8}
=
-\frac{\epsilon}{7}<0
\qquad
(N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6),
\]
while the derivative-anisotropy direction is expected to be irrelevant but is not yet proved microscopically. Thus \eqref{eq:good_negative_bound} is not currently a theorem, but it is the correct target form. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6} :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection*{5. Norm control of the bad part}

Assume that the two remaining bottlenecks satisfy operator-norm bounds on the physical traceless sector:
\begin{equation}
\|M_Z^{(OD)}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|
\le
\eta_{OD},
\qquad
\|M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|
\le
\eta_{\mathrm{gf}},
\label{eq:bad_piece_bounds}
\end{equation}
and define
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{bad}}
:=
\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
\label{eq:eta_bad_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|M_Z^{\mathrm{bad}}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|
\le
\eta_{\mathrm{bad}}.
}
\label{eq:MZ_bad_norm}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Origin of these bounds.}
The \(OD\)-mixed contribution has already been reduced to the projected self-energy derivative test
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p)
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\]
while the gauge/projector contribution has been reduced to the projected polarization derivative test
\[
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\mathcal K_A(0;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{\delta=0}.
\]
Thus \(\eta_{OD}\) and \(\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}\) are explicit finite projected-kernel bounds.

\subsection*{6. Final sufficient negativity criterion}

Now let \(u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}\). Then
\begin{align}
\langle u,M_Zu\rangle
&=
\langle u,M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}u\rangle
+
\langle u,M_Z^{\mathrm{bad}}u\rangle
\nonumber\\
&\le
-\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\|u\|^2
+
\|M_Z^{\mathrm{bad}}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|\,
\|u\|^2
\nonumber\\
&\le
-(\mu_{\mathrm{good}}-\eta_{\mathrm{bad}})\|u\|^2.
\label{eq:MZ_negativity_estimate}
\end{align}
Therefore, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{\mathrm{bad}},
}
\label{eq:master_negativity_condition}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle u,M_Zu\rangle<0
\qquad
\forall u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}\setminus\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:strict_negativity_form}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}})\subset(-\infty,0).
}
\label{eq:spectrum_negative_final}
\end{equation}

This is the final sufficient negativity criterion.

\subsection*{7. Laplacian target as a stronger sufficient criterion}

A stronger algebraic sufficient criterion is the exact Laplacian form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_Z
=
-\lambda
\begin{pmatrix}
2 & -1 & -1\\
-1 & 2 & -1\\
-1 & -1 & 2
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\lambda>0,
}
\label{eq:MZ_laplacian_target_final}
\end{equation}
which has one zero mode in the unphysical common-rescaling direction and two physical eigenvalues
\[
-3\lambda,\qquad -3\lambda.
\]
The notes already identify this as the exact algebraic target that the explicit FRG computation should verify. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

Thus:
\[
\text{Laplacian form with }\lambda>0
\Longrightarrow
\eqref{eq:master_negativity_condition}
\Longrightarrow
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}})<0.
\]

\subsection*{8. Gauge/projector preconditions}

The criterion above must be used together with the gauge-consistency preconditions:
\begin{equation}
p^\mu\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}=0,
\qquad
m_{A,k}^2\to 0,
\qquad
\text{gauge-preserving regulator},
\qquad
\text{Class I/II only}.
\label{eq:gauge_preconditions_final}
\end{equation}
These are necessary for \((M_Z)^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}\) to be a meaningful physical contribution rather than a gauge artifact. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10} 

\subsection*{9. Honest final status}

The exact current logical status is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The criterion }
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{\mathrm{bad}}
\text{ is fully explicit and sufficient,}
}
\label{eq:criterion_explicit}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual numerical/analytic values of }
\mu_{\mathrm{good}},\eta_{OD},\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}
\text{ are not yet derived from the current TECT data.}
}
\label{eq:criterion_not_yet_verified}
\end{equation}
So the frontier is no longer conceptual:
it is the explicit estimation of these finitely many quantities.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
M_Z
=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}
+
M_Z^{(OD)}

Define

A stronger algebraic sufficient target is

\section*{Actual computation priority list}

\subsection*{A. Global status}

The remaining TECT frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is a finite computation / verification program.

On the local fermion side, the unresolved tasks are exactly:
\[
\text{(I) witness nonvanishing,}
\quad
\text{(II) opposite-valley survival/matching,}
\quad
\text{(III) remote spectral gap,}
\quad
\text{(IV) zero constant mixing,}
\quad
\text{(V) mass protection.}
\]
These are explicitly listed as the remaining microscopic verification tasks of the shell-reduced Dirac program. 

On the IR-isotropy side, the quartic anisotropy is already irrelevant for
\[
N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6,
\qquad
\theta_\tau=-\frac{\epsilon}{7}<0,
\]
whereas the derivative-anisotropy / velocity-locking problem still requires the explicit computation of
\[
M_Z.
\]
This is also explicitly stated in the TECT FRG notes. 

\subsection*{B. Final sufficient negativity criterion}

The physical anisotropy problem is controlled by
\[
M_Z
=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}
+
M_Z^{(OD)}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}
\]
restricted to the traceless subspace
\[
\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\{u=(\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D)^T:\ 2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0\}.
\]

Define
\[
M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}
=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})},
\]
\[
M_Z^{\mathrm{bad}}
=
M_Z^{(OD)}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}.
\]
If
\[
\langle u,M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}u\rangle
\le
-\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\|u\|^2
\qquad
(\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>0),
\]
and
\[
\|M_Z^{(OD)}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|\le \eta_{OD},
\qquad
\|M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|\le \eta_{\mathrm{gf}},

then the master sufficient condition is

\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}

Therefore the actual computation priority is dictated by the quantities

\eta_{OD},\qquad

\mu_{\mathrm{good}}.

\subsection*{C. Priority 1: compute \texorpdfstring{$\eta_{OD}$}{etaOD}}

The mixed \(OD\) bottleneck is already reduced to the explicit projected self-energy derivative test
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{O,D\}.
\]
The projected kernels are
\[
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p),
\qquad
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p),
\]
with explicit background-overlap factors and projected propagators.

\paragraph{Why this is Priority 1.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item It is the first genuine off-diagonal anisotropy source.
\item It does not yet require the full gauge/projector implementation.
\item It is the cleanest nontrivial sign bottleneck in the matter-sector background field problem.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Minimal deliverable.}
Produce a rigorous upper bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|M_Z^{(OD)}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|
\le
\eta_{OD}
}
\label{eq:etaOD_deliverable}
\end{equation}
from the projected loop-kernel formulas.

\paragraph{Operational substeps.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Fix the projected mode bases \(u_m,v_n\) for \(\mathcal H_{OO},\mathcal H_{DD}\).
\item Compute / bound the background overlaps
\[
\mathcal B^\chi_{mn},\qquad \mathcal B^n_{nm}.
\]
\item Bound the projected propagators \(G_O,G_D\).
\item Bound the small-\(p\) kernel coefficients
\[
K_I^{(V)},\qquad K_I^{(G)},\qquad K_I^{(VG)}.
\]
\item Extract the traceless-subspace operator norm.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{D. Priority 2: compute \texorpdfstring{$\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}$}{etagf}}

The gauge/projector bottleneck is reduced to the projected polarization-kernel derivative test
\[
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\mathcal K_A(0;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{\delta=0},
\]
where
\[
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
p^2\mathcal K_A(p^2;\bar\Phi_{\min}).
\]

\paragraph{Why this is Priority 2.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item It is the second remaining sign bottleneck.
\item It is structurally more delicate because it requires:
\[
p^\mu\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}=0,
\qquad
m_{A,k}^2\to 0,
\qquad
\text{gauge-preserving regulator},
\qquad
\text{Class I/II only}.
\]
\item Therefore it should be attempted only after the matter-sector \(OD\) bound is already under control.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Minimal deliverable.}
Produce a rigorous upper bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|
\le
\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
}
\label{eq:etagf_deliverable}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Operational substeps.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Fix \(\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}\) explicitly.
\item Verify transversality and zero Proca mass.
\item Fix a gauge-preserving regulator.
\item Split
\[
\mathcal K_A=\mathcal K_A^{(4)}+\mathcal K_A^{(33)}
\]
and identify the dominant projected sign carrier.
\item Bound the anisotropy response derivatives.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{E. Priority 3: compute \texorpdfstring{$\mu_{\mathrm{good}}$}{mugood}}

The good part is
\[
M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}
=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}.
\]

\paragraph{Why this is Priority 3 rather than Priority 1.}
Although it is crucial for the final theorem, it is not the current bottleneck.
The quartic anisotropy sector already has explicit support:
\[
\theta_\tau=-\frac{\epsilon}{7}<0
\qquad
(N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6),
\]
and the derivative anisotropy sector has the strong TECT expectation
\[
\theta_Y<0.
\]
Hence the good part is already expected to be negative; what remains dangerous are the unresolved mixed/gauge pieces. 

\paragraph{Minimal deliverable.}
Produce a coercive negativity constant
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle u,M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}u\rangle
\le
-\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\|u\|^2
\qquad
\forall u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>0.
}
\label{eq:mugood_deliverable}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Operational substeps.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Use the explicit quartic anisotropy eigenvalue to fix a negative lower bound for \(M_Z^{(\tau)}\).
\item Derive / assume a negative derivative-anisotropy eigenvalue for \(M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}\).
\item Show that the self-sector piece is diagonally stabilizing.
\item Combine the three into a single traceless-subspace coercive estimate.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{F. Priority 4: return to the local Dirac finite checks}

Once the \(M_Z\) negativity program is organized, one should return to the remaining local fermion finite checks:

\begin{enumerate}

P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\quad\text{or explicit seed tensors;}

\Delta>0

via finite Bloch-matrix calculation;

\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(H_R,H_D)=0;

\item mass protection:
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M=\{0\}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
These are already explicitly enumerated in the current Dirac-emergence roadmap. 

\subsection*{G. Final ordered list}

The actual ordered computation program is therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\textbf{(1)}\ \eta_{OD}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\textbf{(2)}\ \eta_{\mathrm{gf}}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad

\quad\Longrightarrow\quad

}
