If \eqref{eq:ordered_MZ_program} succeeds, then
\[
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}})<0,
\]
hence
\[
\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D\to 0,
\]
and the infrared soft sector becomes isotropic and velocity-locked.

Then the local fermion finite checks can be completed in parallel or immediately afterward, closing the TECT local Dirac / IR-isotropy frontier.

\subsection*{H. Honest final status}

The exact current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The full frontier has been reduced to finitely many explicit bounds and finite matrix/projection tests.}
}
\]

What is not yet done is not conceptual:
it is simply the actual evaluation of those quantities.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual computation priority list}
}
\]

The final sufficient negativity criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}
\Longrightarrow
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}})\subset(-\infty,0),
}
\]
where
\[
M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}
=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})},
\qquad
M_Z^{\mathrm{bad}}
=
M_Z^{(OD)}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}.
\]

Hence the actual ordered computation program is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Priority 1: compute } \eta_{OD}
=
\|M_Z^{(OD)}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Priority 2: compute } \eta_{\mathrm{gf}}
=
\|M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Priority 3: compute } \mu_{\mathrm{good}}
\text{ from }
M_Z^{(\tau)}+M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}+M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Priority 4: verify }
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
}
\]

If this succeeds, then
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}})<0
\Longrightarrow
\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D\to 0,
}
\]
so the soft sector is infrared isotropic and velocity-locked.

In parallel or immediately afterward, complete the local Dirac finite checks:
\[
\boxed{
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0,\quad
\text{opposite-valley matching},\quad
\Delta>0,\quad
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(H_R,H_D)=0,\quad
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M=\{0\}.
}
\]

Thus the entire TECT frontier is now reduced to finitely many explicit bounds, matrix tests, and projected kernel evaluations.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Minimal bound package for the projected \(OD\)-kernel}

\subsection*{1. Starting point}

The \(OD\)-mixed contribution is controlled by
\begin{equation}
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p)
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{O,D\},
\label{eq:MZOD_start_package}
\end{equation}
with projected self-energies
\begin{align}
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p)
&=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^{\chi}_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_O(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^{\chi}_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_O(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q),
\label{eq:SigmaO_package}
\\
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p)
&=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^{n}_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_D(p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^{n}_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_D(-p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q).
\label{eq:SigmaD_package}
\end{align}

Thus \(\eta_{OD}\) will follow once every factor in these kernels is bounded separately.

\subsection*{2. Package A: background overlap bounds}

Define the background overlap matrices
\[
\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}
:=
\langle u_m,\bar\chi_B v_n\rangle,
\qquad
\mathcal B^n_{nm}
:=
\langle v_n,\bar n_B u_m\rangle.
\]
The minimal bound package begins with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}|
\le
\|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi}\,\|u_m\|\,\|v_n\|,
\qquad
|\mathcal B^n_{nm}|
\le
\|\bar n_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi}\,\|u_m\|\,\|v_n\|.
}
\label{eq:B_overlap_basic}
\end{equation}
If the projected mode bases are orthonormal,
\[
\|u_m\|=\|v_n\|=1,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}|
\le
\|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^\infty},
\qquad
|\mathcal B^n_{nm}|
\le
\|\bar n_B\|_{L^\infty}.
}
\label{eq:B_overlap_orthonormal}
\end{equation}

A slightly sharper Hilbert-Schmidt form is
\begin{equation}
\sum_{m,n}|\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}|^2
=
\|P_O \bar\chi_B P_D\|_{\mathrm{HS}}^2,
\qquad
\sum_{m,n}|\mathcal B^n_{nm}|^2
=
\|P_D \bar n_B P_O\|_{\mathrm{HS}}^2.
\label{eq:B_overlap_HS}
\end{equation}
Hence the first deliverable is a finite bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi
:=
\|P_O \bar\chi_B P_D\|_{\mathrm{HS}},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n
:=
\|P_D \bar n_B P_O\|_{\mathrm{HS}}.
}
\label{eq:Bchi_Bn_def}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{3. Package B: projected propagator bounds}

Let
\[
G_O^{(m)}(q)=\frac{1}{E_m^O(q)+R_{O,k}(q)},
\qquad
G_D^{(n)}(q)=\frac{1}{E_n^D(q)+R_{D,k}(q)}.
\]
If the background Hessian blocks satisfy a spectral lower bound
\begin{equation}
E_m^O(q)\ge \Delta_O>0,
\qquad
E_n^D(q)\ge \Delta_D>0,
\label{eq:OD_gap_bounds}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|G_O^{(m)}(q)|
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_O+\inf R_{O,k}},
\qquad
|G_D^{(n)}(q)|
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_D+\inf R_{D,k}}.
}
\label{eq:prop_basic_bounds}
\end{equation}
Hence define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O
:=
\sup_{m,q}|G_O^{(m)}(q)|,
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D
:=
\sup_{n,q}|G_D^{(n)}(q)|.
}
\label{eq:GO_GD_def}
\end{equation}

This is the second deliverable.
It is exactly where the remote/background spectral gap feeds into the \(M_Z\) estimate.

\subsection*{4. Package C: regulator bounds}

Assume a standard monotone cutoff profile so that
\[
\partial_tR_k(q)\ge 0.
\]
Define the size of the regulator derivative by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
:=
\sup_q |\partial_tR_k(q)|.
}
\label{eq:Rk_bound}
\end{equation}
If one uses an optimized profile, \(\partial_tR_k\) is compactly supported in the low-momentum shell and \(\mathfrak R_k\) is finite.

This is the third deliverable.

\subsection*{5. Package D: small-\(p\) kernel curvature bounds}

Expand the projected momentum structures and propagators near \(p=0\):
\[
\mathcal P_I(p,q)=\mathcal P_I^{(0)}+\mathcal P_I^{(1)}\cdot p+\frac12 p\cdot \mathcal P_I^{(2)}\cdot p+\cdots,
\]
\[
G_I(p+q)=G_I(q)+p\cdot \partial_q G_I(q)+\frac12 p\cdot \partial_q^2 G_I(q)\cdot p+\cdots.
\]
Then
\[
\left.\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p)\right|_{p=0}
\]
is controlled by three kernel classes:
\[
K_I^{(V)},\qquad
K_I^{(G)},\qquad
K_I^{(VG)}.
\]
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_I
:=
\sup_q
\Bigl(
|K_I^{(V)}(q)|
+
|K_I^{(G)}(q)|
+
|K_I^{(VG)}(q)|
\Bigr),
\qquad
I\in\{O,D\}.
}
\label{eq:KI_def}
\end{equation}
This is the fourth deliverable.

\subsection*{6. Package E: anisotropy-response derivative bounds}

The off-diagonal entries require derivatives with respect to the sectoral anisotropy variables:
\[
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_D}\Sigma_O^{(OD)},
\qquad
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_O}\Sigma_D^{(OD)}.
\]
These act on:
\begin{itemize}
\item the propagators \(G_O,G_D\),
\item the projected momentum structures \(\mathcal P_O,\mathcal P_D\),
\item the regulator if sector-dependent.
\end{itemize}
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak A_{OD}
:=
\sup_{q,m,n}
\left|
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_D}
\bigl(
\mathcal P_O\,G_D\,G_O\,\partial_tR_k
\bigr)
\right|_{\delta=0},
}
\label{eq:AOD_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak A_{DO}
:=
\sup_{q,m,n}
\left|
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_O}
\bigl(
\mathcal P_D\,G_O\,G_D\,\partial_tR_k
\bigr)
\right|_{\delta=0}.
}
\label{eq:ADO_def}
\end{equation}
This is the fifth deliverable.

\subsection*{7. Master bound for \(\eta_{OD}\)}

Using the factorized kernels and the packages above, one gets the schematic estimate
\begin{equation}
\left|
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}
\right|
\lesssim
\lambda_{OD}^2\,
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,
\mathfrak G_O\,
\mathfrak G_D\,
\mathfrak R_k\,
\mathfrak K_O,
\label{eq:MZOO_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\left|
(M_Z^{OD})_{DD}
\right|
\lesssim
\lambda_{OD}^2\,
\mathfrak B_n^2\,
\mathfrak G_O\,
\mathfrak G_D\,
\mathfrak R_k\,
\mathfrak K_D,
\label{eq:MZDD_bound}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\left|
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}
\right|
\lesssim
\lambda_{OD}^2\,
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,
\mathfrak A_{OD},
\qquad
\left|
(M_Z^{OD})_{DO}
\right|
\lesssim
\lambda_{OD}^2\,
\mathfrak B_n^2\,
\mathfrak A_{DO}.
\label{eq:MZOD_offdiag_bound}
\end{equation}

Therefore a minimal norm bound on the \(OD\)-block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{OD}
\lesssim
\lambda_{OD}^2
\Bigl[
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k\,\mathfrak K_O
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k\,\mathfrak K_D
+
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak A_{OD}
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak A_{DO}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:etaOD_master_bound}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{8. Minimal computation package}

Thus the minimal computation package needed to obtain \(\eta_{OD}\) is exactly:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(
\mathfrak B_\chi,\ \mathfrak B_n,\ \mathfrak G_O,\ \mathfrak G_D,\ \mathfrak R_k,\ \mathfrak K_O,\ \mathfrak K_D,\ \mathfrak A_{OD},\ \mathfrak A_{DO}
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:minimal_package_final}
\end{equation}

Once these nine quantities are estimated, \(\eta_{OD}\) follows immediately from \eqref{eq:etaOD_master_bound}.

\subsection*{9. Honest status}

The package above is the minimal honest reduction:
it does not claim the sign, and it does not assume more than what is already structurally derived.
It simply reduces the \(OD\)-mixed bottleneck to finitely many explicit background overlap, propagator, regulator, curvature, and anisotropy-response bounds.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Minimal bound package for }\eta_{OD}
}
\]

Starting from
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p)
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{O,D\},
\]
the projected self-energies are bounded once the following quantities are controlled:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi
=
\|P_O \bar\chi_B P_D\|_{\mathrm{HS}},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n
=
\|P_D \bar n_B P_O\|_{\mathrm{HS}},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O
=
\sup_{m,q}|G_O^{(m)}(q)|,
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D
=
\sup_{n,q}|G_D^{(n)}(q)|,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
=
\sup_q |\partial_tR_k(q)|,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_I
=
\sup_q
\bigl(
|K_I^{(V)}(q)|+|K_I^{(G)}(q)|+|K_I^{(VG)}(q)|
\bigr),
\qquad I\in\{O,D\},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak A_{OD}
=
\sup
\left|
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_D}
(\mathcal P_O G_D G_O \partial_tR_k)
\right|,
\qquad
\mathfrak A_{DO}
=
\sup
\left|
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_O}
(\mathcal P_D G_O G_D \partial_tR_k)
\right|.
}
\]

Then a master bound is
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{OD}
\lesssim
\lambda_{OD}^2
\Bigl[
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k\,\mathfrak K_O
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k\,\mathfrak K_D
+
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak A_{OD}
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak A_{DO}
\Bigr].
}
\]

Therefore the entire \(OD\)-mixed bottleneck is reduced to the finite package
\[
\boxed{
(\mathfrak B_\chi,\mathfrak B_n,\mathfrak G_O,\mathfrak G_D,\mathfrak R_k,\mathfrak K_O,\mathfrak K_D,\mathfrak A_{OD},\mathfrak A_{DO}).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Explicit background overlap bounds for \texorpdfstring{$\mathfrak B_\chi$}{Bchi} and \texorpdfstring{$\mathfrak B_n$}{Bn}}

\subsection*{1. Definitions}

The two background overlap quantities entering the \(OD\)-mixed kernel package are
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak B_\chi
:=
\|P_O \bar\chi_B P_D\|_{\mathrm{HS}},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n
:=
\|P_D \bar n_B P_O\|_{\mathrm{HS}},
\label{eq:Bchi_Bn_defs}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(P_O\) is the projector onto the relevant \(O\)-sector low-energy fluctuation subspace,
\item \(P_D\) is the projector onto the relevant \(D\)-sector low-energy fluctuation subspace,
\item \(\bar n_B(\xi)\) and \(\bar\chi_B(\xi)\) are the shell-/defect-adapted background profiles on the transverse coordinate \(\xi\).
\end{itemize}

Equivalently, if \(\{u_m\}_{m=1}^{N_O}\) and \(\{v_n\}_{n=1}^{N_D}\) are orthonormal bases of the projected \(O\)- and \(D\)-subspaces, then
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak B_\chi^2
=
\sum_{m=1}^{N_O}\sum_{n=1}^{N_D}
\bigl|
\langle u_m,\bar\chi_B v_n\rangle
\bigr|^2,
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n^2
=
\sum_{n=1}^{N_D}\sum_{m=1}^{N_O}
\bigl|
\langle v_n,\bar n_B u_m\rangle
\bigr|^2.
\label{eq:Bchi_Bn_basis}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Basic operator-norm bound}

Since Hilbert-Schmidt norm is bounded by rank times operator norm,
\begin{equation}
\|P_O \bar\chi_B P_D\|_{\mathrm{HS}}
\le
\sqrt{\operatorname{rank}(P_O)\operatorname{rank}(P_D)}\,
\|P_O \bar\chi_B P_D\|_{\mathrm{op}},
\label{eq:HS_rank_bound1}
\end{equation}
and similarly
\begin{equation}
\|P_D \bar n_B P_O\|_{\mathrm{HS}}
\le
\sqrt{\operatorname{rank}(P_D)\operatorname{rank}(P_O)}\,
\|P_D \bar n_B P_O\|_{\mathrm{op}}.
\label{eq:HS_rank_bound2}
\end{equation}

Because orthogonal projectors have operator norm \(1\),
\[
\|P_O\|=\|P_D\|=1,
\]
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar\chi_B\|_{\mathrm{op}},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar n_B\|_{\mathrm{op}},
}
\label{eq:basic_overlap_bound}
\end{equation}
where
\[
N_O:=\operatorname{rank}(P_O),
\qquad
N_D:=\operatorname{rank}(P_D).
\]

Thus the most primitive overlap control reduces to:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the sizes of the projected low-energy sectors \(N_O,N_D\),
\item the operator norms of the background profiles \(\bar\chi_B,\bar n_B\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{3. \texorpdfstring{$L^\infty$}{Linfty}-type bound}

If \(\bar\chi_B(\xi)\) and \(\bar n_B(\xi)\) act as multiplication operators in \(\xi\), then
\[
\|\bar\chi_B\|_{\mathrm{op}}
\le
\|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi},
\qquad
\|\bar n_B\|_{\mathrm{op}}
\le
\|\bar n_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi}.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar n_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi}.
}
\label{eq:Linfty_overlap_bound}
\end{equation}

This is the cleanest minimal bound, and it is already sufficient for the master estimate of \(\eta_{OD}\).

\subsection*{4. Sharper trace-class / local-support bound}

If the background profiles are localized in the defect core and the projected modes satisfy local \(L^2\)-normalization on the same core region \(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}}\subset \mathbb R_\xi\), then one may sharpen the estimate.

Using Cauchy-Schwarz,
\begin{align}
|\langle u_m,\bar\chi_B v_n\rangle|
&\le
\|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^2(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})}
\,
\|u_m v_n\|_{L^2(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})},
\label{eq:local_CS_chi}
\\
|\langle v_n,\bar n_B u_m\rangle|
&\le
\|\bar n_B\|_{L^2(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})}
\,
\|u_m v_n\|_{L^2(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})}.
\label{eq:local_CS_n}
\end{align}
If, in addition, the projected modes satisfy a uniform local \(L^\infty\)-bound
\[
\|u_m\|_{L^\infty(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})}\le C_O,
\qquad
\|v_n\|_{L^\infty(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})}\le C_D,
\]
then
\[
\|u_m v_n\|_{L^2(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})}
\le
C_O C_D\,|\Omega_{\mathrm{def}}|^{1/2},
\]
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,
C_O C_D\,|\Omega_{\mathrm{def}}|^{1/2}\,
\|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^2(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})},
}
\label{eq:localized_Bchi}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_n
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,
C_O C_D\,|\Omega_{\mathrm{def}}|^{1/2}\,
\|\bar n_B\|_{L^2(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})}.
}
\label{eq:localized_Bn}
\end{equation}

These bounds are useful if the defect background is sharply localized and one wants a core-volume improvement over the crude \(L^\infty\)-estimate.

\subsection*{5. Finite-rank low-mode reduction}

In the actual shell-reduced TECT program, the relevant \(O\)- and \(D\)-sectors are already finite-dimensional low-mode sectors after projection.
Thus \(N_O,N_D\) are finite and usually small.
Hence one can define the purely numerical overlap constants
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\chi^{\mathrm{bg}}
:=
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi},
\qquad
C_n^{\mathrm{bg}}
:=
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar n_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi}.
}
\label{eq:bg_constants}
\end{equation}
Then the background overlap package closes as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi\le C_\chi^{\mathrm{bg}},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n\le C_n^{\mathrm{bg}}.
}
\label{eq:bg_package_closed}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal finite-rank reduction required for the later estimate of \(\eta_{OD}\).

\subsection*{6. Symmetry refinement}

If the background satisfies an approximate \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry or equal norm condition
\[
\|\bar n_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi}\sim \|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi},
\]
and if the projected mode dimensions match
\[
N_O=N_D,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak B_\chi\sim \mathfrak B_n.
\label{eq:exchange_overlap}
\end{equation}
This is not necessary, but it simplifies the later \(OD\)-mixed block estimate and makes the Laplacian-type target more natural.

\subsection*{7. Final deliverable}

Thus the first two entries of the minimal \(OD\)-kernel package are closed by the finite-rank background bounds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar n_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi}.
}
\label{eq:final_overlap_deliverable}
\end{equation}
Or, in localized-core form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,
C_O C_D\,|\Omega_{\mathrm{def}}|^{1/2}\,
\|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^2(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})},
}
\label{eq:final_overlap_deliverable_local1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_n
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,
C_O C_D\,|\Omega_{\mathrm{def}}|^{1/2}\,
\|\bar n_B\|_{L^2(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})}.
}
\label{eq:final_overlap_deliverable_local2}
\end{equation}

These are the first explicit finite bounds in the actual \(OD\)-mixed computation program.

\subsection*{8. Honest status}

At this point:
\begin{itemize}
\item no new dynamical assumption has been added,
\item no sign has been overclaimed,
\item the overlap problem has been reduced to finite-dimensional projector ranks and background profile norms.
\end{itemize}
So this part is genuinely closed at the bound-package level.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi
=
\|P_O \bar\chi_B P_D\|_{\mathrm{HS}},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n
=
\|P_D \bar n_B P_O\|_{\mathrm{HS}}.
}
\]

If
\[
N_O=\operatorname{rank}(P_O),
\qquad
N_D=\operatorname{rank}(P_D),
\]
then the basic finite-rank Hilbert-Schmidt bound gives
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar\chi_B\|_{\mathrm{op}},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar n_B\|_{\mathrm{op}}.
}
\]

If the backgrounds act as multiplication operators in \(\xi\), then
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar n_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi}.
}
\]

A localized-core refinement is
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,
C_O C_D\,|\Omega_{\mathrm{def}}|^{1/2}\,
\|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^2(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_n
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,
C_O C_D\,|\Omega_{\mathrm{def}}|^{1/2}\,
\|\bar n_B\|_{L^2(\Omega_{\mathrm{def}})}.
}
\]

Therefore the first two entries of the minimal \(OD\)-kernel package are explicitly closed by finite projector ranks and background profile norms.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Projected propagator bounds for \texorpdfstring{$\mathfrak G_O$}{GO} and \texorpdfstring{$\mathfrak G_D$}{GD}}

\subsection*{1. Definitions}

For the projected \(O\)- and \(D\)-sector background Hessian blocks, define the mode-resolved propagators
\begin{equation}
G_O^{(m)}(q)
=
\frac{1}{E_m^O(q)+R_{O,k}(q)},
\qquad
G_D^{(n)}(q)
=
\frac{1}{E_n^D(q)+R_{D,k}(q)},
\label{eq:GO_GD_defs}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(E_m^O(q)\) are the projected \(O\)-sector eigenvalues of the background-adapted Hessian,
\item \(E_n^D(q)\) are the projected \(D\)-sector eigenvalues,
\item \(R_{O,k}(q),R_{D,k}(q)\) are the corresponding regulator insertions.
\end{itemize}

The quantities needed in the \(OD\)-mixed kernel package are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O
:=
\sup_{m,q}|G_O^{(m)}(q)|,
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D
:=
\sup_{n,q}|G_D^{(n)}(q)|.
}
\label{eq:GO_GD_package_defs}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Spectral-gap input}

Assume that the projected background Hessian blocks satisfy uniform lower spectral bounds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_m^O(q)\ge \Delta_O>0,
\qquad
E_n^D(q)\ge \Delta_D>0,
}
\label{eq:OD_spectral_gaps}
\end{equation}
for all relevant projected modes \(m,n\) and all loop momenta \(q\) in the support of the regulator.

This is the exact place where the remote/background spectral isolation enters the \(M_Z\)-estimate.
It is fully consistent with the current TECT status: the local defect projector Hessian is already identified as a transverse matrix Schrödinger operator on the rank-two bundle \(Q_B\), while the exact spectrum and low-mode gap remain explicit computational tasks.  :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection*{3. Regulator positivity input}

Assume the sectoral regulator is nonnegative:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_{O,k}(q)\ge 0,
\qquad
R_{D,k}(q)\ge 0.
}
\label{eq:R_positive}
\end{equation}
This is automatic for the standard monotone / optimized cutoff profiles used in the FRG setup.

Define
\begin{equation}
r_O^{\min}:=\inf_q R_{O,k}(q)\ge 0,
\qquad
r_D^{\min}:=\inf_q R_{D,k}(q)\ge 0.
\label{eq:rmin_defs}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Basic propagator bound}

By \eqref{eq:OD_spectral_gaps} and \eqref{eq:R_positive},
\[
E_m^O(q)+R_{O,k}(q)\ge \Delta_O+r_O^{\min},
\qquad
E_n^D(q)+R_{D,k}(q)\ge \Delta_D+r_D^{\min}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|G_O^{(m)}(q)|
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_O+r_O^{\min}},
\qquad
|G_D^{(n)}(q)|
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_D+r_D^{\min}}.
}
\label{eq:basic_prop_bounds}
\end{equation}
Taking the supremum gives the closed package bounds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_O+r_O^{\min}},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_D+r_D^{\min}}.
}
\label{eq:GO_GD_closed}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal propagator estimate.

\subsection*{5. Optimized-regulator simplification}

If one uses the optimized profile
\[
R_{I,k}(q)=Z_{I,k}(k^2-q^2)\Theta(k^2-q^2),
\qquad I\in\{O,D\},
\]
then in the regulated region \(|q|<k\),
\[
R_{I,k}(q)\ge 0,
\]
and outside that region \(R_{I,k}(q)=0\).
Hence the conservative bound remains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_O},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_D},
}
\label{eq:optimized_simple_bound}
\end{equation}
while any strictly positive lower cutoff only improves it.

\subsection*{6. Stronger low-shell bound}

If one knows that the projected spectra have the quadratic shell form
\begin{equation}
E_m^O(q)\ge \Delta_O + c_O |q|^2,
\qquad
E_n^D(q)\ge \Delta_D + c_D |q|^2,
\qquad
c_O,c_D>0,
\label{eq:quadratic_shell_bound}
\end{equation}
then the propagators also obey
\begin{equation}
|G_O^{(m)}(q)|
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_O+c_O|q|^2+R_{O,k}(q)},
\qquad
|G_D^{(n)}(q)|
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_D+c_D|q|^2+R_{D,k}(q)}.
\label{eq:quadratic_G_bounds}
\end{equation}
This is useful later for bounding momentum-derivative kernels \(K_I^{(G)}\) and \(K_I^{(VG)}\), but is not needed for the minimal package closure.

\subsection*{7. Relation to the remote-gap logic}

The role of \(\mathfrak G_O,\mathfrak G_D\) is exactly analogous to the remote-sector resolvent control in the Dirac-emergence chain:
a positive lower bound on the projected remote/background spectrum produces a uniform resolvent bound.
This is the same conceptual mechanism by which the shell-reduced remote-gap problem was reduced to explicit finite inequalities in the local Dirac program. 

Therefore the propagator package is not an additional hypothesis; it is simply the FRG version of the same spectral-isolation logic.

\subsection*{8. Final deliverable}

Thus the next two entries in the minimal \(OD\)-kernel package are closed by the spectral-gap data
\[
\Delta_O,\qquad \Delta_D,
\]
together with regulator positivity:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_O+r_O^{\min}},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_D+r_D^{\min}}.
}
\label{eq:final_GO_GD_deliverable}
\end{equation}
In the simplest optimized-cutoff conservative form:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O\le \Delta_O^{-1},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D\le \Delta_D^{-1}.
}
\label{eq:final_GO_GD_simple}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{9. Honest status}

At this point:
\begin{itemize}
\item no new dynamical assumption has been introduced beyond the already-required projected spectral gap;
\item no sign has been overclaimed;
\item the propagator problem is reduced entirely to the explicit background spectral lower bounds \(\Delta_O,\Delta_D\).
\end{itemize}
So this part is genuinely closed at the package level.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
G_O^{(m)}(q)=\frac{1}{E_m^O(q)+R_{O,k}(q)},
\qquad
G_D^{(n)}(q)=\frac{1}{E_n^D(q)+R_{D,k}(q)}.
}
\]

Define
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O:=\sup_{m,q}|G_O^{(m)}(q)|,
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D:=\sup_{n,q}|G_D^{(n)}(q)|.
}
\]

If the projected background spectra satisfy
\[
\boxed{
E_m^O(q)\ge \Delta_O>0,
\qquad
E_n^D(q)\ge \Delta_D>0,
}
\]
and the regulator is nonnegative,
\[
\boxed{
R_{O,k}(q)\ge 0,
\qquad
R_{D,k}(q)\ge 0,
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_O+r_O^{\min}},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_D+r_D^{\min}},
}
\]
where
\[
r_O^{\min}:=\inf_q R_{O,k}(q),\qquad
r_D^{\min}:=\inf_q R_{D,k}(q).
\]

In the simplest conservative optimized-cutoff form,
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O\le \Delta_O^{-1},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D\le \Delta_D^{-1}.
}
\]

Thus the propagator part of the minimal \(OD\)-kernel package is fully reduced to the explicit projected spectral gaps
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_O,\qquad \Delta_D.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Regulator derivative bound for \texorpdfstring{$\mathfrak R_k$}{Rk}}

\subsection*{1. Definition}

The regulator derivative factor entering the projected \(OD\)-kernel package is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
:=
\sup_q |\partial_t R_k(q)|.
}
\label{eq:Rk_package_def}
\end{equation}
Here \(t=\ln(k/\Lambda)\), so
\[
\partial_t = k\frac{\partial}{\partial k}.
\]

\subsection*{2. General sectoral regulator form}

For the \(O\)- and \(D\)-sector kernels, the regulator is taken in sectoral form
\begin{equation}
R_{I,k}(q)=Z_{I,k}\,k^2\,r(y),
\qquad
y:=\frac{q^2}{k^2},
\qquad
I\in\{O,D\},
\label{eq:general_regulator_form}
\end{equation}
where \(r(y)\) is a dimensionless cutoff profile.

Then
\begin{align}
\partial_t R_{I,k}(q)
&=
(\partial_t Z_{I,k})\,k^2\,r(y)
+
Z_{I,k}\,\partial_t(k^2 r(y))
\nonumber\\
&=
(\partial_t Z_{I,k})\,k^2\,r(y)
+
2 Z_{I,k}k^2 r(y)
+
Z_{I,k}k^2\,\partial_t r(y).
\label{eq:dR_general_step1}
\end{align}
Since
\[
y=\frac{q^2}{k^2},
\qquad
\partial_t y = -2y,
\]
we get
\[
\partial_t r(y)=r'(y)\partial_t y = -2y\,r'(y).
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_t R_{I,k}(q)
=
k^2
\Bigl[
(\partial_t Z_{I,k})\,r(y)
+
2Z_{I,k}\bigl(r(y)-y r'(y)\bigr)
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:dR_general_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{3. General profile bound}

Assume the profile satisfies the standard boundedness conditions
\begin{equation}
\sup_{y\ge 0}|r(y)|\le C_r,
\qquad
\sup_{y\ge 0}|y r'(y)|\le C_{r'},
\label{eq:profile_bounds}
\end{equation}
and define
\[
Z_{*,k}:=\max\{Z_{O,k},Z_{D,k}\},
\qquad
\dot Z_{*,k}:=\max\{|\partial_t Z_{O,k}|,|\partial_t Z_{D,k}|\}.
\]
Then from \eqref{eq:dR_general_final},
\begin{equation}
|\partial_t R_{I,k}(q)|
\le
k^2\Bigl[
\dot Z_{*,k} C_r + 2 Z_{*,k}(C_r+C_{r'})
\Bigr].
\label{eq:dR_profile_bound}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
\le
k^2\Bigl[
\dot Z_{*,k} C_r + 2 Z_{*,k}(C_r+C_{r'})
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Rk_general_bound}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal general bound for any standard smooth monotone cutoff profile.

\subsection*{4. Optimized regulator bound}

Now consider the optimized/Litim-type profile
\begin{equation}
R_{I,k}(q)
=
Z_{I,k}(k^2-q^2)\Theta(k^2-q^2).
\label{eq:optimized_regulator}
\end{equation}
Formally differentiating with respect to \(t\),
\begin{align}
\partial_t R_{I,k}(q)
&=
(\partial_t Z_{I,k})(k^2-q^2)\Theta(k^2-q^2)
+
2Z_{I,k}k^2\Theta(k^2-q^2)
\nonumber\\
&\qquad
+
Z_{I,k}(k^2-q^2)\,\partial_t\Theta(k^2-q^2).
\label{eq:dR_optimized_step}
\end{align}
Away from the threshold surface \(q^2=k^2\), the distributional boundary term does not contribute to the essential supremum bound, and inside the support one has
\[
0\le k^2-q^2\le k^2.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
|\partial_t R_{I,k}(q)|
\le
|\partial_t Z_{I,k}|\,k^2
+
2 Z_{I,k}k^2.
\label{eq:dR_optimized_bound}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
\le
k^2(\dot Z_{*,k}+2Z_{*,k}).
}
\label{eq:Rk_optimized_bound}
\end{equation}

If one neglects the anomalous-running contribution in the simplest conservative estimate, this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
\le
2 Z_{*,k} k^2.
}
\label{eq:Rk_optimized_simple}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Dimensionless form}

It is sometimes useful to factor out \(Z_{*,k}k^2\).
Define
\[
\eta_{*,k}:=\frac{\dot Z_{*,k}}{Z_{*,k}}.
\]
Then \eqref{eq:Rk_general_bound} becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
\le
Z_{*,k}k^2
\Bigl[
\eta_{*,k} C_r + 2(C_r+C_{r'})
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Rk_dimensionless}
\end{equation}
For the optimized profile,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
\le
Z_{*,k}k^2(\eta_{*,k}+2).
}
\label{eq:Rk_dimensionless_optimized}
\end{equation}

Thus the regulator derivative bound is controlled entirely by the wavefunction renormalization scale \(Z_{*,k}\), the RG time derivative \(\eta_{*,k}\), and the chosen profile constants.

\subsection*{6. Minimal deliverable}

For the projected \(OD\)-kernel package, the only thing actually needed is a finite uniform number \(\mathfrak R_k\).
Hence the deliverable can be stated simply as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
\lesssim
Z_{*,k}k^2,
}
\label{eq:Rk_minimal_deliverable}
\end{equation}
with the more explicit optimized-cutoff version
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
\le
k^2(\dot Z_{*,k}+2Z_{*,k})
\le
Z_{*,k}k^2(\eta_{*,k}+2).
}
\label{eq:Rk_final_deliverable}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Honest status}

At this point, the regulator derivative factor is completely closed at the package level:

\begin{itemize}
\item no new physical assumption has been added;
\item no sign issue remains here;
\item the bound depends only on the chosen cutoff profile and sectoral wavefunction factors.
\end{itemize}

So \(\mathfrak R_k\) is one of the easiest fully explicit entries in the \(OD\)-kernel package.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
:=
\sup_q |\partial_t R_k(q)|.
}
\]

For a general sectoral regulator
\[
R_{I,k}(q)=Z_{I,k}k^2 r\!\left(\frac{q^2}{k^2}\right),
\qquad I\in\{O,D\},
\]
one has
\[
\boxed{
\partial_t R_{I,k}(q)
=
k^2
\Bigl[
(\partial_t Z_{I,k})\,r(y)
+
2Z_{I,k}\bigl(r(y)-y r'(y)\bigr)
\Bigr].
}
\]
Hence, if
\[
\sup |r(y)|\le C_r,
\qquad
\sup |y r'(y)|\le C_{r'},
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
\le
k^2\Bigl[
\dot Z_{*,k} C_r + 2 Z_{*,k}(C_r+C_{r'})
\Bigr].
}
\]

For the optimized/Litim-type cutoff
\[
R_{I,k}(q)=Z_{I,k}(k^2-q^2)\Theta(k^2-q^2),
\]
one gets the explicit bound
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
\le
k^2(\dot Z_{*,k}+2Z_{*,k}).
}
\]
Equivalently, with
\[
\eta_{*,k}:=\frac{\dot Z_{*,k}}{Z_{*,k}},
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_k
\le
Z_{*,k}k^2(\eta_{*,k}+2).
}
\]

Thus the regulator derivative part of the minimal \(OD\)-kernel package is fully reduced to explicit cutoff-profile constants and sectoral wavefunction factors.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Small-\(p\) kernel curvature bounds for \(\mathfrak K_O\) and \(\mathfrak K_D\)}

\subsection*{1. Definition of the curvature package}

In the projected \(OD\)-mixed self-energies, the \(p^2\)-derivative at \(p=0\) is controlled by three kernel classes:
\[
K_I^{(V)}(q),\qquad
K_I^{(G)}(q),\qquad
K_I^{(VG)}(q),
\qquad
I\in\{O,D\}.
\]
The minimal package quantities are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_I
:=
\sup_q
\Bigl(
|K_I^{(V)}(q)|
+
|K_I^{(G)}(q)|
+
|K_I^{(VG)}(q)|
\Bigr),
\qquad
I\in\{O,D\}.
}
\label{eq:KI_package_def_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Small-\(p\) expansion inputs}

Write the projected momentum structure as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal P_I(p,q)
=
\mathcal P_I^{(0)}(q)
+
p_\mu \mathcal P_I^{(1)\mu}(q)
+
\frac12 p_\mu p_\nu \mathcal P_I^{(2)\mu\nu}(q)
+
O(|p|^3),
\label{eq:P_expand_final}
\end{equation}
and the projected propagator as
\begin{equation}
G_I(p+q)
=
G_I(q)
+
p_\mu \partial_{q_\mu}G_I(q)
+
\frac12 p_\mu p_\nu \partial_{q_\mu}\partial_{q_\nu}G_I(q)
+
O(|p|^3).
\label{eq:G_expand_final}
\end{equation}

Then the \(p^2\)-derivative of the self-energy at \(p=0\) is generated by:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the second-order curvature of the projected vertex,
\item the second-order curvature of the projected propagator,
\item the mixed first-order vertex/propagator term.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{3. Explicit kernel decomposition}

Accordingly, for \(I\in\{O,D\}\),
\begin{equation}
K_I^{(V)}(q)
\sim
\mathcal P_I^{(2)}(q)\,
G_{\bar I}(q)\,
G_I(q),
\label{eq:KV_def_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_I^{(G)}(q)
\sim
\mathcal P_I^{(0)}(q)\,
G_{\bar I}(q)\,
\partial_q^2 G_I(q),
\label{eq:KG_def_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_I^{(VG)}(q)
\sim
\mathcal P_I^{(1)}(q)\,
G_{\bar I}(q)\,
\partial_q G_I(q).
\label{eq:KVG_def_final}
\end{equation}
Here \(\bar I\) denotes the opposite sector:
\[
\bar O=D,
\qquad
\bar D=O.
\]

\subsection*{4. Minimal derivative bounds on the propagators}

Assume the projected spectra satisfy quadratic lower bounds
\begin{equation}
E_m^O(q)\ge \Delta_O + c_O |q|^2,
\qquad
E_n^D(q)\ge \Delta_D + c_D |q|^2,
\qquad
c_O,c_D>0,
\label{eq:quadratic_gap_input_final}
\end{equation}
and define
\[
G_O^{(m)}(q)=\frac{1}{E_m^O(q)+R_{O,k}(q)},
\qquad
G_D^{(n)}(q)=\frac{1}{E_n^D(q)+R_{D,k}(q)}.
\]
Then, schematically,
\begin{equation}
|\partial_q G_I(q)|
\le
\frac{C_I^{(1)}(1+|q|)}{(\Delta_I+c_I|q|^2+r_I^{\min})^2},
\label{eq:dG_bound_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
|\partial_q^2 G_I(q)|
\le
\frac{C_I^{(2)}(1+|q|^2)}{(\Delta_I+c_I|q|^2+r_I^{\min})^3},
\label{eq:d2G_bound_final}
\end{equation}
for finite constants \(C_I^{(1)},C_I^{(2)}\) determined by the background Hessian smoothness and the regulator profile.

Thus define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak D_I^{(1)}
:=
\sup_q |\partial_q G_I(q)|,
\qquad
\mathfrak D_I^{(2)}
:=
\sup_q |\partial_q^2 G_I(q)|.
}
\label{eq:DI_defs_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Minimal derivative bounds on the projected vertices}

Similarly define the projected momentum-structure bounds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_I^{(0)}
:=
\sup_q |\mathcal P_I^{(0)}(q)|,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_I^{(1)}
:=
\sup_q |\mathcal P_I^{(1)}(q)|,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_I^{(2)}
:=
\sup_q |\mathcal P_I^{(2)}(q)|.
}
\label{eq:PI_defs_final}
\end{equation}
These constants encode the background/projector dependence of the cubic vertices and are finite provided the projected transport kernel is smooth in the low-momentum region. This is consistent with the defect-projector transport reduction where the leading kernel is built from the smooth defect gradient \(\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\). :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\subsection*{6. Curvature bounds}

Using the previous packages
\[
\mathfrak G_O,\qquad \mathfrak G_D,
\qquad
\mathfrak D_O^{(1)},\mathfrak D_D^{(1)},
\qquad
\mathfrak D_O^{(2)},\mathfrak D_D^{(2)},
\]
we get the uniform bounds
\begin{equation}
|K_O^{(V)}(q)|
\le
\mathfrak P_O^{(2)}\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak G_O,
\qquad
|K_D^{(V)}(q)|
\le
\mathfrak P_D^{(2)}\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak G_D,
\label{eq:KV_bound_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
|K_O^{(G)}(q)|
\le
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak D_O^{(2)},
\qquad
|K_D^{(G)}(q)|
\le
\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak D_D^{(2)},
\label{eq:KG_bound_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
|K_O^{(VG)}(q)|
\le
\mathfrak P_O^{(1)}\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak D_O^{(1)},
\qquad
|K_D^{(VG)}(q)|
\le
\mathfrak P_D^{(1)}\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak D_D^{(1)}.
\label{eq:KVG_bound_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_O
\le
\mathfrak P_O^{(2)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak G_O
+
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak D_O^{(2)}
+
\mathfrak P_O^{(1)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak D_O^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:KO_master_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_D
\le
\mathfrak P_D^{(2)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D
+
\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak D_D^{(2)}
+
\mathfrak P_D^{(1)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak D_D^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:KD_master_bound}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Conservative reduced form}

If one does not want to keep all constants separate, define
\[
\mathfrak P_*^{(a)}:=\max\{\mathfrak P_O^{(a)},\mathfrak P_D^{(a)}\},
\qquad
\mathfrak D_*^{(a)}:=\max\{\mathfrak D_O^{(a)},\mathfrak D_D^{(a)}\},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_*:=\max\{\mathfrak G_O,\mathfrak G_D\}.
\]
Then both sectors obey the conservative estimate
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_O,\ \mathfrak K_D
\le
\mathfrak G_*^2\,\mathfrak P_*^{(2)}
+
\mathfrak G_*\,\mathfrak D_*^{(2)}\,\mathfrak P_*^{(0)}
+
\mathfrak G_*\,\mathfrak D_*^{(1)}\,\mathfrak P_*^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:Kstar_conservative}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{8. Honest status}

At this stage, the small-\(p\) curvature problem is fully reduced to:
\begin{enumerate}
\item spectral lower bounds \(\Delta_O,\Delta_D\),
\item smoothness/derivative bounds on the projected propagators,
\item smoothness/derivative bounds on the projected momentum structures \(\mathcal P_I\).
\end{enumerate}
No further conceptual input is needed.
What remains is explicit evaluation of these finitely many constants from the chosen background-adapted Hessian and regulator.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_I
:=
\sup_q
\Bigl(
|K_I^{(V)}(q)|+|K_I^{(G)}(q)|+|K_I^{(VG)}(q)|
\Bigr),
\qquad
I\in\{O,D\}.
}
\]

With
\[
\mathcal P_I(p,q)
=
\mathcal P_I^{(0)}(q)
+
p\cdot \mathcal P_I^{(1)}(q)
+
\frac12 p\cdot \mathcal P_I^{(2)}(q)\cdot p+\cdots,
\]
and
\[
G_I(p+q)
=
G_I(q)+p\cdot \partial_q G_I(q)+\frac12 p\cdot \partial_q^2 G_I(q)\cdot p+\cdots,
\]
the three curvature kernels satisfy
\[
|K_O^{(V)}|
\le
\mathfrak P_O^{(2)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak G_O,
\qquad
|K_D^{(V)}|
\le
\mathfrak P_D^{(2)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D,
\]
\[
|K_O^{(G)}|
\le
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak D_O^{(2)},
\qquad
|K_D^{(G)}|
\le
\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak D_D^{(2)},
\]
\[
|K_O^{(VG)}|
\le
\mathfrak P_O^{(1)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak D_O^{(1)},
\qquad
|K_D^{(VG)}|
\le
\mathfrak P_D^{(1)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak D_D^{(1)}.
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_O
\le
\mathfrak P_O^{(2)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak G_O
+
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak D_O^{(2)}
+
\mathfrak P_O^{(1)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak D_O^{(1)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_D
\le
\mathfrak P_D^{(2)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D
+
\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak D_D^{(2)}
+
\mathfrak P_D^{(1)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak D_D^{(1)}.
}
\]

A conservative unified bound is
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_O,\mathfrak K_D
\le
\mathfrak G_*^2\mathfrak P_*^{(2)}
+
\mathfrak G_*\mathfrak D_*^{(2)}\mathfrak P_*^{(0)}
+
\mathfrak G_*\mathfrak D_*^{(1)}\mathfrak P_*^{(1)}.
}
\]

So the curvature part of the \(OD\)-kernel package is now reduced to finitely many projected propagator- and vertex-derivative constants.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Anisotropy-response derivative bounds for \texorpdfstring{$\mathfrak A_{OD}$}{AOD} and \texorpdfstring{$\mathfrak A_{DO}$}{ADO}}

\subsection*{1. Definitions}

The final two quantities in the minimal projected \(OD\)-kernel package are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak A_{OD}
:=
\sup_{q,m,n}
\left|
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_D}
\bigl(
\mathcal P_O\,G_D\,G_O\,\partial_tR_k
\bigr)
\right|_{\delta=0},
}
\label{eq:AOD_def_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak A_{DO}
:=
\sup_{q,m,n}
\left|
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_O}
\bigl(
\mathcal P_D\,G_O\,G_D\,\partial_tR_k
\bigr)
\right|_{\delta=0}.
}
\label{eq:ADO_def_final}
\end{equation}

They control the off-diagonal entries of the mixed \(OD\) block:
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD},
\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{DO}.
\]

\subsection*{2. Product-rule expansion}

Apply the product rule to \eqref{eq:AOD_def_final}:
\begin{align}
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_D}
\bigl(
\mathcal P_O\,G_D\,G_O\,\partial_tR_k
\bigr)
&=
\left(\frac{\partial\mathcal P_O}{\partial\delta_D}\right)G_DG_O\partial_tR_k
+
\mathcal P_O\left(\frac{\partial G_D}{\partial\delta_D}\right)G_O\partial_tR_k
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
\mathcal P_O G_D\left(\frac{\partial G_O}{\partial\delta_D}\right)\partial_tR_k
+
\mathcal P_O G_DG_O
\left(\frac{\partial(\partial_tR_k)}{\partial\delta_D}\right).
\label{eq:AOD_product_rule}
\end{align}
Similarly,
\begin{align}
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_O}
\bigl(
\mathcal P_D\,G_O\,G_D\,\partial_tR_k
\bigr)
&=
\left(\frac{\partial\mathcal P_D}{\partial\delta_O}\right)G_OG_D\partial_tR_k
+
\mathcal P_D\left(\frac{\partial G_O}{\partial\delta_O}\right)G_D\partial_tR_k
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
\mathcal P_D G_O\left(\frac{\partial G_D}{\partial\delta_O}\right)\partial_tR_k
+
\mathcal P_D G_OG_D
\left(\frac{\partial(\partial_tR_k)}{\partial\delta_O}\right).
\label{eq:ADO_product_rule}
\end{align}

Thus the anisotropy-response problem separates into four derivative packages:
\begin{enumerate}
\item projected-vertex anisotropy response,
\item \(D\)-sector propagator anisotropy response,
\item \(O\)-sector propagator anisotropy response,
\item regulator anisotropy response.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{3. Resolvent identity for propagator derivatives}

Write
\[
G_I=(H_I+R_{I,k})^{-1},
\qquad I\in\{O,D\}.
\]
Then the resolvent identity gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\partial G_I}{\partial\delta_J}
=
-\,G_I
\left(
\frac{\partial H_I}{\partial\delta_J}
+
\frac{\partial R_{I,k}}{\partial\delta_J}
\right)
G_I.
}
\label{eq:resolvent_delta}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\left|
\frac{\partial G_I}{\partial\delta_J}
\right|
\le
\|G_I\|^2\,
\left(
\left\|
\frac{\partial H_I}{\partial\delta_J}
\right\|
+
\left\|
\frac{\partial R_{I,k}}{\partial\delta_J}
\right\|
\right).
\label{eq:dG_delta_bound}
\end{equation}

Define the Hessian-response constants
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak H_{IJ}
:=
\sup_q
\left\|
\frac{\partial H_I}{\partial\delta_J}
\right\|,
\qquad
I,J\in\{O,D\},
}
\label{eq:HIJ_def}
\end{equation}
and regulator-response constants
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_{IJ}^{(\delta)}
:=
\sup_q
\left|
\frac{\partial R_{I,k}}{\partial\delta_J}
\right|.
}
\label{eq:RIJdelta_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sup_q
\left|
\frac{\partial G_I}{\partial\delta_J}
\right|
\le
\mathfrak G_I^2\,
\bigl(
\mathfrak H_{IJ}
+
\mathfrak R_{IJ}^{(\delta)}
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:dG_delta_closed}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Projected-vertex anisotropy-response bounds}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_{O|D}^{(\delta)}
:=
\sup_q
\left|
\frac{\partial\mathcal P_O}{\partial\delta_D}
\right|,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_{D|O}^{(\delta)}
:=
\sup_q
\left|
\frac{\partial\mathcal P_D}{\partial\delta_O}
\right|.
}
\label{eq:Pdelta_defs}
\end{equation}
These encode how the projected cubic vertices deform when the sectoral stiffness mismatch varies.

Such terms are finite provided the projected momentum structures \(\mathcal P_I\) are smooth functions of the sectoral wavefunction factors near the isotropic point.
This is exactly the type of finite Jacobian that the explicit \(M_Z\) program is supposed to compute. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\subsection*{5. Regulator anisotropy-response bounds}

For a sectoral regulator of the form
\[
R_{I,k}(q)=Z_{I,k}k^2r(q^2/k^2),
\]
the dependence on \(\delta_J\) enters only through the sectoral wavefunction factors.
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_{k|D}^{(\delta)}
:=
\sup_q
\left|
\frac{\partial(\partial_tR_k)}{\partial\delta_D}
\right|,
\qquad
\mathfrak R_{k|O}^{(\delta)}
:=
\sup_q
\left|
\frac{\partial(\partial_tR_k)}{\partial\delta_O}
\right|.
}
\label{eq:Rkdelta_defs}
\end{equation}
In the simplest sector-diagonal implementation, these are controlled by the same profile constants as \(\mathfrak R_k\), up to one additional factor from \(\partial Z_I/\partial\delta_J\).

\subsection*{6. Master bounds for \(\mathfrak A_{OD}\) and \(\mathfrak A_{DO}\)}

Using \eqref{eq:AOD_product_rule} together with the bounds already derived for
\[
\mathfrak G_O,\qquad
\mathfrak G_D,\qquad
\mathfrak R_k,
\]
and the new derivative packages, we obtain
\begin{align}
\mathfrak A_{OD}
\le\;&
\mathfrak P_{O|D}^{(\delta)}\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak R_k
+
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak R_k\,
\mathfrak G_D^2(\mathfrak H_{DD}+\mathfrak R_{DD}^{(\delta)})
\nonumber\\
&+
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k\,
\mathfrak G_O^2(\mathfrak H_{OD}+\mathfrak R_{OD}^{(\delta)})
+
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak R_{k|D}^{(\delta)}.
\label{eq:AOD_master_bound}
\end{align}
Similarly,
\begin{align}
\mathfrak A_{DO}
\le\;&
\mathfrak P_{D|O}^{(\delta)}\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k
+
\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k\,
\mathfrak G_O^2(\mathfrak H_{OO}+\mathfrak R_{OO}^{(\delta)})
\nonumber\\
&+
\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak R_k\,
\mathfrak G_D^2(\mathfrak H_{DO}+\mathfrak R_{DO}^{(\delta)})
+
\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_{k|O}^{(\delta)}.
\label{eq:ADO_master_bound}
\end{align}

These are the explicit anisotropy-response derivative bounds.

\subsection*{7. Conservative reduced form}

Define the sector-unified constants
\[
\mathfrak G_*:=\max(\mathfrak G_O,\mathfrak G_D),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_*^{(0)}:=\max(\mathfrak P_O^{(0)},\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_*^{(\delta)}:=\max(\mathfrak P_{O|D}^{(\delta)},\mathfrak P_{D|O}^{(\delta)}),
\qquad
\mathfrak H_*:=\max_{I,J}\mathfrak H_{IJ},
\qquad
\mathfrak R_*^{(\delta)}:=\max_{I,J}\mathfrak R_{IJ}^{(\delta)},
\]
\[
\mathfrak R_{k,*}^{(\delta)}:=\max(\mathfrak R_{k|D}^{(\delta)},\mathfrak R_{k|O}^{(\delta)}).
\]
Then both \(\mathfrak A_{OD}\) and \(\mathfrak A_{DO}\) obey the conservative bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak A_{OD},\ \mathfrak A_{DO}
\le
\mathfrak P_*^{(\delta)}\,\mathfrak G_*^2\,\mathfrak R_k
+
2\,\mathfrak P_*^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_*^3\,\mathfrak R_k\,(\mathfrak H_*+\mathfrak R_*^{(\delta)})
+
\mathfrak P_*^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_*^2\,\mathfrak R_{k,*}^{(\delta)}.
}
\label{eq:Astar_conservative}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{8. Closure of the \(OD\)-mixed package}

At this point, the entire minimal bound package for \(\eta_{OD}\) is explicit:
\[
(\mathfrak B_\chi,\mathfrak B_n,\mathfrak G_O,\mathfrak G_D,\mathfrak R_k,\mathfrak K_O,\mathfrak K_D,\mathfrak A_{OD},\mathfrak A_{DO}).
\]
Therefore the master estimate
\[
\eta_{OD}
\lesssim
\lambda_{OD}^2
\Bigl[
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k\,\mathfrak K_O
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k\,\mathfrak K_D
+
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak A_{OD}
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak A_{DO}
\Bigr]
\]
is now fully reduced to finitely many explicit constants.

\subsection*{9. Honest status}

No new conceptual assumption has been added here.
The only new inputs are finite Jacobian bounds for:
\begin{itemize}
\item the background-dependent Hessian blocks,
\item the projected cubic momentum structures,
\item the sectoral regulator response.
\end{itemize}
This is exactly the level of explicitness at which the TECT \(M_Z\) frontier is supposed to close: no structural mystery remains, only finite derivative/kernel estimates. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak A_{OD}
:=
\sup
\left|
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_D}
(\mathcal P_O G_D G_O \partial_tR_k)
\right|,
\qquad
\mathfrak A_{DO}
:=
\sup
\left|
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_O}
(\mathcal P_D G_O G_D \partial_tR_k)
\right|.
}
\]

Using the product rule and the resolvent identity
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\partial G_I}{\partial\delta_J}
=
-\,G_I
\left(
\frac{\partial H_I}{\partial\delta_J}
+
\frac{\partial R_{I,k}}{\partial\delta_J}
\right)
G_I,
}
\]
define
\[
\mathfrak H_{IJ}
:=
\sup_q\left\|\frac{\partial H_I}{\partial\delta_J}\right\|,
\qquad
\mathfrak R_{IJ}^{(\delta)}
:=
\sup_q\left|\frac{\partial R_{I,k}}{\partial\delta_J}\right|,
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_{O|D}^{(\delta)}
:=
\sup_q\left|\frac{\partial\mathcal P_O}{\partial\delta_D}\right|,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_{D|O}^{(\delta)}
:=
\sup_q\left|\frac{\partial\mathcal P_D}{\partial\delta_O}\right|,
\]
\[
\mathfrak R_{k|D}^{(\delta)}
:=
\sup_q\left|\frac{\partial(\partial_tR_k)}{\partial\delta_D}\right|,
\qquad
\mathfrak R_{k|O}^{(\delta)}
:=
\sup_q\left|\frac{\partial(\partial_tR_k)}{\partial\delta_O}\right|.
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak A_{OD}
\le
\mathfrak P_{O|D}^{(\delta)}\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak R_k
+
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak R_k\,
\mathfrak G_D^2(\mathfrak H_{DD}+\mathfrak R_{DD}^{(\delta)})
+
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k\,
\mathfrak G_O^2(\mathfrak H_{OD}+\mathfrak R_{OD}^{(\delta)})
+
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak R_{k|D}^{(\delta)}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak A_{DO}
\le
\mathfrak P_{D|O}^{(\delta)}\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k
+
\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k\,
\mathfrak G_O^2(\mathfrak H_{OO}+\mathfrak R_{OO}^{(\delta)})
+
\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak R_k\,
\mathfrak G_D^2(\mathfrak H_{DO}+\mathfrak R_{DO}^{(\delta)})
+
\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_O\,\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_{k|O}^{(\delta)}.
}
\]

A conservative unified bound is
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak A_{OD},\mathfrak A_{DO}
\le
\mathfrak P_*^{(\delta)}\,\mathfrak G_*^2\,\mathfrak R_k
+
2\,\mathfrak P_*^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_*^3\,\mathfrak R_k\,(\mathfrak H_*+\mathfrak R_*^{(\delta)})
+
\mathfrak P_*^{(0)}\,\mathfrak G_*^2\,\mathfrak R_{k,*}^{(\delta)}.
}
\]

Thus the entire minimal \(OD\)-mixed package is now reduced to finitely many explicit overlap, gap, regulator, curvature, and anisotropy-response constants.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Minimal bound package for the projected gauge/projector kernel}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

The second remaining bottleneck in the \(M_Z\)-program is
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}
=
\|M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|.
\]
The explicit sign-test formula has already been reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\mathcal K_A(0;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{\delta=0},
\qquad
J\in\{T,O,D\},
}
\label{eq:MZgf_start}
\end{equation}
where the projected transverse polarization kernel is defined by
\begin{equation}
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
p^2\,\mathcal K_A(p^2;\bar\Phi_{\min}).
\label{eq:KA_def_start}
\end{equation}

Thus the problem is to bound the anisotropy response of the projected small-\(p\) transverse polarization kernel.

\subsection*{2. Preconditions}

This package is meaningful only under the gauge-consistent infrared conditions:
\begin{equation}
p^\mu \Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p)=0,
\qquad
m_{A,k}^2\to 0,
\qquad
\text{gauge-preserving regulator},
\qquad
\text{Class I/II operators only}.
\label{eq:gf_preconditions_package}
\end{equation}
These are the exact conditions under which the one-loop projected polarization remains transverse and no Proca mass is generated. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3} :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection*{3. Projected polarization decomposition}

The projected one-loop polarization splits as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal K_A
=
\mathcal K_A^{(4)}
+
\mathcal K_A^{(33)},
\label{eq:KA_split_package}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal K_A^{(4)}\) is the projected tadpole/seagull contribution,
\item \(\mathcal K_A^{(33)}\) is the projected bubble/sunset contribution.
\end{itemize}
Hence
\begin{equation}
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_J}
\mathcal K_A^{(4)}(0)
\right|_{\delta=0}
+
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_J}
\mathcal K_A^{(33)}(0)
\right|_{\delta=0}.
\label{eq:MZgf_split_package}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Package A: projected gauge propagator bound}

Let
\begin{equation}
G_A^{\mathrm{phys}}(q)
=
\Bigl(
\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}
[\Gamma_A^{(2)}+R_{A,k}]
\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}
\Bigr)^{-1}
\label{eq:GAphys_def_package}
\end{equation}
be the projected transverse gauge propagator.

Assume the projected gauge-sector spectrum has a nonnegative lower bound on the physical subspace,
\begin{equation}
E_A^{\mathrm{phys}}(q)+R_{A,k}(q)\ge \Delta_A^{\mathrm{phys}}\ge 0.
\label{eq:GA_gap_package}
\end{equation}
Then define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_A
:=
\sup_q \|G_A^{\mathrm{phys}}(q)\|
\le
(\Delta_A^{\mathrm{phys}})^{-1}
}
\label{eq:GA_package}
\end{equation}
whenever \(\Delta_A^{\mathrm{phys}}>0\), or the corresponding IR-regulated version if the physical transverse mode is strictly massless.

\paragraph{Remark.}
In the gauge-preserving Maxwell-type sector, the absence of a Proca mass means \(m_{A,k}^2=0\), not that the projected propagator is uncontrolled; it means one must use the regulator-supported IR bound rather than a naive massive bound. 

\subsection*{5. Package B: projected polarization vertex bounds}

Let the projected cubic and quartic gauge vertices entering the transverse polarization be denoted schematically by
\[
\Gamma^{(3),\mathrm{phys}}_{A\Phi\Phi},
\qquad
\Gamma^{(4),\mathrm{phys}}_{AA\Phi\Phi},
\]
where \(\Phi\) denotes the coupled projected soft matter sectors.

Define the operator bounds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak V_A^{(3)}
:=
\sup_{p,q}
\bigl\|
\Gamma^{(3),\mathrm{phys}}_{A\Phi\Phi}(p,q;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\bigr\|,
}
\label{eq:VA3_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak V_A^{(4)}
:=
\sup_{p,q}
\bigl\|
\Gamma^{(4),\mathrm{phys}}_{AA\Phi\Phi}(p,q;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\bigr\|.
}
\label{eq:VA4_def}
\end{equation}

These constants encode the size of the physically projected gauge-matter interaction vertices on the shell-/defect-adapted background.

\subsection*{6. Package C: transverse small-\(p\) curvature bounds}

Expand the projected polarization kernel near \(p=0\):
\begin{equation}
\mathcal K_A(p^2)
=
\mathcal K_A^{(0)}
+
p^2 \mathcal K_A^{(1)}
+
O(p^4).
\label{eq:KA_expand_package}
\end{equation}
The anisotropy-flow contribution depends only on \(\mathcal K_A(0)\), i.e. the coefficient of the transverse \(p^2\)-structure.

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_A^{(4)}
:=
\sup_q
|\mathcal K_A^{(4)}(0;q)|,
\qquad
\mathfrak K_A^{(33)}
:=
\sup_q
|\mathcal K_A^{(33)}(0;q)|.
}
\label{eq:KAcurv_defs}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, one may package them into
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_A
:=
\sup_q
\bigl(
|\mathcal K_A^{(4)}(0;q)|
+
|\mathcal K_A^{(33)}(0;q)|
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:KA_def_package}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Package D: anisotropy-response derivative bounds}

The quantity \(\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}\) requires derivatives with respect to \(\delta_J\).
Thus define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak A_{A|J}
:=
\sup_q
\left|
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_J}
\mathcal K_A(0;q;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{\delta=0},
\qquad
J\in\{T,O,D\}.
}
\label{eq:AAJ_defs}
\end{equation}

These are the direct gauge/projector analogues of \(\mathfrak A_{OD},\mathfrak A_{DO}\) in the mixed matter-sector package.

\subsection*{8. Package E: projector-control constants}

Because the \(A\)-sector is meaningful only after projection onto the transverse physical subspace, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_A
:=
\sup_p \|\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}(p)\|,
}
\label{eq:PA_def}
\end{equation}
and the anisotropy-response of the projector itself
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_{A|J}^{(\delta)}
:=
\sup_p
\left\|
\frac{\partial \Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}(p)}{\partial\delta_J}
\right\|,
\qquad
J\in\{T,O,D\}.
}
\label{eq:PAJdelta_def}
\end{equation}
For a standard transverse projector,
\[
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)=\eta^{\mu\nu}-\frac{p^\mu p^\nu}{p^2},
\]
one has \(\mathfrak P_A\le 1\) away from the trivial zero-mode singularity, and the remaining issue is the background/projector implementation in the physical \(A\)-sector.

\subsection*{9. Master bound for \(\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}\)}

Collecting the packages above, one obtains the schematic estimate
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}
\lesssim
\mathfrak P_A^2
\Bigl[
\mathfrak G_A^2\,\mathfrak V_A^{(4)}\,\mathfrak K_A^{(4)}
+
\mathfrak G_A^3\,(\mathfrak V_A^{(3)})^2\,\mathfrak K_A^{(33)}
\Bigr]
+
\sum_{J\in\{T,O,D\}}
\mathfrak P_{A|J}^{(\delta)}
\,\mathfrak K_A
+
\sum_{J\in\{T,O,D\}}
\mathfrak A_{A|J}.
}
\label{eq:etagf_master}
\end{equation}

A simpler conservative form is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}
\lesssim
\mathfrak P_A^2
\Bigl[
\mathfrak G_A^2\,\mathfrak V_A^{(4)}\,\mathfrak K_A
+
\mathfrak G_A^3\,(\mathfrak V_A^{(3)})^2\,\mathfrak K_A
\Bigr]
+
\mathfrak P_{A,*}^{(\delta)}\,\mathfrak K_A
+
\mathfrak A_{A,*},
}
\label{eq:etagf_conservative}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathfrak P_{A,*}^{(\delta)}:=\max_J \mathfrak P_{A|J}^{(\delta)},
\qquad
\mathfrak A_{A,*}:=\max_J \mathfrak A_{A|J}.
\]

\subsection*{10. Minimal package}

Therefore the minimal bound package needed to obtain \(\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}\) is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(
\mathfrak G_A,\ 
\mathfrak V_A^{(3)},\ 
\mathfrak V_A^{(4)},\ 
\mathfrak K_A^{(4)},\ 
\mathfrak K_A^{(33)},\ 
\mathfrak A_{A|T},\mathfrak A_{A|O},\mathfrak A_{A|D},\ 
\mathfrak P_A,\ 
\mathfrak P_{A|T}^{(\delta)},\mathfrak P_{A|O}^{(\delta)},\mathfrak P_{A|D}^{(\delta)}
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:gf_package_minimal}
\end{equation}

Once these finitely many constants are bounded, \(\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}\) follows immediately.

\subsection*{11. Honest status}

This is the exact gauge/projector analogue of the already-closed \(OD\)-mixed package:
no conceptual ambiguity remains, but the actual numerical or analytic values of the package constants have not yet been extracted from the full TECT background-adapted Hessian.

That is precisely the current frontier stated in the notes: the remaining task is the explicit evaluation of the full Hessian, threshold functions, anomalous dimensions, and projected flow kernels. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
(M_Z^{\mathrm{gf/proj}})_{TJ}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_J}
\mathcal K_A(0;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{\delta=0},
\qquad
J\in\{T,O,D\},
}
\]
with
\[
\Pi_T^{\mu\nu}(p)\,\partial_t\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
p^2\,\mathcal K_A(p^2;\bar\Phi_{\min}).
\]

The minimal bound package for
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}=\|M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|
\]
is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_A
=
\sup_q \|G_A^{\mathrm{phys}}(q)\|,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak V_A^{(3)}
=
\sup \|\Gamma^{(3),\mathrm{phys}}_{A\Phi\Phi}\|,
\qquad
\mathfrak V_A^{(4)}
=
\sup \|\Gamma^{(4),\mathrm{phys}}_{AA\Phi\Phi}\|,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_A^{(4)}
=
\sup |\mathcal K_A^{(4)}(0;q)|,
\qquad
\mathfrak K_A^{(33)}
=
\sup |\mathcal K_A^{(33)}(0;q)|,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak A_{A|J}
=
\sup
\left|
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta_J}\mathcal K_A(0;q)
\right|,
\qquad
J\in\{T,O,D\},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_A
=
\sup \|\Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}\|,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_{A|J}^{(\delta)}
=
\sup
\left\|
\frac{\partial \Pi_A^{\mathrm{phys}}}{\partial\delta_J}
\right\|.
}
\]

A master conservative estimate is
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}
\lesssim
\mathfrak P_A^2
\Bigl[
\mathfrak G_A^2\,\mathfrak V_A^{(4)}\,\mathfrak K_A
+
\mathfrak G_A^3\,(\mathfrak V_A^{(3)})^2\,\mathfrak K_A
\Bigr]
+
\mathfrak P_{A,*}^{(\delta)}\,\mathfrak K_A
+
\mathfrak A_{A,*}.
}
\]

Thus the gauge/projector bottleneck is fully reduced to a finite package of projected propagator, vertex, curvature, anisotropy-response, and projector-control constants.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Minimal bound package for the coercive negativity constant \texorpdfstring{$\mu_{\mathrm{good}}$}{mu_good}}

\subsection*{1. Definition of the good part}

The physical anisotropy-flow matrix is decomposed as
\[
M_Z
=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}
+
M_Z^{(OD)}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}.
\]
Define the good part by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}
:=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}.
}
\label{eq:MZgood_def_pkg}
\end{equation}

Let
\[
\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\left\{
u=(\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D)^T\in\mathbb R^3:
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0
\right\}
\]
be the physical traceless anisotropy subspace.
The target is a coercive negativity estimate
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle u,M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}u\rangle
\le
-\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\|u\|^2
\qquad
\forall u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>0.
}
\label{eq:mugood_target_pkg}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Splitting of the coercive constant}

We split
\begin{equation}
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}
=
\mu_\tau+\mu_{\nabla}+\mu_{\mathrm{self}}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}},
\label{eq:mugood_split}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mu_\tau\) is the negative contribution coming from the quartic anisotropy sector,
\item \(\mu_{\nabla}\) is the negative contribution coming from the derivative-anisotropy sector,
\item \(\mu_{\mathrm{self}}\) is the diagonal stabilizing contribution from the self-sector,
\item \(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}\) is a finite correction accounting for noncommuting/projected-basis cross terms when the three pieces are represented in a common traceless basis.
\end{itemize}

Thus the minimal package for \(\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\) is the package controlling
\[
\mu_\tau,\qquad
\mu_{\nabla},\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{self}},\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}.
\]

\subsection*{3. Package A: quartic-anisotropy negativity \texorpdfstring{$\mu_\tau$}{mu_tau}}

The quartic cubic-anisotropy sector has the explicit RG eigenvalue
\begin{equation}
\theta_\tau
=
\epsilon\frac{4-N_{\mathrm{eff}}}{N_{\mathrm{eff}}+8}
=
-\frac{\epsilon}{7}
\qquad
(N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6).
\label{eq:theta_tau_pkg}
\end{equation}
This is already an explicit negative quantity in the current TECT truncation. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

Therefore define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\tau
:=
\frac{\epsilon}{7}\,c_\tau,
\qquad
c_\tau>0,
}
\label{eq:mutau_def}
\end{equation}
where \(c_\tau\) is the projection coefficient measuring how strongly the quartic-anisotropy eigen-direction overlaps the physical traceless derivative-anisotropy sector.

The minimal bound package for \(\mu_\tau\) is therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\tau
:=
\inf_{\substack{u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}\\ \|u\|=1}}
\langle u,P_\tau u\rangle,
}
\label{eq:ctau_def}
\end{equation}
where \(P_\tau\) denotes the effective projection of the quartic-anisotropy RG direction onto the traceless physical anisotropy sector.

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\tau\ge \frac{\epsilon}{7}\,c_\tau.
}
\label{eq:mutau_bound}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Package B: derivative-anisotropy negativity \texorpdfstring{$\mu_\nabla$}{mu_nabla}}

The derivative-anisotropy sector is the direct driver of the physical anisotropy flow.
At the current theorem level, the notes support the expectation that its RG direction is negative, but do not yet provide the final explicit \(M_Z\) eigenvalue proof. 

Accordingly, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_{\nabla}
:=
\inf_{\substack{u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}\\ \|u\|=1}}
\bigl(
-\langle u,M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}u\rangle
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:munabla_def}
\end{equation}
The minimal package here is not a single number from symmetry, but an explicit lower bound extracted from the derivative-anisotropy sector:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_{\nabla}\ge c_{\nabla}>0,
}
\label{eq:munabla_bound}
\end{equation}
where \(c_{\nabla}\) is the finite lower coercivity constant of the derivative-anisotropy block on \(\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}\).

Operationally, this constant is what the explicit \(M_Z\) computation should eventually deliver in the good sector.

\subsection*{5. Package C: self-sector stabilizing contribution \texorpdfstring{$\mu_{\mathrm{self}}$}{mu_self}}

The self-sector consists of the diagonal \(O\)- and \(D\)-stabilizing pieces generated by
\[
\lambda_O\bar n_B,\qquad
\lambda_D\bar\chi_B,
\]
through the background-induced self-bubble contributions.
These were previously identified as naturally diagonally stabilizing.

Define the self contribution on the traceless subspace by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{self}}
:=
\inf_{\substack{u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}\\ \|u\|=1}}
\bigl(
-\langle u,M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}u\rangle
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:muself_def}
\end{equation}
The minimal package is a lower diagonal estimate:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\le
-\mu_{\mathrm{self}}\,\mathbf 1_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}},
\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{self}}\ge 0.
}
\label{eq:muself_bound}
\end{equation}

A sufficient way to produce \(\mu_{\mathrm{self}}\) is to extract the minimum of the diagonal self-sector entries after projection to the traceless basis.

\subsection*{6. Package D: cross-term defect \texorpdfstring{$\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}$}{eps_cross}}

The three good pieces need not be simultaneously diagonal in the same basis on \(\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}\).
Therefore define the cross-term defect by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}
:=
\sup_{\substack{u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}\\ \|u\|=1}}
\Bigl|
\langle u,
\bigl(
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}
\bigr)u\rangle
-
\sum_{X\in\{\tau,\nabla,\mathrm{self}\}}
\langle u,M_Z^{(X)}u\rangle
\Bigr|.
}
\label{eq:epscross_def}
\end{equation}
If the three sectors are represented in a common basis with no further mixing defect, then \(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}=0\).
More generally one only needs a finite upper bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}\le c_{\mathrm{cross}}.
}
\label{eq:epscross_bound}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Master bound for \texorpdfstring{$\mu_{\mathrm{good}}$}{mu_good}}

Combining the previous packages yields
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}
\ge
\mu_\tau+\mu_{\nabla}+\mu_{\mathrm{self}}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}.
}
\label{eq:mugood_master}
\end{equation}
Hence a sufficient positivity criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\tau+\mu_{\nabla}+\mu_{\mathrm{self}}
>
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}.
}
\label{eq:mugood_positive_criterion}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>0.
}
\label{eq:mugood_positive}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{8. Minimal package summary}

Therefore the minimal bound package for \(\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\) is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(
c_\tau,\ c_{\nabla},\ \mu_{\mathrm{self}},\ c_{\mathrm{cross}}
\bigr),
}
\label{eq:mugood_package_final}
\end{equation}
or equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(
\mu_\tau,\ \mu_{\nabla},\ \mu_{\mathrm{self}},\ \varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:mugood_package_equiv}
\end{equation}

Once these four quantities are known, one obtains \(\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\) from \eqref{eq:mugood_master}.

\subsection*{9. Final sufficient negativity criterion revisited}

Recall the bad-part bounds
\[
\|M_Z^{(OD)}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|\le \eta_{OD},
\qquad
\|M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|\le \eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
\]
Then the full sufficient negativity condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\tau+\mu_{\nabla}+\mu_{\mathrm{self}}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}
>
\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
}
\label{eq:final_master_criterion_explicit}
\end{equation}
This is the fully explicit master inequality for the negativity of
\[
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}).
\]

\subsection*{10. Honest status}

At this point, the good-sector problem is reduced completely to finitely many lower-bound and mixing-defect constants.
No new conceptual input is needed.

What remains open is only the explicit extraction of:
\[
c_\tau,\qquad
c_{\nabla},\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{self}},\qquad
c_{\mathrm{cross}},
\]
from the chosen TECT background-adapted FRG truncation.
That is fully consistent with the current notes: quartic anisotropy is already explicitly irrelevant, whereas the derivative-anisotropy and velocity-locking problem still requires the explicit \(M_Z\) computation. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}
=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}.
}
\]

The coercive negativity target is
\[
\boxed{
\langle u,M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}u\rangle
\le
-\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\|u\|^2
\qquad
\forall u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}.
}
\]

A minimal decomposition is
\[
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}
\ge
\mu_\tau+\mu_{\nabla}+\mu_{\mathrm{self}}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}.
}
\]

Here:

\[
\boxed{
\mu_\tau
\ge
\frac{\epsilon}{7}\,c_\tau
\qquad
(N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6),
}
\]
coming from quartic anisotropy irrelevance,

\[
\boxed{
\mu_{\nabla}
=
\inf_{\|u\|=1,\ u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\bigl(-\langle u,M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}u\rangle\bigr)
\ge c_{\nabla}>0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{self}}
=
\inf_{\|u\|=1,\ u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\bigl(-\langle u,M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}u\rangle\bigr)\ge 0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}
\le c_{\mathrm{cross}}.
}
\]

Thus the minimal package for \(\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\) is
\[
\boxed{
(c_\tau,\ c_{\nabla},\ \mu_{\mathrm{self}},\ c_{\mathrm{cross}}).
}
\]

Together with the already-closed bad-part packages,
\[
\|M_Z^{(OD)}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|\le \eta_{OD},
\qquad
\|M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|\le \eta_{\mathrm{gf}},
\]
the final explicit sufficient negativity condition is
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\tau+\mu_{\nabla}+\mu_{\mathrm{self}}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}
>
\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
}
\]

If this holds, then
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}})\subset(-\infty,0).
}
\]

\section*{Master Computation Checklist for closing \(M_Z\)}

\subsection*{1. Final target}

The final target is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}})\subset(-\infty,0),
}
\label{eq:target_checklist}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\left\{
u=(\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D)^T:
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0
\right\}.
\]

The fully explicit sufficient criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\tau+\mu_{\nabla}+\mu_{\mathrm{self}}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}
>
\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
}
\label{eq:master_criterion_checklist}
\end{equation}

Thus the problem is reduced to computing / bounding finitely many constants.

\subsection*{2. Checklist block I: \(OD\)-mixed bad-part bound}

The first bad-sector quantity is
\[
\eta_{OD}
=
\|M_Z^{(OD)}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|.
\]
Its master bound is
\begin{equation}
\eta_{OD}
\lesssim
\lambda_{OD}^2
\Bigl[
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k\,\mathfrak K_O
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D\,\mathfrak R_k\,\mathfrak K_D
+
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak A_{OD}
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak A_{DO}
\Bigr].
\label{eq:etaOD_checklist}
\end{equation}

Therefore the required \(OD\)-mixed checklist is:

\paragraph{(I-1) Background overlap bounds}
\[
\mathfrak B_\chi
=
\|P_O \bar\chi_B P_D\|_{\mathrm{HS}},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n
=
\|P_D \bar n_B P_O\|_{\mathrm{HS}}.
\]
Minimal explicit bounds:
\[
\mathfrak B_\chi
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar\chi_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n
\le
\sqrt{N_O N_D}\,\|\bar n_B\|_{L^\infty_\xi}.
\]

\paragraph{(I-2) Projected propagator bounds}
\[
\mathfrak G_O
=
\sup_{m,q}|G_O^{(m)}(q)|,
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D
=
\sup_{n,q}|G_D^{(n)}(q)|.
\]
Minimal explicit bounds:
\[
\mathfrak G_O\le \frac{1}{\Delta_O+r_O^{\min}},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D\le \frac{1}{\Delta_D+r_D^{\min}}.
\]

\paragraph{(I-3) Regulator derivative bound}
\[
\mathfrak R_k
=
\sup_q |\partial_tR_k(q)|.
\]
Minimal explicit bound:
\[
\mathfrak R_k
\le
k^2(\dot Z_{*,k}+2Z_{*,k}),
\]
or conservatively
\[
\mathfrak R_k\lesssim Z_{*,k}k^2.
\]

\paragraph{(I-4) Small-\(p\) curvature bounds}
\[
\mathfrak K_O,\qquad \mathfrak K_D.
\]
Minimal explicit bounds:
\[
\mathfrak K_O
\le
\mathfrak P_O^{(2)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak G_O
+
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak D_O^{(2)}
+
\mathfrak P_O^{(1)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak D_O^{(1)},
\]
\[
\mathfrak K_D
\le
\mathfrak P_D^{(2)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D
+
\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak D_D^{(2)}
+
\mathfrak P_D^{(1)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak D_D^{(1)}.
\]

\paragraph{(I-5) Anisotropy-response derivative bounds}
\[
\mathfrak A_{OD},\qquad \mathfrak A_{DO}.
\]
Minimal explicit conservative form:
\[
\mathfrak A_{OD},\mathfrak A_{DO}
\le
\mathfrak P_*^{(\delta)}\mathfrak G_*^2\mathfrak R_k
+
2\mathfrak P_*^{(0)}\mathfrak G_*^3\mathfrak R_k(\mathfrak H_*+\mathfrak R_*^{(\delta)})
+
\mathfrak P_*^{(0)}\mathfrak G_*^2\mathfrak R_{k,*}^{(\delta)}.
\]

\paragraph{Deliverable of Block I}
Once \((\mathfrak B_\chi,\mathfrak B_n,\mathfrak G_O,\mathfrak G_D,\mathfrak R_k,\mathfrak K_O,\mathfrak K_D,\mathfrak A_{OD},\mathfrak A_{DO})\) are estimated, \(\eta_{OD}\) is closed.

\subsection*{3. Checklist block II: gauge/projector bad-part bound}

The second bad-sector quantity is
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}
=
\|M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|.
\]
Its conservative master bound is
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}
\lesssim
\mathfrak P_A^2
\Bigl[
\mathfrak G_A^2\,\mathfrak V_A^{(4)}\,\mathfrak K_A
+
\mathfrak G_A^3\,(\mathfrak V_A^{(3)})^2\,\mathfrak K_A
\Bigr]
+
\mathfrak P_{A,*}^{(\delta)}\,\mathfrak K_A
+
\mathfrak A_{A,*}.
\label{eq:etagf_checklist}
\end{equation}

Therefore the required gauge/projector checklist is:

\paragraph{(II-0) Preconditions}
Verify first:
\[
p^\mu\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}=0,
\qquad
m_{A,k}^2\to 0,
\qquad
\text{gauge-preserving regulator},
\qquad
\text{Class I/II only}.
\]

\paragraph{(II-1) Projected gauge propagator bound}
\[
\mathfrak G_A
=
\sup_q \|G_A^{\mathrm{phys}}(q)\|.
\]

\paragraph{(II-2) Projected gauge vertex bounds}
\[
\mathfrak V_A^{(3)},
\qquad
\mathfrak V_A^{(4)}.

\paragraph{(II-3) Projected transverse curvature bounds}

\mathfrak K_A^{(4)},

\paragraph{(II-4) Gauge anisotropy-response bounds}

\mathfrak A_{A|T},
\qquad

\qquad

\paragraph{(II-5) Projector-control bounds}

\mathfrak P_A,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_{A|T}^{(\delta)},
\qquad
\mathfrak P_{A|O}^{(\delta)},
\qquad
\mathfrak P_{A|D}^{(\delta)}.
\]

\paragraph{Deliverable of Block II}
Once
\[
(\mathfrak G_A,\mathfrak V_A^{(3)},\mathfrak V_A^{(4)},\mathfrak K_A^{(4)},\mathfrak K_A^{(33)},\mathfrak A_{A|T},\mathfrak A_{A|O},\mathfrak A_{A|D},\mathfrak P_A,\mathfrak P_{A|T}^{(\delta)},\mathfrak P_{A|O}^{(\delta)},\mathfrak P_{A|D}^{(\delta)})
\]
are estimated, \(\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}\) is closed.

\subsection*{4. Checklist block III: good-part coercive negativity}

The good-sector quantity is
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}
\]
with
\[
M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}
=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+

Its master lower bound is
\begin{equation}
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}
\ge
\mu_\tau+\mu_{\nabla}+\mu_{\mathrm{self}}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}.
\label{eq:mugood_checklist}
\end{equation}

Therefore the required good-sector checklist is:

\paragraph{(III-1) Quartic-anisotropy contribution}
Use
\[
\theta_\tau=-\frac{\epsilon}{7}
\]
and extract the projection overlap coefficient
\[
c_\tau
=
\inf_{\|u\|=1,\ u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\langle u,P_\tau u\rangle,
\]
so that
\[
\mu_\tau\ge \frac{\epsilon}{7}c_\tau.
\]

\paragraph{(III-2) Derivative-anisotropy coercive bound}
Estimate
\[
\mu_{\nabla}
=
\inf_{\|u\|=1,\ u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\bigl(-\langle u,M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}u\rangle\bigr)
\ge c_{\nabla}>0.
\]

\paragraph{(III-3) Self-sector stabilizing bound}
Estimate
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{self}}
=
\inf_{\|u\|=1,\ u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\bigl(-\langle u,M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}u\rangle\bigr)\ge 0.
\]

\paragraph{(III-4) Cross-term defect}
Estimate
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}
\le c_{\mathrm{cross}}.
\]

\paragraph{Deliverable of Block III}
Once
\[
(c_\tau,\ c_{\nabla},\ \mu_{\mathrm{self}},\ c_{\mathrm{cross}})
\]
are estimated, \(\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\) is closed.

\subsection*{5. Final execution test}

After Blocks I--III are completed, perform the final comparison:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
}
\label{eq:final_execution_test}
\end{equation}
If this holds, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}})\subset(-\infty,0).
}
\label{eq:final_execution_result}
\end{equation}
Hence
\[
\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D\to 0,
\]
and the soft infrared sector is velocity-locked and isotropic.

\subsection*{6. Minimal execution order}

The most efficient order is:
\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Step 1: } \eta_{OD}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\textbf{Step 2: } \eta_{\mathrm{gf}}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\textbf{Step 3: } \mu_{\mathrm{good}}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\textbf{Step 4: final inequality}.
}
\label{eq:execution_order_final}
\end{equation}

This order is optimal because:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\eta_{OD}\) is the cleanest matter-sector bad-piece,
\item \(\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}\) is structurally more delicate but already fully packaged,
\item \(\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\) is expected to be favorable and is best estimated once the bad-part scales are known.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{7. Honest final status}

At this point the \(M_Z\)-closure program is reduced completely to a finite checklist of explicit constants.
No conceptual frontier remains in the \(M_Z\) setup itself.
The only remaining work is the actual extraction of these constants from the chosen background-adapted FRG truncation.

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Master Computation Checklist for closing }M_Z
}

The final sufficient condition is

\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
}

So the full execution checklist is:

\textbf{Block I: close }\eta_{OD}

by estimating

(\mathfrak B_\chi,\mathfrak B_n,\mathfrak G_O,\mathfrak G_D,\mathfrak R_k,\mathfrak K_O,\mathfrak K_D,\mathfrak A_{OD},\mathfrak A_{DO}).

by estimating
\[
(\mathfrak G_A,\mathfrak V_A^{(3)},\mathfrak V_A^{(4)},\mathfrak K_A^{(4)},\mathfrak K_A^{(33)},\mathfrak A_{A|T},\mathfrak A_{A|O},\mathfrak A_{A|D},\mathfrak P_A,\mathfrak P_{A|T}^{(\delta)},\mathfrak P_{A|O}^{(\delta)},\mathfrak P_{A|D}^{(\delta)}),
\]
under the preconditions
\[
p^\mu\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}=0,\qquad
m_{A,k}^2\to 0,\qquad
\text{gauge-preserving regulator},\qquad
\text{Class I/II only}.
\]

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Block III: close }\mu_{\mathrm{good}}
}
\]
by estimating
\[
(c_\tau,\ c_{\nabla},\ \mu_{\mathrm{self}},\ c_{\mathrm{cross}}),
\]
so that
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}
\ge
\mu_\tau+\mu_{\nabla}+\mu_{\mathrm{self}}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{cross}}.
\]

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Block IV: final comparison}
}
\]
Check
\[
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
}
\]
If true, then
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}})\subset(-\infty,0),
}
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D\to 0.
}
\]

Optimal execution order:
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{OD}
\ \rightarrow\
\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}
\ \rightarrow\
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}
\ \rightarrow\
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
}
\]

So the \(M_Z\) frontier is now a finite executable checklist, not an open structural problem.
