\section*{Strongest honest closure theorem currently available for TECT}

\subsection*{A. Closed theorem-level inputs}

At the theorem level, the following structures are already closed.

\paragraph{A1. Local Weyl/Dirac reduction.}
The local shell-reduced fermion problem is reduced to the finite witness data
\[
W_\parallel,\qquad W_I,\qquad W_J,
\]
or equivalently the reduced coefficient matrix \(M\), such that local Weyl nondegeneracy is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
W_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(W_I,W_J)\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:weyl_witness_cond_closed}
\end{equation}
and opposite-valley doubling reduces to equality of the witness triples at \(\pm G_*\). 

\paragraph{A2. Stability of the local Dirac block.}
If the remote sector is spectrally gapped,
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R)\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing,
\qquad \Delta>0,
\]
and the mixing obeys
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
then the Schur-complement correction is only
\[
O(|p|^2/\Delta),
\]
and does not alter the leading first-order Dirac block. 

\paragraph{A3. Mass protection reduction.}
The constant-mass problem is reduced to a finite residual-symmetry algebra check:
if no symmetry-allowed constant Hermitian \(4\times 4\) operator is a Dirac mass, then the reduced Dirac cone remains massless. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\paragraph{A4. Quartic anisotropy irrelevance.}
In the TECT infrared truncation with
\[
\Phi=(A_1,A_2,n_1,n_2,\chi_1,\chi_2),
\qquad
N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6,
\]
the quartic cubic anisotropy eigenvalue is
\begin{equation}
\theta_\tau
=
\epsilon\frac{4-N_{\mathrm{eff}}}{N_{\mathrm{eff}}+8}
=
-\frac{\epsilon}{7}<0.
\label{eq:theta_tau_closed}
\end{equation}
Hence the leading quartic anisotropy is rigorously infrared-irrelevant at this schematic FRG level. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\paragraph{A5. Gauge-consistent transverse sector.}
The \(A\)-sector must satisfy
\[
p^\mu\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}=0,
\qquad
m_{A,k}^2\to 0,
\]
with a gauge-preserving regulator and no Class III gauge-breaking operators. Under these conditions, the projected polarization remains transverse and no spurious Proca mass is generated. 

\subsection*{B. Explicit microscopic inputs still not yet verified}

What is not yet theorem-level closed in the final microscopic realization is the following finite input list.

\paragraph{B1. Actual witness realization.}
The reduced witness theorem is closed, but the actual microscopic TECT/Class II realization still requires verification that the relevant transport tensor sector is genuinely present in the physical defect background. 

\paragraph{B2. Opposite-valley realization.}
The formal pairing criterion is closed, but the actual equality of the witness triples at \(\pm G_*\) still has to be checked microscopically. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\paragraph{B3. Remote gap.}
The remote-gap theorem is closed as a reduction theorem, but the actual positive value of
\[
\Delta>0
\]
must still be computed from the relevant Bloch matrix / projected Hessian. 

\paragraph{B4. Zero constant mixing.}
The operational test
\[
\operatorname{Hom}_{H_*}(H_R,H_D)=0
\]
is explicit, but the actual shell-relevant irrep mismatch must still be checked in the final microscopic representation content. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

\paragraph{B5. Mass protection.}
The reduction theorem is closed, but the actual residual constant algebra
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\]
must still be computed in the final microscopic realization. :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\paragraph{B6. Derivative-anisotropy sign.}
The physical derivative-anisotropy problem is reduced to the sign of the linearized kinetic-flow matrix
\[
M_Z
\]
on the traceless subspace
\[
\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\left\{
u=(\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D)^T:
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0
\right\}.
\]
The notes are explicit that this part remains open: the full Hessian, regulator, threshold functions, anomalous dimensions, and gauge constraints are still needed to determine the sign of the nontrivial eigenvalues of \(M_Z\). 

\subsection*{C. Strongest conditional closure theorem}

Collect the finite microscopic inputs into the list:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Class II / admissible carrier realization:}
the actual microscopic tensor space contains a nontrivial symmetry-allowed Class II sector or equivalent admissible witness carrier;

\item \textbf{Weyl witness nonvanishing:}
\[
W_\parallel^\pm\neq 0,
\qquad
(W_I^\pm,W_J^\pm)\neq (0,0);
\]

\item \textbf{opposite-valley matching:}
\[
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+);
\]

\item \textbf{remote spectral gap:}
\[
\Delta>0;
\]

\item \textbf{zero constant mixing:}
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|;
\]

\item \textbf{mass protection:}
no symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass exists in the actual residual microscopic algebra;

\item \textbf{gauge-consistent projected sector:}
\[
p^\mu\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}=0,
\qquad
m_{A,k}^2\to 0,
\qquad
\text{gauge-preserving regulator},
\qquad
\text{Class I/II only};
\]

\item \textbf{IR-isotropy sign:}
\[
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}})\subset(-\infty,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then the strongest currently honest conditional theorem is:

\begin{theorem}[Strongest honest conditional closure theorem for TECT]
Assume items (1)--(8) above.
Then the final microscopic TECT realization contains:
\begin{enumerate}
\item an actual pair of opposite local Weyl valleys at \(\pm G_*\),
\item an actual local doubled Dirac block,
\item a spectrally isolated massless local Dirac cone,
\item an infrared soft sector whose sectoral kinetic anisotropies decay,
\[
\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D\to 0,
\]
so that the low-energy theory is velocity-locked and infrared-isotropic.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
Items (2) and (3) imply actual Weyl valleys at \(\pm G_*\) by the witness criterion.
Item (4) implies these valleys pair into a local Dirac block.
Items (5) and (6) imply the remote sector alters the local Dirac block only by higher-order terms and cannot generate a constant Dirac mass.
Hence the microscopic theory contains a stable spectrally isolated massless local Dirac cone.

On the infrared bosonic side, item (7) ensures the \(A\)-sector contribution is physically meaningful.
Item (8) implies that the physical derivative-anisotropy variables on the traceless sector decay under the RG flow.
Combined with quartic anisotropy irrelevance \eqref{eq:theta_tau_closed}, this yields infrared isotropy and velocity locking.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{D. What is genuinely proved versus not yet proved}

Therefore the exact logical status is:

\paragraph{What is already proved.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item the theorem-level reduction of the Weyl/Dirac problem to finite witness/gap/mixing/mass conditions;
\item the theorem-level reduction of the isotropy problem to the sign of \(M_Z\);
\item quartic anisotropy irrelevance for \(N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6\);
\item the gauge-consistency preconditions for a physical transverse \(A\)-sector.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{What is not yet proved.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item that the final microscopic TECT action actually realizes the required witness carrier sector;
\item that the actual microscopic coefficients satisfy the witness conditions;
\item that the actual projected spectrum has the required positive gap \(\Delta\);
\item that the residual microscopic symmetry forbids constant mass terms;
\item that the physical eigenvalues of \(M_Z\) are in fact negative.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{E. Honest final closure statement}

Thus the strongest possible honest closure statement at the present stage is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{TECT is not yet fully unconditionally closed microscopically,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{its remaining frontier has been reduced to a finite conditional verification theorem.}
}
\end{equation}

Equivalently:
\[
\text{no conceptual gap remains at the roadmap level,}
\]
and the only remaining work is the explicit microscopic verification of the finite inputs.

\section*{Dirac Step 1: explicit witness computation inside the concrete Class II ansatz}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

The local shell-reduced Weyl/Dirac problem is already reduced to the explicit witness triple
\[
(W_\parallel,W_I,W_J),
\]
or equivalently to the reduced mixed symbol coefficients
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]
For the natural local \(S2\) branch, the mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:S2_symbol_step1}
\end{equation}
The exact local nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:S2_nondeg_step1}
\end{equation}
This is explicitly stated in the local CP\(^2\)-defect transport notes. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection*{2. Concrete Class II transport ansatz}

The concrete minimal microscopic transport action is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
g_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
\label{eq:Ltrans_step1}
\end{equation}
Projecting this transport operator onto the graded low-mode sector gives the explicit coefficients
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:lambda_step1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:alphabeta_step1}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in the notation of the same derivation,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
\]
with the explicit defect integrals already computed. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0
\Longleftrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq(0,0)
\Longleftrightarrow
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:gcgego_equiv_step1}
\end{equation}

So Step 1 reduces to the finite coefficient extraction problem for
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O.
\]

\subsection*{3. Minimal Class II seed parameterization}

Now choose the shell-adapted Class II microscopic tensor basis in the axial frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\):
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\label{eq:m3_step1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:cpar_step1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{31}_{ij}
=
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}
=
-\,c_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:cIJ_step1}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the minimal shell-relevant Class II seed family appearing in the Class II completion notes. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

Using the shell-frame decomposition of the induced tensor, the Class II correction has the shell-relevant coefficients
\[
\delta A\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
\delta B\propto c_I,\qquad
\delta C\propto c_J,
\]
and therefore the corresponding witness shifts satisfy
\begin{equation}
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\label{eq:gccicj_step1}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the induced witness corrections are
\[
\delta W_\parallel\propto A,
\qquad
\delta W_I\propto B,
\qquad
\delta W_J\propto C.
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

\subsection*{4. Explicit witness seeds}

The seed directions are now immediate.

\paragraph{Longitudinal seed.}
Take
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
c_I=c_J=0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
g_E=g_O=0,
\label{eq:long_seed_step1}
\end{equation}
hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Even transverse seed.}
Take
\[
c_\parallel=0,
\qquad
c_I\neq 0,
\qquad
c_J=0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
g_E\neq 0,
\qquad
g_c=g_O=0,
\label{eq:even_seed_step1}
\end{equation}
hence
\[
\alpha\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Odd transverse seed.}
Take
\[
c_\parallel=0,
\qquad
c_I=0,
\qquad
c_J\neq 0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
g_O\neq 0,
\qquad
g_c=g_E=0,
\label{eq:odd_seed_step1}
\end{equation}
hence
\[
\beta\neq 0.
\]

Therefore the chosen Class II parameterization already contains:
\begin{enumerate}
\item an explicit longitudinal witness seed;
\item an explicit transverse witness seed.
\end{enumerate}
This is exactly the finite-witness closure theorem proved in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

\subsection*{5. Determinant and local Weyl criterion}

For the \(S2\) symbol \eqref{eq:S2_symbol_step1},
\[
\det A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel
\Bigl(
\alpha^2(p_1^2+p_2^2)+\beta^2(p_1^2+p_2^2)
\Bigr)
\]
up to the standard shell normalization factor. Equivalently, in the shell witness notation,
\begin{equation}
\det M
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
W_\parallel
\bigl(W_I^2+W_J^2\bigr).
\label{eq:detM_step1}
\end{equation}
Hence local Weyl nondegeneracy is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(W_I,W_J)\neq(0,0),
}
\label{eq:weyl_criterion_step1}
\end{equation}
or equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:geometric_weyl_step1}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\subsection*{6. What is actually closed in Step 1}

At this point, the following is rigorously closed inside the Class II truncation:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the local \(S2\) symbol is explicitly written;
\item the witness coefficients are explicitly matched to \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\);
\item the minimal Class II tensor family contains explicit longitudinal and transverse witness seeds;
\item therefore the witness problem is generically closed on the allowed finite-dimensional Class II tensor space.
\end{enumerate}

In particular, once one longitudinal seed and one transverse seed exist, finite-dimensional genericity implies:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c(N)\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
(g_E(N),g_O(N))\neq(0,0)
}
\label{eq:generic_closed_step1}
\end{equation}
for an open dense full-measure subset of the allowed Class II tensor space \(V_{II}\). :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12}

\subsection*{7. Honest remaining open point}

What is \emph{not} yet closed is stronger than this Step 1 result:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the true complete TECT action must still be shown to realize a nontrivial Class II sector in the physically relevant defect background.}
}
\label{eq:still_open_step1}
\end{equation}

So the exact honest conclusion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{inside the concrete Class II truncation, Step 1 is closed;}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the full microscopic TECT realization of that Class II sector remains to be verified.}
}
\end{equation}
This is stated explicitly in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13} :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\]

For the concrete Class II transport ansatz,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

Therefore the exact local nondegeneracy condition is
\[
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

For the minimal shell-adapted Class II seed family
\[
m^a(P_0)=m\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
\[
C^{31}_{ij}
=
c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}
=
- c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_I \hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
one has
\[
\boxed{
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
}
\]

Hence explicit witness seeds already exist:

\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,\ c_I=c_J=0
\Longrightarrow
g_c\neq 0,
\]
\[
c_\parallel=0,\ c_I\neq 0,\ c_J=0
\Longrightarrow
g_E\neq 0,
\]
\[
c_\parallel=0,\ c_I=0,\ c_J\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
g_O\neq 0.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the concrete Class II truncation, the Step 1 witness problem is closed.}
}
\]

What remains open is only:
\[
\boxed{
\text{whether the full complete TECT action actually realizes a nontrivial Class II sector in the relevant defect background.}
}
\]

\section*{Dirac Step 2: opposite-valley witness matching in the concrete Class II ansatz}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

The local shell-reduced Dirac criterion is not merely:
\[
\text{Weyl at }+G_*,
\qquad
\text{Weyl at }-G_*.
\]
One also needs opposite-valley pairing in the matched frame, equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+).
}
\label{eq:opp_valley_match_goal}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the finite witness formulation of local Dirac doubling. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

\subsection*{2. Positive-valley witness data}

At the positive valley \(+G_*\), with adapted frame
\[
\{\hat n^+,e_1^+,e_2^+\},
\qquad
\hat n^+=\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\]
the reduced shell-enriched operator is
\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}^{(1)}
=
g_\parallel O_\parallel + g_I O_I + g_J O_J,
\]
with
\[
O_\parallel=p_\parallel \sigma_3,
\qquad
O_I=p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2,
\qquad
O_J=-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2.
\]
The corresponding witness functionals satisfy
\begin{equation}
W_\parallel^+=g_\parallel^+,
\qquad
W_I^+=g_I^+,
\qquad
W_J^+=g_J^+.
\label{eq:Wp_data}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

Inside the concrete Class II transport ansatz, these coefficients are read as
\[
g_\parallel^+\leftrightarrow g_c^+,
\qquad
g_I^+\leftrightarrow g_E^+,
\qquad
g_J^+\leftrightarrow g_O^+.
\]
Thus Step 1 already gives
\[
W_\parallel^+=g_c^+,
\qquad
W_I^+=g_E^+,
\qquad
W_J^+=g_O^+.
\]

\subsection*{3. Negative-valley frame and matching convention}

At the opposite valley \(-G_*\), one does \emph{not} compare coefficients in an arbitrary raw coordinate frame.
One first chooses the matched opposite-valley frame
\[
\{\hat n^-,e_1^-,e_2^-\}
\]
so that the opposite-valley Hamiltonian is compared in the standard doubled form
\[
h^-(p)=-h^+(-p)
\]
to leading order.
This is the exact witness formulation of opposite-valley pairing in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11} :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12}

Therefore the correct matching problem is not “do the raw coefficients literally coincide in the same laboratory basis,” but rather:

\[
\boxed{
\text{after the matched opposite-valley frame choice, do the two witness triples coincide?}
}
\]

\subsection*{4. Class II tensor data at the two valleys}

Inside the concrete minimal Class II family,
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:ClassII_seed_pairing}
\end{equation}
On this family, the shell/defect dictionary gives
\begin{equation}
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\label{eq:ClassII_gcgego_pairing}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13} :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14}

Now pass from \(+G_*\) to \(-G_*\).
Then
\[
\hat n^-=-\hat n^+.
\]
If one simultaneously uses the matched transverse basis
\[
e_1^-=-e_1^+,\qquad e_2^-=e_2^+
\]
or any equivalent right-handed matched choice, then the shell-relevant tensor structures are read in the same oriented local coordinates.
Under this matched-frame prescription, the coefficients extracted by the witness functionals are the same scalar amplitudes:
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel^- = c_\parallel^+,
\qquad
c_I^- = c_I^+,
\qquad
c_J^- = c_J^+.
\label{eq:c_matching}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
g_c^- = g_c^+,
\qquad
g_E^- = g_E^+,
\qquad
g_O^- = g_O^+.
\label{eq:g_matching}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Witness matching}

By the witness dictionary,
\[
W_\parallel^\pm=g_c^\pm,
\qquad
W_I^\pm=g_E^\pm,
\qquad
W_J^\pm=g_O^\pm.
\]
Therefore \eqref{eq:g_matching} implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_\parallel^- = W_\parallel^+,
\qquad
W_I^- = W_I^+,
\qquad
W_J^- = W_J^+.
}
\label{eq:W_matching_final}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the opposite-valley witness matching criterion required for local Dirac doubling. :contentReference[oaicite:15]{index=15}

\subsection*{6. Consequence}

Combining Step 1 and Step 2:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Step 1 gives local Weyl nondegeneracy at one valley:
\[
g_c\neq 0,\qquad (g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

\item The same concrete Class II seed family exists at the opposite valley.

\item In the matched opposite-valley frame, the witness triples coincide:
\[
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore, inside the concrete Class II truncation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{opposite-valley pairing is closed at the witness level.}
}
\label{eq:opp_pair_closed}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Honest remaining open point}

What remains open is stronger than the statement above:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the full microscopic TECT action must still be shown to realize the required opposite shell pair } \pm G_*
\text{ as actual low-energy valleys.}
}
\label{eq:opp_pair_open}
\end{equation}
This is explicitly listed in the notes as one of the remaining microscopic tasks. :contentReference[oaicite:16]{index=16} :contentReference[oaicite:17]{index=17}

So the exact honest conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the concrete Class II witness truncation, Step 2 is closed;}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the full microscopic existence of the opposite shell-pair valleys remains to be verified.}
}
\]

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Dirac Step 2: opposite-valley witness matching}
}
\]

Local Dirac doubling requires
\[
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+).
}
\]

Inside the concrete Class II ansatz,
\[
\boxed{
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J,
}
\]
and the witness dictionary is
\[
\boxed{
W_\parallel=g_c,\qquad
W_I=g_E,\qquad
W_J=g_O.
}
\]

Using the matched opposite-valley frame, the same seed amplitudes are read at the two valleys:
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel^- = c_\parallel^+,\qquad
c_I^- = c_I^+,\qquad
c_J^- = c_J^+,
}
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
g_c^- = g_c^+,\qquad
g_E^- = g_E^+,\qquad
g_O^- = g_O^+.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
W_\parallel^- = W_\parallel^+,\qquad
W_I^- = W_I^+,\qquad
W_J^- = W_J^+.
}
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the concrete Class II witness truncation, opposite-valley pairing is closed at the witness level.}
}
\]

What remains open is only:
\[
\boxed{
\text{whether the full microscopic TECT action actually realizes the shell pair } \pm G_*
\text{ as genuine low-energy valleys.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Dirac Step 3: zero constant mixing \texorpdfstring{$V(0)=0$}{V(0)=0} in the concrete Class II setting}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

After Step 1 (actual Weyl witness inside the Class II truncation) and Step 2 (opposite-valley witness matching), the next stability condition for the local Dirac block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:goal_V0_step3}
\end{equation}
Here \(V(p)\) is the off-diagonal mixing block between the local doubled Dirac sector and the remote sector:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Hfull_step3}
\end{equation}
The symbol \(V(0)=0\) means absence of \emph{constant hybridization} at the crossing, not vanishing vacuum energy. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5} :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection*{2. The theorem-level zero-mixing statement}

Let \(H_*\) be the little group at the selected shell crossing \(p=0\), and assume the full Hilbert space decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R,
\label{eq:Hsplit_step3}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_D\) is the isolated doubled shell block carrying the local Dirac sector,
\item \(\mathcal H_R\) is the orthogonal remote sector.
\end{itemize}
Assume further that the decomposition is \(H_*\)-invariant and that the microscopic Hamiltonian is \(H_*\)-equivariant at \(p=0\). Then the constant mixing block obeys
\begin{equation}
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\label{eq:V0_Hom_step3}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:Hom_to_V0_step3}
\end{equation}
This is already theorem-level closed. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection*{3. Practical sectorwise audit}

The theorem is turned into a finite practical audit by decomposing the remote sector into \(H_*\)-invariant pieces
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a.
\label{eq:HR_decomp_step3}
\end{equation}
If every sector \(K_a\) differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label, then
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
\qquad
\forall a,
\label{eq:Ka_Hom_zero_step3}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
V(0)=0.
\label{eq:HR_Hom_zero_step3}
\end{equation}
The practical checklist given in the notes is:

a remote sector is excluded from constant mixing if it differs from the local Dirac block in at least one of
\begin{enumerate}
\item the selected shell-pair label \(\pm G_*\),
\item transverse versus longitudinal/volumetric character,
\item presence of the enriched shell-relevant internal doublet,
\item residual grading / parity / chirality,
\item any extra conserved microscopic label.
\end{enumerate}
:contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9} :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

\subsection*{4. Minimal truncated remote sector}

The smallest dangerous remote completion used in the notes is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\label{eq:Hfull_tr_step3}
\end{equation}
Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\) is the local doubled Dirac carrier,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}\) is the volumetric/longitudinal sector,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}\) is the higher-shell sector not belonging to the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\),
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}\) is the same-shell but non-enriched sector,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}\) contains modes with internal content not matching the selected enriched shell doublet.
\end{itemize}
This is explicitly introduced as the smallest truncation containing all previously identified dangerous remote channels. :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11} :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12}

\subsection*{5. Why the concrete Class II ansatz is compatible with \(V(0)=0\)}

The canonical minimal Class II representative is
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:ClassII_canonical_step3}
\end{equation}
Its effect is to renormalize the shell-level first-order coefficients
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}},\qquad B_{\mathrm{eff}},\qquad C_{\mathrm{eff}},
\]
or equivalently the Weyl witness triple.
It does \emph{not} by construction insert an independent constant \(4\times4\) Dirac mass term, and it does not by itself define a constant Dirac--remote intertwiner.
Therefore the exact logical status is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II is compatible with }V(0)=0,
\text{ but does not itself prove }V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:ClassII_compat_V0}
\end{equation}
This is explicitly stated in the compatibility theorem for the canonical minimal Class II choice. :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13} :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14}

\subsection*{6. Concrete closure of Step 3}

What can now be honestly closed is the following theorem.

\begin{theorem}[Step 3 closure in the concrete Class II setting]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the concrete Class II witness truncation of Steps 1--2 is realized on the local doubled shell block \(\mathcal H_D\);
\item the full microscopic crossing is \(H_*\)-equivariant at \(p=0\);
\item the remote sector admits an \(H_*\)-invariant decomposition
\[
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}};
\]
\item each remote summand differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label.
\end{enumerate}
Then
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\qquad
V(0)=0.
\label{eq:Step3_closed_theorem}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \(H_*\)-equivariance and invariant block decomposition,
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Because
\[
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a,
\]
one has
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)
\cong
\bigoplus_a \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D).
\]
By assumption, every \(K_a\) mismatches \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label, hence
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
\qquad\forall a.
\]
Therefore
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
and thus \(V(0)=0\).
\end{proof}

\subsection*{7. Honest remaining open point}

The theorem above closes Step 3 only \emph{conditionally on the actual remote-sector label audit}.
Therefore the exact honest status is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Step 3 is reduced completely to a finite remote-sector irrep/label audit.}
}
\label{eq:Step3_reduced_audit}
\end{equation}
What is still not yet fully closed microscopically is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual final TECT truncation must still be audited to prove that no remote sector shares the same shell-relevant irrep as }\mathcal H_D.
}
\label{eq:Step3_actual_open}
\end{equation}
This is exactly how the notes summarize the present status of Task V. :contentReference[oaicite:15]{index=15} :contentReference[oaicite:16]{index=16} :contentReference[oaicite:17]{index=17}

\subsection*{8. Strongest honest conclusion of Step 3}

Thus the strongest currently honest conclusion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{inside the concrete Class II ansatz, }V(0)=0\text{ is not automatic,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{its verification is fully reduced to a finite little-group mismatch audit of the remote sector.}
}
\end{equation}
So Step 3 is closed at the reduction-theorem level.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
}
\]

Hence the theorem-level zero-mixing statement is
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

The practical finite audit is:
a remote sector is excluded from constant mixing if it differs from the local Dirac block in at least one of
\[
\boxed{
\text{shell-pair label},\quad
\text{transverse vs volumetric character},\quad
\text{presence of enriched internal doublet},\quad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},\quad
\text{extra conserved microscopic label}.
}
\]

In the minimal dangerous truncation,
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
}
\]

The canonical minimal Class II representative
\[
\boxed{
m^a(P_0)=m\delta^{a3},\ 
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,\ 
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},\ 
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}
}
\]
renormalizes the shell-level derivative witness coefficients but does not by itself prove \(V(0)=0\).

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II is compatible with }V(0)=0,\text{ but }V(0)=0\text{ still requires an independent little-group mismatch audit.}
}
\]

So the strongest honest Step 3 conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{zero constant mixing is fully reduced to a finite remote-sector irrep/label audit.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Dirac Step 4: remote spectral gap \texorpdfstring{$\Delta>0$}{Delta>0} in the concrete Class II setting}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

After Step 3, the next stability condition for the local doubled Dirac block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing
\qquad
\text{for small }p,
\qquad
\Delta>0.
}
\label{eq:goal_gap_step4}
\end{equation}
This means that the remote sector remains spectrally separated from the local Dirac crossing.

The notes are explicit that the remote-gap theorem itself is already closed, but the actual value of the gap must still be checked in the final microscopic truncation. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

\subsection*{2. Pointwise and uniform spectral lower-bound theorem}

Let the remote block be written as
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+E_R(p),
\]
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(D_R(p)\) is the remote diagonal / benchmark part,
\item \(E_R(p)\) is the off-diagonal / correction part.
\end{itemize}
Define
\begin{equation}
\delta_0(p):=\min_a |(D_R)_{aa}(p)|,
\qquad
\eta_R(p):=\|E_R(p)\|.
\label{eq:delta0_etaR_step4}
\end{equation}
Then the pointwise remote-gap theorem states:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_0(p)>\eta_R(p)
\Longrightarrow
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta(p),\Delta(p))=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta(p)\ge \delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p)>0.
}
\label{eq:point_gap_step4}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

Fix a neighborhood
\[
N_\rho:=\{p:|p|\le \rho\},
\]
and define
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}:=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\label{eq:uniform_data_step4}
\end{equation}
Then the uniform theorem is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing
\quad \forall |p|\le \rho,
}
\label{eq:uniform_gap_cond_step4}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho:=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\label{eq:uniform_gap_value_step4}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

Thus the remote-gap problem is already reduced to a finite Bloch-spectral inequality.

\subsection*{3. Perturbative gap-stability theorem}

Assume there exists an unperturbed microscopic realization
\begin{equation}
H_R^{(0)}(p)
\quad\text{with}\quad
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap(-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing
\qquad
(\Delta_0>0),
\label{eq:unpert_gap_step4}
\end{equation}
for all sufficiently small \(p\).
Now perturb by
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=H_R^{(0)}(p)+\delta H_R(p),
\qquad
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|\le \varepsilon.
\label{eq:pert_gap_step4}
\end{equation}
Then the bounded-perturbation remote-gap theorem gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon<\Delta_0
\Longrightarrow
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta:=\Delta_0-\varepsilon>0.
}
\label{eq:gap_stability_step4}
\end{equation}
Moreover, under the stronger bound
\[
\varepsilon<\frac{\Delta_0}{2},
\]
one gets
\[
\Delta>\frac{\Delta_0}{2}>0.
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12} :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

This is precisely the theorem-level meaning of the statement that a sufficiently small Class II correction is gap-compatible if the starting realization is already gapped.

\subsection*{4. Resolvent bound and Schur-complement consequence}

If \(|E|<\Delta/2\), then
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
\label{eq:resolvent_step4}
\end{equation}
Therefore, if in addition
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
the Schur complement obeys
\begin{equation}
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2,
\label{eq:selfenergy_step4}
\end{equation}
so the remote sector modifies the local Dirac Hamiltonian only at order
\[
O(|p|^2/\Delta).
\]
This is the exact theorem-level mechanism by which the remote gap enters spectral isolation. :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14} :contentReference[oaicite:15]{index=15}

\subsection*{5. Concrete Class II compatibility statement}

The canonical minimal Class II representative modifies only the shell-relevant derivative tensor coefficients:
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J,
\]
with
\[
\mu=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m.
\]
It does not by itself prove a remote gap.
The exact honest theorem in the Class II notes is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II is compatible with }\Delta>0,
\text{ but }\Delta>0\text{ still requires an independent microscopic gap check,}
}
\label{eq:classII_gap_compat_step4}
\end{equation}
or, alternatively, perturbative stability from an already-gapped realization:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\ II}}\|<\frac{\Delta_0}{2}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta\ge \Delta_0-\|\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\ II}}\|>\frac{\Delta_0}{2}>0.
}
\label{eq:classII_gap_stable_step4}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:16]{index=16} :contentReference[oaicite:17]{index=17}

\subsection*{6. Strongest honest closure of Step 4}

Thus the strongest theorem-level closure available now is the following.

\begin{theorem}[Step 4 closure in the concrete Class II setting]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the final microscopic TECT truncation admits a remote block decomposition \(H_R(p)\);
\item either:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the direct Bloch-spectral inequality holds on a small neighborhood \(N_\rho\),
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\]
or
\item there exists an already-gapped unperturbed realization with gap \(\Delta_0>0\), and the Class II correction obeys
\[
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|<\Delta_0;
\]
\end{enumerate}
\item the local Dirac block satisfies Step 3:
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad \|V(p)\|\le c|p|.
\]
\end{enumerate}
Then the remote sector has a positive gap
\[
\Delta>0,
\]
and the Schur-complement correction to the local Dirac block is only
\[
O(|p|^2/\Delta).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
In case (2a), apply the uniform spectral lower-bound theorem \eqref{eq:uniform_gap_cond_step4}--\eqref{eq:uniform_gap_value_step4}.  
In case (2b), apply the bounded perturbation theorem \eqref{eq:gap_stability_step4}.  
Then use the resolvent estimate \eqref{eq:resolvent_step4} together with \(\|V(p)\|\le c|p|\) to obtain \eqref{eq:selfenergy_step4}. This proves that the remote sector remains spectrally separated and contributes only subleading curvature corrections.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{7. Honest remaining open point}

What remains open is not the theorem but the actual microscopic input:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual numerical or analytic verification of }
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\text{ (or of a concrete already-gapped realization with small perturbation).}
}
\label{eq:actual_gap_open_step4}
\end{equation}
This is explicitly listed in the notes as one of the remaining finite microscopic tasks. :contentReference[oaicite:18]{index=18} :contentReference[oaicite:19]{index=19}

\subsection*{8. Strongest honest conclusion of Step 4}

Therefore the strongest honest Step 4 conclusion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the remote-gap problem is completely reduced to a finite Bloch-spectral inequality (or bounded-perturbation gap audit);}
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the concrete Class II ansatz is gap-compatible, but does not by itself prove }\Delta>0.
}
\end{equation}
So Step 4 is closed at the reduction-theorem level.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Dirac Step 4: remote gap } \Delta>0
}
\]

The theorem-level remote-gap criterion is:

\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing
\quad(|p|\le \rho),
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

An equivalent perturbative stability route is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap(-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|<\Delta_0
}
\]
implies
\[
\boxed{
\Delta=\Delta_0-\sup\|\delta H_R\|>0.
}
\]

Then, if
\[
\boxed{
V(0)=0,\qquad \|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
}
\]
the resolvent obeys
\[
\boxed{
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}
\qquad (|E|<\Delta/2),
}
\]
and the Schur-complement correction is only
\[
\boxed{
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|\le \frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2.
}
\]

For the concrete Class II ansatz:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II is compatible with }\Delta>0,
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\Delta>0\text{ still requires an independent microscopic gap check,}
}
\]
or a sufficiently small bounded perturbation of an already-gapped realization.

So the strongest honest Step 4 conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the remote-gap problem is fully reduced to a finite Bloch-spectral inequality / bounded-perturbation audit.}
}
\]

\section*{Dirac Step 5: mass protection in the concrete Class II setting}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

After:
\begin{itemize}
\item Step 1: actual local Weyl witness,
\item Step 2: opposite-valley witness matching,
\item Step 3: zero constant mixing \(V(0)=0\),
\item Step 4: remote spectral gap \(\Delta>0\),
\end{itemize}
the final local Dirac-stability condition is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{no symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass exists on the isolated doubled shell block.}
}
\label{eq:mass_goal_step5}
\end{equation}

The notes are explicit that this question is no longer an infinite-dimensional PDE problem.
It is exactly a finite algebraic classification problem on \(4\times 4\) Hermitian matrices. :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\subsection*{2. Minimal doubled Dirac block and mass space}

Assume the matched local doubled Dirac block has the form
\begin{equation}
H_D(q)=\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i),
\qquad i=1,2,3.
\label{eq:HD_step5}
\end{equation}
The constant Dirac mass space is defined by
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M
:=
\left\{
K\in \mathrm{Herm}(4):
\{K,\rho_3\otimes \sigma_i\}=0
\ \forall i=1,2,3
\right\}.
\label{eq:Mspace_def_step5}
\end{equation}
The exact classification theorem gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\}.
}
\label{eq:Mspace_exact_step5}
\end{equation}
Thus the constant mass space is exactly two-dimensional. :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12} :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

Without any further symmetry, these masses are allowed, and the node is gapped:
\[
H_D^{(m)}(q)
=
\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i)
+
m_1\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
with spectrum
\[
E_\pm(q)=\pm\sqrt{|q|^2+m_1^2+m_2^2}.
\]
Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the minimal doubled Dirac algebra alone does not protect the node.}
}
\label{eq:no_auto_massprot}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14}

\subsection*{3. Finite mass-protection criterion}

Let \(G_{\mathrm{res}}\) be the actual residual low-energy symmetry group acting on the doubled shell block, and let
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}
:=
\{K\in \mathrm{Herm}(4): U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K\ \forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}\}
\label{eq:Ares_def_step5}
\end{equation}
be the corresponding allowed constant operator algebra.

Then the exact finite criterion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}
\Longrightarrow
\text{mass protection}.
}
\label{eq:finite_masscrit_step5}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, one may solve:
\[
U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K,
\qquad
\{K,\Gamma_i\}=0,
\]
and check whether the only solution is \(K=0\). :contentReference[oaicite:15]{index=15}

Thus Step 5 is already theorem-level reduced to a finite \(4\times4\) linear algebra problem.

\subsection*{4. Explicit sufficient mechanism: residual valley \(U(1)_V\)}

Define the valley-charge generator
\begin{equation}
Q_V:=\rho_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_V(\theta)=e^{i\theta Q_V}.
\label{eq:QV_def_step5}
\end{equation}
The kinetic Dirac block is invariant because
\[
[Q_V,\rho_3\otimes \sigma_i]=0.
\]
Under this symmetry the two mass generators rotate as
\begin{equation}
U_V(\theta)(\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_V(\theta)^{-1}
=
(\cos 2\theta)\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
(\sin 2\theta)\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:rho1_rot_step5}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
U_V(\theta)(\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_V(\theta)^{-1}
=
-(\sin 2\theta)\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
(\cos 2\theta)\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:rho2_rot_step5}
\end{equation}
Hence the mass space transforms as a nontrivial doublet and no nonzero mass element is invariant under all \(\theta\).
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:U1_massprot_step5}
\end{equation}
So exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) is a sufficient mechanism for full constant mass protection. :contentReference[oaicite:16]{index=16} :contentReference[oaicite:17]{index=17}

\subsection*{5. Weaker sufficient mechanism: residual \texorpdfstring{$\mathbb Z_2^V$}{Z2V}}

The full continuous \(U(1)_V\) is stronger than necessary.
The discrete remnant
\begin{equation}
S_V:=\rho_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
S_V^2=\mathbf 1_4
\label{eq:SV_def_step5}
\end{equation}
already suffices, because
\begin{equation}
S_V(\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\qquad
S_V(\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:SV_forbid_step5}
\end{equation}
Thus an exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) also forbids all constant Dirac masses:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathbb Z_2^V}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:Z2_massprot_step5}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:18]{index=18}

\subsection*{6. Stability under remote-sector elimination}

If the residual valley symmetry is exact in the full microscopic theory and the remote-sector elimination preserves that symmetry, then no symmetry-preserving self-energy correction can generate a constant Dirac mass.
In the little-group scalar sector the self-energy at \((\omega,p)=(0,0)\) has the restricted form
\[
\Sigma(0,0)=a_0\,\mathbf 1_4+a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
so no term proportional to
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\quad\text{or}\quad
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
can be generated.
Hence mass protection is radiatively stable, provided the residual valley symmetry is exact. :contentReference[oaicite:19]{index=19}

\subsection*{7. Compatibility with the concrete Class II ansatz}

The canonical minimal Class II representative is
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:ClassII_step5}
\end{equation}
Its role is to renormalize the derivative shell tensor coefficients \(A,B,C\), equivalently the first-order local Weyl/Dirac witnesses.
It does not by construction insert an independent constant \(4\times4\) Dirac mass operator.

Therefore the exact honest compatibility statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II is mass-protection compatible, but does not by itself prove mass protection.}
}
\label{eq:ClassII_masscompat_step5}
\end{equation}
The actual proof of mass protection still depends on the residual symmetry algebra of the isolated doubled shell block. 

\subsection*{8. Strongest honest closure of Step 5}

We can now state the strongest theorem-level closure available in the concrete Class II setting.

\begin{theorem}[Step 5 closure in the concrete Class II setting]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item Steps 1--4 already hold, so that an isolated doubled local Dirac block
\[
H_D(q)=\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i)+O(|q|^2/\Delta)
\]
exists;
\item the actual residual low-energy symmetry algebra on the isolated doubled shell block contains an exact valley symmetry \(U(1)_V\) generated by \(Q_V=\rho_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2\), or at least its \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) remnant generated by \(S_V=\rho_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2\);
\item remote-sector elimination preserves that residual symmetry.
\end{enumerate}
Then
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\},
\qquad
\mathcal M=\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\},
\label{eq:Step5_thm_concl}
\end{equation}
hence no symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass exists, and the isolated local Dirac cone is mass-protected.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By the explicit mass-space classification, every constant Dirac mass belongs to
\[
\mathcal M=\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
\]
Under exact \(U(1)_V\) these two generators rotate as a nontrivial doublet, so none is invariant unless its coefficient vanishes.
Hence
\[
A_{U(1)_V}\cap\mathcal M=\{0\}.
\]
The same conclusion follows already from the \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) remnant, since both mass generators are odd under \(S_V\).
Because remote-sector elimination preserves the symmetry, no radiative constant mass term can be generated.
Therefore all symmetry-allowed constant Dirac masses are forbidden.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{9. Honest remaining open point}

What is still open microscopically is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{whether the actual full TECT/Class II realization indeed preserves exact residual }U(1)_V
\text{ (or at least }\mathbb Z_2^V\text{).}
}
\label{eq:Step5_actual_open}
\end{equation}
The notes are explicit that this is still a separate microscopic check. :contentReference[oaicite:21]{index=21} :contentReference[oaicite:22]{index=22}

\subsection*{10. Strongest honest conclusion of Step 5}

Therefore the strongest honest Step 5 conclusion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{mass protection is fully reduced to a finite residual-symmetry exclusion test on the isolated doubled shell block;}
}
\label{eq:Step5_reduced}
\end{equation}
more concretely,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}
=
\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:Step5_explicit_reduced}
\end{equation}
And an exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) or \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) is an explicit sufficient mechanism.
So Step 5 is closed at the reduction-theorem level.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Dirac Step 5: mass protection}
}
\]

For the isolated doubled local Dirac block
\[
H_D(q)=\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i),
\]
the constant Dirac mass space is exactly
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\}.
}
\]

Thus the finite mass-protection criterion is
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}
\Longrightarrow
\text{mass protection}.
}
\]

An explicit sufficient mechanism is exact residual valley symmetry
\[
\boxed{
Q_V=\rho_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_V(\theta)=e^{i\theta Q_V},
}
\]
because under it
\[
\boxed{
U_V(\theta)(\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_V(\theta)^{-1}
=
(\cos 2\theta)\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
(\sin 2\theta)\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
U_V(\theta)(\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_V(\theta)^{-1}
=
-(\sin 2\theta)\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
(\cos 2\theta)\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
}
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}.
}

A weaker but still sufficient mechanism is the residual
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb Z_2^V:\quad S_V=\rho_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
}
\]
under which both mass generators are odd, so again
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathbb Z_2^V}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}.
}
\]

For the concrete Class II ansatz:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II is mass-protection compatible,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{mass protection itself still requires an independent residual-symmetry check.}
}
\]

So the strongest honest Step 5 conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{mass protection is fully reduced to a finite residual-symmetry exclusion test on }
\mathcal M=\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
}
\]

\section*{Local Dirac Closure Theorem in the concrete Class II setting}

\subsection*{A. Setting}

We consider the shell-reduced local fermion problem near a selected shell pair
\[
\pm G_*,
\]
with the concrete Class II microscopic witness truncation acting on the low-energy doubled shell block.
The local doubled shell carrier is denoted by
\[
\mathcal H_D,
\]
and the remote sector by
\[
\mathcal H_R,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R.
\]

The goal is to determine when the full microscopic TECT linearization contains a stable, spectrally isolated, massless local Dirac cone.

\subsection*{B. Step 1: actual local Weyl witness inside the concrete Class II truncation}

On the natural local \(S2\) branch, the reduced mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:A1_local_classII_theorem}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:lambda_alpha_beta_theorem}
\end{equation}
Therefore local Weyl nondegeneracy is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:weyl_nondeg_classII_theorem}
\end{equation}
Inside the minimal shell-adapted Class II tensor family,
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J,
\]
so explicit longitudinal and transverse witness seeds exist.
Hence the witness problem is closed inside the concrete Class II truncation: an open dense full-measure subset of the allowed Class II tensor space produces a nondegenerate local Weyl symbol. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5} :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection*{C. Step 2: opposite-valley witness matching}

Let
\[
(W_\parallel^\pm,W_I^\pm,W_J^\pm)
\]
denote the witness triples at \(\pm G_*\).
Local Dirac doubling requires not only Weyl nondegeneracy at each valley, but also matched opposite-valley data:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+).
}
\label{eq:Dirac_pairing_theorem}
\end{equation}
In the matched opposite-valley frame, the same Class II seed amplitudes are read at the two valleys:
\[
c_\parallel^-=c_\parallel^+,
\qquad
c_I^-=c_I^+,
\qquad
c_J^-=c_J^+,
\]
hence
\[
g_c^-=g_c^+,
\qquad
g_E^-=g_E^+,
\qquad
g_O^-=g_O^+,
\]
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_\parallel^- = W_\parallel^+,
\qquad
W_I^- = W_I^+,
\qquad
W_J^- = W_J^+.
}
\label{eq:witness_matching_theorem}
\end{equation}
Thus opposite-valley pairing is closed at the witness level inside the concrete Class II truncation. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection*{D. Step 3: zero constant mixing}

Write the full block Hamiltonian as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:block_H_step3_theorem}
\end{equation}
At the crossing \(p=0\), let \(H_*\) be the corresponding little group.
Then the theorem-level statement is
\begin{equation}
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D),
\label{eq:V0_Hom_theorem}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:V0_zero_theorem}
\end{equation}
The practical remote-sector audit is finite: if every remote sector differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label (shell-pair, transverse/volumetric character, enriched internal doublet, grading/parity/chirality, extra conserved label), then no constant intertwiner exists.
Thus zero constant mixing is fully reduced to a finite remote-sector irrep/label mismatch audit.
The concrete Class II ansatz is compatible with this condition, but does not by itself prove it. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9} :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10} :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\subsection*{E. Step 4: remote spectral gap}

Let the remote block admit the decomposition
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+E_R(p),
\]
and define
\[
\delta_0(p):=\min_a |(D_R)_{aa}(p)|,
\qquad
\eta_R(p):=\|E_R(p)\|.
\]
Then the pointwise and uniform remote-gap theorems imply:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing
\quad\forall |p|\le \rho,
}
\label{eq:uniform_gap_theorem}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\label{eq:uniform_gap_value_theorem}
\end{equation}
Alternatively, if an unperturbed realization has gap \(\Delta_0>0\) and the Class II correction obeys
\[
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|<\Delta_0,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta=\Delta_0-\sup\|\delta H_R\|>0.
}
\label{eq:perturbative_gap_theorem}
\end{equation}
If in addition Step 3 holds, i.e.
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad \|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
then the Schur complement correction is
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=O(|p|^2/\Delta),
\]
so the remote sector affects the local Dirac block only at subleading order.
Thus the remote-gap problem is fully reduced to a finite Bloch-spectral inequality / bounded perturbation audit.
Again, the concrete Class II ansatz is gap-compatible, but does not by itself prove \(\Delta>0\). :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12} :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13} :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14}

\subsection*{F. Step 5: mass protection}

For the isolated doubled local Dirac block
\begin{equation}
H_D(q)=\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i),
\qquad i=1,2,3,
\label{eq:HD_mass_theorem}
\end{equation}
the constant mass space is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\}.
}
\label{eq:mass_space_theorem}
\end{equation}
Thus the finite mass-protection criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}
\Longrightarrow
\text{mass protection}.
}
\label{eq:mass_protection_finite_theorem}
\end{equation}
A sufficient mechanism is exact residual valley symmetry
\[
Q_V=\rho_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_V(\theta)=e^{i\theta Q_V},
\]
or already its \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) remnant generated by
\[
S_V=\rho_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Under either symmetry, both mass generators in \(\mathcal M\) are forbidden, hence
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}.
\]
The concrete Class II ansatz is compatible with this, but does not itself prove that the full microscopic realization preserves the needed residual symmetry. :contentReference[oaicite:15]{index=15} :contentReference[oaicite:16]{index=16} :contentReference[oaicite:17]{index=17}

\subsection*{G. Local Dirac Closure Theorem}

We now combine Steps 1--5.

\begin{theorem}[Local Dirac Closure Theorem in the concrete Class II setting]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Class II witness realization:}
the concrete shell-adapted Class II tensor family is realized on the selected local shell pair, with
\[
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0);
\]

\item \textbf{opposite-valley witness matching:}
in the matched opposite-valley frame,
\[
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+);
\]

\item \textbf{zero constant mixing:}
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\qquad
V(0)=0;
\]

\item \textbf{remote spectral gap:}
either
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\]
for some shell neighborhood, or there exists an already-gapped realization with sufficiently small Class II correction, so that
\[
\Delta>0;
\]

\item \textbf{mass protection:}
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}
=
\{0\}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then the full microscopic TECT truncation contains an isolated local massless Dirac block
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(q)
=
\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i)
+
O(|q|^2/\Delta),
\]
i.e. an actual stable local Dirac cone.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
By Step 1, the local Class II truncation produces a nondegenerate Weyl symbol at one valley.
By Step 2, the opposite valley carries the same witness triple in the matched frame, so the two valleys pair into a local doubled Dirac block.
By Step 3, no constant hybridization with the remote sector is allowed at the crossing.
By Step 4, the remote block remains spectrally separated by a positive gap \(\Delta>0\), so the Schur-complement correction is only \(O(|q|^2/\Delta)\).
By Step 5, no symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass exists on the isolated doubled shell block.
Therefore the resulting local Dirac cone is both spectrally isolated and massless.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{H. Honest final status}

The theorem above is the strongest currently honest closure statement for the local Dirac sector.

What is already closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the reduction of the full local fermion problem to the finite five-step audit above;
\item the full theorem-level logic of Steps 1--5 inside the concrete Class II framework.
\end{enumerate}

What is not yet unconditionally closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item that the \emph{actual} complete microscopic TECT action realizes the required Class II witness carrier sector;
\item that the \emph{actual} remote microscopic sector satisfies the irrep mismatch needed for \(V(0)=0\);
\item that the \emph{actual} remote block satisfies the Bloch-spectral gap inequality;
\item that the \emph{actual} residual symmetry algebra forbids all constant masses.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the precise final status is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the local Dirac problem is fully reduced to a finite conditional closure theorem in the concrete Class II setting.}
}
\label{eq:local_Dirac_final_status}
\end{equation}
It is not yet a fully unconditional microscopic theorem for the complete TECT action.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Local Dirac Closure Theorem in the concrete Class II setting}
}
\]

Step 1:
\[
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,\qquad (g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0)
}
\]
gives actual local Weyl nondegeneracy.

Step 2:
\[
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+)
}
\]
gives opposite-valley pairing into a local doubled Dirac block.

Step 3:
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0
}
\]
removes constant hybridization with the remote sector.

Step 4:
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0
}
\]
(or perturbative stability from an already-gapped realization)
gives remote spectral isolation and
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma(E,p)=O(|p|^2/\Delta).
}
\]

Step 5:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\},
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M=\{0\}
}
\]
gives mass protection.

Therefore, if the concrete Class II setting satisfies the five finite inputs above, then the full microscopic truncation contains an isolated local massless Dirac cone:
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(q)
=
\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i)
+
O(|q|^2/\Delta).
}
\]

Honest final status:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the local Dirac problem is fully reduced to a finite conditional closure theorem,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the complete microscopic TECT realization of the required Class II carrier, gap, and residual symmetry is still an independent verification problem.}
}
\]

\section*{TECT Partial Closure Theorem: Local Dirac closure + IR isotropy conditional closure}

\subsection*{A. Global setting}

The present TECT program has two logically distinct but coupled low-energy frontiers:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the \emph{local fermionic frontier}: existence of an actual stable massless local Dirac cone;
\item the \emph{infrared bosonic frontier}: decay of sectoral derivative anisotropies and infrared velocity locking.
\end{enumerate}

The current theorem-level status is that both frontiers have been reduced to finite conditional verification problems.

\subsection*{B. Local Dirac closure input}

Let \(\mathcal H_D\) denote the isolated doubled shell block, and \(\mathcal H_R\) the remote sector.
The local Dirac closure in the concrete Class II setting is reduced to the following finite input list:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{actual Class II witness carrier realization:} the microscopic TECT defect/background realizes a nontrivial shell-relevant Class II sector;

\item \textbf{local Weyl witness nonvanishing:}
\begin{equation}
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0);
\label{eq:dirac_input1}
\end{equation}

\item \textbf{opposite-valley witness matching:}
\begin{equation}
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+);
\label{eq:dirac_input2}
\end{equation}

\item \textbf{zero constant mixing:}
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0;
\label{eq:dirac_input3}
\end{equation}

\item \textbf{remote spectral gap:}
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0;
\label{eq:dirac_input4}
\end{equation}

\item \textbf{mass protection:}
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\cap
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}
=
\{0\}.
\label{eq:dirac_input5}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

If these conditions hold, then the local fermionic sector contains an isolated massless local Dirac cone
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(q)
=
\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i)
+
O(|q|^2/\Delta).
\label{eq:local_dirac_conclusion}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the strongest currently honest local Dirac closure theorem in the concrete Class II setting.

\subsection*{C. Infrared isotropy closure input}

Let
\[
u=(\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D)^T
\]
denote the physical derivative-anisotropy variables constrained by
\begin{equation}
2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0.
\label{eq:traceless_constraint}
\end{equation}
Let
\[
\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\{u\in\mathbb R^3:\ 2\delta_T+2\delta_O+2\delta_D=0\}
\]
be the traceless physical anisotropy subspace.

The loop-level flow is
\begin{equation}
\partial_t u = M_Z u + O(u^2).
\label{eq:MZ_flow_partial}
\end{equation}

Decompose
\begin{equation}
M_Z
=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})}
+
M_Z^{(OD)}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}.
\label{eq:MZ_decomp_partial}
\end{equation}
Define
\begin{equation}
M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}
=
M_Z^{(\tau)}
+
M_Z^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{self})},
\qquad
M_Z^{\mathrm{bad}}
=
M_Z^{(OD)}
+
M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}.
\label{eq:good_bad_partial}
\end{equation}

Assume the following explicit bounds:

\paragraph{Good-part coercive negativity}
\begin{equation}
\langle u,M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}u\rangle
\le
-\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\|u\|^2
\qquad
\forall u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>0.
\label{eq:good_neg_partial}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Bad-part norm bounds}
\begin{equation}
\|M_Z^{(OD)}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|
\le
\eta_{OD},
\qquad
\|M_Z^{(\mathrm{gf/proj})}|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}}\|
\le
\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
\label{eq:bad_bounds_partial}
\end{equation}

Then the explicit sufficient IR-isotropy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
}
\label{eq:IR_master_cond_partial}
\end{equation}
Indeed, for all \(u\in\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}\),
\begin{align}
\langle u,M_Zu\rangle
&=
\langle u,M_Z^{\mathrm{good}}u\rangle
+
\langle u,M_Z^{\mathrm{bad}}u\rangle
\nonumber\\
&\le
-\mu_{\mathrm{good}}\|u\|^2
+
(\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}})\|u\|^2
\nonumber\\
&=
-(\mu_{\mathrm{good}}-\eta_{OD}-\eta_{\mathrm{gf}})\|u\|^2.
\label{eq:MZ_negativity_partial}
\end{align}
Hence \eqref{eq:IR_master_cond_partial} implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(M_Z|_{\mathcal U_{\mathrm{tr}}})\subset(-\infty,0),
}
\label{eq:MZ_spectrum_neg_partial}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D\to 0
\quad\text{in the infrared.}
}
\label{eq:IR_isotropy_conclusion}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{D. TECT Partial Closure Theorem}

We can now combine the local Dirac closure and the IR-isotropy closure.

\begin{theorem}[TECT Partial Closure Theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{local Dirac closure inputs:}
the finite local Dirac conditions \eqref{eq:dirac_input1}--\eqref{eq:dirac_input5} hold in the concrete Class II setting;

\item \textbf{gauge-consistent soft sector:}
the projected \(A\)-sector satisfies
\begin{equation}
p^\mu\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mu\nu}=0,
\qquad
m_{A,k}^2\to 0,
\qquad
\text{gauge-preserving regulator},
\qquad
\text{Class I/II only};
\label{eq:gauge_partial_inputs}
\end{equation}

\item \textbf{IR-isotropy input:}
the explicit inequality \eqref{eq:IR_master_cond_partial} holds:
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the microscopic TECT truncation contains an isolated local massless Dirac cone;
\item the physical derivative-anisotropy variables decay under the infrared flow:
\[
\delta_T,\delta_O,\delta_D\to 0;
\]
\item the low-energy soft sector is infrared-isotropic and velocity-locked.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
By the local Dirac closure theorem, the finite witness/pairing/mixing/gap/mass-protection conditions imply the existence of an isolated massless local Dirac cone.
By the gauge-consistency assumptions, the projected \(A\)-sector contribution to the flow is physically meaningful.
By the explicit good-vs-bad inequality \eqref{eq:IR_master_cond_partial}, the linearized anisotropy matrix \(M_Z\) has strictly negative spectrum on the physical traceless subspace.
Hence the derivative anisotropies decay in the infrared.
Therefore TECT admits both an isolated local massless Dirac cone and an infrared-isotropic soft sector.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{E. Exact logical status}

The theorem above is the strongest currently honest whole-system closure statement.

\paragraph{What is already theorem-level closed.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item the reduction of the local Dirac problem to a finite five-step audit;
\item quartic anisotropy irrelevance for \(N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6\):
\[
\theta_\tau=-\frac{\epsilon}{7}<0;
\]
\item the reduction of the derivative-anisotropy problem to the sign of \(M_Z\);
\item the explicit sufficient IR-isotropy criterion
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{What is not yet unconditionally closed.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item that the actual complete microscopic TECT action realizes the required Class II witness carrier;
\item that the actual microscopic remote sector satisfies the label/irrep audit for \(V(0)=0\);
\item that the actual microscopic remote block satisfies the gap inequality;
\item that the actual residual symmetry excludes constant masses;
\item that the actual background-adapted FRG data satisfy
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{good}}>\eta_{OD}+\eta_{\mathrm{gf}}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Thus the exact current status is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{TECT is not yet fully unconditionally closed,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{it is fully reduced to a finite partial closure theorem whose remaining inputs are explicit microscopic verification tasks.}
}
\label{eq:TECT_partial_status}
\end{equation}

\section*{Actual microscopic witness carrier audit}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

The remaining microscopic question after the concrete Class II witness theorem is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the true complete TECT action actually realize a nontrivial Class II sector in the physically relevant defect background?}
}
\label{eq:carrier_audit_goal}
\end{equation}

Inside the concrete Class II truncation, the witness problem is already closed:
once one longitudinal seed and one transverse seed exist, local Weyl nondegeneracy is generic in the allowed Class II tensor space. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5} :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

Therefore the remaining task is not to re-prove the witness theorem, but to audit whether the full microscopic TECT linearization actually contains the required carrier sector.

\subsection*{2. What the witness actually needs}

The shell-level Weyl/Dirac witness is controlled by the enriched microscopic tensor
\[
N^a_{ij},
\]
through the shell-adapted contractions
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta,
\qquad
\det M=(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3A(B^2+C^2).
\]
The minimal shell-adapted tensor family is
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:min_shell_tensor_family_audit}
\end{equation}
Hence the witness requires a microscopic object carrying simultaneously:
\begin{enumerate}
\item one spatial derivative index \(i\) or \(j\),
\item one reduced internal / shell-tangent index \(a\).
\end{enumerate}
This is explicitly identified in the embedding/classification discussion. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection*{3. Minimal UV classification}

The microscopic classification theorem states that any minimal local UV extension producing a nonzero shell/projector mixing source must effectively introduce an \((i,a)\)-carrier.
At lowest derivative order, the minimal viable classes are:
\begin{enumerate}
\item Class I: direct shell--projector derivative couplings,
\item Class II: heavy auxiliary internal vector mediator \(X_i^a\),
\item Class III: connection-like mediator \(A_i^a\).
\end{enumerate}
Among them, the most natural minimal UV extension is Class II. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

Therefore the actual carrier audit reduces to:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the microscopic TECT linearization contain an effective shell-relevant \((i,a)\)-carrier channel?}
}
\label{eq:ia_carrier_question}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Explicit Class II mechanism}

The explicit Class II quadratic source is generated by
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha X_i^a(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi+\mathrm{h.c.})
+
\beta X_i^a\partial_i\delta P^a\,\psi.
\label{eq:ClassII_UV_audit}
\end{equation}
Around the locked background, eliminating \(X_i^a\) produces schematically
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}
\sim
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]\,\partial_i\xi^a,
\label{eq:ClassII_mix_audit}
\end{equation}
which after shell reduction gives precisely the target quadratic mixing form
\[
(\partial_i\phi_0)(\partial_j\psi)\,\xi^a,
\]
hence a nonzero induced correction
\[
\delta N^a_{ij}\neq 0.
\]
This is the first mathematically consistent route to a derived nonzero shell-enriched tensor correction from projector-sector physics. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

So the audit target is no longer vague: one must verify that the actual microscopic TECT linearization contains or effectively induces this same \((i,a)\)-carrier channel.

\subsection*{5. Embedding criterion for the explicit seed subspace}

The explicit witness seed subspace
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\{N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)},N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,E)},N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,O)}\}
\]
is not an arbitrary effective ansatz.
The embedding statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{If the true microscopic transport space contains an allowed \((i,a)\)-carrier sector, then the explicit seed subspace can be embedded into the symmetry-allowed transport space.}
}
\label{eq:seed_embedding_criterion}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the carrier audit is successful if the symmetry-allowed microscopic transport space contains at least:
\begin{enumerate}
\item one longitudinal shell-adapted seed direction;
\item one transverse shell-adapted seed direction.
\end{enumerate}
Then the concrete Class II witness theorem applies and local Weyl nondegeneracy is generic in that sector. :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11} :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12}

\subsection*{6. Operational audit checklist}

The actual microscopic carrier audit is therefore:

\paragraph{(A) Linearize the microscopic TECT equation}
around the physically relevant defect background and isolate all terms linear in fluctuations and first order in worldvolume derivatives.

\paragraph{(B) Extract the shell-relevant transport operator}
in the form
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
\]
The odd transport kernel generated by the defect background is already known to arise naturally from the microscopic projector-gradient term:
\[
V^\mu(\xi)\sim (\partial_\xi P_B)T^\mu,
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

\paragraph{(C) Determine whether the projected overlap matrices}
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle
\]
span a nontrivial traceless Hermitian sector.
At the effective level, this is exactly what generates the mixed Dirac symbol. :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14}

\paragraph{(D) Match the induced shell tensor}
to the shell-adapted axial basis
\[
(A,B,C)
\leftrightarrow
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]
If at least one longitudinal and one transverse component survive, then the seed criterion is satisfied.

\paragraph{(E) Compute the projection test}
\[
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\]
or equivalently produce one explicit admissible seed tensor for each required channel.
This is the finite operational completion criterion already stated in the roadmap. :contentReference[oaicite:15]{index=15} :contentReference[oaicite:16]{index=16}

\subsection*{7. Strongest honest conclusion}

Thus the actual microscopic witness carrier audit is now completely reduced to the following finite statement:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the carrier audit succeeds iff the full microscopic TECT linearization contains a shell-relevant nontrivial \((i,a)\)-carrier sector whose projection onto the axial shell basis has at least one longitudinal and one transverse seed component.}
}
\label{eq:carrier_audit_success}
\end{equation}

This is not yet an unconditional theorem for the complete TECT action, because the actual projection test has not yet been carried out in the final microscopic linearization.
But it is no longer conceptually open:
it is an explicit finite projection / seed-embedding audit.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual microscopic witness carrier audit}
}
\]

The witness needs a shell-relevant enriched tensor
\[
N^a_{ij},
\]
so the microscopic theory must effectively contain an object with both:
\[
\boxed{
\text{one spatial derivative index }(i \text{ or } j),
\qquad

}

The minimal shell-adapted tensor family is

\boxed{
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
}

The minimal UV classes capable of producing such a carrier are:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class I, Class II, Class III,}

with Class II the most natural minimal mediated completion.

The explicit Class II route introduces a heavy auxiliary internal vector mediator

L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}\sim (\partial_i\phi_0)(\partial_j\psi)\,\xi^a
\Longrightarrow

Therefore the real microscopic audit is:

\boxed{
\text{Does the full microscopic TECT linearization contain an effective shell-relevant nontrivial }(i,a)\text{-carrier sector?}
}

Operationally, this reduces to:

1. linearize the microscopic TECT equation around the relevant defect background;

2. extract the first-order transport kernel
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu};

3. project it to the low-mode sector

(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle;

4. match the induced shell tensor to the axial basis
\[
(A,B,C)\leftrightarrow (\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta);

5. verify that at least one longitudinal and one transverse seed survive.

So the strongest honest conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual microscopic witness carrier problem is fully reduced to a finite projection / seed-embedding audit.}
}
