\section*{Projection test \texorpdfstring{$P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0$}{PV T(alpha) != 0} in concrete carrier-audit language}

\subsection*{1. Abstract tensor-space formulation}

Let
\[
W=\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the ambient shell-enriched tensor space, and let
\[
V\subset W
\]
be the finite-dimensional real vector space of all symmetry-allowed microscopic enriched tensors surviving the microscopic TECT linearization around the condensed defect background.

For each shell-Dirac channel \(\alpha=1,2\), define the shell contraction
\begin{equation}
L_\alpha(N)=\langle T^{(\alpha)},N\rangle,
\label{eq:Lalpha_projection_audit}
\end{equation}
where \(T^{(\alpha)}\) is the target covector built from the selected shell direction, transverse frame, and internal reduced mode.
The exact dichotomy is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_\alpha|_V\equiv 0
\iff
P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0.
}
\label{eq:PV_exact_dichotomy}
\end{equation}
Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0
\Longrightarrow
\text{the channel is symmetry-forbidden},
}
\label{eq:PV_forbidden}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{the channel is generically nonvanishing on an open dense full-measure subset of }V.
}
\label{eq:PV_generic}
\end{equation}
This is the exact practical criterion stated in the finite witness reduction. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection*{2. Carrier-audit reinterpretation}

The abstract condition \(P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0\) has the following concrete meaning:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual microscopic TECT linearization contains at least one shell-relevant admissible transport direction whose projection onto channel }\alpha\text{ is nonzero.}
}
\label{eq:carrier_reinterp}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the carrier audit succeeds in channel \(\alpha\) iff the symmetry-allowed microscopic transport space \(V\) contains at least one tensor
\[
N^{(\alpha)}\in V
\]
such that
\[
L_\alpha(N^{(\alpha)})\neq 0.
\]

Thus \(P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0\) is not merely a formal projection statement:
it is the statement that the true microscopic theory actually realizes a nontrivial seed in the corresponding shell-relevant carrier direction.

\subsection*{3. Stronger practical sufficient condition: explicit seed test}

A stronger practical sufficient condition is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists\ N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\alpha)}\in V
\quad\text{such that}\quad
\langle T^{(\alpha)},N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\alpha)}\rangle\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:explicit_seed_test}
\end{equation}
Then automatically
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:explicit_seed_implies_projection}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the seed/witness test stated in the witness-reduction notes. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

So the actual microscopic carrier audit has two equivalent operational routes:

\paragraph{Route A: direct projection route}
\begin{enumerate}
\item determine the residual symmetry group \(H\);
\item determine the allowed tensor space \(V\subset W\);
\item compute the orthogonal projection \(P_VT^{(\alpha)}\).
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Route B: explicit seed route}
\begin{enumerate}
\item determine the residual symmetry group \(H\);
\item determine the allowed tensor space \(V\subset W\);
\item construct one explicit admissible tensor \(N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\alpha)}\in V\);
\item check that \(\langle T^{(\alpha)},N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\alpha)}\rangle\neq 0\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{4. Concrete Class II seed subspace}

Inside the concrete Class II ansatz, the explicit seed directions are already known:

\begin{equation}
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
:\quad
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\label{eq:seed_long_audit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
:\quad
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:seed_even_audit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
:\quad
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:seed_odd_audit}
\end{equation}

For
\[
N
=
c_\parallel N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
+
c_E N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
+
c_O N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
\]
the reduced witnesses are exactly
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:seed_witness_eval_audit}
\end{equation}
Since
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
the symbol is nondegenerate iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:seed_nondeg_audit}
\end{equation}
Thus inside the concrete Class II ansatz space, the finite witness problem is already exactly closed. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection*{5. What remains open microscopically}

Because the Class II seed subspace is explicit, the remaining question is no longer “do such seeds exist abstractly?”
Instead it is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the complete microscopic TECT transport space actually contain }
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\{N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\}
\text{, or at least its required longitudinal/transverse seed directions?}
}
\label{eq:real_open_seed_embedding}
\end{equation}
This is explicitly identified as the remaining frontier. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

\subsection*{6. Sharp carrier-audit completion criterion}

Therefore the actual microscopic carrier audit can now be stated sharply:

\begin{theorem}[Carrier-audit completion criterion]
Let \(V\subset W\) be the symmetry-allowed microscopic transport space obtained from the full TECT linearization around the relevant defect background.
Then the witness carrier audit succeeds iff either of the following equivalent conditions holds:

\begin{enumerate}
\item for each required shell channel \(\alpha\),
\[
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0;
\]

\item \(V\) contains at least one admissible longitudinal seed and at least one admissible transverse seed with nonzero overlap against the corresponding target covectors.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

In particular, because the explicit Class II seed subspace already realizes the required longitudinal and transverse overlaps, the remaining microscopic task is exactly:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{prove that the full microscopic TECT transport space contains }V_{\mathrm{seed}}
\text{, or at least one longitudinal and one transverse seed direction from it.}
}
\label{eq:carrier_audit_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Strongest honest conclusion}

Thus the strongest honest conclusion is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
}
\end{equation}
means:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual microscopic TECT linearization contains a shell-relevant nontrivial carrier direction in channel }\alpha.
}
\end{equation}

So the remaining carrier problem is no longer an infinite-dimensional PDE mystery.
It is an explicit finite projection / seed-embedding audit on the symmetry-allowed microscopic transport space.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
L_\alpha(N)=\langle T^{(\alpha)},N\rangle,
\qquad
L_\alpha|_V\equiv 0
\iff
P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0.
}
\]

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0
\Longrightarrow
\text{channel }\alpha\text{ is symmetry-forbidden,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{channel }\alpha\text{ is generically nonvanishing on }V.
}
\]

In concrete carrier-audit language,
\[
\boxed{
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\iff
\text{the full microscopic TECT transport space contains at least one shell-relevant admissible carrier direction with nonzero overlap in channel }\alpha.
}
\]

A stronger practical sufficient condition is:
\[
\boxed{
\exists N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\alpha)}\in V
\text{ such that }
\langle T^{(\alpha)},N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\alpha)}\rangle\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0.
}
\]

Inside the concrete Class II ansatz, explicit seeds already exist:
\[
\boxed{
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},\qquad
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},\qquad
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}.
}
\]
They satisfy
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
}
\]
so the witness problem is already exactly closed inside that ansatz.

Therefore the actual remaining microscopic question is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the complete microscopic TECT transport space contain }
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
\text{, or at least one longitudinal and one transverse seed direction from it?}
}
\]

So the carrier audit is fully reduced to a finite projection / seed-embedding test.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Minimal practical sufficient condition for actual microscopic carrier survival}

\subsection*{1. Ambient formulation}

Let
\[
W=\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the ambient enriched tensor space, and let
\[
V_{\mathrm{micro}}\subset W
\]
be the actual symmetry-allowed transport tensor space extracted from the full microscopic TECT linearization around the relevant defect background.

For each shell channel \(\alpha\), define the shell witness functional
\[
L_\alpha(N)=\langle T^{(\alpha)},N\rangle.
\]
Then the exact dichotomy is:
\[
P_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}T^{(\alpha)}=0
\iff
L_\alpha|_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}\equiv 0,
\]
and
\[
P_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}T^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\iff
L_\alpha \text{ is generically nonzero on }V_{\mathrm{micro}}.
\]

\subsection*{2. Strong practical sufficient condition}

A stronger sufficient condition is the existence of one explicit admissible seed:
\[
\exists\,N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\alpha)}\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\quad\text{such that}\quad
\langle T^{(\alpha)},N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\alpha)}\rangle\neq 0.
\]
Then automatically
\[
P_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}T^{(\alpha)}\neq 0.
\]

Therefore the actual carrier audit succeeds if one can exhibit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one longitudinal seed \(N_\parallel\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}\) with
\[
\langle T^{(\parallel)},N_\parallel\rangle\neq 0;
\]

\item one transverse seed \(N_\perp\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}\) with
\[
\langle T^{(\perp)},N_\perp\rangle\neq 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{3. Minimal practical sufficient condition}

Hence the minimal practical sufficient condition for actual microscopic carrier survival is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists\,N_\parallel,N_\perp\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\text{ such that }
\langle T^{(\parallel)},N_\parallel\rangle\neq 0,
\qquad
\langle T^{(\perp)},N_\perp\rangle\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:min_practical_carrier_survival}
\end{equation}

This immediately implies
\[
P_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}T^{(\parallel)}\neq 0,
\qquad
P_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}T^{(\perp)}\neq 0,
\]
hence the witness channels survive generically.

\subsection*{4. Relation to the concrete Class II seed space}

Inside the concrete Class II ansatz, the explicit seed subspace is already known:
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\{N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\}.
\]
Therefore a still sharper practical sufficient condition is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\mathrm{seed}}\cap V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\text{ contains at least one nonzero longitudinal seed and at least one nonzero transverse seed.}
}
\label{eq:seed_embedding_practical}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, it is enough to prove
\[
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{micro}},
\qquad
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\]
or
\[
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{micro}},
\qquad
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}.
\]

\subsection*{5. Strongest honest practical conclusion}

Thus the remaining microscopic carrier problem does not require proving the full Class II completion first.
A much weaker and sufficient condition already closes the witness-carrier question:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{actual microscopic carrier survival is proved once one longitudinal and one transverse admissible seed survive in the true microscopic transport space.}
}
\label{eq:practical_conclusion_carrier}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Minimal practical sufficient condition for actual microscopic carrier survival}
}
\]

Let \(V_{\mathrm{micro}}\) be the true symmetry-allowed microscopic transport space.

It is sufficient to find:

\[
\boxed{
\exists\,N_\parallel\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\text{ such that }
\langle T^{(\parallel)},N_\parallel\rangle\neq 0,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\exists\,N_\perp\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\text{ such that }
\langle T^{(\perp)},N_\perp\rangle\neq 0.
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
P_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}T^{(\parallel)}\neq 0,
\qquad
P_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}T^{(\perp)}\neq 0,
}
\]
so the longitudinal and transverse witness channels both survive generically.

Since the concrete Class II ansatz already provides explicit seeds
\[
\boxed{
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
\qquad
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
\qquad
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
}
\]
an even sharper sufficient condition is simply:

\[
\boxed{
V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\text{ contains at least one longitudinal seed direction and at least one transverse seed direction from }V_{\mathrm{seed}}.
}
\]

So the practical carrier audit reduces to a finite seed-embedding check, not a full PDE proof.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Microscopic extraction protocol for \texorpdfstring{$V_{\mathrm{micro}}$}{V_micro}}

\subsection*{1. Purpose}

The remaining microscopic witness-carrier problem is no longer:
\[
\text{``solve the full PDE exactly''}.
\]
It is the finite extraction problem:
\[
\text{determine the actual symmetry-allowed microscopic transport space }V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\]
from the full TECT linearization around the relevant defect background, and test whether it contains one longitudinal and one transverse seed direction. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6} :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\subsection*{2. Step 0: choose the defect background}

Fix a physically relevant static defect projector background
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi),
\qquad
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi),
\label{eq:PB_protocol}
\end{equation}
depending only on the transverse coordinate \(\xi\).

Its tangent bundle is
\begin{equation}
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\dim_\mathbb C Q_B=2.
\label{eq:QB_protocol}
\end{equation}
Thus the fluctuation field on the defect core is a complex doublet.
This is the natural microscopic origin of the low-mode internal \(2\)-component sector. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection*{3. Step 1: linearize the microscopic TECT equation}

Start from the microscopic condensate equation linearized around the condensed background,
\begin{equation}
i\partial_t \Phi = L(-i\nabla)\Phi.
\label{eq:Lmicro_protocol}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in projector form one has the linearized fluctuation equation
\begin{equation}
\rho \partial_t^2 \delta P
-
C_{ij}\partial_i\partial_j \delta P
+
H_B^{\mathrm{stat}}\delta P
+
T(\delta P)=0,
\label{eq:linearized_projector_protocol}
\end{equation}
where the first-order transport term comes from derivatives acting on the background projector as well as on the fluctuation. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

\subsection*{4. Step 2: isolate the first-order transport kernel}

Expanding derivatives on \(P_B+\delta P\) yields the first-order transport term
\begin{equation}
T(\delta P)
=
-C_{ij}\Big[(\partial_i P_B)\partial_j\delta P+(\partial_j P_B)\partial_i\delta P\Big].
\label{eq:TdeltaP_protocol}
\end{equation}
Writing derivatives along the defect worldvolume as
\[
y^\mu=(t,x_1,x_2),
\]
this takes the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
}
\label{eq:L1_protocol}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)\sim (\partial_\xi P_B)T^\mu.
\label{eq:Vmu_protocol}
\end{equation}
Because \(P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi)\), one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
}
\label{eq:Vmu_odd_protocol}
\end{equation}
Thus the microscopic TECT linearization naturally supplies the odd transport kernel required in the reduced Dirac framework. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

\subsection*{5. Step 3: construct the low-mode sector}

Solve the static transverse operator on the defect core
\begin{equation}
H_B=-\partial_\xi^2+U_B(\xi)
\label{eq:HB_protocol}
\end{equation}
on the rank-two bundle \(Q_B\), and extract its low even/odd modes
\[
u_a^+(\xi),\qquad u_b^-(\xi),
\qquad a,b=1,2.
\]
This is the isolated graded \(2+2\) sector required by the reduced Dirac theorem. :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\subsection*{6. Step 4: project the transport kernel}

Compute the projected overlap matrices
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle
=
\int d\xi\,
(u_a^+)^\dagger V^\mu(\xi)u_b^-.
}
\label{eq:Mmu_protocol}
\end{equation}
Since
\[
u_a^+(\xi)\ \text{is even},\qquad
u_b^-(\xi)\ \text{is odd},\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)\ \text{is odd},
\]
the integrand is even, so the overlap is generically nonzero. This is the direct microscopic origin of the mixed first-order symbol. :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12}

At this point, one may already regard the span of the projected matrices \(M^\mu\) as the effective extracted transport space.

\subsection*{7. Step 5: choose the selected shell pair and project to the valley block}

Fix a selected shell vector \(G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\) and write
\[
k=G_*+p,
\qquad
p=p_\parallel \hat n + p_1 e_1 + p_2 e_2,
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\]
Assume the microscopic symbol admits the Taylor expansion
\begin{equation}
L(G_*+p)=L_*+p_i K_i+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L(k)\big|_{k=G_*}.
\label{eq:Ki_protocol}
\end{equation}
Let \(P_*\) denote the orthogonal projector onto the selected low-energy \(2\)-dimensional valley block \(H_*\).
Then the reduced first-order Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)=P_*\,(p_iK_i)\,P_*\big|_{H_*}.
\label{eq:hlin_protocol}
\end{equation}
Since \(h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)\) is Hermitian \(2\times 2\), define the Pauli-resolved coefficient matrix
\begin{equation}
M_{\mu i}
=
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}_{H_*}\bigl(\sigma_\mu P_*K_iP_*\bigr),
\qquad
\mu=1,2,3.
\label{eq:Mmui_protocol}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)=M_{\mu i}p_i\sigma_\mu.
\]
Thus the local Weyl data are determined directly by the projected first derivatives \(K_i\). :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

\subsection*{8. Step 6: extract the witness coefficients}

Choose the adapted shell frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\).
Then the concrete shell witnesses are read as the coefficients of
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{wit}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel(\hat n\cdot p)\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:Hwit_protocol}
\end{equation}
Equivalently:
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel = M_{3,\parallel},
\qquad
\alpha = \text{coefficient of }(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2),
\qquad
\beta = \text{coefficient of }(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:lambdabeta_protocol}
\end{equation}

Now define the actual microscopic transport tensor space \(V_{\mathrm{micro}}\) to be the finite-dimensional real span of all shell-relevant microscopic tensors contributing to these projected coefficients.

Then the witness carrier audit reduces to the finite test:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{find one admissible longitudinal seed with }\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\quad
\text{and one admissible transverse seed with }(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:final_micro_protocol_test}
\end{equation}
By the finite witness theorem, this is enough to guarantee generic nondegeneracy on an open dense full-measure subset of \(V_{\mathrm{micro}}\). :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14} :contentReference[oaicite:15]{index=15}

\subsection*{9. Practical yes/no outputs of the protocol}

The extraction protocol produces exactly four logically distinct outputs:

\paragraph{(O1) Carrier survival}
Do we obtain at least one longitudinal and one transverse seed direction?
If yes, the microscopic witness carrier survives.

\paragraph{(O2) Valley witness}
Do the resulting coefficients satisfy
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)?
\]
If yes, the selected valley is Weyl.

\paragraph{(O3) Opposite-valley matching}
Repeat the same extraction at \(-G_*\) and check matched-frame equality of the witness triple.

\paragraph{(O4) Data for later audits}
The same extraction provides the actual low-energy block and projected operators needed for:
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad \Delta>0,\qquad \text{mass protection},
\qquad M_Z.
\]

\subsection*{10. Strongest honest conclusion}

Thus the microscopic extraction protocol for \(V_{\mathrm{micro}}\) is now completely explicit:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_B(\xi)
\ \Longrightarrow\
V^\mu(\xi)
\ \Longrightarrow\
u_a^\pm
\ \Longrightarrow\
(M^\mu)_{ab}
\ \Longrightarrow\
P_*K_iP_*
\ \Longrightarrow\
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\ \Longrightarrow\
\text{actual witness carrier audit}.
}
\label{eq:protocol_chain_final}
\end{equation}

No further conceptual ambiguity remains.
What remains is the actual evaluation of these projections in the chosen microscopic TECT linearization.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Microscopic extraction protocol for }V_{\mathrm{micro}}
}
\]

1. Fix a defect background
\[
\boxed{
P_B(\xi),\qquad P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi).
}
\]

2. Linearize the microscopic TECT equation around it:
\[
\boxed{
i\partial_t\Phi=L(-i\nabla)\Phi.
}
\]

3. Extract the first-order transport term
\[
\boxed{
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)\sim (\partial_\xi P_B)T^\mu,
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
}
\]

4. Solve the static transverse defect operator and obtain the even/odd low modes
\[
\boxed{
u_a^+,\qquad u_b^-.
}
\]

5. Compute the projected overlap matrices
\[
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
}
\]

6. At a selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\), compute the projected first derivatives
\[
\boxed{
M_{\mu i}
=
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}_{H_*}\bigl(\sigma_\mu P_*K_iP_*\bigr).
}
\]

7. Read off the witness coefficients
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
}
\]
from the adapted shell Hamiltonian
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{wit}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel(\hat n\cdot p)\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\]

Then the actual microscopic carrier audit is reduced to the finite test:
\[
\boxed{
\text{find one admissible longitudinal seed with }\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\quad
\text{and one admissible transverse seed with }(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

So:
\[
\boxed{
P_B
\to
V^\mu
\to
u^\pm
\to
(M^\mu)_{ab}
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
}
\]
is the full microscopic extraction chain for the actual witness carrier problem.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Minimal explicit toy extraction of the microscopic carrier}

\subsection*{1. Reflection-symmetric defect background}

Take the explicit CP\(^2\)-type defect representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\qquad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:toy_zB}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi),
\label{eq:toy_PB}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi),
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1 z_B^\dagger+z_B e_1^\dagger\bigr).
\label{eq:toy_dPB}
\end{equation}
Hence every leading transport kernel linear in the defect gradient factors through \(\theta'(\xi)\). :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\subsection*{2. Explicit \(Q_B\)-frame}

A convenient even orthonormal frame of
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp
\]
is
\begin{equation}
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:toy_frame}
\end{equation}
Both are reflection-even because \(\theta(\xi)\) is even. :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12}

\subsection*{3. Explicit even/odd low modes}

Choose the concrete even/odd defect profiles
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:toy_fpm}
\end{equation}
Then define
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:toy_upm}
\end{equation}
These are not merely trial functions:
they are exact zero modes of the explicit graded defect operator
\[
L_0=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_+ & 0\\
0 & H_-
\end{pmatrix}\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
with
\[
H_+=-\partial_\xi^2+\kappa^2-2\kappa^2\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
H_-=-\partial_\xi^2+\kappa^2-6\kappa^2\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi).
\]
Thus the \(2+2\) graded low-energy carrier is explicit. :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13} :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14}

\subsection*{4. Odd transport kernel}

Take the leading worldvolume transport kernel in factorized form
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\Sigma^\mu,
\label{eq:toy_Vmu}
\end{equation}
where \(\Sigma^\mu\) is a constant Hermitian \(2\times 2\) matrix acting on the local \(Q_B\)-doublet.
Because \(\theta(\xi)\) is even,
\begin{equation}
\theta'(-\xi)=-\theta'(\xi),
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
\label{eq:toy_odd_V}
\end{equation}
Hence same-parity overlaps vanish, while mixed overlaps are allowed. :contentReference[oaicite:15]{index=15} :contentReference[oaicite:16]{index=16}

\subsection*{5. Mixed overlap integral}

The projected mixed overlap matrices are
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}
d\xi\,
(u_a^+)^\dagger V^\mu(\xi)u_b^-.
\label{eq:toy_Mmu_def}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:toy_upm} and \eqref{eq:toy_Vmu},
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)\,
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma^\mu\,
e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:toy_Mmu_expand}
\end{equation}
If \(\Sigma^\mu\) is constant in the chosen \(Q_B\)-frame, then
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
I_\theta\,\Sigma^\mu,
\qquad
I_\theta:=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}
d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi).
\label{eq:toy_Mmu_factor}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Explicit evaluation of \(I_\theta\)}

Using
\[
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(\xi)=-\theta_0\kappa\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi)\tanh(\kappa\xi),
\]
together with \eqref{eq:toy_fpm},
we have
\begin{align}
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)
&=
\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}
\,
\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi)\,
\tanh(\kappa\xi)\,
\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi)\,
\bigl(-\theta_0\kappa\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi)\tanh(\kappa\xi)\bigr)
\nonumber\\
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\kappa}{2}\,\theta_0\kappa\,
\mathrm{sech}^3(\kappa\xi)\tanh^2(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:toy_integrand}
\end{align}
Thus
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0\kappa^2}{2}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}
d\xi\,
\mathrm{sech}^3(\kappa\xi)\tanh^2(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:Itheta_precalc}
\end{equation}
Set \(x=\kappa\xi\). Then
\[
d\xi=\frac{dx}{\kappa},
\]
so
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0\kappa}{2}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}
dx\,
\mathrm{sech}^3 x\,\tanh^2 x.
\label{eq:Itheta_x}
\end{equation}
Using
\[
\tanh^2x=1-\mathrm{sech}^2x,
\]
we get
\begin{equation}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}\mathrm{sech}^3x\,\tanh^2x\,dx
=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}\mathrm{sech}^3x\,dx
-
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}\mathrm{sech}^5x\,dx
=
\frac{\pi}{2}-\frac{3\pi}{8}
=
\frac{\pi}{8}.
\label{eq:sech_integral}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:Itheta_final_toy}
\end{equation}
This matches the explicit formula already recorded in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:17]{index=17}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
I_\theta\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Itheta_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Explicit projected symbol}

It follows that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu=I_\theta\,\Sigma^\mu.
}
\label{eq:Mmu_final_toy}
\end{equation}
Hence the reduced principal symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
I_\theta\,p_\mu \Sigma^\mu.
\label{eq:A1_toy}
\end{equation}
If one chooses
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^1=v_1\sigma_1,
\qquad
\Sigma^2=v_2\sigma_2,
\qquad
\Sigma^3=v_3\sigma_3,
\qquad
v_i\neq 0,
\label{eq:Sigma_choice_toy}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
I_\theta\,(v_1p_1\sigma_1+v_2p_2\sigma_2+v_3p_3\sigma_3),
\label{eq:A1_explicit_toy}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\det A_1(p)
=
-\,I_\theta^2\,
\bigl(v_1^2p_1^2+v_2^2p_2^2+v_3^2p_3^2\bigr).
\label{eq:detA1_toy}
\end{equation}
So for generic \(p\neq 0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det A_1(p)\neq 0
\qquad
\text{provided}
\qquad
I_\theta\neq 0,\quad v_1v_2v_3\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:nondeg_toy}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the explicit minimal effective Dirac realization described in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:18]{index=18} :contentReference[oaicite:19]{index=19}

\subsection*{8. Carrier-audit interpretation}

The toy extraction proves the following.

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the microscopic extraction chain }
P_B
\to
V^\mu
\to
u^\pm
\to
M^\mu
\to
A_1(p)
\text{ can be carried out explicitly in a concrete defect model.}
}
\label{eq:toy_chain_conclusion}
\end{equation}

What it proves:
\begin{enumerate}
\item an explicit reflection-symmetric defect background exists;
\item an explicit \(2+2\) graded low-mode carrier exists;
\item the odd transport kernel arises naturally from \(\partial_\xi P_B\);
\item the mixed overlap integral is explicitly nonzero:
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\neq 0;
\]
\item with a full-rank \(\Sigma^\mu\), the projected symbol is Dirac.
\end{enumerate}

What it does \emph{not} prove:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{that the full complete microscopic TECT defect linearization is literally identical to this toy model.}
}
\label{eq:toy_not_full}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the honest limitation stated in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:20]{index=20} :contentReference[oaicite:21]{index=21}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Minimal explicit toy extraction}
}
\]

Take the reflection-symmetric defect background
\[
\boxed{
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
}
\]
and the even \(Q_B\)-frame
\[
\boxed{
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

Choose explicit even/odd low modes
\[
\boxed{
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
u_a^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_a(\xi).
}
\]

Take the odd transport kernel
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\Sigma^\mu,
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
}
\]

Then the projected mixed overlap is
\[
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi)
=
I_\theta\,(\Sigma^\mu)_{ab},
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\theta'
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
I_\theta\neq 0.
}
\]

Therefore the reduced symbol is
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu=I_\theta\,p_\mu\Sigma^\mu.
}
\]

If
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma^1=v_1\sigma_1,\qquad
\Sigma^2=v_2\sigma_2,\qquad
\Sigma^3=v_3\sigma_3,
\qquad
v_1v_2v_3\neq 0,
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\det A_1(p)
=
-\,I_\theta^2\,
\bigl(v_1^2p_1^2+v_2^2p_2^2+v_3^2p_3^2\bigr)\neq 0
\quad
\text{for generic }p\neq 0.
}
\]

So the toy model explicitly realizes:
\[
\boxed{
P_B
\to
V^\mu
\to
u^\pm
\to
M^\mu
\to
A_1(p)
\sim p_i\sigma_i.
}
\]

This proves explicit realizability of the projected Dirac mechanism, but not yet its necessity in the full microscopic TECT PDE.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Direct matching of the toy extraction to the S2 witness branch}

\subsection*{1. S2 witness branch}

The natural local symmetry-compatible branch is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:S2_branch_match}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det\Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:Lambda_match}
\end{equation}
Thus S2 nondegeneracy is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:S2_nondeg_match}
\end{equation}
This is the exact local branch already derived in the witness analysis. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection*{2. Toy extracted symbol}

From the explicit toy extraction one obtains
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}=I_\theta(\Sigma^\mu)_{ab},
\qquad
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:toy_Mmu_match}
\end{equation}
Hence the projected first-order symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1^{\mathrm{toy}}(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
I_\theta\,p_\mu \Sigma^\mu.
\label{eq:A1_toy_match}
\end{equation}

To compare with the S2 branch, choose the adapted shell/worldvolume frame
\[
p=(p_1,p_2,p_\parallel),
\]
and write the constant \(2\times 2\) matrices in the form
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^1=g_E\sigma_1-g_O\sigma_2,
\qquad
\Sigma^2=g_O\sigma_1+g_E\sigma_2,
\qquad
\Sigma^\parallel=g_c^{(\mathrm{toy})}\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Sigma_S2_choice_match}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{align}
A_1^{\mathrm{toy}}(p)
&=
I_\theta\Big[
p_1(g_E\sigma_1-g_O\sigma_2)
+
p_2(g_O\sigma_1+g_E\sigma_2)
+
p_\parallel g_c^{(\mathrm{toy})}\sigma_3
\Big]
\nonumber\\
&=
I_\theta\Big[
g_c^{(\mathrm{toy})}p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
g_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
g_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\Big].
\label{eq:A1_toy_S2_match}
\end{align}

Therefore the toy-extracted S2 coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{toy}}=I_\theta\,g_c^{(\mathrm{toy})},
\qquad
\alpha^{\mathrm{toy}}=I_\theta\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{toy}}=I_\theta\,g_O.
}
\label{eq:toy_coeffs_match}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{3. Comparison with the concrete Class II local formula}

For the concrete local Class II transport ansatz, the exact projected witnesses are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
}
\label{eq:exact_local_ClassII_match}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:Itheta_I3_match}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

Comparing \eqref{eq:toy_coeffs_match} with \eqref{eq:exact_local_ClassII_match}, one finds:

\paragraph{Transverse match.}
The transverse coefficients agree exactly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{toy}}=\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{toy}}=\beta=g_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:transverse_exact_match}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Longitudinal mismatch in origin.}
The longitudinal coefficient in the exact Class II transport is not of \(I_\theta\)-type.
Instead it is generated by the primitive commutator channel
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\]
which produces the transport seed
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
hence the witness
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
So the exact longitudinal sector lives in a distinct primitive channel. 

\subsection*{4. Interpretation}

The toy extraction therefore proves the following.

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The odd-gradient toy kernel already realizes the full transverse S2 witness sector }(\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:toy_proves_transverse}
\end{equation}

However:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the longitudinal witness } \lambda_\parallel
\text{ requires an additional primitive } \sigma_3\text{-type channel,}
}
\label{eq:toy_needs_longitudinal}
\end{equation}
namely the commutator-square channel of the concrete Class II transport action.

Thus the toy model is not the full local Class II transport kernel.
It is precisely the transverse part of it.

\subsection*{5. Strongest honest consequence}

Combining the toy extraction and the exact local Class II formulas, the strongest honest conclusion is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item The transverse witness carrier is explicitly realized:
\[
(\alpha,\beta)=(g_EI_\theta,g_OI_\theta),
\qquad
I_\theta\neq 0.
\]

\item The longitudinal witness requires a stronger primitive shell channel:
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

\item Therefore the full S2 nondegeneracy condition is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq(0,0),
}
\label{eq:full_S2_condition_match}
\end{equation}
but the toy extraction directly proves only the second part, i.e. the survival of the transverse sector.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{6. Practical consequence for the carrier audit}

The actual microscopic carrier audit is now sharply split into two subaudits:

\paragraph{(A) Transverse carrier audit.}
Verify that the full microscopic transport kernel contains the odd-gradient channel whose low-mode projection produces
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
\]

\paragraph{(B) Longitudinal carrier audit.}
Verify that the full microscopic transport kernel contains the primitive commutator-square channel whose low-mode projection produces
\[
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

Thus the toy model already solves half of the microscopic witness-carrier problem explicitly: the transverse half.
What remains is the explicit microscopic realization of the longitudinal primitive channel.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Direct matching of toy extraction to the S2 witness branch}
}
\]

The S2 branch is
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\det\Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
}
\]

From the toy extraction,
\[
\boxed{
M^\mu=I_\theta\,\Sigma^\mu,
\qquad
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

Choosing
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma^1=g_E\sigma_1-g_O\sigma_2,\qquad
\Sigma^2=g_O\sigma_1+g_E\sigma_2,\qquad
\Sigma^\parallel=g_c^{(\mathrm{toy})}\sigma_3,
}
\]
gives
\[
\boxed{
A_1^{\mathrm{toy}}(p)
=
I_\theta\Big[
g_c^{(\mathrm{toy})}p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
g_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
g_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\Big].
}
\]

Hence the toy coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{toy}}=I_\theta g_c^{(\mathrm{toy})},
\qquad
\alpha^{\mathrm{toy}}=I_\theta g_E,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{toy}}=I_\theta g_O.
}
\]

The exact local Class II coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\alpha,\beta\text{ match exactly between the toy extraction and the exact local Class II formula.}
}
\]

But:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\text{ does \emph{not} come from the toy }I_\theta\text{-channel;}
\text{ it comes from the distinct primitive }I_{\theta'^3}\text{-channel.}
}
\]

So the toy extraction explicitly proves the transverse S2 witness sector, while the longitudinal witness still requires the primitive commutator-square transport channel.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Actual microscopic carrier audit: transverse solved, longitudinal remaining}

\subsection*{1. The minimal witness criterion}

The full local Weyl/Dirac witness problem is reduced to the existence of:
\begin{enumerate}
\item one admissible longitudinal witness,
\item one admissible transverse witness.
\end{enumerate}
Equivalently, in the shell-adapted S2 branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:minimal_witness_criterion_finalaudit}
\end{equation}
This is the exact finite witness reduction of the local Weyl problem. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5} :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection*{2. Concrete explicit seed space}

Inside the concrete Class II seed subspace
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\Bigl\{
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
\Bigr\},
\]
the projected witnesses are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:seed_witness_coeffs_finalaudit}
\end{equation}
Therefore the reduced S2 symbol is nondegenerate iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:seed_nondeg_finalaudit}
\end{equation}
This means that inside the concrete ansatz space itself, the finite witness problem is already exactly closed. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection*{3. Explicit transverse solution}

The explicit transverse-even seed is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:perp_even_seed_finalaudit}
\end{equation}
for which
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=0,
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=0.
\label{eq:perp_even_witness_finalaudit}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
T_\perp=
\begin{pmatrix}
I_\theta & 0\\
0 & I_\theta
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det T_\perp=I_\theta^2>0.
\label{eq:perp_even_det_finalaudit}
\end{equation}
So an explicit transverse witness already exists. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

Likewise, the optional transverse-odd seed
\[
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\]
gives
\[
\lambda_\parallel=0,\qquad \alpha=0,\qquad \beta=I_\theta\neq 0,
\]
so the transverse channel is doubly realizable. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

Thus the transverse half of the carrier audit is already explicitly solved:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\quad\text{is explicitly realizable.}
}
\label{eq:transverse_solved_finalaudit}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Explicit longitudinal requirement}

The explicit longitudinal seed is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\label{eq:long_seed_finalaudit}
\end{equation}
for which
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=0,
\qquad
\beta=0.
\label{eq:long_seed_witness_finalaudit}
\end{equation}
Since \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\), an explicit longitudinal witness exists \emph{inside the concrete seed space}. :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

However, unlike the transverse toy extraction built directly from the odd-gradient channel \(\theta'(\xi)\Sigma^\mu\), the longitudinal witness requires the distinct primitive channel
\[
\theta'(\xi)^3\,\sigma_3.
\]
Therefore the actual remaining microscopic question is no longer whether a longitudinal witness can exist in principle, but whether the full microscopic TECT linearization actually generates this primitive channel in the physically relevant defect background.

Equivalently:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the unresolved microscopic carrier question is precisely the survival of the longitudinal primitive channel.}
}
\label{eq:long_remaining_finalaudit}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Embedding statement}

The embedding theorem already proves that if the true microscopic TECT transport sector contains one of the minimal viable UV classes (Class I or Class II), then there exists a three-dimensional microscopic tensor subspace
\[
V_{\mathrm{mic}}^{(3)}\subset V_{\mathrm{mic}}
\]
whose reduced defect/projector image is isomorphic to
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}.
\]
Equivalently, the longitudinal seed witness and the transverse seed doublet can both be realized by admissible microscopic transport tensors. :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12}

Therefore the remaining question is not abstract compatibility.
It is the concrete yes/no question:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{does the full complete microscopic TECT action actually realize Class I or Class II in the relevant defect background?}
}
\label{eq:embedding_yesno_finalaudit}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Strongest honest carrier-audit theorem}

We can now state the sharpest honest result.

\begin{theorem}[Actual microscopic carrier audit: transverse solved, longitudinal remaining]
Assume the relevant defect background admits the explicit odd-gradient transport extraction described earlier, so that the transverse seed channel produces a nonzero overlap
\[
I_\theta\neq 0.
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the transverse witness carrier survives explicitly in the true microscopic transport extraction;
\item hence the transverse nondegeneracy condition
\[
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\]
is no longer the open part of the carrier problem;
\item the only remaining microscopic carrier question is whether the full TECT linearization contains the primitive longitudinal seed channel producing
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
Therefore the full witness-carrier audit is reduced to one residual yes/no question:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the physically relevant microscopic TECT linearization realize a nonzero longitudinal primitive channel?}
}
\]
\end{theorem}

\subsection*{7. Honest final status}

Thus the exact logical status is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the carrier problem is no longer “three channels open”; it is “transverse solved, longitudinal remaining”.}
}
\label{eq:carrier_status_finalaudit}
\end{equation}
This is a substantial strengthening of the previous frontier statement, because the surviving open part is now only one primitive shell-relevant channel rather than the whole witness tensor problem.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual microscopic carrier audit: transverse solved, longitudinal remaining}
}
\]

The full local witness criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Inside the explicit seed space,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\]

Explicit transverse seed:
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
}
\]
gives
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=0,\qquad \alpha=I_\theta,\qquad \beta=0,
\qquad
\det T_\perp=I_\theta^2>0.
}
\]

Explicit longitudinal seed:
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
}
\]
gives
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta=0.
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the transverse witness carrier is explicitly solved,}
}
\]
because the odd-gradient extraction already realizes \(I_\theta\neq 0\);

while

\[
\boxed{
\text{the only remaining microscopic carrier question is the survival of the longitudinal primitive channel }
\theta'^3\sigma_3.
}
\]

So the witness-carrier frontier is now reduced to one residual yes/no question:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the full microscopic TECT linearization realize a nonzero longitudinal primitive channel?}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Microscopic origin of the longitudinal primitive channel \texorpdfstring{$\theta'^3\sigma_3$}{theta'^3 sigma_3}}

\subsection*{1. What still remains open}

The current carrier-audit status is:

\[
\text{transverse solved, longitudinal remaining.}
\]

Inside the explicit seed space one already has
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
\label{eq:long_remain_start}
\end{equation}
with
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]
So the unresolved microscopic question is not whether a longitudinal witness can exist in principle, but:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{what is the natural microscopic origin of the primitive longitudinal seed }
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3?
}
\label{eq:long_origin_question}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Primitive longitudinal seed already identified in the explicit seed space}

The explicit longitudinal seed recorded in the concrete Class II construction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
:=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:explicit_long_seed_origin}
\end{equation}
Its projected witnesses are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha=0,
\qquad
\beta=0.
\label{eq:explicit_long_seed_witness}
\end{equation}
So the only remaining issue is microscopic survival of the operator
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\subsection*{3. Geometric interpretation of the channel}

Let \(P_B(\xi)\) be the reflection-symmetric defect projector background, and
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp
\]
its rank-two tangent bundle.
The first-order transport kernel is already known to arise from the defect gradient:
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)\sim (\partial_\xi P_B)\,T^\mu,
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
\]
This generates the transverse odd-gradient channel. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

To obtain a longitudinal witness, one needs a \(\sigma_3\)-type traceless operator on the internal \(Q_B\)-doublet.
The natural source is the \emph{quadratic transverse response} of the defect geometry in the \(Q_B\)-sector:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi:\Gamma(Q_B)\to \Gamma(Q_B),
\qquad
\mathcal T_\xi^2:\Gamma(Q_B)\to \Gamma(Q_B).
\label{eq:Txi_def}
\end{equation}
Projecting to \(Q_B\) and removing the scalar part gives
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
-
\frac12
\mathrm{Tr}_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q\bigr)\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:Txi2_tr}
\end{equation}

This is the unique lowest-order internal traceless scalar compatible with the shell-adapted longitudinal channel.

\subsection*{4. Why \(\sigma_3\) appears naturally}

In the explicit defect frame
\[
Q_B=\mathrm{span}_\mathbb C\{e_1,e_2\},
\]
the two tangent directions are not geometrically equivalent:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(e_1\) is the direction directly tied to the defect bending through \(\partial_\xi z_B=\theta' e_1\),
\item \(e_2\) is the orthogonal internal spectator direction.
\end{itemize}

Therefore the quadratic response operator \(\mathcal T_\xi^2\) need not act isotropically on \((e_1,e_2)\).
Its traceless part naturally distinguishes the two directions, and in the adapted frame this distinction is represented by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
\propto \sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:sigma3_natural}
\end{equation}

For the explicit seed construction, the proportionality is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Txi2_sigma3_exact}
\end{equation}
Then multiplying by the already-present odd defect gradient factor gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:theta3sigma3_exact}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the primitive longitudinal seed.
:contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection*{5. Parity and why this channel is allowed}

For a reflection-symmetric defect,
\[
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(-\xi)=-\theta'(\xi).
\]
Hence
\[
\theta'(\xi)^2
\quad\text{is even},
\qquad
\theta'(\xi)^3
\quad\text{is odd}.
\]
Therefore:
\begin{itemize}
\item \((\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\sim \theta'^2\sigma_3\) is an even internal operator,
\item multiplying by \(\theta'(\xi)\) makes the full transport kernel odd.
\end{itemize}
Thus the mixed overlap with even/odd low modes is parity-allowed:
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)\ \text{even},
\qquad
u_b^-(\xi)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)\ \text{odd}
\Longrightarrow
(u_a^+)^\dagger V^\mu_{(\parallel)}u_b^-
\ \text{is even}.
\label{eq:parity_allowed_long}
\end{equation}
So the primitive longitudinal channel is not only symmetry-compatible; it is exactly of the parity type required to survive the low-mode projection.

\subsection*{6. Projected witness coefficient}

With
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
the projected mixed symbol produces
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
\label{eq:lambda_from_long}
\end{equation}
The explicit defect calculation gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\neq 0
}
\label{eq:Itheta3_nonzero_exact}
\end{equation}
for nontrivial defect amplitude \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\). :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
}
\label{eq:lambda_nonzero_long}
\end{equation}
provided the primitive channel actually survives in the full microscopic transport extraction.

\subsection*{7. Strongest honest microscopic statement}

Therefore the sharpest honest microscopic statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the longitudinal primitive channel is geometrically natural if the defect }Q_B\text{-sector has a non-isotropic quadratic response whose traceless part survives as }(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\propto \sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:sharpest_long_statement}
\end{equation}

In that case, the odd defect gradient automatically upgrades it to the transport seed
\[
\frac12\,\theta'^3 n^\mu \sigma_3,
\]
which yields \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\).

So the remaining carrier question is not “invent a mysterious extra term,” but the much sharper audit:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{does the full microscopic TECT linearization produce a nonzero traceless quadratic }Q_B\text{-response channel?}
}
\label{eq:final_long_audit_question}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{8. Honest final status}

What is already effectively established:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the transverse odd-gradient channel is explicitly realized;
\item the longitudinal primitive seed has an explicit geometrically natural form;
\item its projected coefficient is explicitly nonzero once the channel survives.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual survival of }(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
\text{ in the full microscopic TECT transport extraction.}
}
\label{eq:open_long_survival}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire microscopic witness-carrier frontier is now reduced to one residual yes/no question about one primitive longitudinal channel.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Microscopic origin of the longitudinal primitive channel}
}
\]

The explicit longitudinal seed is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\]

So the primitive microscopic ingredient is
\[
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
}
\]

In the adapted \(Q_B\)-frame, the defect-bending direction \(e_1\) and the spectator direction \(e_2\) are not equivalent, so the quadratic \(Q_B\)-response need not be isotropic.
Its traceless part naturally takes the form
\[
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
\propto \sigma_3.
}
\]

For the explicit seed construction,
\[
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
}
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\sigma_3.
}
\]

This produces the longitudinal witness
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\neq 0.
}
\]

Therefore the remaining microscopic question is sharply reduced to:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the full microscopic TECT linearization produce a nonzero traceless quadratic }Q_B\text{-response channel }(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}?
}
\]

So the carrier frontier is now:
\[
\boxed{
\text{transverse explicit, longitudinal reduced to one primitive yes/no channel.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Minimal sufficient condition for survival of the longitudinal primitive channel}

\subsection*{1. The remaining microscopic question}

The carrier-audit status is now:

\[
\text{transverse solved, longitudinal remaining.}
\]

Inside the explicit seed space one has
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:long_cond_start}
\end{equation}
Hence the only residual microscopic question is whether the full microscopic TECT linearization actually realizes the longitudinal seed direction.

\subsection*{2. Primitive longitudinal seed}

The explicit longitudinal seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu.
}
\label{eq:Vlong_minimal}
\end{equation}
In the explicit representative used in the seed construction,
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3,
\label{eq:Txi2_tr_explicit}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Vlong_explicit}
\end{equation}
Projecting to the even/odd low modes gives
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
\label{eq:lambda_long_projection}
\end{equation}
Since
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0),
\label{eq:Itheta3_nonzero_longcond}
\end{equation}
the longitudinal witness is nonzero whenever the primitive channel survives. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection*{3. Minimal sufficient condition: operator form}

Therefore the weakest natural sufficient condition is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:min_suff_operator}
\end{equation}

This implies that the microscopic transport extraction contains a nonzero longitudinal primitive seed, hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:lambda_nonzero_from_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Geometric sufficient criterion}

A more geometric sufficient condition is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the quadratic }Q_B\text{-response is anisotropic in the adapted defect frame }(e_1,e_2),
}
\label{eq:geom_suff1}
\end{equation}
meaning that the two internal directions are not eigen-equivalent at quadratic order, so that
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
\neq
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}_{Q_B}(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)\,\mathbf 1_2.
\]
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:geom_suff2}
\end{equation}

If this anisotropic traceless quadratic response is aligned with the shell axis through the factor \(n^\mu\), then the odd defect gradient upgrades it to the first-order transport kernel \eqref{eq:Vlong_minimal}, and the parity structure guarantees that the even/odd low-mode overlap is allowed.

So the geometric content of the sufficient condition is simply:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{non-isotropic quadratic }Q_B\text{-response} + \text{odd defect gradient} + \text{nonzero low-mode overlap}
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:geom_suff_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Practical finite test}

Hence the actual microscopic longitudinal audit can be implemented as the finite three-step test:

\paragraph{(L1)}
Compute the projected quadratic response
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q.
\]

\paragraph{(L2)}
Remove the scalar part and check whether the traceless part vanishes:
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
\stackrel{?}{=} 0.
\]

\paragraph{(L3)}
If it is nonzero, compute the one-dimensional overlap
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
}
\label{eq:Jparallel_def}
\]
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:Jparallel_nonzero}
\end{equation}
then the longitudinal primitive channel survives and
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\subsection*{6. Strongest honest conclusion}

Therefore the sharpest minimal sufficient condition for longitudinal primitive survival is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
J_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:final_min_suff_long}
\end{equation}

This is much weaker than proving the full Class II completion.
It is only a finite operator-and-overlap check.

Inside the explicit seed representative, this condition is satisfied automatically because
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\qquad
J_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]
So the open frontier is not conceptual.
It is the verification that the full microscopic TECT linearization obeys this same finite condition.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Minimal sufficient condition for survival of the longitudinal primitive channel}
}
\]

The primitive longitudinal seed is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu.
}
\]

Therefore a minimal sufficient condition for longitudinal survival is:

\[
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
\neq 0.
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

In the explicit seed representative,
\[
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3,
}
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
J_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
}
\]

Hence the remaining microscopic frontier is reduced to one finite test:

\[
\boxed{
\text{does the full microscopic TECT linearization produce a nonzero traceless quadratic }Q_B\text{-response whose low-mode overlap }J_\parallel\text{ is nonzero?}
}
\]

This is the weakest practical sufficient condition for closing the longitudinal half of the witness-carrier audit.

\section*{Dirac closure status update: transverse fixed, longitudinal reduced to one finite test}

\subsection*{1. Previous frontier formulation}

Previously, the local Dirac closure theorem required the following carrier-level microscopic input:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the full microscopic TECT transport space must contain one admissible longitudinal witness direction and one admissible transverse witness direction.}
}
\label{eq:old_carrier_frontier}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the local S2 witness criterion required
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:S2_old_frontier}
\end{equation}

At that stage, both the longitudinal and transverse halves of the witness-carrier problem appeared open.

\subsection*{2. Explicit transverse resolution}

Inside the explicit seed space, one has
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:seed_coeffs_update}
\end{equation}
An explicit transverse-even seed exists:
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:transverse_seed_update}
\end{equation}
for which
\[
\lambda_\parallel=0,\qquad \alpha=I_\theta,\qquad \beta=0.
\]
Likewise an explicit transverse-odd seed exists:
\[
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel=0,\qquad \alpha=0,\qquad \beta=I_\theta.
\]

Moreover, the explicit toy extraction evaluates
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\neq 0
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0).
}
\label{eq:Itheta_update}
\end{equation}
Hence the transverse witness channel is no longer hypothetical:
it is explicitly realized.

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\quad\text{is already explicitly solved at the carrier level.}
}
\label{eq:transverse_solved_update}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{3. Longitudinal primitive channel}

The explicit longitudinal seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu.
}
\label{eq:Vparallel_update}
\end{equation}
In the explicit seed representative,
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\label{eq:T2tr_update}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Vparallel_explicit_update}
\end{equation}
Projecting to the graded low modes gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_update}
\end{equation}

Thus the longitudinal channel is also explicitly realizable \emph{inside the seed representative}.
What remains open is more specific:
whether the full microscopic TECT transport extraction actually preserves this primitive channel.

\subsection*{4. Minimal remaining longitudinal test}

The weakest practical sufficient condition for longitudinal survival is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
J_\parallel\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:remaining_long_test}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel
:=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
}
\label{eq:Jparallel_update}
\end{equation}
If \eqref{eq:remaining_long_test} holds, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:remaining_long_test_implies}
\end{equation}

So the longitudinal half of the witness-carrier problem has been reduced to one primitive finite operator-and-overlap test.

\subsection*{5. Updated carrier-audit status}

Combining Sections 2--4 gives the sharpest updated statement:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the carrier audit is no longer “transverse + longitudinal open”.}
}
\label{eq:not_both_open}
\end{equation}

Instead:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{transverse carrier survival is explicitly solved,}
}
\label{eq:transverse_fixed_update}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the only remaining carrier question is the survival of the primitive longitudinal channel.}
}
\label{eq:long_only_remaining_update}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the entire microscopic carrier frontier is reduced to the single finite yes/no test \eqref{eq:remaining_long_test}.

\subsection*{6. Updated local Dirac closure theorem}

The local Dirac closure theorem may therefore be sharpened as follows:

\begin{theorem}[Updated local Dirac closure status]
At the carrier level, the concrete Class II local Dirac closure problem is reduced to:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{already fixed:} transverse witness survival,
\[
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\]
via the explicit odd-gradient extraction with \(I_\theta\neq 0\);

\item \textbf{remaining finite test:} longitudinal primitive survival,
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
J_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Hence the carrier portion of the local Dirac theorem is now reduced to one residual primitive yes/no test rather than a full open tensor-space audit.
\end{theorem}

\subsection*{7. Honest final status}

Thus the strongest honest status update is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Local Dirac closure is substantially sharper than before:}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{carrier problem }=
\text{transverse fixed}
+
\text{one remaining longitudinal primitive test}.
}
\label{eq:final_status_update}
\end{equation}

This is a real closure improvement, because one entire half of the previous carrier frontier has already been explicitly settled.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Dirac closure status update}
}
\]

Previously, the witness-carrier frontier looked like:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad

with both halves apparently open.

Inside the explicit seed space:

\qquad

\boxed{
