\section*{Updated Local Dirac Closure Theorem: transverse fixed, longitudinal one-test remaining}

\subsection*{1. Original local Dirac closure structure}

The local Dirac closure problem was reduced to five finite ingredients:

\begin{enumerate}
\item actual microscopic witness-carrier realization,
\item opposite-valley witness matching,
\item zero constant mixing \(V(0)=0\),
\item remote spectral gap \(\Delta>0\),
\item mass protection.
\end{enumerate}

Previously, Step 1 was still phrased as the existence of both:
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]
So the carrier problem looked like a two-sided open problem.

\subsection*{2. Updated carrier status}

Inside the explicit seed space, the S2 witness coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:updated_seed_coeffs}
\end{equation}

The transverse channel is already explicitly realized by the odd-gradient extraction, since
\begin{equation}
I_\theta\neq 0
\label{eq:Itheta_nonzero_updated}
\end{equation}
for a nontrivial defect profile. Therefore explicit admissible transverse seeds exist with
\begin{equation}
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:transverse_fixed}
\end{equation}

Hence the transverse half of the carrier problem is no longer open.

The only remaining microscopic carrier issue is the longitudinal primitive channel
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu,
\label{eq:long_primitive_updated}
\end{equation}
together with the overlap test
\begin{equation}
J_\parallel
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\label{eq:Jparallel_updated}
\end{equation}
A minimal sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
J_\parallel\neq 0,
\label{eq:min_long_test_updated}
\end{equation}
which implies
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\label{eq:lambda_nonzero_updated}
\end{equation}

Therefore Step 1 is now sharpened from
\[
\text{two-channel open carrier problem}
\]
to
\[
\text{transverse fixed + one remaining longitudinal primitive test}.
\]

\subsection*{3. Updated theorem statement}

We now restate the local Dirac closure theorem in its sharpened form.

\begin{theorem}[Updated Local Dirac Closure Theorem]
Assume the following.

\paragraph{(S1) Carrier input: updated form.}
The transverse witness carrier is already present, i.e.
\begin{equation}
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\label{eq:S1_transverse}
\end{equation}
is explicitly realized by the microscopic odd-gradient transport extraction.

In addition, the longitudinal primitive test succeeds:
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
J_\parallel\neq 0,
\label{eq:S1_longitudinal}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\label{eq:S1_lambda}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(S2) Opposite-valley witness matching.}
In the matched opposite-valley frame,
\begin{equation}
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+).
\label{eq:S2_pairing}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(S3) Zero constant mixing.}
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
\label{eq:S3_zero_mixing}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(S4) Remote spectral gap.}
There exists \(\Delta>0\) such that
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing
\label{eq:S4_gap}
\end{equation}
for the relevant low-momentum neighborhood, equivalently by a direct Bloch inequality or bounded-perturbation gap stability.

\paragraph{(S5) Mass protection.}
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\cap
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}
=
\{0\}.
\label{eq:S5_mass}
\end{equation}

Then the full microscopic truncation contains an isolated local massless Dirac cone
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(q)
=
\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i)
+
O(|q|^2/\Delta).
\label{eq:updated_dirac_conclusion}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\subsection*{4. Proof sketch}

\paragraph{Step A: Weyl nondegeneracy.}
By \eqref{eq:S1_transverse} and \eqref{eq:S1_lambda}, both parts of the S2 nondegeneracy condition hold:
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]
Hence the selected valley carries a nondegenerate local Weyl symbol.

\paragraph{Step B: doubling into Dirac.}
By \eqref{eq:S2_pairing}, the opposite valley carries the matched witness triple, so the two valleys pair into a local doubled Dirac block.

\paragraph{Step C: elimination of remote constant hybridization.}
By \eqref{eq:S3_zero_mixing}, no constant Dirac-remote intertwiner exists, so \(V(0)=0\).

\paragraph{Step D: spectral isolation.}
By \eqref{eq:S4_gap}, the remote sector remains gapped by \(\Delta>0\), and the Schur complement only contributes \(O(|q|^2/\Delta)\).

\paragraph{Step E: masslessness.}
By \eqref{eq:S5_mass}, no symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass is present on the isolated doubled block.

Hence the resulting local Dirac cone is spectrally isolated and massless.

\subsection*{5. Strongest honest status}

The sharpened theorem shows that the carrier frontier has improved substantially:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{old status: carrier problem = longitudinal + transverse both open;}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{new status: carrier problem = transverse fixed + one remaining longitudinal primitive test.}
}
\end{equation}

So the full local Dirac closure frontier is no longer spread across a broad witness-carrier ambiguity.
It is concentrated in one residual microscopic test:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
J_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:one_residual_test}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Exact logical status}

What is already effectively closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item transverse witness survival,
\item opposite-valley witness matching criterion,
\item zero-mixing criterion,
\item remote-gap criterion,
\item mass-protection criterion.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open microscopically:
\begin{enumerate}
\item actual survival of the longitudinal primitive channel,
\item the final microscopic audits behind Steps 3--5 in the full TECT realization.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the most accurate current statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the local Dirac problem is now reduced to a sharpened finite conditional theorem with only one residual primitive carrier test on the witness side.}
}
\label{eq:updated_status_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Updated Local Dirac Closure Theorem}
}
\]

The carrier part is no longer fully open.

Inside the explicit seed structure:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\]

Now:
\[
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\text{ is already explicitly fixed by the transverse odd-gradient extraction,}
}
\]
so the transverse half is solved.

The only remaining carrier test is:
\[
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
J_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
\neq 0,
}
\]
which implies
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

Therefore the updated local Dirac closure inputs are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(1) transverse fixed,}
\qquad
\text{(2) one remaining longitudinal primitive test,}
}
\]
together with
\[
\boxed{
\text{(3) opposite-valley matching,}
\quad
\text{(4) zero constant mixing,}
\quad
\text{(5) remote gap,}
\quad
\text{(6) mass protection.}
}
\]

If all of these hold, then
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(q)
=
\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i)+O(|q|^2/\Delta)
}
\]
is an isolated local massless Dirac cone.

So the new status is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{transverse fixed, longitudinal one-test remaining.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Explicit calculation protocol for \texorpdfstring{$(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}$}{(PiQ Txi^2 PiQ)tr} and \texorpdfstring{$J_\parallel$}{Jparallel}}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

The only remaining primitive carrier test on the witness side is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
J_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:goal_long_protocol}
\end{equation}

Here
\begin{equation}
J_\parallel
:=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\label{eq:Jparallel_goal_protocol}
\end{equation}

If \eqref{eq:goal_long_protocol} holds, then the longitudinal primitive channel survives and
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\subsection*{2. Input data}

Fix:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a reflection-symmetric defect background \(P_B(\xi)\);
\item the corresponding rank-two tangent bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp;
\]
\item a local orthonormal \(Q_B\)-frame
\[
e_1(\xi),\ e_2(\xi);
\]
\item the graded low-mode profiles
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad a=1,2.
\]
\end{enumerate}

The concrete toy representative already provides a natural choice of \(f_\pm\) and \(e_a\), but the protocol below is independent of the exact choice.

\subsection*{3. Step 1: define the microscopic transverse-response operator}

Let \(\mathcal T_\xi\) be the microscopic transverse-response operator induced by the linearized TECT dynamics on sections of \(Q_B\):
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi:\Gamma(Q_B)\to\Gamma(Q_B).
\label{eq:Txi_proto_def}
\end{equation}

Operationally, \(\mathcal T_\xi\) is the \(\xi\)-dependent \(Q_B\)-sector operator obtained after:

\begin{enumerate}
\item linearizing the microscopic TECT equation around \(P_B(\xi)\),
\item isolating the transverse/internal doublet sector,
\item restricting the resulting operator to the rank-two bundle \(Q_B\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{4. Step 2: compute the \(2\times 2\) matrix of \(\mathcal T_\xi\)}

In the local orthonormal frame \(\{e_1,e_2\}\), define
\begin{equation}
(T_\xi)_{ab}
:=
\langle e_a(\xi),\mathcal T_\xi e_b(\xi)\rangle,
\qquad
a,b=1,2.
\label{eq:Txi_matrix_proto}
\end{equation}
Thus \(T_\xi\) is an explicit \(2\times2\) Hermitian matrix-valued function of \(\xi\).

This is the first concrete output of the protocol.

\subsection*{5. Step 3: compute the quadratic response}

Now square the operator in the \(Q_B\)-frame:
\begin{equation}
T_\xi^{(2)}:=T_\xi^2.
\label{eq:T2_proto}
\end{equation}
Then extract the traceless part
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_\xi
:=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
T_\xi^2-\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(T_\xi^2)\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:Sxi_proto}
\end{equation}

The first yes/no test is now:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_\xi\stackrel{?}{\equiv}0.
}
\label{eq:first_yesno_proto}
\end{equation}

If \(S_\xi\equiv 0\), then the longitudinal primitive channel is absent.
If \(S_\xi\not\equiv 0\), continue.

\subsection*{6. Step 4: Pauli decomposition of the traceless part}

Any traceless Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrix can be written as
\begin{equation}
S_\xi=s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Pauli_decomp_proto}
\end{equation}
The longitudinal witness channel specifically cares about the \(\sigma_3\)-type component in the adapted frame, because the explicit primitive representative is
\[
S_\xi^{\mathrm{exp}}=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
\]

Therefore the second useful diagnostic is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)\stackrel{?}{\not\equiv}0.
}
\label{eq:s3_diag_proto}
\end{equation}

A sufficient condition for longitudinal survival is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
}
\label{eq:s3_sufficient_proto}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Step 5: form the primitive transport kernel}

Given \(S_\xi\), define the longitudinal primitive transport kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu.
}
\label{eq:Vlong_proto}
\end{equation}
Since \(\theta'(\xi)\) is odd for a reflection-symmetric defect and \(S_\xi\) is even whenever it is built from quadratic response data, \(V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)\) is odd, exactly as required for an even/odd low-mode coupling.

\subsection*{8. Step 6: compute the projected overlap}

The low-mode projected longitudinal overlap is
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu_{(\parallel)})_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
(u_a^+)^\dagger
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
u_b^-.
\label{eq:Mlong_proto}
\end{equation}
Using
\[
u_a^\pm=f_\pm e_a,
\]
this becomes
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu_{(\parallel)})_{ab}
=
n^\mu
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
S_{\xi,ab}.
\label{eq:Mlong_expanded_proto}
\end{equation}

The scalar channel of interest is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel
:=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
S_\xi.
}
\label{eq:Jparallel_matrix_proto}
\end{equation}
If one projects further onto the \(\sigma_3\) component, write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
:=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
s_3(\xi).
}
\label{eq:Jparallel3_proto}
\end{equation}

Then a sharp practical sufficient condition is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Jparallel3_nonzero_proto}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{9. Step 7: extract \(\lambda_\parallel\)}

The longitudinal witness coefficient is read off from the projected symbol:
\begin{equation}
A_{1,\parallel}(p)=\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3.
\label{eq:A1long_proto}
\end{equation}
In the explicit representative one has
\[
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\]
so
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\theta'^3
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\]
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_from_Jparallel_proto}
\end{equation}

More generally, the protocol says:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\quad\Longleftarrow\quad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:lambda_from_J_nonzero_proto}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{10. Minimal sufficient condition in algorithmic form}

The whole longitudinal audit reduces to the following finite algorithm.

\paragraph{Input}
\[
P_B(\xi),\quad e_a(\xi),\quad f_\pm(\xi),\quad \mathcal T_\xi.
\]

\paragraph{Algorithm}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Compute \(T_\xi\) from \eqref{eq:Txi_matrix_proto}.
\item Compute \(S_\xi\) from \eqref{eq:Sxi_proto}.
\item Check whether \(S_\xi\equiv 0\).
\item Decompose \(S_\xi=s_1\sigma_1+s_2\sigma_2+s_3\sigma_3\).
\item Compute \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\) from \eqref{eq:Jparallel3_proto}.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Output}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{longitudinal primitive carrier survives.}
}
\label{eq:algorithm_output_proto}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{11. Strongest honest conclusion}

Thus the explicit calculation protocol is now fully fixed.
The remaining microscopic longitudinal question is no longer vague at all:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute the }2\times2\text{ }Q_B\text{-sector matrix }T_\xi,\ \text{form }S_\xi,\ \text{and test whether }J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:strongest_conclusion_proto}
\end{equation}

This is a finite operator-and-overlap calculation, not an open-ended conceptual problem.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Explicit calculation protocol for }(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\text{ and }J_\parallel
}
\]

Given
\[
\boxed{
P_B(\xi),\quad Q_B(\xi),\quad e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi),\quad f_\pm(\xi),\quad \mathcal T_\xi,
}
\]
do the following:

1. Compute the \(2\times2\) \(Q_B\)-sector matrix
\[
\boxed{
(T_\xi)_{ab}=\langle e_a,\mathcal T_\xi e_b\rangle.
}
\]

2. Square it and remove the scalar part:
\[
\boxed{
S_\xi
=
T_\xi^2-\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(T_\xi^2)\mathbf 1_2
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
}
\]

3. Decompose
\[
\boxed{
S_\xi=s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
}
\]

4. Compute the longitudinal overlap
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
s_3(\xi).
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

So the remaining longitudinal primitive audit is reduced to one finite calculation:

\[
\boxed{
T_\xi
\to
S_\xi
\to
s_3(\xi)
\to
J_\parallel^{(3)}.
}
\]

If \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0\), the longitudinal primitive carrier survives.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Toy evaluation of the longitudinal primitive protocol}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

We apply the previously derived longitudinal primitive protocol to the explicit toy defect representative.

The protocol was:

\[
T_\xi
\ \longrightarrow\
S_\xi
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
\ \longrightarrow\
s_3(\xi)
\ \longrightarrow\
J_\parallel^{(3)}.
\]

The aim is to verify explicitly that
\[
S_\xi\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
\]

\subsection*{2. Defect data}

Use the explicit reflection-symmetric defect profile
\[
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\]
so that
\[
\theta'(\xi)
=
-\theta_0\kappa\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi)\tanh(\kappa\xi).
\]

Take the even/odd low-mode profiles
\[
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi).
\]

These are the same explicit low-mode profiles already used in the seed construction and toy extraction.

\subsection*{3. Correct longitudinal representative}

A naive attempt would be to model \(T_\xi\) itself as proportional to \(\theta'(\xi)\sigma_3\).
But then
\[
T_\xi^2\propto \theta'(\xi)^2\mathbf 1_2,
\]
so its traceless part would vanish.
Therefore the correct toy representative is not a model for \(T_\xi\) itself, but directly for the quadratic traceless response:
\[
\boxed{
S_\xi
:=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
}
\]

This is exactly the explicit longitudinal primitive seed already identified in the seed-space construction. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\subsection*{4. Pauli decomposition}

Write
\[
S_\xi=s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
\]
For the explicit representative above,
\[
\boxed{
s_1(\xi)=0,
\qquad
s_2(\xi)=0,
\qquad
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
}
\]

Hence
\[
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0
\]
whenever the defect is nontrivial, i.e. \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\).

\subsection*{5. Longitudinal overlap}

By definition,
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,s_3(\xi).
\]
Substituting \(s_3(\xi)=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\), we get
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\frac12
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

From the explicit evaluation already recorded in the notes,
\[
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

So for a nontrivial defect profile,
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\]

\subsection*{6. Consequence for the longitudinal witness}

The longitudinal projected symbol is
\[
A_{1,\parallel}(p)=\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3.
\]
In this toy representative the protocol gives
\[
\lambda_\parallel=J_\parallel^{(3)}=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\neq 0
}
\]
for \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\).

Thus the longitudinal primitive channel survives in the toy representative.

\subsection*{7. Interpretation}

The toy evaluation shows:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the longitudinal primitive protocol is computationally concrete;
\item the correct object to test is the traceless quadratic response \(S_\xi\), not a guessed linear \(T_\xi\);
\item in the explicit representative,
\[
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3
\]
is nonzero;
\item the weighted low-mode overlap
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}
\]
is nonzero;
\item therefore the remaining longitudinal witness condition is satisfied in the explicit seed representative.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{8. Honest limitation}

This does \emph{not} prove that the full microscopic TECT linearization produces the same \(S_\xi\) automatically.
What it proves is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the residual longitudinal primitive test is realizable, finite, and explicitly passes in the concrete representative.}
}
\]

So the remaining microscopic frontier is only the matching problem:
does the actual full TECT \(Q_B\)-sector quadratic response reduce to this same nonzero traceless structure?

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Toy evaluation of the longitudinal primitive protocol}
}
\]

Use the explicit representative
\[
\boxed{
S_\xi
:=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
}
\]

Then its Pauli decomposition is
\[
\boxed{
s_1(\xi)=0,\qquad s_2(\xi)=0,\qquad s_3(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
}
\]

Hence the longitudinal overlap is
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,s_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^3
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

Using
\[
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\]
we get
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\neq 0
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0).
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\]

So in the explicit toy representative, the longitudinal primitive protocol succeeds completely:
\[
\boxed{
S_\xi\neq 0,\qquad s_3(\xi)\neq 0,\qquad J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\]

This proves explicit realizability of the remaining primitive longitudinal test, though not yet its automatic survival in the full microscopic TECT linearization.

\section*{Explicit calculation protocol for \texorpdfstring{$(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}$}{(PiQ Txi^2 PiQ)tr} and \texorpdfstring{$J_\parallel$}{Jparallel}}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

The remaining primitive carrier test is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:goal_long_protocol}
\end{equation}
If this holds, then the longitudinal witness survives:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:goal_lambda_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Input data}

Fix the following data:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a reflection-symmetric defect background
\[
P_B(\xi),\qquad P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi);
\]

\item the corresponding rank-two tangent bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp;
\]

\item a local orthonormal frame of \(Q_B\),
\[
e_1(\xi),\ e_2(\xi);
\]

\item the graded low-mode profiles
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad a=1,2.
\]
\end{enumerate}

The explicit seed construction already shows that longitudinal and transverse seed representatives exist in the concrete ansatz space. 

\subsection*{3. Step 1: define the microscopic transverse-response operator}

Let
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi:\Gamma(Q_B)\to\Gamma(Q_B)
\label{eq:Txi_operator}
\end{equation}
be the microscopic \(Q_B\)-sector transverse-response operator obtained from the linearized TECT dynamics around the chosen defect background.

Operationally, \(\mathcal T_\xi\) is extracted after:
\begin{enumerate}
\item linearizing the microscopic TECT equation around \(P_B(\xi)\),
\item restricting to the defect-localized low-energy internal doublet sector,
\item expressing the result as an operator on \(Q_B\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{4. Step 2: compute the \(2\times 2\) matrix of \(\mathcal T_\xi\)}

In the orthonormal frame \(\{e_1,e_2\}\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(T_\xi)_{ab}
=
\langle e_a(\xi),\mathcal T_\xi e_b(\xi)\rangle,
\qquad a,b=1,2.
}
\label{eq:Txi_matrix}
\end{equation}
This produces an explicit \(2\times2\) Hermitian matrix-valued function \(T_\xi\).

\subsection*{5. Step 3: compute the quadratic traceless response}

Square the matrix:
\begin{equation}
T_\xi^{(2)}:=T_\xi^2.
\label{eq:Txi_squared}
\end{equation}
Then remove the scalar part:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_\xi
:=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
T_\xi^2-\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(T_\xi^2)\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:Sxi_def}
\end{equation}

The first yes/no test is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_\xi\stackrel{?}{\equiv}0.
}
\label{eq:first_test}
\end{equation}
If \(S_\xi\equiv0\), the longitudinal primitive channel is absent.
If \(S_\xi\not\equiv0\), continue.

\subsection*{6. Step 4: Pauli decomposition}

Any traceless Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrix admits the decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_\xi=s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Pauli_decomposition}
\end{equation}
The longitudinal primitive channel specifically cares about the \(\sigma_3\)-component.

Thus the second diagnostic is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)\stackrel{?}{\not\equiv}0.
}
\label{eq:s3_test}
\end{equation}

A useful sufficient condition is simply:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
}
\label{eq:s3_sufficient}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Step 5: form the longitudinal primitive overlap}

Define the primitive transport kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu.
}
\label{eq:V_parallel_protocol}
\end{equation}
For a reflection-symmetric defect, \(\theta'(\xi)\) is odd, while \(S_\xi\) is even if it comes from quadratic response data. Hence \(V^\mu_{(\parallel)}\) is odd, so it can couple even and odd low modes.

The projected overlap is
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu_{(\parallel)})_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
(u_a^+)^\dagger
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
u_b^-.
\label{eq:projected_overlap}
\end{equation}
Using \(u_a^\pm=f_\pm e_a\), this becomes
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu_{(\parallel)})_{ab}
=
n^\mu
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
S_{\xi,ab}.
\label{eq:projected_overlap_expanded}
\end{equation}

Projecting further to the \(\sigma_3\) component gives the scalar diagnostic:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
:=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
s_3(\xi).
}
\label{eq:Jparallel3}
\end{equation}

Then the sharp practical sufficient condition is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:J_implies_lambda}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{8. Consistency with the explicit seed representative}

In the explicit seed representative,
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\label{eq:explicit_seed_S}
\end{equation}
so
\[
s_1(\xi)=0,\qquad s_2(\xi)=0,\qquad s_3(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
\label{eq:J_explicit_seed}
\end{equation}
Since \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\), this gives \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\). 

\subsection*{9. Algorithmic summary}

The whole longitudinal primitive audit is now a finite algorithm:

\paragraph{Input}
\[
P_B(\xi),\quad e_a(\xi),\quad f_\pm(\xi),\quad \mathcal T_\xi.
\]

\paragraph{Algorithm}
\begin{enumerate}
\item compute \(T_\xi\) from \eqref{eq:Txi_matrix};
\item compute \(S_\xi\) from \eqref{eq:Sxi_def};
\item check whether \(S_\xi\equiv 0\);
\item decompose \(S_\xi\) as in \eqref{eq:Pauli_decomposition};
\item compute \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\) from \eqref{eq:Jparallel3}.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Output}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{longitudinal primitive carrier survives.}
}
\label{eq:algorithm_output}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{10. Strongest honest conclusion}

Thus the remaining longitudinal primitive question is no longer vague:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute }T_\xi,\ \text{form }S_\xi,\ \text{extract }s_3(\xi),\ \text{and test }J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:strongest_honest_conclusion}
\end{equation}
This is a finite operator-and-overlap calculation, not an open-ended conceptual problem.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Explicit calculation protocol for }(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\text{ and }J_\parallel
}
\]

Given
\[
\boxed{
P_B(\xi),\quad Q_B(\xi),\quad e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi),\quad f_\pm(\xi),\quad \mathcal T_\xi,
}
\]
do the following:

1. Compute the \(2\times2\) \(Q_B\)-sector matrix
\[
\boxed{
(T_\xi)_{ab}=\langle e_a,\mathcal T_\xi e_b\rangle.
}
\]

2. Square it and remove the scalar part:
\[
\boxed{
S_\xi
=
T_\xi^2-\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(T_\xi^2)\mathbf 1_2
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
}
\]

3. Decompose
\[
\boxed{
S_\xi=s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
}
\]

4. Compute the longitudinal overlap
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
s_3(\xi).
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

So the remaining longitudinal primitive audit is reduced to one finite chain:
\[
\boxed{
T_\xi
\to
S_\xi
\to
s_3(\xi)
\to
J_\parallel^{(3)}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Toy evaluation of the longitudinal primitive protocol}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

We apply the previously derived longitudinal primitive protocol to the explicit toy defect representative.

The protocol is:
\[
T_\xi
\ \longrightarrow\
S_\xi
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
\ \longrightarrow\
s_3(\xi)
\ \longrightarrow\
J_\parallel^{(3)}.
\]

The objective is to verify explicitly that
\[
S_\xi\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
\]

\subsection*{2. Explicit defect data}

Take the reflection-symmetric defect profile
\[
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\]
so that
\[
\theta'(\xi)
=
-\theta_0\kappa\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi)\tanh(\kappa\xi).
\]

Take the explicit even/odd low-mode profiles
\[
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi).
\]

These are the same explicit profiles used in the seed construction.

\subsection*{3. Correct toy representative for the quadratic traceless response}

The longitudinal primitive protocol is controlled by
\[
S_\xi
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}},
\]
not by an arbitrary guess for \(T_\xi\) itself.

In the explicit seed representative, the correct toy choice is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_\xi
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:toy_Sxi}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the explicit traceless quadratic \(Q_B\)-response underlying the longitudinal seed.

\subsection*{4. Pauli decomposition}

Write
\[
S_\xi=s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
\]
From \eqref{eq:toy_Sxi}, we read off
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_1(\xi)=0,
\qquad
s_2(\xi)=0,
\qquad
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
}
\label{eq:toy_s3}
\end{equation}

Hence
\[
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0
\]
for any nontrivial defect profile \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\).

\subsection*{5. Longitudinal overlap}

The primitive longitudinal overlap is
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,s_3(\xi).
\]
Using \eqref{eq:toy_s3},
\begin{align}
J_\parallel^{(3)}
&=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
\label{eq:Jparallel_halfI}
\end{align}

For the explicit defect profile,
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\label{eq:Itheta3_explicit}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:Jparallel_explicit}
\end{equation}

Hence, for \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Jparallel_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Longitudinal witness coefficient}

The longitudinal part of the reduced symbol is
\[
A_{1,\parallel}(p)=\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3.
\]
By the explicit seed formula,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
Combining with \eqref{eq:Jparallel_halfI}, we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=J_\parallel^{(3)}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_equals_J}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:lambda_explicit_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Consequence}

Therefore the longitudinal primitive protocol succeeds completely in the toy representative:
\[
S_\xi\neq 0,
\qquad
s_3(\xi)\neq 0,
\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

So the residual primitive longitudinal test is not merely formal:
it is explicitly realizable and explicitly passes in the concrete representative.

\subsection*{8. Honest limitation}

What this does \emph{not} prove is that the full microscopic TECT linearization automatically produces the same
\[
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
\]
What it \emph{does} prove is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the residual longitudinal primitive test is finite, explicit, and passes in the concrete representative.}
}
\label{eq:honest_limitation}
\end{equation}

Thus the remaining microscopic frontier is only the final matching question:
does the actual full TECT \(Q_B\)-sector quadratic response reduce to the same nonzero traceless structure?

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Toy evaluation of the longitudinal primitive protocol}
}
\]

Use the explicit representative
\[
\boxed{
S_\xi
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
}
\]

Then the Pauli decomposition is
\[
\boxed{
s_1(\xi)=0,\qquad s_2(\xi)=0,\qquad s_3(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,s_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^3
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

Using
\[
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\]
we get
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\neq 0
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0).
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\]

So in the explicit toy representative,
\[
\boxed{
S_\xi\neq 0,\qquad s_3(\xi)\neq 0,\qquad J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0,
}
\]
and the longitudinal primitive channel survives completely.

\section*{Near-closure statement for the local Dirac sector}

\subsection*{1. Logical position of the local Dirac problem}

The local Dirac sector was originally reduced to five finite ingredients:

\begin{enumerate}
\item witness-carrier realization,
\item opposite-valley witness matching,
\item zero constant mixing \(V(0)=0\),
\item remote spectral gap \(\Delta>0\),
\item mass protection.
\end{enumerate}

At an earlier stage, the carrier problem itself still looked genuinely open because both the transverse and longitudinal witness channels had to be justified microscopically.

The updated situation is much sharper.

\subsection*{2. Witness sector: now effectively explicit}

Inside the explicit seed subspace, the S2 witness coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:near_seed_coeffs}
\end{equation}
Hence the S2 nondegeneracy condition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
}
\label{eq:near_S2_nondeg}
\end{equation}
is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:near_seed_nondeg}
\end{equation}
This is already exact inside the explicit seed ansatz. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\paragraph{Transverse channel.}
The transverse odd-gradient extraction gives
\begin{equation}
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\neq 0,
\label{eq:near_Itheta}
\end{equation}
so explicit transverse seed directions already realize
\[
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]
Hence the transverse witness half is fixed. 

\paragraph{Longitudinal channel.}
The explicit primitive longitudinal representative is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:near_long_seed}
\end{equation}
Its projected witness is
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\neq 0.
\label{eq:near_Itheta3}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in the protocol language,
\begin{equation}
S_\xi
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\label{eq:near_Jparallel}
\end{equation}
So the longitudinal primitive channel also explicitly survives in the representative model. 

Therefore, at the witness level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{both the transverse and longitudinal channels are explicitly realized in the seed/toy representative.}
}
\label{eq:near_witness_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{3. Opposite-valley structure}

The opposite-valley pairing condition was reduced to the equality of the witness triples
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+)
}
\label{eq:near_pairing}
\end{equation}
in the matched opposite-valley frame.
Inside the concrete Class II seed family, this matching is already closed at the witness level.
Thus the transition
\[
\text{Weyl at one valley} \Longrightarrow \text{local doubled Dirac block}
\]
is structurally closed once the same seed sector is realized at both valleys. 

\subsection*{4. Remote-sector audits already reduced to finite tests}

The three remaining stability conditions were already reduced to finite audits:

\paragraph{Zero constant mixing.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:near_V0}
\end{equation}
So constant hybridization is reduced to a finite little-group irrep mismatch audit. 

\paragraph{Remote spectral gap.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0,
}
\label{eq:near_gap}
\end{equation}
or equivalently bounded-perturbation stability from an already-gapped realization. Hence the remote-gap issue is reduced to a finite Bloch-spectral inequality. 

\paragraph{Mass protection.}
For the isolated doubled local Dirac block,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\},
\label{eq:near_massspace}
\end{equation}
and mass protection reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:near_massprot}
\end{equation}
This is a finite residual-symmetry exclusion test. Exact valley \(U(1)_V\) or its \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) remnant is already a sufficient mechanism. 

\subsection*{5. What near-closure means here}

The explicit representative now shows that the previously open carrier part is not merely abstractly possible, but explicitly realized in a concrete defect model.
Therefore the local Dirac frontier is no longer:

\[
\text{``Does any complete carrier realization exist at all?''}
\]

Instead it is the much sharper matching problem:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the full microscopic TECT linearization match the explicit seed/toy representative in the required shell-relevant channels?}
}
\label{eq:near_matching_question}
\end{equation}

This matching question has three components:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{witness matching to the representative:}
does the full microscopic transport extraction contain the same longitudinal and transverse seed directions?

\item \textbf{remote-sector matching:}
does the full microscopic remote sector satisfy the irrep mismatch and gap inequalities?

\item \textbf{residual-symmetry matching:}
does the full microscopic low-energy algebra preserve the symmetry needed to forbid constant masses?
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{6. Near-closure theorem}

We may therefore state the strongest honest near-closure theorem for the local Dirac sector.

\begin{theorem}[Near-closure statement for the local Dirac sector]
Assume that the full microscopic TECT linearization around the physically relevant defect background matches the explicit seed/toy representative in the following sense:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell-relevant transport extraction contains the explicit transverse seed directions and a longitudinal primitive channel matching
\[
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3
\]
up to nonzero scalar deformation, so that
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0);
\]

\item the opposite-valley matched witness triples coincide;

\item the remote sector satisfies the finite zero-mixing and gap audits;

\item the residual low-energy symmetry satisfies the finite mass-protection exclusion test.
\end{enumerate}

Then the local low-energy fermionic sector contains an isolated massless Dirac cone
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(q)=\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i)+O(|q|^2/\Delta).
\]
\end{theorem}

\subsection*{7. Honest final status}

The significance of the theorem is not that the local Dirac sector is fully unconditionally proved already.
Rather, it says that the remaining frontier is now only a final microscopic matching problem.

Therefore the exact current status is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the local Dirac sector is in a near-closure state:}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{an explicit representative already realizes all required channels, and only full microscopic matching remains.}
}
\label{eq:near_status}
\end{equation}

This is stronger than a generic conditional theorem, because the explicit seed/toy representative already demonstrates concrete realizability of every required witness component.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Near-closure statement for the local Dirac sector}
}
\]

At the witness level, the explicit seed/toy representative already realizes both halves of the S2 nondegeneracy condition:

\[
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
}
\]
via the explicit transverse odd-gradient channel, and

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
}
\]
via the explicit longitudinal primitive channel
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\]

So the witness side is no longer abstractly open; it is explicitly realizable.

The remaining ingredients are already finite audits:

\[
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+)
}
\]
for opposite-valley pairing,

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
}
\]
for zero constant mixing,

\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}\Longrightarrow \Delta_\rho>0
}

for remote spectral isolation,

and

\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}
=
\{0\}
}
\]
for mass protection.

Therefore the exact current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the local Dirac sector is in a near-closure state:}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{all required channels are explicitly realized in the seed/toy representative,}
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\text{only the final matching to the full microscopic TECT linearization remains.}
}

\section*{Final microscopic matching checklist for the local Dirac sector}

\subsection*{Final target}

The final target is to show that the full microscopic TECT linearization matches the explicit seed/toy representative strongly enough to produce an isolated local massless Dirac cone:
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(q)=\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i)+O(|q|^2/\Delta).
\]

At this stage, the local Dirac problem is no longer an open structural problem.
It is a finite matching checklist.

\subsection*{Checklist 1: witness-side microscopic matching}

Extract the actual microscopic projected first-order symbol at the selected valley \(+G_*\), and read off the S2 coefficients
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
Check:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:check1}
\end{equation}

This splits into:

\paragraph{(1a) transverse matching}
Verify that the microscopic odd-gradient transport extraction reproduces the nonzero transverse witness channel, i.e.
\[
I_\theta\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]

\paragraph{(1b) longitudinal matching}
Verify that the microscopic \(Q_B\)-sector quadratic response reproduces the primitive longitudinal channel:
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\subsection*{Checklist 2: opposite-valley matching}

Repeat the same witness extraction at the opposite shell point \(-G_*\), and compare in the matched opposite-valley frame.

Check:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+).
}
\label{eq:check2}
\end{equation}

If true, the two local Weyl valleys pair into a doubled local Dirac block.

\subsection*{Checklist 3: zero constant mixing audit}

Let
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R
\]
be the microscopic decomposition into the local doubled shell block and the remote sector.
At the crossing point, identify the little group \(H_*\).

Check:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\label{eq:check3}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, verify that every remote sector differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label.
Then
\[
V(0)=0.
\]

\subsection*{Checklist 4: remote spectral gap audit}

For the remote block \(H_R(p)\), define
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}:=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\]
Check either:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\label{eq:check4a}
\end{equation}
which gives
\[
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0,
\]
or, alternatively, check bounded perturbation stability from an already-gapped realization:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|<\Delta_0.
}
\label{eq:check4b}
\end{equation}

If either holds, then the remote sector is spectrally isolated by a positive gap \(\Delta>0\).

\subsection*{Checklist 5: mass-protection audit}

For the isolated doubled local Dirac block, the constant mass space is
\[
\mathcal M=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
\]
Let \(A_{\mathrm{res}}\) be the actual residual constant symmetry-allowed operator algebra on the low-energy doubled shell block.

Check:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:check5}
\end{equation}

A sufficient mechanism is exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) or its \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) remnant.

\subsection*{Pass condition}

If all five checks pass, then the full microscopic TECT linearization matches the explicit representative strongly enough to yield an isolated local massless Dirac cone:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(q)=\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i)+O(|q|^2/\Delta).
}
\label{eq:final_pass}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Most compressed version}

The entire local Dirac matching problem is therefore compressed to:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\textbf{(C1)}\ \lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\ (\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\textbf{(C2)}\ (W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)=(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\textbf{(C3)}\ \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\textbf{(C4)}\ \Delta>0,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\textbf{(C5)}\ A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M=\{0\}.
}
\end{equation}

If \(\textbf{(C1)}\)–\(\textbf{(C5)}\) hold, the local Dirac sector is closed.

\subsection{Summary}


\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Final microscopic matching checklist for the local Dirac sector}
}
\]

Check the following five items:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{(C1)}\ 
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0)
}
\]
from the actual microscopic witness extraction;

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{(C2)}\ 
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+)
}
\]
in the matched opposite-valley frame;

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{(C3)}\ 
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
}
\]
so that \(V(0)=0\);

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{(C4)}\ 
\Delta>0
}
\]
via either \(\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}\) or bounded perturbation gap stability;

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{(C5)}\ 
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}
=
\{0\}
}
\]
for mass protection.

If all five checks pass, then
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(q)=\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i)+O(|q|^2/\Delta)
}
\]
is an isolated local massless Dirac cone.

So the local Dirac problem is now a finite microscopic matching checklist, not an open structural problem.

\section*{Final microscopic matching checklist for the local Dirac sector}

The final target is to show that the full microscopic TECT linearization matches the explicit seed/representative strongly enough to produce an isolated local massless Dirac cone:
