\section*{Longitudinal seed embedding test}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

The only remaining unresolved part of C1 is whether the full microscopic transport space
\[
V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\]
actually contains the explicit longitudinal seed direction
\[
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
\sim
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu.
\]
Inside the explicit representative this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:long_seed_embed_goal}
\end{equation}
So the embedding problem is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\mathrm{micro}}\ni N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}} \ ? 
}
\label{eq:embedding_question}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Minimal tensor structure that must appear}

A longitudinal seed requires the simultaneous presence of the following three ingredients in the microscopic transport kernel:

\paragraph{(L1) odd defect-gradient factor}
An odd scalar profile proportional to
\[
\theta'(\xi).
\]

\paragraph{(L2) traceless internal \(Q_B\)-scalar}
A \(2\times2\) Hermitian traceless operator on the \(Q_B\)-doublet, i.e.
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
\]

\paragraph{(L3) shell-axis worldvolume factor}
A contraction with the distinguished shell/worldvolume direction \(n^\mu\).

Thus the minimal longitudinal transport structure is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{micro}}(\xi)
\supset
\theta'(\xi)\,
\Bigl[s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3\Bigr]
\,n^\mu.
}
\label{eq:min_long_structure}
\end{equation}

For the explicit representative, only the \(\sigma_3\)-part survives:
\[
s_1=s_2=0,
\qquad
s_3=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]

\subsection*{3. Embedding criterion in Pauli language}

Let the actual microscopic first-order transport kernel projected to the \(Q_B\)-doublet be
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\mathrm{micro}}(\xi)
=
v_0^\mu(\xi)\mathbf 1_2
+
v_1^\mu(\xi)\sigma_1
+
v_2^\mu(\xi)\sigma_2
+
v_3^\mu(\xi)\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Vmicro_Pauli}
\end{equation}

The longitudinal seed embedding succeeds if the \(\sigma_3\)-component contains a nonzero shell-axis odd piece:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_3^\mu(\xi)\supset n^\mu\,\theta'(\xi)\,q(\xi),
\qquad
q(\xi)\not\equiv 0,
}
\label{eq:Pauli_embedding_condition}
\end{equation}
with \(q(\xi)\) even.
In the explicit representative,
\[
q(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]

So a sharp sufficient criterion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the projected microscopic kernel has a nonzero odd }n^\mu\sigma_3\text{-component.}
}
\label{eq:sharp_embedding_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Equivalent overlap test}

Instead of reading the Pauli coefficient directly, one may test the overlap against the explicit longitudinal seed profile.
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal E_\parallel
:=
\int d\xi\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
\mathrm{Tr}_{Q_B}\!\Bigl[
\sigma_3\,n_\mu\,V^\mu_{\mathrm{micro}}(\xi)
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:embedding_overlap}
\end{equation}
Then a sufficient condition for longitudinal embedding is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal E_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:embedding_overlap_nonzero}
\end{equation}

If one also includes the graded low-mode weights, the strongest practical version is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal J_\parallel
:=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\mathrm{Tr}_{Q_B}\!\Bigl[
\sigma_3\,n_\mu\,V^\mu_{\mathrm{micro}}(\xi)
\Bigr]
\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:weighted_embedding_test}
\end{equation}
This is the direct embedding analogue of the representative identity
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

\subsection*{5. Relation to the representative}

In the explicit representative,
\[
V^\mu_{\mathrm{rep}}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\]
Then
\[
\mathrm{Tr}_{Q_B}\!\Bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\,V^\mu_{\mathrm{rep}}(\xi)\Bigr]
=
\theta'(\xi)^3
\]
up to normalization, and
\[
\mathcal J_\parallel
\propto
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^3
=
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]
So the representative passes the embedding test exactly.

\subsection*{6. Final practical algorithm}

The longitudinal seed embedding test is therefore:

\paragraph{Step A}
Compute the projected microscopic kernel \(V^\mu_{\mathrm{micro}}(\xi)\) on the \(Q_B\)-doublet.

\paragraph{Step B}
Pauli-decompose it as in \eqref{eq:Vmicro_Pauli}.

\paragraph{Step C}
Check whether \(v_3^\mu(\xi)\) contains a nonzero odd \(n^\mu\)-aligned piece.

\paragraph{Step D}
Compute the weighted overlap \(\mathcal J_\parallel\) in \eqref{eq:weighted_embedding_test}.

\paragraph{Pass condition}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal J_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\text{ is embedded in }V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:long_embedding_pass}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Strongest honest conclusion}

Thus the last unresolved part of C1 is now reduced to a single finite matching test:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the full microscopic projected transport kernel contain a nonzero odd }n^\mu\sigma_3\text{-component with nonvanishing graded overlap?}
}
\label{eq:final_long_embedding_question}
\end{equation}

This is strictly sharper than the earlier carrier-audit phrasing.
It is not a broad search over tensor spaces anymore; it is one explicit coefficient/overlap test.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Longitudinal seed embedding test}
}
\]

The explicit longitudinal representative is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\]

So in the full microscopic projected kernel
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{micro}}(\xi)
=
v_0^\mu(\xi)\mathbf 1_2
+
v_1^\mu(\xi)\sigma_1
+
v_2^\mu(\xi)\sigma_2
+
v_3^\mu(\xi)\sigma_3,
}
\]
the embedding succeeds if the \(\sigma_3\)-component contains a nonzero odd shell-axis piece:
\[
\boxed{
v_3^\mu(\xi)\supset n^\mu\,\theta'(\xi)\,q(\xi),
\qquad
q(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
}
\]

A direct weighted overlap test is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal J_\parallel
:=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\mathrm{Tr}_{Q_B}\!\Bigl[
\sigma_3\,n_\mu\,V^\mu_{\mathrm{micro}}(\xi)
\Bigr].
}
\]

If
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal J_\parallel\neq 0,
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\subset V_{\mathrm{micro}},
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

So the last unresolved part of C1 is now one explicit finite test:
\[
\boxed{
\text{nonzero odd }n^\mu\sigma_3\text{-component + nonvanishing graded overlap.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{C2: opposite-valley matching}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

After C1, the selected valley \(+G_*\) carries a nondegenerate local Weyl symbol.
To obtain a local doubled Dirac block, one must verify that the opposite valley \(-G_*\) carries the matched witness data.

The exact C2 condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+)
}
\label{eq:C2_goal}
\end{equation}
in the matched opposite-valley frame. This is the finite witness formulation of local Dirac doubling. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\subsection*{2. What must be compared}

At \(+G_*\), extract the projected first-order symbol
\[
A_1^+(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel^+ p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha^+(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta^+(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
and define
\[
W_\parallel^+=\lambda_\parallel^+,
\qquad
W_I^+=\alpha^+,
\qquad
W_J^+=\beta^+.
\]

At \(-G_*\), do the same:
\[
A_1^-(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel^- p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha^-(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta^-(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
with
\[
W_\parallel^-=\lambda_\parallel^-,
\qquad
W_I^-=\alpha^-,
\qquad
W_J^-=\beta^-.
\]

Then C2 is exactly \eqref{eq:C2_goal}.

\subsection*{3. Why raw comparison is not the right comparison}

One must not compare the coefficients in an arbitrary laboratory basis.
The correct comparison is done after choosing the matched opposite-valley frame
\[
\{\hat n^+,e_1^+,e_2^+\},
\qquad
\{\hat n^-,e_1^-,e_2^-\},
\]
so that the opposite-valley Hamiltonian is brought to the standard doubled form.

Thus the real C2 question is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{after matched-frame identification, do the two witness triples coincide?}
}
\]

This is exactly how the witness-level opposite-valley theorem is formulated. 

\subsection*{4. Concrete Class II seed family}

Inside the concrete Class II family, the same seed amplitudes
\[
c_\parallel,\qquad c_I,\qquad c_J
\]
determine the witness data at both valleys.
In the matched opposite-valley frame, they are read identically:
\[
c_\parallel^-=c_\parallel^+,
\qquad
c_I^-=c_I^+,
\qquad
c_J^-=c_J^+.
\]
Hence
\[
W_\parallel^-=W_\parallel^+,
\qquad
W_I^-=W_I^+,
\qquad
W_J^-=W_J^+.
\]

Therefore, inside the explicit seed/representative family, C2 is already closed at the witness level. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection*{5. Final microscopic matching test for C2}

So the only remaining microscopic task is not to invent a new criterion, but to verify that the full microscopic extraction produces the same matched seed sector at both valleys.

Operationally:

\paragraph{(C2-a)}
Extract
\[
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+)
\]
from the projected microscopic symbol at \(+G_*\).

\paragraph{(C2-b)}
Extract
\[
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
\]
from the projected microscopic symbol at \(-G_*\).

\paragraph{(C2-c)}
Pass to the matched opposite-valley frame.

\paragraph{(C2-d)}
Check
\[
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+).
\]

If true, C2 passes.

\subsection*{6. Strongest honest conclusion}

Thus C2 is already structurally closed.
The remaining part is only a final microscopic matching check:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{does the full microscopic TECT extraction yield the same witness triple at }\pm G_*
\text{ in the matched frame?}
}
\label{eq:C2_final_question}
\end{equation}
This is a finite comparison problem, not an open structural problem.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{C2: opposite-valley matching}
}
\]

The exact condition is
\[
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+)
}
\]
in the matched opposite-valley frame.

Inside the explicit Class II seed/representative family, this is already closed, because the same seed amplitudes
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel,\qquad c_I,\qquad c_J
}
\]
are read identically at the two valleys after matched-frame identification.

So the remaining microscopic C2 task is only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{extract the witness triple at }+G_*\text{ and }-G_*,
\text{ pass to the matched frame, and compare them.}
}
\]

If they are equal, then the two Weyl valleys pair into a local doubled Dirac block.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{C3: zero constant mixing}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

Write the full microscopic Hamiltonian near the selected crossing as
\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
where \(\mathcal H_D\) is the local doubled shell Dirac block and \(\mathcal H_R\) is the remote sector.

The target is
\[
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\]

\subsection*{2. Theorem-level criterion}

Let \(H_*\) be the little group / residual symmetry at the crossing \(p=0\).
Assume the Hamiltonian is \(H_*\)-equivariant and the decomposition
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R
\]
is \(H_*\)-invariant.

Then
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:C3_main}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{3. Sectorwise reduction}

Decompose the remote sector into \(H_*\)-invariant pieces
\[
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a.
\]
Then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)
\cong
\bigoplus_a \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D).
\]
So it is enough to prove
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
\qquad
\forall a.
\]

\subsection*{4. Practical label audit}

A remote sector \(K_a\) is excluded from constant mixing if it differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label:

\begin{enumerate}
\item selected shell-pair label \(\pm G_*\),
\item transverse vs longitudinal/volumetric character,
\item enriched internal doublet label,
\item residual parity / grading / chirality,
\item any extra conserved microscopic label.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the practical test is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{for every }K_a\subset \mathcal H_R,\ \text{find at least one mismatch label relative to }\mathcal H_D.
}
\]

Then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
\]
for all \(a\), hence
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\]
and therefore \(V(0)=0\).

\subsection*{5. Minimal truncation checklist}

In the minimal dangerous truncation
\[
\mathcal H_R=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non-enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong-int}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}},
\]
the default eliminations are:

\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}:\ \text{volumetric mismatch},
\]
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}:\ \text{different shell orbit mismatch},
\]
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non-enr}}:\ \text{no enriched internal doublet},
\]
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong-int}}:\ \text{wrong internal representation},
\]
while \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\) must be checked case by case.

\subsection*{6. Completion criterion}

Thus C3 is complete once one proves
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\]
Equivalently:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the local Dirac block and the remote sector share no common shell-relevant irreducible representation.}
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\]

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{C3: zero constant mixing}
}
\]

The exact theorem-level criterion is
\[
\boxed{
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D),
\qquad
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

So C3 reduces to a finite sectorwise label audit.

Decompose
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a.
}
\]
A sector \(K_a\) is excluded from constant mixing if it differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one of:

\[
\boxed{
\pm G_*,\quad
\text{transverse vs volumetric character},\quad
\text{enriched internal doublet},\quad
\text{parity/grading/chirality},\quad
\text{extra conserved label}.
}
\]

Hence the completion criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\forall a,\ \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

So C3 is a finite remote-sector label audit, not an open structural problem.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{C4: remote gap \texorpdfstring{$\Delta>0$}{Delta>0}}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

Let the microscopic Hamiltonian near the selected crossing be written as
\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
where \(H_D\) acts on the local doubled shell Dirac block \(\mathcal H_D\) and \(H_R\) acts on the remote sector \(\mathcal H_R\). The C4 target is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing
\qquad
\text{for small }p,
\quad
\Delta>0.
}
\label{eq:C4_goal}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Route A: direct Bloch/spectral lower-bound test}

Write the remote block as
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+E_R(p),
\]
where \(D_R(p)\) is a diagonal or benchmark part and \(E_R(p)\) is the remaining correction.

Define
\begin{equation}
\delta_0(p):=\min_a |(D_R)_{aa}(p)|,
\qquad
\eta_R(p):=\|E_R(p)\|.
\label{eq:C4_delta_eta_pointwise}
\end{equation}
For a low-momentum neighborhood
\[
N_\rho=\{p:|p|\le \rho\},
\]
define
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}:=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\label{eq:C4_delta_eta_uniform}
\end{equation}

Then the direct remote-gap criterion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho:=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0,
}
\label{eq:C4_direct_criterion}
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing
\qquad
\forall |p|\le \rho.
}
\label{eq:C4_direct_gap}
\end{equation}

This is the finite Bloch/spectral lower-bound route.

\subsection*{3. Route B: bounded perturbation stability from an already-gapped realization}

Suppose there exists a reference remote block \(H_R^{(0)}(p)\) satisfying
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap(-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing
\qquad
(\Delta_0>0)
}
\label{eq:C4_ref_gap}
\end{equation}
for all \(|p|\le p_*\), and write
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=H_R^{(0)}(p)+\delta H_R(p).
\label{eq:C4_pert_split}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|\le \varepsilon<\Delta_0,
}
\label{eq:C4_eps_bound}
\end{equation}
then the perturbed remote block still has a positive gap
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta=\Delta_0-\varepsilon>0,
\qquad
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing.
}
\label{eq:C4_pert_gap}
\end{equation}
A common strong form is
\[
\|\delta H_R\|<\Delta_0/2,
\]
which implies
\[
\Delta>\Delta_0/2>0.
\]

\subsection*{4. Consequence for the resolvent and Schur complement}

Once C4 holds, for \(|E|<\Delta/2\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
}
\label{eq:C4_resolvent}
\end{equation}
If C3 also holds, i.e.
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
then the Schur-complement self-energy obeys
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(E,p)=V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
}
\label{eq:C4_schur}
\end{equation}
Hence the remote sector changes the local Dirac block only at quadratic order.

\subsection*{5. Minimal practical checklist for C4}

To complete C4 in practice, do one of the following.

\paragraph{Direct route.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Build the reduced remote block \(H_R(p)\).
\item Choose a benchmark diagonal part \(D_R(p)\).
\item Compute \(\delta_{0,\rho}\).
\item Estimate \(\eta_{R,\rho}\).
\item Check whether \(\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}\).
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Perturbative route.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Choose an already-gapped reference model \(H_R^{(0)}(p)\) with gap \(\Delta_0\).
\item Compute the correction \(\delta H_R(p)\).
\item Estimate \(\sup\|\delta H_R\|\).
\item Check whether \(\sup\|\delta H_R\|<\Delta_0\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{6. Strongest honest conclusion}

Therefore C4 is not an open structural problem.
It is a finite spectral check:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{either prove }\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\quad\text{or prove }\sup\|\delta H_R\|<\Delta_0.
}
\label{eq:C4_final_practical}
\end{equation}
If either succeeds, then \(\Delta>0\) is established.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{C4: remote gap } \Delta>0
}
\]

There are two standard ways to prove C4.

\paragraph{Route A: direct lower-bound test}
Write
\[
\boxed{
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+E_R(p),
}
\]
define
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}:=\inf_{|p|\le\rho}\min_a |(D_R)_{aa}(p)|,
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le\rho}\|E_R(p)\|,
}
\]
and check
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Route B: bounded perturbation stability}
If
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap(-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|<\Delta_0,
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta=\Delta_0-\sup\|\delta H_R\|>0.
}
\]

Once C4 holds,
\[
\boxed{
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}
\qquad
(|E|<\Delta/2),
}
\]
and together with C3,
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma(E,p)=O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
}
\]

So C4 is a finite Bloch/spectral lower-bound check, not an open structural problem.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Actual C3 audit in the minimal truncation}

\subsection*{1. Target}

We want to prove, not merely restate, that in the minimal shell-relevant truncation
\[
V(0)=0.
\]
The theorem-level criterion is already known:
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D),
\qquad
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
\]
So the task is a sectorwise actual mismatch audit.

\subsection*{2. Minimal truncated Hilbert space}

Use the minimal truncation
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\label{eq:min_trunc_C3}
\end{equation}
Here
\[
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
is the local doubled Dirac carrier, while the four remote sectors are explicitly identified as the nearest potentially dangerous competitors. This is exactly the first nontrivial finite truncation introduced for Tasks III and V. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection*{3. Sectorwise audit}

We now verify, one by one, that each remote sector differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label.

\paragraph{3.1. Volumetric sector}
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\]
is the volumetric/longitudinal sector, whereas \(\mathcal H_D\) is the transverse shell-relevant doubled Dirac carrier.
Hence there is an immediate mismatch in the label
\[
\text{transverse vs longitudinal/volumetric character}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\label{eq:vol_zero}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{3.2. Higher-shell sector}
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\]
contains modes not belonging to the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\), while \(\mathcal H_D\) is built precisely on that selected shell pair.
Hence there is an immediate mismatch in the label
\[
\text{selected shell-pair / shell orbit}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\label{eq:high_zero}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{3.3. Same-shell but non-enriched sector}
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\]
may lie on the same shell, but by definition does not carry the shell-relevant enriched internal doublet.
By contrast,
\[
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
does carry exactly that doubled internal structure.
Hence there is an immediate mismatch in the label
\[
\text{presence of enriched internal doublet}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\label{eq:nonenr_zero}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{3.4. Wrong-internal sector}
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\]
contains modes whose internal content does not match the selected shell doublet.
Hence there is an immediate mismatch in the label
\[
\text{internal representation}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\label{eq:wrongint_zero}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Assemble the result}

Since
\[
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\]
we have
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}},\mathcal H_D)
\cong
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}},\mathcal H_D)
\oplus
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}},\mathcal H_D)
\oplus
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\mathcal H_D)
\oplus
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},\mathcal H_D).
\]
Using \eqref{eq:vol_zero}--\eqref{eq:wrongint_zero}, every summand vanishes. Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\label{eq:HRtr_zero}
\end{equation}

By \(H_*\)-equivariance of the truncated Hamiltonian at \(p=0\),
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}},\mathcal H_D).
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:V0_done}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Exact status}

Thus C3 is actually completed in the minimal truncation:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{for }
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\quad
V(0)=0
\text{ is proved.}
}
\label{eq:C3_completed_minimal}
\end{equation}

What would remain open only concerns any additional remote sectors beyond the minimal truncation, if such sectors are later added. But for the stated minimal truncation, C3 is done.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual C3 result in the minimal truncation}
}
\]

Use
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
}
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\ \text{mismatches }\mathcal H_D
\text{ by transverse vs volumetric character}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\ \text{mismatches }\mathcal H_D
\text{ by shell orbit}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\ \text{mismatches }\mathcal H_D
\text{ by lack of enriched internal doublet}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\ \text{mismatches }\mathcal H_D
\text{ by wrong internal representation}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}},\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

So, in the minimal truncation, **C3 is completed**.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Actual C4 status in the minimal truncation}

\subsection*{1. Minimal truncated remote block}

In the minimal shell-relevant truncation, the full Hilbert space is
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\]
The remote sector is therefore
\[
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\]

Write the truncated Hamiltonian as
\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V_{DR}(p)\\
V_{DR}(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p).
\]

Here \(D_R(p)\) is the diagonal sector-center part and \(R_R(p)\) is the remote-remote mixing remainder.

\subsection*{2. Exact lower-bound reduction}

Define
\[
\delta_0(p)=
\min\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|
\},
\]
\[
\eta_R(p)=\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

Then the minimal truncation remote-gap theorem gives the pointwise operator bound
\[
\boxed{
\|H_R(p)\psi\|
\ge
(\delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p))\|\psi\|.
}
\]

Hence, if
\[
\delta_0(p)>\eta_R(p),
\]
then the remote sector has a pointwise gap
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta(p),\Delta(p))=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta(p)\ge \delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p)>0.
\]

On a neighborhood
\[
N_\rho=\{p:|p|\le \rho\},
\]
define
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing
\quad(|p|\le \rho),
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

Equivalently, one may use the Gershgorin lower bound
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_a
\Bigl(
|(H_R)_{aa}(p)|-\sum_{b\neq a}|(H_R)_{ab}(p)|
\Bigr)>0.
\]

\subsection*{3. What is actually completed}

Therefore, at the theorem level, C4 is already completely reduced to the finite inequality
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0.
}
\]

This means that the abstract remote-gap question has been converted into a finite-dimensional lower-bound problem on the minimal truncated remote matrix.

\subsection*{4. What is not yet numerically/analytically completed}

To actually conclude
\[
\Delta_\rho>0,
\]
one still needs the explicit lower bounds for the four sector-center energies:
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p),
\]
and an explicit upper bound for
\[
\eta_R(p)=\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

At the present stage, the uploaded material does not yet provide these four actual center-energy formulas in a fully evaluated form for the final microscopic TECT realization.
Hence the final sign of
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}
\]
has not yet been numerically or analytically verified.

\subsection*{5. Exact honest status of C4}

So the honest status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{C4 is closed as a finite lower-bound theorem in the minimal truncation,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual positive value of }\Delta_\rho
\text{ still requires explicit evaluation of }
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}},\mu_{\mathrm{high}},\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]

Thus C4 is not structurally open anymore, but it is not yet numerically completed either.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual C4 status}
}
\]

In the minimal truncation,
\[
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\qquad
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p).
\]

Define
\[
\delta_0(p)=
\min\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|
\},
\qquad
\eta_R(p)=\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\|H_R(p)\psi\|
\ge
(\delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p))\|\psi\|.
}
\]

Hence, on
\[
N_\rho=\{p:|p|\le \rho\},
\]
if
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0,
\qquad
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing.
}
\]

So C4 is already reduced to a finite matrix lower-bound problem.

What is still not completed is the actual evaluation of
\[
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}},\ \mu_{\mathrm{high}},\ \mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\ \mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},\ \eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{C4 is theorem-level closed in the minimal truncation, but not yet numerically/analytically fully verified.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Actual C5 audit: mass protection}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

We want to determine whether the isolated doubled local Dirac block admits any symmetry-allowed constant mass term.

The low-energy block is
\begin{equation}
H_D(q)=\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i),
\qquad i=1,2,3.
\label{eq:C5_HD}
\end{equation}
The C5 target is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M=\{0\},
}
\label{eq:C5_goal}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal M\) is the constant Dirac mass space and \(A_{\mathrm{res}}\) is the residual symmetry-allowed constant operator algebra.

\subsection*{2. Actual mass-space classification}

The constant mass space is defined by
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M
:=
\left\{
K\in \mathrm{Herm}(4):
\{K,\rho_3\otimes \sigma_i\}=0
\ \forall i=1,2,3
\right\}.
\label{eq:C5_mass_def}
\end{equation}
The exact classification theorem gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\}.
}
\label{eq:C5_mass_space}
\end{equation}
So there are exactly two independent constant Dirac masses. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

Therefore any possible constant mass has the form
\begin{equation}
K_m
=
m_1\,\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:C5_general_mass}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{3. Valley symmetry test}

Define the residual valley-charge generator
\begin{equation}
Q_V:=\rho_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_V(\theta)=e^{i\theta Q_V}.
\label{eq:C5_QV}
\end{equation}
Since
\[
[Q_V,\rho_3\otimes \sigma_i]=0,
\]
the kinetic Dirac block is valley symmetric.

Now act on the two mass generators:
\begin{equation}
U_V(\theta)(\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_V(\theta)^{-1}
=
(\cos 2\theta)\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
(\sin 2\theta)\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:C5_rot1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
U_V(\theta)(\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_V(\theta)^{-1}
=
-(\sin 2\theta)\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
(\cos 2\theta)\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:C5_rot2}
\end{equation}
Thus the mass space \(\mathcal M\) transforms as a nontrivial doublet under \(U(1)_V\).
Hence no nonzero mass element is \(U(1)_V\)-invariant:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:C5_U1}
\end{equation}
So exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) implies mass protection. 

\subsection*{4. Weaker discrete symmetry is already sufficient}

Even the discrete remnant
\begin{equation}
S_V:=\rho_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
S_V^2=\mathbf 1_4
\label{eq:C5_SV}
\end{equation}
is enough.
Indeed,
\begin{equation}
S_V(\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\qquad
S_V(\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:C5_Z2_action}
\end{equation}
Hence both mass generators are odd under \(S_V\), so again
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathbb Z_2^V}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:C5_Z2}
\end{equation}
Thus an exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) is already sufficient for mass protection. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection*{5. Connection with C3}

C3 already showed, in the minimal truncation, that
\[
V(0)=0
\]
because
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]
This means constant Dirac--remote hybridization is absent at the crossing.
Therefore the remaining source of a constant gap is not remote hybridization, but an allowed constant operator living directly in the isolated doubled block.

But the previous sections show that any such constant operator must lie in \(\mathcal M\), and if residual valley symmetry is exact, then no nonzero element of \(\mathcal M\) is allowed.

So C3 + residual valley symmetry implies:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{no constant mass is generated at the local Dirac point.}
}
\label{eq:C5_with_C3}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Actual C5 result}

Therefore the actual C5 audit gives the following:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{At the level of the isolated doubled Dirac block, the complete mass classification is done.}
}
\label{eq:C5_done_classification}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{If the residual microscopic symmetry contains }U(1)_V\text{ or at least }\mathbb Z_2^V,
\text{ then C5 is proved.}
}
\label{eq:C5_if_symmetry}
\end{equation}

Equivalently:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}
=
\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:C5_final_actual}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{7. Exact honest status}

What is actually completed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the full constant mass-space classification;
\item the proof that residual \(U(1)_V\) forbids all masses;
\item the proof that residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) already suffices.
\end{enumerate}

What still remains open microscopically:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{whether the full microscopic TECT truncation preserves exact residual }U(1)_V
\text{ or at least }\mathbb Z_2^V.
}
\label{eq:C5_open_last}
\end{equation}

So C5 is not structurally open.
It is reduced to one residual symmetry-preservation matching question.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual C5 result}
}
\]

For the isolated doubled local Dirac block
\[
\boxed{
H_D(q)=\rho_3\otimes(q_i\sigma_i),
}
\]
the full constant mass space is exactly
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\rho_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\rho_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
}
\]

If the residual microscopic symmetry contains
\[
\boxed{
Q_V=\rho_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
}
\]
or already its discrete remnant
\[
\boxed{
S_V=\rho_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
}
\]
then both mass generators are forbidden, so
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}.
}
\]

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\text{C5 is completed once residual valley }U(1)_V\text{ or }\mathbb Z_2^V\text{ is actually preserved in the microscopic truncation.}
}
\]

So C5 is reduced to one final residual-symmetry preservation check.

\section*{C1 last unresolved part: actual longitudinal seed embedding}

\subsection*{1. What remains}

Inside the explicit seed/representative family, the longitudinal witness is already realized:
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
and hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

So the remaining C1 question is not whether a longitudinal seed can exist in principle.
It is only:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the full microscopic projected transport kernel actually contain a nonzero }n^\mu\sigma_3\text{ component?}
}
\label{eq:C1_last_question}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Microscopic projected kernel}

Let the full microscopic first-order transport kernel projected to the \(Q_B\)-doublet be
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\mathrm{micro}}(\xi)
=
v_0^\mu(\xi)\mathbf 1_2
+
v_1^\mu(\xi)\sigma_1
+
v_2^\mu(\xi)\sigma_2
+
v_3^\mu(\xi)\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Vmicro_pauli}
\end{equation}

The longitudinal seed embedding is controlled only by the \(\sigma_3\) channel.

\subsection*{3. Shell-axis projection}

Let \(n^\mu\) be the distinguished shell/worldvolume axis.
Project the \(\sigma_3\) coefficient along \(n^\mu\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_\parallel(\xi):=n_\mu\,v_3^\mu(\xi).
}
\label{eq:qparallel_def}
\end{equation}

Then the microscopic kernel contains the desired longitudinal structure iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_\parallel(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
}
\label{eq:qparallel_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Graded low-mode overlap}

Let
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi)
\]
be the even/odd low modes.
The actual projected longitudinal overlap is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal J_\parallel
:=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
q_\parallel(\xi).
\label{eq:Jparallel_actual}
\end{equation}

This is the full microscopic analogue of the representative quantity
\[
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

\subsection*{5. Pass/fail criterion}

The actual longitudinal seed embedding passes iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal J_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Jparallel_pass}
\end{equation}

If \(\mathcal J_\parallel\neq 0\), then the microscopic transport space contains the longitudinal seed direction, hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:lambda_from_J}
\end{equation}

If \(\mathcal J_\parallel=0\), then the present microscopic truncation does not realize the longitudinal witness.

\subsection*{6. Final reduction of C1}

Therefore the last unresolved part of C1 is completely reduced to the single scalar test:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal J_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,n_\mu v_3^\mu(\xi)
\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
}
\label{eq:C1_final_scalar_test}
\end{equation}

So C1 is now split as:

\[
\text{transverse part: fixed},
\qquad
\text{longitudinal part: one scalar overlap test}.
\]

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{C1 final unresolved test}
}
\]

Write the full microscopic projected transport kernel as
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{micro}}(\xi)
=
v_0^\mu(\xi)\mathbf 1_2
+
v_1^\mu(\xi)\sigma_1
+
v_2^\mu(\xi)\sigma_2
+
v_3^\mu(\xi)\sigma_3.
}
\]

Project the \(\sigma_3\) channel along the shell axis:
\[
\boxed{
q_\parallel(\xi):=n_\mu v_3^\mu(\xi).
}
\]

Then define the graded overlap
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal J_\parallel
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,q_\parallel(\xi).
}
\]

If
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal J_\parallel\neq 0,
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
}
\]
so the longitudinal seed is embedded in the full microscopic transport space.

Therefore the last unresolved part of C1 is reduced to one scalar coefficient/overlap test:
\[
\boxed{
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,n_\mu v_3^\mu(\xi)\neq 0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Actual residual symmetry preservation check for C5}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

The final unresolved part of C5 is not the mass classification itself.
That is already closed:
\[
\mathcal M
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\}.
\]
The remaining question is whether the corrected microscopic shell block actually preserves a residual symmetry that excludes all elements of \(\mathcal M\).

\subsection*{2. Corrected shell block}

For the canonical minimal Class II correction, the shell-level coefficients are renormalized as
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J.
\]
Thus the corrected local doubled shell block remains of the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_D(p)
=
\tau_z\otimes
\Bigl(
B_{\mathrm{eff}}p_1\sigma_1
+
C_{\mathrm{eff}}p_2\sigma_2
+
A_{\mathrm{eff}}p_\parallel\sigma_3
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:shell_block_C5}
\end{equation}
So the Class II correction changes only the derivative shell tensor coefficients.
It does not insert an independent constant shell-level mass operator. 

\subsection*{3. Residual valley-charge generator}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:QV_shell}
\end{equation}
Then for each kinetic generator,
\[
[Q_V,\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i]=0,
\qquad i=1,2,3.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_V,H_D(p)]=0.
}
\label{eq:Q_comm_HD}
\end{equation}
So the corrected shell block preserves the residual valley \(U(1)_V\) symmetry.

\subsection*{4. Exclusion of constant masses}

Any constant Dirac mass lies in
\[
\mathcal M
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\}.
\]
Under
\[
U_V(\theta)=e^{i\theta Q_V},
\]
these generators transform as
\[
U_V(\theta)(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_V(\theta)^{-1}
=
(\cos 2\theta)\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
(\sin 2\theta)\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
\[
U_V(\theta)(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_V(\theta)^{-1}
=
-(\sin 2\theta)\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
(\cos 2\theta)\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Thus no nonzero element of \(\mathcal M\) is invariant under the residual \(U(1)_V\).
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:AU1_mass_zero}
\end{equation}
So shell-level mass protection holds.

\subsection*{5. Actual shell-level result}

Combining \eqref{eq:shell_block_C5}, \eqref{eq:Q_comm_HD}, and \eqref{eq:AU1_mass_zero}, we obtain:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the canonical minimal Class II corrected shell block preserves residual valley symmetry and forbids all constant Dirac masses.}
}
\label{eq:shell_level_C5_done}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{6. Honest remaining microscopic issue}

What still remains open is the stronger full-microscopic statement:
does the complete TECT Hamiltonian, including the remote sector and its elimination, preserve the same symmetry?

If the full microscopic theory admits a symmetry action
\[
(U_\theta\oplus U_{R,\theta})H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)(U_\theta\oplus U_{R,\theta})^{-1}=H_{\mathrm{full}}(p),
\]
then the Schur-complement effective Hamiltonian inherits it, and in particular the zero-momentum self-energy satisfies
\[
[Q_V,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\]
Under little-group scalarity this implies
\[
\Sigma(0,0)=a_0\mathbf 1_4+a_3\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
so no radiatively generated term proportional to
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\quad\text{or}\quad
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
can appear. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

Thus the only residual open part of C5 is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{full microscopic symmetry inheritance under remote-sector elimination.}
}
\label{eq:C5_last_open}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual C5 shell-level result}
}
\]

For the canonical minimal Class II correction, the corrected shell block remains
\[
\boxed{
H_D(p)
=
\tau_z\otimes
\Bigl(
B_{\mathrm{eff}}p_1\sigma_1
+
C_{\mathrm{eff}}p_2\sigma_2
+
A_{\mathrm{eff}}p_\parallel\sigma_3
\Bigr).
}
\]

Hence the residual valley-charge generator
\[
\boxed{
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
}
\]
still satisfies
\[
\boxed{
[Q_V,H_D(p)]=0.
}
\]

Since the full constant mass space is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\},
}
\]
and these two generators transform nontrivially under \(U(1)_V\),
\[
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M=\{0\}.
}
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{shell-level C5 is passed: the corrected local shell block preserves residual valley symmetry and forbids all constant Dirac masses.}
}
\]

The only remaining microscopic open part is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the full microscopic TECT theory, including remote-sector elimination, preserve the same residual symmetry?}
}
\]

\boxed{
\Delta_{\min}:=
\min\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}},
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}},
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},

\},

\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}(\omega,k)=M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2k^2-\omega^2.
}
\]

In the low-energy regime \(|\omega|,|k|\ll M_\sigma\), after restricting to a sufficiently small neighborhood,
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}(\omega,k)\ge \frac{M_\sigma^2}{2}>0.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}),0\bigr)\ge \frac{M_\sigma^2}{2},
}
\]
and equivalently, at the Hamiltonian level,
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma>0.
}

\section*{Actual computation of the higher-shell lower bound \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}$}{Delta_high^(0)}}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

We want to prove an explicit positive lower bound for the higher-shell part of the remote spectrum.

The relevant diagonal kernel is of Brazovskii type:
\begin{equation}
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2,
\qquad K>0.
\label{eq:Lambda_high}
\end{equation}

For the higher-shell sector, define the radial shell-separation parameter
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
\inf_{Q\in\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}}\bigl||Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr|.
\label{eq:delta_shell_def}
\end{equation}
Then the theorem-level sufficient bound is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2>|r_*|
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|>0.
}
\label{eq:high_general_bound}
\end{equation}
This is explicitly stated in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection*{2. BCC reciprocal-shell arithmetic}

For the selected BCC first shell, the integer reciprocal representatives are
\[
\widetilde S_{\mathrm{BCC}}
=
\{(\pm1,\pm1,0),(\pm1,0,\pm1),(0,\pm1,\pm1)\},
\]
and the compatible reciprocal lattice is
\[
L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*
=
\{(h,k,\ell)\in\mathbb Z^3: h+k+\ell\equiv 0 \pmod 2\}.
\]
The notes compute the first radial separation above the selected shell and conclude:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=2
}
\label{eq:delta_shell_BCC}
\end{equation}
in the integer reciprocal convention. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection*{3. Insert the explicit BCC value}

Substituting \eqref{eq:delta_shell_BCC} into \eqref{eq:high_general_bound}, we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|
=
4K-|r_*|.
}
\label{eq:Delta_high_explicit}
\end{equation}
Therefore, a completely explicit sufficient positivity condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
4K>|r_*|
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}>0.
}
\label{eq:Delta_high_positive}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in unit-shell normalization the same statement is sometimes written as
\[
\widehat\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}\ge K-|r_*|.
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection*{4. Interpretation}

This is an actual completed sectorwise result, not merely a structural reduction:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the higher-shell radial separation is no longer abstract;
\item the BCC arithmetic fixes it explicitly to \(\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=2\);
\item therefore the higher-shell diagonal remote lower bound is explicitly
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}\ge 4K-|r_*|.
\]
\end{enumerate}

So the higher-shell part of C4 is genuinely closed once the standard low-shell regime
\[
4K>|r_*|
\]
is imposed.

\subsection*{5. Position inside the tail-gap theorem}

The tail-gap decomposition theorem collects the explicit sectorwise bounds:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)},\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)},\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)},\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}.
\]
With
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}}
=
\min\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}
\},
\]
if
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}},
\]
then the full tail block is uniformly gapped:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}}
-
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
>0.
\]


Thus, after the present computation, the higher-shell contribution is no longer part of the open C4 frontier.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual higher-shell result}
}
\]

For the Brazovskii-type diagonal kernel
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2,
}
\]
the higher-shell lower bound is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|.
}
\]

For the selected BCC first shell, the reciprocal-shell arithmetic gives
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=2.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
4K-|r_*|.
}
\]

Hence the explicit sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
4K>|r_*|
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}>0.
}
\]

So the higher-shell piece of C4 is actually closed.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Actual computation of the wrong-internal lower bound \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}$}{Delta_wrong-int^(0)}}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

We want an explicit positive lower bound for the wrong-internal contribution to the remote gap.

Let \(U_D\) denote the selected internal shell-point doublet space with energy \(E_*\), and let
\[
U_{\mathrm{wrong}}=Q(\mathbb C^3)
\]
denote the complementary wrong-internal sector, where \(Q\) is the orthogonal projector onto the complement of the selected doublet.

Let \(I_0\) be the unperturbed internal shell-point operator.

\subsection*{2. Exact identification of the wrong-internal gap}

The wrong-internal diagonal contribution is identified as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:Delta_wrongint_ident}
\end{equation}
This is stated explicitly in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

So the wrong-internal gap is simply the spectral separation between the selected internal doublet energy and the complement internal spectrum.

\subsection*{3. Minimal \(\mathbb C^3\) carrier}

In the minimal \(\mathbb C^3\) shell-point carrier, the selected internal sector is a transverse doublet with energy \(E_*\), while the complement is the one-dimensional longitudinal direction \(\hat n\), satisfying
\begin{equation}
I_0\hat n=E_L\hat n.
\label{eq:EL_def}
\end{equation}
Hence
\[
\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)=\{E_L\}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
|E_L-E_*|.
}
\label{eq:Delta_wrongint_minimal}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the minimal-carrier wrong-internal gap corollary. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_L\neq E_*
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}>0.
}
\label{eq:Delta_wrongint_positive}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Stability under bounded internal perturbations}

Now allow a bounded perturbation of the internal shell-point operator:
\[
I=I_0+\delta I,
\qquad
\|Q\delta I Q\|\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]
Then the perturbed complement spectrum satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_{\mathrm{int}}
:=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QIQ)\bigr)
\ge
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
}
\label{eq:wrongint_stable}
\end{equation}
Hence, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}<m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)},
}
\label{eq:wrongint_eps_small}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_{\mathrm{int}}>0.
}
\label{eq:wrongint_positive_pert}
\end{equation}
So the wrong-internal sector gap is stable under sufficiently small internal perturbations. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection*{5. Consequence for the tail-gap theorem}

The tail-gap decomposition theorem uses
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}}
=
\min\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}
\}.
\]
The present computation gives the explicit wrong-internal contribution:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}=|E_L-E_*|
}
\]
in the minimal carrier, and more generally
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)\bigr).
}
\]

Thus the wrong-internal piece of C4 is no longer structurally open.
It is reduced to one actual internal spectral-separation number.

\subsection*{6. Strongest honest conclusion}

Therefore the wrong-internal sector of C4 is actually closed up to one explicit internal spectral input:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_L\neq E_*
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}=|E_L-E_*|>0.
}
\label{eq:wrongint_final}
\end{equation}
Moreover, this positivity is stable under bounded internal perturbations.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual wrong-internal result}
}
\]

The wrong-internal lower bound is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)\bigr).
}
\]

In the minimal \(\mathbb C^3\) shell-point carrier,
\[
\boxed{
I_0\hat n=E_L\hat n,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}=|E_L-E_*|.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
E_L\neq E_*
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}>0.
}
\]

Under a bounded internal perturbation
\[
\boxed{
\|Q\delta I Q\|\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}},
}
\]
one still has
\[
\boxed{
m_{\mathrm{int}}
\ge
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}},
}
\]
so if
\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}<m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)},
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
m_{\mathrm{int}}>0.
}
\]

So the wrong-internal piece of C4 is actually closed once the selected internal doublet is spectrally separated from the longitudinal internal mode.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Actual estimate of the tail/remote mixing norm \texorpdfstring{$\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}$}{eta_rem,rho}}

\subsection*{1. Goal}

The last unresolved part of C4 is no longer the diagonal remote gaps themselves, but the total remote mixing budget
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]
The full remote block is written as
\begin{equation}
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p),
\label{eq:HRfull_split_eta}
\end{equation}
where \(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) is the diagonal benchmark operator and \(R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) collects all remote--remote off-diagonal mixing, tail couplings, and bounded residual corrections.

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\|.
}
\label{eq:eta_rem_def}
\end{equation}
The C4 objective is to show
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
\]
which then implies a positive full remote gap.

\subsection*{2. Explicit master bound}

The notes give the following explicit estimate:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}} K_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}} \frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge 1.
}
\label{eq:eta_rem_master_bound}
\end{equation}
Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}\) denotes active low-order remote couplings,
\item \(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}\) denotes heavy-mediated contributions,
\item \(K_a,\widetilde K_a>0\) are operator-norm constants,
\item \(r_a\ge 1\) is the order at which the corresponding coupling begins in momentum,
\item \(M_a^{\sigma_a}\) encodes heavy-mass suppression.
\end{itemize}
This is the exact quantitative form of the tail-coupling estimate theorem. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection*{3. Immediate consequence: infrared smallness}

Since every exponent satisfies \(r_a\ge 1\), one immediately gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}\xrightarrow[\rho\to 0]{}0.
}
\label{eq:eta_goes_zero}
\end{equation}
More concretely, if
\[
r_{\min}:=\min_a r_a \ge 1,
\]
then for sufficiently small \(\rho\),
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
=
O(\rho^{r_{\min}}).
\label{eq:eta_asymptotic}
\end{equation}
Thus the total remote mixing is an infrared-small quantity.

\subsection*{4. Combination with the diagonal benchmark}

The full remote-gap theorem uses the benchmark inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:master_gap_ineq}
\end{equation}
If this holds, then the full remote block has a uniform positive gap:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
>0.
}
\label{eq:Delta_full_bound}
\end{equation}
This is the master explicit spectral inequality theorem. 

\subsection*{5. Explicit sufficient benchmark form}

The notes also give the stronger explicit sufficient inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\Biggr\}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:explicit_master_gap}
\end{equation}
This packages the higher-shell, volumetric, wrong-internal/effective-internal, and extra-sector diagonal lower bounds into one benchmark condition. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection*{6. What is actually closed now}

At this stage, the structural problem is finished:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}\) has an explicit operator-norm upper bound;
\item that upper bound tends to zero as \(\rho\to 0\);
\item therefore, once the diagonal benchmark is positive, there exists a sufficiently small \(\rho\) such that
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

So the remaining practical work is only to estimate the constants
\[
K_a,\qquad \widetilde K_a,\qquad r_a,\qquad M_a,
\]
for the actual microscopic truncation.

\subsection*{7. Strongest honest conclusion}

Therefore the last missing part of C4 is no longer conceptual.
It is reduced to a finite small-coupling estimate:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}} K_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}} \frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\qquad r_a\ge 1,
}
\end{equation}
together with the explicit benchmark inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}>0.
}
\end{equation}

In particular, infrared smallness of the tail/remote couplings is already theorem-level established.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual result for the last C4 bottleneck}
}
\]

The full remote block is written as
\[
\boxed{
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p),
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\|.
}

The explicit master bound is

\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}} K_a \rho^{r_a}
+

\qquad
r_a\ge 1.
}

Hence
\[
\boxed{

\qquad

Therefore, if the diagonal benchmark gap is positive and satisfies

\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}

So the last C4 bottleneck is reduced to estimating finitely many constants \(K_a,\widetilde K_a,r_a,M_a\), not to any new structural problem.

\[

can be generated. Therefore radiative constant Dirac masses are forbidden.

\section*{Reduction of the last C1 bottleneck to the coefficient \texorpdfstring{$A$}{A}}

\subsection*{1. Remaining issue}

The last unresolved part of C1 had been written as the longitudinal overlap test
\[
\mathcal J_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\, n_\mu v_3^\mu(\xi).
\]
The question is whether this quantity is nonzero in the full microscopic TECT linearization.

\subsection*{2. Extraction theorem}

Let the microscopic linearized operator near a selected shell point \(G_*\) admit
\[
L(G_*+p)=L_*+p_iK_i+O(|p|^2),
\]
and let \(P_*\) be the projector onto the two-dimensional low-energy valley space \(H_*\).
Then the reduced first-order Hamiltonian is
\[
h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)=P_*(p_iK_i)P_*|_{H_*},
\]
and the Pauli-resolved coefficients are
\[
M_{\mu i}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}(\sigma_\mu P_*K_iP_*).
\]
Thus the local Weyl data are read directly from the projected first derivatives \(K_i\). :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection*{3. Minimal actual operator ansatz}

For the minimal actual symmetry-compatible operator,
\[
L_{\mathrm{act}}(G_*+p)
=
E_*\mathbf 1_4
+
A(\hat n\!\cdot\!p)\,\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
B(p_1\tau_1\otimes s_1+p_2\tau_1\otimes s_2)
+
C(-p_2\tau_1\otimes s_1+p_1\tau_1\otimes s_2)
+O(|p|^2),
\]
the projected two-band valley Hamiltonian is
\[
h_+(p)
=
A p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
B(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
C(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
+O(|p|^2).
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=A,\qquad \alpha=B,\qquad \beta=C.
}
\label{eq:ABC_id}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection*{4. Microscopic tensor form}

Equivalently, the shell-compatible enriched tensors are
\[
N^3_{ij}=\frac{A}{\kappa_*|G_*|}\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=\frac{1}{\kappa_*|G_*|}(B\hat n_ie_{1j}+C\hat n_ie_{2j}),
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=\frac{1}{\kappa_*|G_*|}(-C\hat n_ie_{1j}+B\hat n_ie_{2j}).
\]
So the longitudinal projector channel is exactly the coefficient \(A\). 

\subsection*{5. Final reduction}

Hence the last unresolved longitudinal question is not a separate mysterious overlap problem.
It is exactly the microscopic coefficient test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:A_nonzero}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal J_\parallel\neq 0
\Longleftrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\Longleftrightarrow
A\neq 0,
\]
up to the normalization conventions of the chosen projected basis.

\subsection*{6. Strongest honest conclusion}

So the last unresolved part of C1 is now compressed to:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Extract the coefficient }A\text{ from the full microscopic projected first-order operator and check whether }A\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:last_C1_reduction}
\end{equation}

No further structural reduction is needed.


\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Final reduction of the last C1 bottleneck}
}
\]

The longitudinal overlap test is not independent.
By the extraction theorem, the projected first-order microscopic operator directly yields the Weyl coefficients
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel,\ \alpha,\ \beta.
}
\]

For the minimal actual operator ansatz,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=A,\qquad \alpha=B,\qquad \beta=C.
}
\]

Equivalently, the longitudinal projector channel is
\[
\boxed{
N^3_{ij}=\frac{A}{\kappa_*|G_*|}\hat n_i\hat n_j.
}
\]

Therefore the last unresolved part of C1 is simply:
\[
\boxed{
A\neq 0.
}
\]

So the remaining local microscopic task is no longer
“compute a mysterious overlap,”
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{extract }A\text{ from the full microscopic projected first-order operator and verify }A\neq 0.
}

\section*{Actual extraction formula for the last C1 condition: \(A\neq 0\)}

\subsection*{1. Microscopic linearization near the selected shell point}

Let the full microscopic linearized operator admit the expansion near the selected shell point \(G_*\):
\begin{equation}
L(G_*+p)=L_*+p_iK_i+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
K_i:=\partial_{k_i}L(k)\big|_{k=G_*}.
\label{eq:L_expand_A}
\end{equation}
Let \(P_*\) be the orthogonal projector onto the two-dimensional low-energy valley space \(H_*\cong\mathbb C^2\).
Then the reduced first-order valley Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)=P_*(p_iK_i)P_*|_{H_*}.
\label{eq:hlin_A}
\end{equation}
By Pauli decomposition,
\begin{equation}
h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)=a_0(p)\mathbf 1_2+a_\mu(p)\sigma_\mu,
\qquad
a_\mu(p)=M_{\mu i}p_i,
\label{eq:Pauli_decomp_A}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
M_{\mu i}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_\mu P_*K_iP_*\bigr).
\label{eq:Mmui_A}
\end{equation}
Thus all local Weyl data are determined directly by the projected first derivatives \(K_i\). :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection*{2. Adapted shell frame and longitudinal coefficient}

Choose the adapted frame
\[
p=p_\parallel \hat n+p_1e_1+p_2e_2,
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\]
In the minimal actual symmetry-compatible ansatz, the reduced Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
h_+(p)
=
A p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
B(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
C(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
+O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:hplus_ABC_A}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=A,\qquad
\alpha=B,\qquad
\beta=C.
}
\label{eq:ABC_equals_lambda}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

Therefore the last unresolved part of C1 is simply the longitudinal coefficient test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:A_test}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{3. Direct projector formula for \(A\)}

Let
\[
K_\parallel:=\hat n_i K_i.
\]
Then the coefficient of \(p_\parallel\sigma_3\) is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_3 P_*K_\parallel P_*\bigr).
}
\label{eq:A_projector_formula}
\end{equation}
So the full microscopic C1 question has now become the single finite projector-contraction test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_3 P_*K_\parallel P_*\bigr)\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
}
\label{eq:A_single_test}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Equivalent tensor-contraction formula}

In microscopic tensor language, the minimal enriched tensors realizing the actual operator are
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}
=
\frac{A}{\kappa_*|G_*|}\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}
=
\frac{1}{\kappa_*|G_*|}(B\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\hat n_i e_{2j}),
\qquad
N^2_{ij}
=
\frac{1}{\kappa_*|G_*|}(-C\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\hat n_i e_{2j}).
\label{eq:N_ABC_A}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|A,
\qquad
\alpha=\kappa_*|G_*|B,
\qquad
\beta=\kappa_*|G_*|C.
\label{eq:lambda_from_tensor_A}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

Thus the longitudinal channel is equivalently the microscopic tensor contraction
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\hat n_i\hat n_j N^3_{ij}\neq 0
\Longleftrightarrow
A\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:tensor_equiv_A}
\end{equation}
This is the tensor-form version of the same test.

\subsection*{5. Final reduction of C1}

Therefore the last unresolved microscopic content of C1 is no longer a vague overlap problem.
It is exactly one of the following equivalent tests:

\end{equation}
or equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\hat n_i\hat n_j N^3_{ij}\neq 0.
}
\end{equation}

No further structural reduction is needed.

\subsection{Summary}

Near the selected shell point \(G_*\),

\section*{Method A: direct projector-derivative extraction of \(A\)}

\subsection*{1. Starting point}

Near the selected shell point \(G_*\), write the microscopic linearized operator as
\begin{equation}
L(G_*+p)=L_*+p_iK_i+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
K_i:=\partial_{k_i}L(k)\big|_{k=G_*}.
\label{eq:A_method_start}
\end{equation}
Let \(P_*\) be the orthogonal projector onto the two-dimensional low-energy valley space \(H_*\).

Then the reduced first-order valley Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)=P_*(p_iK_i)P_*|_{H_*}.
\label{eq:hlin_projected}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{2. Pauli-resolved coefficient matrix}

Since \(h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)\) is Hermitian on \(H_*\cong\mathbb C^2\), it decomposes as
\begin{equation}
h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)=a_0(p)\mathbf 1_2+a_\mu(p)\sigma_\mu,
\qquad
a_\mu(p)=M_{\mu i}p_i,
\label{eq:pauli_coeffs}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
M_{\mu i}
=
\frac12 \operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_\mu P_*K_iP_*\bigr).
\label{eq:Mmui_formula}
\end{equation}
Thus all local Weyl data are extracted directly from the projected first derivatives \(K_i\). :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection*{3. Adapted shell frame}

Choose the adapted frame
\[
p=p_\parallel \hat n+p_1e_1+p_2e_2,
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\]
Then define
\begin{equation}
K_\parallel:=\hat n_iK_i,
\qquad
K_1:=e_{1i}K_i,
\qquad
K_2:=e_{2i}K_i.
\label{eq:adapted_K}
\end{equation}

In the minimal symmetry-compatible Weyl form,
\begin{equation}
h_+(p)
=
A p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
B(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
C(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
+O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:ABC_form}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A
=
\frac12 \operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_3 P_*K_\parallel P_*\bigr).
}
\label{eq:A_projector_trace}
\end{equation}
Likewise, \(B\) and \(C\) are extracted from the \(\sigma_1,\sigma_2\) components of \(P_*K_1P_*,P_*K_2P_*\). :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5} :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection*{4. What Method A reduces the problem to}

Hence the final C1 condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A\neq 0
\iff
\frac12 \operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_3 P_*K_\parallel P_*\bigr)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:A_nonzero_methodA}
\end{equation}

So Method A completely removes the need for any additional abstract reduction.
The only remaining task is to compute the microscopic \(K_i\) from the true TECT linearized operator and insert them into \eqref{eq:A_projector_trace}. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\subsection*{5. Cross-check with the explicit local representative}

In the explicit actual-local representative, the projected overlap formulas give
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:lambda_overlap}
\end{equation}
and for the explicit canonical representative,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\label{eq:explicit_rep_lambda}
\end{equation}
Thus in the representative model,
\[
A=\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\]
so Method A indeed returns a nonzero longitudinal coefficient whenever \(\lambda_c\neq 0\). 

\subsection*{6. Honest status}

What is rigorously closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact projector-trace formula for \(A\),
\item the equivalence \(A\neq 0 \iff \lambda_\parallel\neq 0\),
\item the explicit nonzero value of \(A\) in the representative model.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual microscopic computation of }K_i=\partial_{k_i}L(k)\big|_{k=G_*}
\text{ for the full TECT linearized operator.}
}
\label{eq:remaining_open_methodA}
\end{equation}
So Method A converts the final C1 bottleneck into one explicit coefficient-extraction calculation from the true microscopic PDE.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Method A reduces the last C1 problem to one projector trace}
}
\]

Near the selected shell point \(G_*\),
\[
\boxed{
L(G_*+p)=L_*+p_iK_i+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)=P_*(p_iK_i)P_*|_{H_*}.
}
\]

In the adapted shell frame,
\[
\boxed{
h_+(p)
=
A p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
B(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
C(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
+O(|p|^2),
}
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
A
=
\frac12 \operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_3 P_*K_\parallel P_*\bigr),
\qquad
K_\parallel=\hat n_iK_i.
}
\]

Therefore the final unresolved C1 condition is simply
\[
\boxed{
A\neq 0
\iff
\frac12 \operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_3 P_*K_\parallel P_*\bigr)\neq 0.
}
\]

In the explicit local representative,
\[
\boxed{
A=\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
}
\]
so Method A already gives a nonzero longitudinal coefficient there.

Thus Method A turns the last C1 bottleneck into one explicit coefficient-extraction calculation from the full microscopic TECT linearized operator.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section*{Method A pushed one step further: explicit formula for \(A\)}

\subsection*{1. Projector-derivative extraction formula}

Near the selected shell point \(G_*\),
\[
L(G_*+p)=L_*+p_iK_i+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L(k)\big|_{k=G_*}.
\]
Let \(P_*\) be the projector onto the two-dimensional low-energy valley space \(H_*\).
Then
\[
h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)=P_*(p_iK_i)P_*|_{H_*}.
\]
In the adapted shell frame,
\[
h_+(p)
=
A p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
B(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
C(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
+O(|p|^2),
\]
so
\[
A=\lambda_\parallel.
\]

\subsection*{2. Explicit projected symbol in the actual local projector-defect operator class}

For the concrete minimal microscopic transport term already extracted from the local projector-defect geometry, the projected mixed symbol is
\[
M^\mu
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
I_\theta
\Bigl[
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr].
\]
Hence the reduced S2 symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:explicit_lambdaABC}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A=\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:A_explicit_lambda_c}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection*{3. Explicit defect integral}

For the explicit reflection-symmetric defect profile,
\[
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]
Substituting into \eqref{eq:A_explicit_lambda_c},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:A_explicit_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore, for a nontrivial defect profile \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
A\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:A_nonzero_from_lambda_c}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Final nondegeneracy condition in this explicit operator class}

Since also
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\]
the transverse coefficients satisfy
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\]
Thus the full S2 nondegeneracy condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:full_S2_explicit_condition}
\end{equation}

So within the explicit actual-local projector-defect operator class, Method A completely reduces the last C1 issue to checking the scalar coefficient \(\lambda_c\).

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Method A actual result in the explicit local operator class}
}
\]

The longitudinal coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
A=\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

For the explicit defect profile,
\[
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
A
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
A\neq 0.
}
\]

Likewise,
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
}
\]
so the full explicit S2 nondegeneracy condition is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]
