\section*{Next actual task after Method A: microscopic identification of \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_c$}{lambda_c}}

\subsection*{1. What Method A already achieved}

Method A reduced the last unresolved part of C1 to the longitudinal coefficient
\[
A=\lambda_\parallel.
\]
In the explicit local projector-defect operator class one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:lambda_c_reduction}
\end{equation}
Since \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\) for a nontrivial defect profile, this implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
A\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:lambda_c_implies_A}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

Therefore the actual remaining C1 problem is no longer \(A\neq 0\) directly, but the microscopic identification of the coefficient \(\lambda_c\).

\subsection*{2. Microscopic origin of the longitudinal channel}

The key internal channel is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
\label{eq:Txi_origin_lambda_c}
\end{equation}
Direct restriction gives
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\]
but its quadratic channel is nontrivial:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
}
\label{eq:Txi2_nontrivial}
\end{equation}


A naive singlet source proportional to \(\theta'^2\sigma_3\) fails by parity because
\[
f_+ \text{ is even},\qquad
f_- \text{ is odd},\qquad
\theta'^2 \text{ is even},
\]
so
\[
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^2=0.
\]
Therefore the viable longitudinal first-order channel must contain one additional odd factor:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q\,n^\mu.
}
\label{eq:good_long_channel}
\end{equation}
Taking the traceless part gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{tr}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:good_long_channel_tr}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the longitudinal witness channel. 

\subsection*{3. Minimal composite transport operator}

Combining the longitudinal commutator-induced singlet with the transverse doublet source, the minimal composite local transport operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{comp}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:composite_transport}
\end{equation}
This produces the full S2 witness triplet explicitly, with
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\]


\subsection*{4. Final microscopic coefficient problem}

Therefore the strongest honest current reduction is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the complete microscopic local Dirac closure is reduced to extracting the finite coefficients }
(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\text{ from the true TECT linearized PDE.}
}
\label{eq:finite_coeff_problem}
\end{equation}
In particular, the last longitudinal issue is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the full microscopic TECT linearization generate the commutator-induced longitudinal coupling }\lambda_c\neq 0?
}
\label{eq:last_longitudinal_question}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Strongest honest conclusion}

So the next actual task is not another structural reduction.
It is the coefficient-identification step:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{start from the true local TECT projector/condensate transport term, project it to the }Q_B\text{-doublet, and read off the coefficient multiplying }
\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu.
}
\label{eq:next_actual_task_lambda_c}
\end{equation}
If that coefficient is nonzero, then \(A\neq 0\) follows immediately.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Next actual task after Method A}
}
\]

Method A already reduced the longitudinal condition to
\[
\boxed{
A=\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]
Since
\[
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0
}
\]
for a nontrivial defect,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0\Longrightarrow A\neq 0.
}
\]

The microscopic origin of \(\lambda_c\) is the commutator-induced channel
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3).
}
\]

Hence the viable longitudinal transport term is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q\,n^\mu,
}
\]
whose traceless part is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{tr}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\]

Therefore the next real microscopic task is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{derive the true local TECT transport term and extract the coefficient multiplying }
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}n^\mu.
}
\]

If that coefficient is nonzero, then
\[
\boxed{
A\neq 0.
}
\]

\section*{Method B: microscopic origin of the longitudinal coefficient \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_c$}{lambda_c}}

\subsection*{1. Why the primitive channel fails}

A natural primitive traceless internal tensor is
\begin{equation}
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3.
\label{eq:primitive_channel}
\end{equation}
However, on the defect tangent bundle
\[
Q_B=(\mathbb C z_B)^\perp,
\]
its restriction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T(P_B)\big|_{Q_B}=-\mathbf 1_{Q_B}.
}
\label{eq:primitive_restriction}
\end{equation}
So the primitive channel produces only an identity-valued transport operator on \(Q_B\), not a traceless Pauli triplet, and in particular not a distinguished longitudinal \(\sigma_3\)-splitting. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

Therefore the primitive channel is too coarse to produce the full S2 witness structure.

\subsection*{2. The first genuinely gradient-sensitive channel}

The first nontrivial gradient-sensitive refinement is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
}
\label{eq:Txi_def}
\end{equation}
For the explicit background,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi
=
i\theta'(\xi)\bigl(z_B e_1^\dagger-e_1 z_B^\dagger\bigr).
\label{eq:Txi_explicit}
\end{equation}
Its direct restriction vanishes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0.
}
\label{eq:Txi_linear_zero}
\end{equation}
But its quadratic channel is nontrivial:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
}
\label{eq:Txi_quadratic}
\end{equation}
Hence the traceless part is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Txi_traceless}
\end{equation}
This is the first natural longitudinal \(\sigma_3\)-type splitting channel. 

\subsection*{3. Parity obstruction and the need for one more odd factor}

The graded low modes satisfy
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\]
with
\[
f_+ \text{ even},\qquad f_- \text{ odd}.
\]
Since \(\theta'(\xi)^2\) is even, the overlap
\[
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^2
\]
vanishes by parity.
Therefore the quadratic channel \eqref{eq:Txi_traceless} cannot by itself contribute to the first-order mixed symbol.

Hence one additional odd factor is required, and the minimal viable longitudinal source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu.
}
\label{eq:good_long_source}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:Txi_traceless}, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:good_long_source_explicit}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the longitudinal witness channel. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection*{4. Mixed-symbol projection}

Projecting to the graded low modes gives
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:mixed_projection}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:good_long_source_explicit},
\begin{equation}
M^\mu_{\parallel}
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}
\left(
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3
\right)
n^\mu\sigma_3
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:long_mixed_symbol}
\end{equation}
Thus the longitudinal Weyl coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_lambda_c}
\end{equation}
Since \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\) for a nontrivial defect profile,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
A\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:lambda_c_implies_A}
\end{equation}


\subsection*{5. The minimal composite transport operator}

Combining the longitudinal commutator-induced singlet with the transverse doublet channels yields the minimal composite transport operator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{comp}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Vcomp}
\end{equation}
Its projected witnesses are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:witness_triplet}
\end{equation}
Therefore the full S2 nondegeneracy condition is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:S2_condition_lambda_c}
\end{equation}


\subsection*{6. Strongest honest conclusion}

Thus Method B proves the following.
The longitudinal coefficient \(\lambda_c\) is not an arbitrary free parameter introduced by hand.
It is precisely the coefficient of the first viable commutator-induced longitudinal transport channel
\[
\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu.
\]
Therefore the last unresolved microscopic content of C1 is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the full microscopic TECT linearization generate this commutator-induced longitudinal channel with nonzero coefficient }\lambda_c?
}
\label{eq:last_question_lambda_c}
\end{equation}
This is the sharpest currently honest formulation of the remaining longitudinal witness problem.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Method B result}
}
\]

The primitive channel
\[
\boxed{
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3
}
\]
is too coarse on \(Q_B\), because
\[
\boxed{
T(P_B)\big|_{Q_B}=-\mathbf 1_{Q_B}.
}
\]

The first genuinely gradient-sensitive longitudinal source is instead
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
}
\]

Although
\[
\boxed{
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
}
\]
its quadratic channel is nontrivial:
\[
\boxed{
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr),
\qquad
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\sigma_3.
}
\]

Because \(\theta'^2\) is even, one more odd factor is required. Hence the minimal viable longitudinal source is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\]

Projecting to the graded low modes yields
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
A\neq 0.
}
\]

So Method B reduces the remaining longitudinal witness problem to one sharp microscopic question:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the full microscopic TECT linearization generate the commutator-induced channel }
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}n^\mu
\text{ with nonzero coefficient }\lambda_c?
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_i\hat n_jN_{ij}^3.
}
\]

For the axial shell-compatible family
\[
N_{ij}^3=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N_{ij}^1=B\,\hat n_ie_{1j}+C\,\hat n_ie_{2j},
\qquad
N_{ij}^2=-C\,\hat n_ie_{1j}+B\,\hat n_ie_{2j},
\]
one gets

\qquad

\qquad

\iff

\section*{Method B applied to the minimal local PDE ansatz}

Start from the shell-enriched first-order coupling
\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\]

For the minimal projector/enriched completion,
\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
g_\parallel (\partial_i\phi_0)\hat n_i \bigl(\hat n\!\cdot\!(-i\nabla)\bigr)\otimes s_3
+
g_I (\partial_i\phi_0)\hat n_i \Big[(e_1\!\cdot\!(-i\nabla))\otimes s_1+(e_2\!\cdot\!(-i\nabla))\otimes s_2\Big]
+
g_J (\partial_i\phi_0)\hat n_i \Big[-(e_2\!\cdot\!(-i\nabla))\otimes s_1+(e_1\!\cdot\!(-i\nabla))\otimes s_2\Big].
\]

Comparing term by term gives
\[
\boxed{
N_{ij}^3=g_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N_{ij}^1=g_I\hat n_i e_{1j}-g_J\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N_{ij}^2=g_I\hat n_i e_{2j}+g_J\hat n_i e_{1j}.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\hat n_i\hat n_jN_{ij}^3=g_\parallel,
}
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
A\neq 0
\iff
\hat n_i\hat n_jN_{ij}^3\neq 0
\iff
g_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

Using the shell-matching formula,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|\,g_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=\kappa_*|G_*|\,g_I,
\qquad
\beta=-\kappa_*|G_*|\,g_J.
}
\]

So the local Weyl condition becomes
\[
\boxed{
g_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_I,g_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

For the Class II auxiliary-mediator realization,
\[
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C_{ij}^{ab}.
\]
If the shell-relevant decomposition of \(m^a C_{ij}^{ab}\) contains
\[
A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j\delta^{b3},
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\delta N_{ij}^3
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j+\cdots,
\qquad
\delta W_\parallel
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}A\neq 0.
}
\]

Thus Method B reduces the microscopic longitudinal question to a single shell-relevant tensor coefficient:
\[
\boxed{
\hat n_i\hat n_jN_{ij}^3\neq 0.
}
\]

\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a
\]

\[
N_{ij}^3=g_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N_{ij}^1=g_I\hat n_i e_{1j}-g_J\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N_{ij}^2=g_I\hat n_i e_{2j}+g_J\hat n_i e_{1j}
\]

\[
\hat n_i\hat n_jN_{ij}^3=g_\parallel
\]

\[
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|\,g_\parallel
\]

\[
A\neq 0
\iff
g_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\section*{Method B pushed to the final microscopic coefficient formula}

\subsection*{1. Tensor-contraction extraction of the longitudinal coefficient}

For the shell-enriched first-order coupling
\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a,
\]
the longitudinal Weyl coefficient is extracted by
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_i\hat n_j N_{ij}^3.
\]
In the minimal shell-compatible ansatz
\[
N_{ij}^3=g_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
g_\parallel=\hat n_i\hat n_j N_{ij}^3.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
g_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
A\neq 0.
\]

\subsection*{2. Class II induced enriched tensor}

For the Class II heavy auxiliary mediator completion, the induced enriched tensor is
\[
\boxed{
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C_{ij}^{ab}.
}
\]
After shell-adapted projection, the longitudinal axial coefficient is obtained by contracting the \(b=3\) component along \(\hat n_i\hat n_j\):
\[
\delta g_\parallel
=
\hat n_i\hat n_j\,\delta N_{ij}^3.
\]
Substituting the Class II formula gives
\[
\boxed{
\delta g_\parallel
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,
m^a\,\hat n_i\hat n_j\,C_{ij}^{a3}.
}
\]

Thus the last microscopic longitudinal test is precisely
\[
\boxed{
m^a\,\hat n_i\hat n_j\,C_{ij}^{a3}\neq 0.
}
\]

\subsection*{3. Minimal seed realization}

For the minimal seed choice
\[
m^a=m\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C_{ij}^{33}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
one gets
\[
m^a\,\hat n_i\hat n_j\,C_{ij}^{a3}
=
m\,\hat n_i\hat n_j\,C_{ij}^{33}
=
m\,c_\parallel.
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\delta g_\parallel
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m\,c_\parallel.
}
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
m\,c_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
g_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
A\neq 0.
}
\]

\subsection*{4. Final reduction}

So Method B reduces the final longitudinal witness problem to one explicit shell-relevant tensor coefficient:
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute }m^a\hat n_i\hat n_j C_{ij}^{a3}.
}
\]
If it is nonzero, then the longitudinal coefficient is nonzero.

\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a
\]

For the minimal enriched local ansatz,
\[
N_{ij}^3=g_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,\qquad
N_{ij}^1=g_I\hat n_i e_{1j}-g_J\hat n_i e_{2j},\qquad
N_{ij}^2=g_I\hat n_i e_{2j}+g_J\hat n_i e_{1j}.
\]

Hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_i\hat n_jN_{ij}^3
=\kappa_*|G_*|\,g_\parallel.
\]

Therefore, within this minimal enriched local ansatz,
\[
g_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\section*{Method B: corrected final version}

\subsection*{1. Scope}

We work inside the \emph{minimal enriched local ansatz}, not yet the full microscopic TECT linearization.

Let
\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a,
\qquad
a=1,2,3.
\]

Fix a selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\), define
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\]
and choose an adapted transverse frame \((e_1,e_2)\).

\subsection*{2. Exact tensor-contraction formulas}

The shell-level Weyl coefficients are read from the microscopic enriched tensor by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_i\hat n_jN_{ij}^3,
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_tensor_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\left(
e_{1j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^1+e_{2j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^2
\right),
}
\label{eq:alpha_tensor_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\left(
e_{2j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^1-e_{1j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^2
\right),
}
\label{eq:beta_tensor_final}
\end{equation}
where the overall sign of \(\beta\) is convention-dependent under reorientation of the transverse frame. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\subsection*{3. Minimal shell-compatible enriched ansatz}

For the minimal enriched local ansatz,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N_{ij}^3=g_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N_{ij}^1=g_I\hat n_i e_{1j}-g_J\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N_{ij}^2=g_I\hat n_i e_{2j}+g_J\hat n_i e_{1j}.
}
\label{eq:minimal_N_final}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\hat n_i\hat n_jN_{ij}^3
=
g_\parallel(\hat n\cdot\hat n)^2
=
g_\parallel,
\label{eq:nnN3_final}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|\,g_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:lambda_gparallel_final}
\end{equation}

Likewise,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\kappa_*|G_*|\,g_I,
\qquad
\beta=\pm\,\kappa_*|G_*|\,g_J,
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_gIJ_final}
\end{equation}
where the sign of \(\beta\) depends on the transverse orientation convention.

\subsection*{4. Weyl criterion}

Therefore the shell-level Weyl determinant is
\begin{equation}
\det M
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3\,
g_\parallel\,
(g_I^2+g_J^2),
\label{eq:detM_final}
\end{equation}
and the exact local Weyl criterion inside this ansatz is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_I,g_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:Weyl_criterion_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{5. Exact honest status}

What is rigorously established is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item inside the minimal enriched local ansatz, the longitudinal coefficient is exactly controlled by
\[
\hat n_i\hat n_jN_{ij}^3;
\]

\item the shell-level Weyl condition is exactly
\[
g_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (g_I,g_J)\neq (0,0);
\]

\item no further structural reduction is needed at this ansatz level.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{whether the true full microscopic TECT linearization actually generates the same nonzero enriched tensor coefficients }N_{ij}^a.
}
\label{eq:honest_open_final}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Open problems on the full PDE side}
}
\]

\begin{aligned}
&1.\ \text{The final full microscopic TECT condensate PDE is not yet uniquely closed from first principles.}\\
&2.\ \text{The actual linearized microscopic operator }L(k)\text{ has not yet been derived in final form.}\\
&3.\ \text{Hence the true coefficients }K_i=\partial_{k_i}L(k)|_{k=G_*}\text{ are still not explicitly computed.}\\
&4.\ \text{The actual shell/valley crossing }\pm G_*,\ \text{spectral isolation, chiral grading,}\\
&\qquad \text{and Clifford isotropy are not yet verified directly in the full TECT dynamics.}\\
&5.\ \text{Equivalently, the remaining microscopic Dirac task is the explicit extraction of }g_c,g_E,g_O\\
&\qquad \text{(or }N_{ij}^a\text{, or }\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta\text{) from the true full PDE.}
\end{aligned}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Open problems on the FRG side}
}
\]

\begin{aligned}
&1.\ \text{Quartic cubic anisotropy is largely under control, but derivative anisotropy remains open.}\\
&2.\ \text{The kinetic-flow matrix }M_Z\text{ has not yet been fully computed.}\\
&3.\ \text{Therefore the signs of the derivative-anisotropy eigenvalues are not yet known.}\\
&4.\ \text{Sectoral wavefunction flows and velocity-locking flows are not yet fully evaluated.}\\
&5.\ \text{Hence full IR isotropy / emergent Lorentz invariance is not yet completely closed.}
\end{aligned}
